# Operator — Agent Context

*Working memory for coding agents. Human-readable roadmap: `docs/roadmap.md`.*
*Living document — update at the end of each session.*

---

## Working Style (follow for every step)

- One step at a time. Test and commit before moving on. Never batch steps.
- Before making any change: explain what you're about to do and why, in plain language.
- Smallest possible change. If a step can be broken down, do so.
- Don't touch anything out of scope. Note it, don't change it.
- Audience: technical product manager, not a senior engineer. Define terms when used.

---

## Current Status

**Session 205 (May 7, 2026) — endurance audit continuation (A3 + C1 fixed, C2/C3/C5 dispositioned), Tier 3 audit doc reconciled, two queued small cleanups landed.** Four atomic-per-axis commits this session: `58adf88` (Tier 3 audit doc reconciliation), `3d5cc1d` (A3 + C1 endurance fixes + CHAINED TURNS prompt rule + roadmap deferred entry), `49ce78e` (`llm.py` dead `wrap_spoken`/`SAFETY_RULES` chain purge), `e827677` (`google_signin.py` chrome_path dedup via `chrome_preflight.CHROME_PATH`). 19/19 tests green throughout. **Branch is now 7 commits ahead of `origin/main`** (4 from this session + 3 carried over from earlier work). Apple Dev cert still in flight from S198, no movement.

**Four S205 commits in detail:**

1. **`58adf88` — pre-launch-audit.md Tier 3 reconciliation.** The S203 parallel session closed Tier 3 (12/12 cells) but only updated `agent-context.md` — `pre-launch-audit.md` itself kept all 13 Tier 3 boxes unchecked despite the work being done. Fixed: marked all 12 closeable cells [x] with inline per-cell findings narratives matching Tier 1/2 style, sourced from the eleven S203 commit messages. The 13th item (audio-helper Swift binary) stays unchecked with an explicit "deferred to 14.20.5 pre-notarize" note. Populated the previously-empty revisit/wontfix log with five concrete deferred items (install_preflight + readiness orphan product call with the four-option decision tree, openai+anthropic deps gating on second-provider scope, caption-text-in-INFO-log cross-file finding, magic-string `kind` values, untested S199 heartbeat watchdog). Doc now matches reality: 32 cells across all three tiers closed, what's left is the standalone workflow passes (Pass 1 install dry-run, Pass 7 dep pinning, Pass 8 runbook) and Apple-cert-gated /ultrareview + /security-review.

2. **`3d5cc1d` — A3 stderr deque cap + C1 CDP staleness fix + CHAINED TURNS prompt rule + roadmap deferred entry.** **A3** swapped `claude_cli._stderr_buf` from an unbounded `list[str]` (daemon thread `extend()`-ing every byte for an entire meeting) to `deque(maxlen=500)`. Read sites (`"".join(self._stderr_buf[-20:])`) updated to `list(self._stderr_buf)[-20:]` since deque doesn't support slicing. Generous over the 20-line diagnostic read window but bounded — no more monotonic growth on chatty inner-claude meetings. **C1** addressed macos_adapter's CDP staleness window. Root cause turned out to be structural: macos_adapter runs Playwright inside a daemon thread under `with sync_playwright()` (line 476), and Playwright's sync API objects can only be called from the thread that created them — so the cross-thread "is the page alive?" question can't directly call `self._browser.is_connected()` like attach_adapter does (which runs Playwright on the main thread, line 429). Fix: added `self._browser_alive: threading.Event` distinct from the existing `_browser_closed` (now load-bearingly separate — _browser_closed = teardown signal, _browser_alive = browser thread holds a live page), set after successful join, cleared at every detection-of-death path. Per-tick `page.is_closed()` probe in the 500ms holding loop reads cached state with no CDP round-trip — catches cleanly-closed pages immediately. Reduced the existing active health probe (page.url access, the one that catches frozen-WebSocket zombies) from 30s to 10s, so worst-case detection lag drops from ~30s to ~10s. `is_connected()` now returns `_browser_alive.is_set() AND NOT _browser_closed.is_set()` — ChatRunner gets a sub-10s zombie signal instead of waiting for the loop to break and finally to set the closed flag. Detection-only fix per S204 handoff scoping; reconnect-and-resume after a transient blip stays deferred (would need session-state rehydration, captions observer re-injection, chat panel re-open, participant-name cache rebuild). **CHAINED TURNS section** added to `_PRE_TOOL_VOICE_RULE` and `_PRE_TOOL_VOICE_RULE_YOLO_OVERRIDE` in `claude_cli.py`: addresses the failure mode where multi-turn agentic tool runs collapse narration to once-per-task and silently chain subsequent tool calls (user can't tell what the third or fourth tool is doing from a narration that scrolled past several seconds ago); rule now requires one preceding text block per tool_use, never one narration covering several. **Roadmap deferred entry** added: "Self-correcting MCP-hint loop" — log MCP-usage misses, offer hints durably attached to tools, accumulate per-user hints in `~/.operator/hints/`. Pairs naturally with the mid-meeting brain-reset entry. Open design Qs on scoping (per-tool/per-server/per-(tool,intent)) and pruning.

3. **`49ce78e` — `llm.py` dead `wrap_spoken`/`SAFETY_RULES` chain purge.** Post-S204 commit `6b20483` (chat-only prompt tail) captions no longer enter the LLM prompt — they're served on-demand to inner-claude via the bundled transcript MCP server. Made the entire `<spoken>`-block protection chain dead in src/: `SAFETY_RULES` instructed the model how to treat `<spoken>` blocks that no longer exist; `wrap_spoken` built those blocks but had no callers; `_neutralize_close` + `_ZWSP` existed solely to harden wrap_spoken's output. Removed all four plus the seven-line safety-rationale comment block. The `_system_prompt` attribute and three call sites that read it are gone — calls now pass `system=""` directly, which claude_cli's compose path on line 419-421 filters out of `rule_parts`, so an empty system is a no-op there (and would be the same for any future provider following the LLMProvider API). Kept `_sanitize_speaker` since `intro()` still uses it for participant-name scrubbing. Test changes: dropped `test_wrap_spoken_sanitizes_speaker` entirely; updated `test_ask_no_tools_calls_provider_once` to assert `kwargs["system"] == ""` instead of `== SAFETY_RULES`. Module + test docstrings refreshed. Net −38 LOC src + −22 LOC tests.

4. **`e827677` — `google_signin.py` chrome_path dedup.** Flagged out-of-scope but worth doing during the S203 google_signin audit cell: the literal `"/Applications/Google Chrome.app/Contents/MacOS/Google Chrome"` at line 196 duplicated `chrome_preflight.CHROME_PATH` (line 26 of chrome_preflight.py). The comment block immediately above the literal even referenced `str(CHROME_PATH)` by name as the canonical reference, but the actual call site re-typed the path. Replaced with a top-of-file `from chrome_preflight import CHROME_PATH` import and `executable_path=str(CHROME_PATH)` at the launch site. Single source of truth.

**C2/C3/C5 dispositioning.** Read each remaining 🟡 catalog item and concluded:

- **C2 (MCP subprocess death over an hour)** — out of operator scope. Operator only writes the per-spawn `mcp.json`; inner-claude spawns and manages all MCP subprocesses. A dying MCP server surfaces as a tool-call error to inner-claude, which narrates back. No operator-layer plumbing to add.

- **C3 (OAuth token mid-meeting expiry)** — three surfaces, none warrant operator code: (1) hosted MCP OAuth via mcp-remote in `~/.mcp-auth/` — mcp-remote owns refresh; failed refresh surfaces as a tool error. (2) Google session for the Meet UI in `slip_profile/` (slip mode) and `browser_profile/` (dial mode) — once admitted to the call, Google doesn't kick you out for token expiry; expiry bites at next meeting join only. UX papercut for v1, runbook item for Pass 8. (3) `auth_state.json` recovery seed — only consulted at meeting join by the linux adapter's recovery ladder. User pushed back hard on my initial dismissal — sharpened the answer when checking that slip mode does own its own Google session via the persistent `slip_profile/` (first-run user signs in manually, cookies persist), but mid-meeting blast radius is still nil for the active call.

- **C5 (audio helper 1-hour behavior)** — no unbounded growth in static read (buffers drain per utterance, mlx-whisper-base is memory-mapped fixed state, hallucination filter creates per-call GC-able objects). Two findings stay deferred: (1) **No restart-on-death of the Swift audio helper** — comment at `attach_adapter.py:864` explicitly defers it. Mid-meeting Swift crash → audio captioning permanently dead, user has to leave + rejoin. Same shape as C1's deferred reconnect-and-resume; not a v1 fix. (2) **`utterance_audio +=` O(N²) byte-string concatenation** — already flagged S200 as cosmetic (~6.4MB redundant copies per 10s utterance, dwarfed by mlx-whisper compute on modern Mac).

**Three uncommitted user-authored fixes live in the working tree from a parallel live slip session:**

- **`attach_adapter.py` self-heal for CDP-reuse zombie Chrome.** When a previous slip session detached cleanly (slip leaves Chrome alive by design) and the user later closed the last slip window, on macOS Chrome stays alive in the menu bar with **zero browser contexts**. CDP socket still listens on 9222; `_cdp_endpoint_alive()` says yes; `_cdp_belongs_to_slip()` says yes (the `--user-data-dir=$HOME/.operator/slip_profile` flag is still in argv); reuse path takes it; Playwright's `connect_over_cdp` calls `Browser.setDownloadBehavior` and gets back "Browser context management is not supported." Fix: track whether reuse path was taken; if `connect_over_cdp` raises and reuse path was taken, evict the zombie Chrome via existing `_evict_other_chrome_on_cdp_port()`, settle 0.5s, relaunch via `_launch_slip_chrome`, retry connect once. Only retry on the reuse path — connect failure on a freshly-launched path is a real OS-level problem that should surface, not be papered over.

- **`chat_runner.py` auto-leave when participant count drops to 0.** Previously only fired when count==1 after `_saw_others=True` — meaning if Meet booted the bot back to the landing page (lobby idle timeout, host declined admission and the request expired, network drop re-routed the tab) the chat loop would poll forever because `_saw_others` stayed False (bot was alone in the lobby) and the original branch only fires on count==1. New branch covers count==0 regardless of `_saw_others`, with a different log line and `ui.warn("Lost the meeting — dropping out.")` so the user sees a distinct message vs the "everyone left" path. The grace window (`ALONE_EXIT_GRACE_SECONDS`) absorbs transient 0s during reconnect/state changes. Also added an `else: self._alone_since = None` reset so the lobby-wait case (count==1, `_saw_others==False`) doesn't accidentally accumulate alone-timer state.

- **`agent-context.md` Hard-Won Knowledge entry** documenting the zombie Chrome CDP issue — preserved in this docs sweep; not overwriting.

User asked me to leave these uncommitted at end-session for them to commit themselves.

**Open carryovers (deliberately deferred, not blocking S205):**

Same shape as the S199-S202 deletions of `run_signin_step`, `read_user_mcp_config`, dead config constants — but bigger blast radius if we delete the test files (drops 11+11+13 test classes that pass vacuously today).

- **`openai` + `anthropic` Python deps in pyproject.toml + requirements.txt** — gated on the second-provider scope call. If a second LLM provider is in v1 scope they stay; if not they go in the same commit as cleaning up any remaining vestigial provider machinery.

- **Cross-file caption-text-in-INFO-log finding** across three files (transcript.py + audio.py + captions_js.py). Needs cross-file logging-policy review for PII risk in `/tmp/operator.log`. Not a small cleanup — multi-file decision about what level captions log at.

- **Magic-string `kind` values** across five files (no central enum; typo on `session_start` comparison silently breaks LLM session scoping). Multi-file refactor.

- **No tests for the S199 heartbeat watchdog.** Nice-to-have; runtime path is exercised in production but not unit-tested.

- **At-next-join Google session expiry papercut** — runbook item for Pass 8, captured here so it doesn't get lost.

**Exact next step (session 206):** user lands the three uncommitted live-session fixes (attach_adapter zombie Chrome recovery + chat_runner count==0 auto-leave + the Hard-Won Knowledge entry), then either continues endurance reads on remaining 🟢 catalog items, pivots to standalone workflow passes (Pass 1 install dry-run on a fresh Mac is highest-leverage; Pass 7 dep pinning; Pass 8 runbook including the OAuth re-auth + Google session expiry papercuts), or takes the install_preflight/readiness orphan product call. `/ultrareview` + `/security-review` (Passes 5+6) remain gated on slip captions per memory.

## Prior Status (preserved)

**Session 204 (May 6, 2026) — 1-hour-meeting endurance audit + closed deferred llm.py product call.** Started a new audit axis (resource/time behavior in long meetings, distinct from the pre-launch static-cleanup audit). Produced a 20-row suspect catalog across five failure-mode buckets: unbounded growth (transcript dict, tool-loop scratchpad, seen-IDs, log files), time drift (poll loops, silence-gap, heartbeat watchdog), stale handles (CDP, MCP pipes, OAuth tokens), retries, and participant flapping. Top three 🔴 candidates diagnosed in detail:

1. **A3 (`claude_cli._stderr_buf`)** — daemon thread `extend()`-s every byte of subprocess stderr into a plain list for the entire meeting; only ever read as `[-20:]` for error diagnostics. Simple `deque(maxlen=N)` swap. Not yet fixed — flagged for a follow-up commit.

2. **A4 (`_tail_messages` + full-file tail) — RESOLVED.** Two coupled bugs in one shape: (a) `MeetingRecord.tail()` re-read the entire JSONL + JSON-parsed every line on every LLM call → growing latency over an hour-long meeting with captions on; (b) the user surfaced the bigger insight that captions were being prompt-stuffed even though the transcript MCP server already exposes them on demand → architectural duplication, plus chat-history was being crowded out of the 40-slot budget by ambient talk. Chose option (b) "keep tail but chat-only" over total deletion: chat carries a UI continuity expectation captions don't (people reference ambient talk explicitly when they want it). Fix landed in commit `6b20483`: dropped captions from `_tail_messages`, added a `deque(maxlen=200)` chat tail in `MeetingRecord` populated by `append()`, new `tail_chat(n)` method serves it without I/O. JSONL on disk and `tail()` for generic queries unchanged. 19/19 tests green. Closes the long-deferred `pipeline/llm.py` product decision (`docs/pre-launch-audit.md` line 161).

3. **C1 (post-join CDP staleness)** — `macos_adapter.is_connected()` checks an internal `_browser_closed` flag, not actual CDP/page health. After Mac sleep / 30s network blip, the flag stays unset while chat read/captures are dead → bot enters "looks alive but isn't" zombie state. attach_adapter does the right probe. Downgraded from 🔴 to 🟡 — fix is detection-only (probe `page.is_closed()` + `context.browser.is_connected()`); reconnect-and-resume is a bigger feature. Not yet fixed.

**S204 dead-code carry-forward:** `wrap_spoken` / `_neutralize_close` / `SAFETY_RULES` in `llm.py` are now dead in src/ post-`6b20483` (still tested in `test_wrap_spoken_sanitizes_speaker`). One-commit cleanup whenever the user wants.

**Independent of S204 product decision:** the S203 question about whether `openai` + `anthropic` Python deps stay or go is **still open** — they were paired with the llm.py decision in S203's narrative, but they're independent. The deps decision turns on "is a second LLM provider in v1 scope?", not on how chat history is plumbed.

**Exact next step (session 205):** A3 fix (claude_cli stderr deque swap) — ~1 LOC change, then a quick read of the remaining 🟡 endurance-audit items (C2 MCP pipe death, C3 OAuth token expiry mid-meeting, C4 Google session expiry mid-meeting, C5 audio helper 1hr behavior). Or pivot to the standalone workflow passes from `docs/pre-launch-audit.md` (install dry-run on a fresh Mac is the highest-leverage one — Pass 1, the #1 launch-day failure mode). Or address the S203 phantom-feature product calls (install_preflight + readiness preflight orphans, ~600 LOC of test coverage of unreachable code).

**`/end-session` lesson saved to memory** (`feedback_no_git_acrobatics.md`): when asked to split coupled changes into separate commits, don't do revert+reapply manual disentangling — use `git add -p` or push back on the split request and explain why a combined commit communicates the design move better.

**Session 203 (May 6, 2026) — Pre-launch audit Tier 3 closed (12/12 cells complete) running in parallel with S202's Tier 2 work. Eleven S203 audit-cell commits landed in atomic per-cell shape; two cells closed REVIEW-only awaiting product call (`install_preflight.py`, `readiness.py`'s preflight orphan); ~−470 LOC src, ~−403 LOC tests across the session. Apple Dev cert still pending; 14.20.5 still gated on it.**

**Eleven S203 commits land this session, all using the plain-language / 🟡🟢 / disposition-emoji finding format:**

1. **`62a9da8` — oauth_cache.py.** Real bug fix: `mcp_remote_cache_dir()` was using `sorted(...)[-1]` to pick the latest `~/.mcp-auth/mcp-remote-X.Y.Z/` directory. As strings, `mcp-remote-0.1.10 < mcp-remote-0.1.9` (digit-boundary inversion) — a user with both an older `0.1.4` cache and the current `0.1.38` cache would have `0.1.4` selected. Real false-positive shape: `oauth_cache_exists` reports True off the stale dir, mcp-remote@0.1.38 reads from its own dir, finds nothing, hangs at OAuth popup at meeting join. Switched to mtime-based pick — currently-installed mcp-remote writes to its own dir, so its mtime is freshest. Robust to any version naming (semver, prerelease tags). Also dropped dead `mcp_client` references from module + function docstrings (mcp_client.py was deleted in 14.19.11; today only `readiness.py` is a caller).

2. **`b458e58` — chrome_preflight.py.** Refreshed module docstring to match session-163 reality. Was claiming "Both the wizard sign-in step (`pipeline/google_signin.py`) and the macOS adapter (`connectors/macos_adapter.py`) hard-code the system Chrome binary because Chrome profiles aren't compatible across binaries." Both halves are out of date: `macos_adapter` switched to Playwright's bundled Chromium in S163 (the bundle-ID singleton bug fix), and that same session disproved the profile-incompat claim. Today's reality: real Chrome is still required because (1) `google_signin.py` hardcodes it for Google's signin flow, and (2) `attach_adapter.py` CDP-attaches to it for slip mode. The `require_chrome_or_exit` call from `MacOSAdapter.join()` is defense-in-depth against future code paths bypassing `__main__`. No code change.

3. **`5fe1198` — ui.py.** Dropped dead `chat_in()` + `chat_out()` narrators (zero callers anywhere in src/ or tests/). Looked like a partially-implemented "echo every chat message to stderr" mode that never got wired up — runtime uses `ui.ok(f"Replied — ...")` for outbound and doesn't echo inbound (Meet's chat panel already shows it). Removed the now-unused `cyan` and `blue` color entries too. −13 LOC.

4. **`8f1f167` — claude_code_import.py.** Module-wide slim-down. `read_user_mcp_config()` + `user_config_path()` + `_USER_CONFIG_CANDIDATES` were dead in production — module + test docstrings claimed they were "Used by claude_cli to translate operator's `disabledMcpjsonServers` overlay back to JSON-keyed names" but `claude_cli.py:_maybe_write_mcp_config` writes a fresh per-spawn `mcp.json` with just the transcript server, never reads `~/.claude.json`. Today only `claude_code_installed_and_logged_in()` is alive (used by `_run_bot` + `_run_slip`). Deleted the orphans, deleted `tests/test_claude_code_import.py` whose four tests targeted the now-removed function (the live wrapper is exercised in `test_1574_readiness.py`). Module name is now historical — flagged in the docstring. −161 LOC.

5. **`e487380` — _disclaimed_spawn.py.** Latent fd leak fix: if the second `os.pipe()` call (stdout_r/stdout_w) hit the fd limit and raised `OSError`, the first pipe (stdin_r/stdin_w) was never closed — leaks two fds per failure. Real failure rate is low (only fires near per-process fd limit) but the fix is a trivial try/except that closes the first pipe on the rare second-pipe failure and re-raises. Bonus cleanups: dropped unused `import io` + `import errno` (latter only mentioned in a docstring), dropped a docstring claim about `context-mgr exit` for `__enter__`/`__exit__` that don't exist (only caller doesn't use `with`).

6. **`1bf4527` — doctor.py.** Two doc-staleness / slop fixes (no behavior change). (1) `_check_chromium()` had a local `import sys` that was already imported at module top; redundant. (2) Module docstring claimed "Phase 14.20 will add a Screen & System Audio Recording check when slip caption capture ships" — those TCC checks are already at lines 182-238 (landed in 14.20.4). Refreshed to describe today's reality. Also fixed `CheckResult` field list in the docstring — was `(name, status, fix)` but the dataclass actually has four fields (`name, ok, detail, fix`).

7. **`1d6d44e` — linux_adapter.py.** Parity-with-S201 cleanups against the secondary-platform adapter. (1) `import re as _re` was running every 500ms iteration of the meeting-holding while loop (~7,200/hr for a 1-hour meeting) — same hot-loop import S201 cleaned in macos_adapter. Hoisted `re` to module top, dropped the `_re` alias, updated two call sites. (2) Chmod scaffolding in `_ensure_chat_open` (debug screenshot) and `_browser_session` (user_data_dir) — same trust-the-OS pattern S201 cleaned across macos_adapter / attach_adapter / session.py. Chmod stays load-bearing (`mode=` doesn't fire on existing dirs); only the wrappers go.

8. **`9362c25` — pyproject.toml + requirements.txt.** Three pinned Python deps with zero imports anywhere (left over from earlier phases): `readchar==4.2.2` (was for the wizard's arrow-key picker), `ruamel.yaml>=0.18.0` (was for the wizard's round-trip YAML edits), `soundfile==0.13.1` (audio I/O the pipeline ended up not needing — numpy + mlx_whisper handle frames directly). Removed all three from both files. **Kept** `openai==2.29.0` and `anthropic==0.94.0` despite zero src/ imports — same product call gates them as the vestigial `_tail_messages` / `_build_messages` in `llm.py`: if a second provider is in v1 scope they stay, if dropped they go in the same commit as the llm.py cleanup. Refreshed stale wizard comments on `rich` and `pyyaml` lines.

9. **`51faf04` — agents/{claude,codex}/ + tests/test_bundled_mcps_bootable_static.py.** The `src/_1_800_operator/agents/{claude,codex}/` directories were empty (only stale `__pycache__/` artifacts from a removed prior version's `framework.py` / `__init__.py`). Per commit `e7ccadf` (14.19.7-C "delete bundled agent presets, bundled skills, ensure-helpers"), the bundled-preset scheme was intentionally removed in the chat-first pivot; today's runtime uses user-scoped `~/.operator/agents/claude/config.yaml` exclusively. Zero git-tracked files in the tree. Removed via `rm -rf`. Also deleted `tests/test_bundled_mcps_bootable_static.py` (242 LOC) which globbed `agents/*/config.yaml` (zero hits today) and `custom_template.yaml` (file doesn't exist) — all three test functions passed vacuously. Trimmed a stale 4-line pyproject comment about hatch bundling agent presets that don't exist (referencing nonexistent "pm, engineer, designer"). −242 LOC.

10. **`9d4fe40` — google_signin.py (re-audit after parallel S202 path canonicalization).** Three follow-on cleanups against the S202-canonicalized state. (1) Trust-the-OS: dropped two inner `try/except OSError: log.warning` wrappers around `os.chmod(0o600)` on auth_state.json and google_account.json. Files are written under the `os.umask(0o077)` set by `__main__.main()`, so chmod is belt-and-suspenders for existing-file overwrites; the wrapper was dead defense. Outer try/except around storage_state / write_text stays — Playwright + disk write are real failure modes. (2) Hoisted `import os as _os` out of `_write_artifacts` to module-top imports as plain `import os`. (3) Refreshed the session 178 / T1.11 docstring comment — said "wizard sign-in uses real Google Chrome explicitly" but the wizard's `run_signin_step` entry was deleted in S202 `da6dcb8`; `_launch_signin_flow` is now invoked only via `operator login claude`. Tightened to "this flow uses real Google Chrome explicitly."

11. **`6e307bb` — readiness.py (re-audit after parallel S202 config canonicalization).** Dropped duplicate `load_dotenv` call. Pre-S202, readiness inlined `load_dotenv(...)` because the wizard constraint prevented `from _1_800_operator import config`. Post-S202 (commit `da6dcb8`) the module imports config directly, and `config.py` already calls `load_dotenv` at its own module load — so by the time readiness's line was running, the env was already populated. Dead duplication. Dropped the call, the `from dotenv import load_dotenv` import, the now-unused `from pathlib import Path`, and the override=False explanation comment. Kept `from _1_800_operator import config` with `noqa: F401` so the import chain that triggers config's load_dotenv is explicit.

**Two cells closed REVIEW-only (no commit, awaiting product call):**

- **`install_preflight.py`** — `run_install_preflight()` is the docstring-promised entry for "the top of `operator setup`" but there's no `operator setup` subcommand in `__main__.py`. The `uv tool install` install path is genuinely broken today: a user bypassing `install.sh` lands on `operator dial` with chromium missing and gets an opaque Playwright error. The `chromium_installed` helper IS used (by `doctor.py`) so it stays regardless. Decision needed: (a) add `operator setup` subcommand wired to the orchestrator, (b) auto-invoke at top of `dial`/`slip`/`login` (silent when ready), (c) document curl|sh as the only path + delete orphans, (d) keep as scaffolding.
- **`readiness.py`'s preflight orphan** — `preflight_mcp_readiness()` + `report_mcp_readiness()` have zero src/ callers outside the orphan-internal chain. The preflight docstring describes "Runs inside `_run_bot()` after `OPERATOR_BOT` is set..." but `_run_bot` doesn't wire it in. Same phantom-feature pattern. **Latent landmine**: `from _1_800_operator.pipeline.auth import run_auth` at line 245 — `pipeline/auth.py` doesn't exist. Tests pass a mock `run_auth_fn` so the import never fires; if the orphan is ever wired in or a non-test caller invokes without the mock, ImportError. References to `operator auth <name>` at lines 167 + 288 also point at a non-existent CLI subcommand. ~600 LOC of test coverage of unreachable code (`test_1574_readiness.py`, `test_15745_preflight.py`).

## Prior Status (preserved)

**Session 201 (May 6, 2026) — Pre-launch audit Tier 1 closed (11/11 cells complete). Connector trio audited (session.py, attach_adapter.py, macos_adapter.py) plus the deferred claude_cli cell resolved when its two carry-forward findings turned out to be already addressed by other cells. Four commits, ~13 findings landed. Apple Dev cert still pending; 14.20.5 still gated on it.**

**Four commits land this session, all using the plain-language / 🟡🟢 / disposition-emoji finding format:**

1. **`d992052` — session.py.** Added `ps -p PID -o comm=` verification before SIGTERMing the saved operator PID in `_chrome_kill_and_clear`. macOS recycles PIDs aggressively, so a stale `.operator.pid` from a crashed prior run could otherwise get `--force`'d into killing an unrelated user process (browser, IDE). Scoped to the `.operator.pid` path only since Chrome's SingletonLock self-cleans on exit (its stale-lock window is far narrower; comment in code explains the asymmetry). Bonus cleanups: deleted four `try/except OSError: pass` wrappers around `os.chmod` calls in `save_debug` (trust-the-OS pattern from S200 cells 5+7 — chmod on a file we just created as the running user can't fail), and refreshed the module docstring to mention `_chrome_kill_and_clear` (single-instance / `--force`) and `save_debug`, both previously absent.

2. **`8dc8b62` — connector cell A (cross-adapter promotion + slip hardening).** Promoted `_is_real_meet_room` + `_MEET_ROOM_RE` from `macos_adapter` into `session.py`. The original code had a self-acknowledged "temporary smell — if a third adapter ever needs this, promote to session.py" comment; attach_adapter being the second adapter using it was the threshold the comment named for promotion. Both adapters now import from session; macos_adapter sheds its now-dead `re` and `urlparse` imports. Other attach_adapter cleanups bundled in the same commit: dropped chmod try/except around the debug-screenshot fallback in `_ensure_chat_open` (same trust-the-OS pattern); added belt-and-suspenders `os.chmod(SLIP_PROFILE_DIR, 0o700)` after `makedirs` since `mode=` doesn't tighten existing dirs (Google session cookies in slip profile shouldn't be world-readable on shared hosts); wrapped `stderr_sink = open("/tmp/operator.log", "ab")` in a `with` block in `_start_audio_pipeline` so the parent fd closes after `spawn_disclaimed`'s dup2; tightened `_cdp_belongs_to_slip` from a plain `SLIP_PROFILE_DIR in stdout` substring match to `f"--user-data-dir={SLIP_PROFILE_DIR}" in stdout` to eliminate false-positive against sibling profile paths like `~/.operator/slip_profile_backup`.

3. **`9e07751` — macos_adapter.py.** Hot-loop hygiene: `import re as _re` was running every 500ms tick of the meeting-holding loop (~7,200/hr for a 1-hour meeting). `sys.modules` cache makes each one cheap so no measurable runtime cost — but it was noise in the hot path. Hoisted `import re` to module top, dropped the `_re` alias which existed only to fit the local-import shape. Dead-attribute deletion: `self._seen_message_ids = set()` initialized in `__init__` but never read or written anywhere in this file. Left over from before the JS MutationObserver + `data-message-id` snapshot dedup path; `linux_adapter` still uses the name legitimately. Trust-the-OS cleanups (consistent with prior cells): dropped `try/except OSError` around chmod 0o600 on debug screenshot in `_ensure_chat_open`, and around chmod 0o700 on `BROWSER_PROFILE` (the chmod itself stays — `mode=` doesn't fire on existing dirs — only the wrapper was dead). Narrowed the outer-finally `os.remove(pid_file)` catch from `OSError` to `FileNotFoundError` since that's the only legitimate failure mode; permission errors on a file we own would be unexpected and shouldn't be silently swallowed.

4. **`bbd25fd` — claude_cli.py.** The two deferred findings carried from S199 + llm.py audits are already resolved by other cells: heartbeat wedge detection landed in S199 commit `b0d0d65` (`HEARTBEAT_SILENCE_SECONDS = 60` at line 60, `_check_heartbeat` at lines 750-764, called from both event loops), and `ContextOverflowError` was deleted entirely in S200 commit `8e64bd2`. Audit doc still listed both as open; updated to mark resolved. **Latent leak fix:** when ClaudeCLIProvider is wired with captions/transcript MCP but without a permission_handler, `_maybe_write_mcp_config` creates a standalone `_mcp_only_tempdir`, but `_teardown_permission_bridge` had an early-return guard on `_perm_tempdir is None` so the mcp-only tempdir's cleanup at the end of the function was never reached in this configuration. Today's wiring always sets a permission_handler (ChatRunner does it), so the path doesn't fire in production — but it's a real leak for any future code path that wires the provider without one. Restructured so the mcp-only cleanup runs first, before the bridge-state early return. Bonus cleanups: dropped two `try/except Exception: pass` wrappers around `shutil.rmtree(..., ignore_errors=True)` (`ignore_errors=True` is documented to never raise, so the outer try/except is dead defense); explicit `__init__` initialization for `_mcp_only_tempdir` for consistency with sibling state attrs.

**Tier-1 progress:** 11/11 cells done (chat_runner ✅ S199, llm ✅ S199, claude_cli ✅ S201, providers/base ✅ S200, meeting_record ✅ S200, confirmation ✅ S200, transcript ✅ S200, audio ✅ S200, session ✅ S201, attach_adapter ✅ S201, macos_adapter ✅ S201). **Tier 1 closed.** Tier 2 progress: 3/9 cells already done in parallel S202 commits — `446dfde` (`bridges/claude.py` cell A: purged dead `spawn_argv()` + `transcript_mcp_spec()` + unused REPLY_PREFIX_DIAL/DEPLOY; -56 LOC), `36f37c7` (`config.py` cell B: purged four pre-14.19.7 dead constants `TOOL_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` + `DEFAULT_TOOL_TIMEOUTS` + `TOOL_RESULT_MAX_CHARS` + `LLM_STUCK_THRESHOLD_SECONDS`; -25 LOC), and `permission_bridge.py` reviewed CLEAN (no commit — defensive-shim contract intentionally catches every failure mode; broad `except Exception` is the spec, not slop). ## Prior Status (preserved)

**Session 199 (May 6, 2026) — Pre-launch audit underway. Three Tier-1 cells complete (chat_runner.py, llm.py, claude_cli.py), 9 to go. Net ~1,000 LOC of dead code purged, plus the wedge watchdog landed. Apple Dev cert still pending (no movement this session); 14.20.5 still gated on it.**

**Three commits land this session:**

1. **`0ac3a6a` — chat_runner.py audit cell.** Findings fixed: narration prompts no longer leak SDK exception bodies into the LLM context (only the exception class name reaches the model). The 196-line `_loop` is now a 35-line orchestrator delegating to four focused helpers (`_seed_loop_state`, `_advance_intro_state`, `_check_participant_state`, `_process_messages`); per-loop state promoted to instance attrs. New `_safe_leave()` wraps `connector.leave()` in error paths so Playwright tear-down failures don't compound primary errors. Stale `kind="confirmation"` paragraph dropped from `_send` docstring (described a scrapped templated-card design). Redundant `text_stripped` reassignment removed.

2. **`091a348` — llm.py audit cell + cascading dead-code purge** (-921 LOC across source + tests). Sanitized participant display names before they hit the `intro` prompt — same `_sanitize_speaker` helper that already protects caption rows. Deleted `LLMClient.ask_stream` (no callers anywhere), `LLMClient.send_tool_result` (was the manual tool-loop driver for direct OpenAI/Anthropic providers; replaced by claude_cli's internal loop), `extra_system` parameter, the `tool_call` return branch in `ask` (claude_cli never surfaces tool_calls at this layer), the `_scratch` instance state, `wrap_tool_result` + `_sanitize_tool_name` + `_TOOL_NAME_RE`. Updated `SAFETY_RULES` to drop the now-irrelevant `<tool_result>` clause. Deleted `pipeline/guardrails.py` outright (zero callers post-pivot). Trimmed `tests/test_llm_client.py`, deleted `tests/test_guardrails.py` and `tests/test_913_tool_history_collapse.py` (were testing the deleted machinery).

3. **`b0d0d65` — claude_cli.py audit cell.** Big one. Added **heartbeat-based wedge watchdog** (`HEARTBEAT_SILENCE_SECONDS = 60`): tracks `last_event_ts` + `tool_in_flight` per turn. If subprocess silent > 60s AND no tool currently in flight → raise `ClaudeCLIProtocolError` early so chat_runner's narrate-failure path can recover in ~1 minute instead of waiting the 600s ceiling. `tool_in_flight` flips True on `tool_use` blocks in assistant events, False on top-level text deltas + `tool_result` blocks in user events (which the loop now handles — was previously silently dropped). Fixed bridge-tempdir leak when Popen fails: the OSError handler now calls `_teardown_permission_bridge` before re-raising. Extracted `_check_heartbeat`, `_dispatch_assistant_blocks`, `_user_event_carries_tool_result` as shared helpers used by both event loops — dedupes the watchdog logic and the content-block walking. Purged the unreachable `ContextOverflowError` chain end-to-end: removed the catch in `llm.py`, the `_max_messages` instance field, the field's mutation logic, the `kind == "context_overflow"` branch in `chat_runner._dispatch_result`, the misleading "I've cleared the history" chat message, and the test that exercised the dead halving path. The exception class itself stays in `providers/base.py` for now (other audit cells can decide its fate).

Component list regenerated against the current tree. Standalone workflows (install dry-run, /ultrareview, /security-review, dep pinning, runbook) preserved at the bottom. The `pipeline/providers/claude_cli.py` finding section in the doc carries deferred items from prior cells (heartbeat, characterize claude's overflow signaling, vestigial machinery) — all now resolved by `b0d0d65`.

User signed up for Apple Dev Program mid-session — productized signing path is ready to land the moment certs come through.**

**14.20.4 — slip-mode local STT online.** Three discrete wins this session:

1. **Wire-up (committed `d05c514`, pushed).** Re-added `mlx-whisper==0.4.3`/`numpy==2.4.3`/`soundfile==0.13.1` deps. New `src/_1_800_operator/pipeline/audio.py` (152 LOC) — slip-only `AudioProcessor`, mlx-whisper-base-only branch, VAD constants + 0.5s pre-pad carried verbatim from voice-preserved, `is_speaking` echo guard + debug WAV dump dropped. `attach_adapter.py` (+273 LOC) — `_resolve_audio_helper`, `set_caption_callback` (mirrors macos_adapter contract), `_start_audio_pipeline` spawns helper + reader + two utterance threads, `_stop_audio_pipeline` ladder (capturing=False → stop_event → stdin close → SIGTERM → SIGKILL). `_run_slip` writes captions DIRECTLY to `MeetingRecord.append(speaker, text, kind="caption", ts)` — bypasses `TranscriptFinalizer` because whisper output is already finalized; routing through TF would double-buffer + risk coalescing same-speaker utterances inside its 0.7s silence window. install.sh new step 8: swiftc the helper + ad-hoc codesign with `--identifier com.operator.audio-capture` (stable id is load-bearing; without it, every rebuild invalidates TCC). 24/24 tests green.

2. **Audio-bug archaeology + fixes.** Three sub-fixes that turn up live:
   - **Empty-buffer counter bug**: `SystemAudioOutput.stream` was incrementing `systemStats.callbacks` AFTER `guard n > 0 else { return }`. SCK fires audio callbacks at the configured rate even during silence (with empty / no data buffer). Counter never advanced → 10s watchdog FATAL'd on quiet system. Fix: `systemStats.callbacks += 1` at the very top, before any guard. Voice-preserved did this exact thing.
   - **Cursor responsibility-chain**: from Cursor's terminal, `posix_spawn` attributes the helper's responsible process to Cursor (`com.todesktop.230313mzl4w4u92` → `/Applications/Cursor.app`). TCC keys the SCK gate against the responsible process; Cursor's grant is satisfying preflight (`CGPreflightScreenCaptureAccess` returns true) but SCK itself silently denies. Fix: new `pipeline/_disclaimed_spawn.py` ctypes wrapper that uses `responsibility_spawnattrs_setdisclaim(&attrs, 1)` to make the helper its own responsible process. AttachAdapter spawns through this instead of `subprocess.Popen`. From Cursor's terminal post-disclaim: mic + whisper + caption fired end-to-end (`CAPTION [user] 'Next test!!!'` confirmed in live smoke). Files & Folders TCC prompt fires on first run because the binary lives under `~/Desktop/` — user clicks Allow on it + SR + Mic dialogs (3 total).
   - **Soft system-silent watchdog**: was `[S]==0 cb at 10s → exit(4)` which tore the whole helper down (also killing mic). Now logs WARN, helper continues, mic keeps flowing. SCK can self-recover later in the session if it fires. Mic-silent at 10s remains FATAL (exit 5) — that's a real bug we always want to surface. Helper gained periodic stats (`stats t=2s [S]=N cb / NB [M]=N cb / NB`, every 2s through 12s) for time-series visibility.
   - **`excludesCurrentProcessAudio = false`**: changed from `true` to match voice-preserved's working config exactly. Disclaim shifts what "current process" means to SCK; `true` was filtering more than we wanted in some intermittent SCK startup races.

3. **System-audio diagnosis (deferred to 14.20.5).** Even with disclaim + codesign + manual System Settings drag + `tccutil reset ScreenCapture`, system-audio callbacks never fire from this Mac in this Cursor-launched setup. Time-series proof: `[S]=0cb/0B` for 10 full seconds, every run. The hard-won knowledge from voice-preserved cracked it: **"ScreenCaptureKit requires `.app` bundle on macOS — silently fails from plain Python script"** (see `voice-preserved:docs/agent-context.md`). Voice-preserved made it work by wrapping the entire Python orchestrator in a `rumps`-based `.app` — they had `app.py` running as `/Applications/Operator.app`, and the helper was spawned by that .app. We're spawning from plain CLI Python, which is the failure mode they explicitly documented.

**Apple Dev path (locked, awaiting approval).** User enrolled in the Apple Developer Program mid-session ($99/yr, 1-2 day wait). Productization path is documented at `docs/apple-dev-setup.md` — enrollment, two signing identities, bundle-ID reservation, `.app` bundle structure with `NSScreenCaptureUsageDescription`, hardened-runtime codesign, notarytool submission. With Developer-ID + `.app` + entitlements, TCC keys against a stable identity that survives reboots, rebuilds, app updates, and `tccutil reset`. That's the productized end state. The Swift helper itself becomes the `.app` bundle (not the whole orchestrator); the CLI workflow stays a CLI.

## Prior Status (preserved)

**Session 197 (May 5, 2026) — Phase 14.20.2 + 14.20.3 SHIPPED. Slip's audio capture pipeline and its doctor visibility are both in place; only the Python-side wiring (14.20.4) and live-test (14.20.5) remain before slip captions match dial captions.**

**Why we jumped 14.19.9-11.** S196 handoff queued 14.19.9 (install.sh sendoff polish) → 14.19.10 (fresh-Mac live-test) → 14.19.11 (docs refresh + `mcp_client.py` deletion) before 14.20.2-5. User asked about slip transcript access mid-session, surfaced that 14.20 is the launch-blocking unknown. Tradeoff: 14.19.9-11 are small polish (~3h total), 14.20.2-5 are the meaty unknowns (~13h, blocks launch). With the spike fresh from S193 it was the right session to crack the audio helper. 14.19.9-11 all carry forward as post-launch polish — none gate launch.

**14.20.2 — Swift dual-stream binary.** `src/_1_800_operator/swift/operator-audio-capture.swift` (288 LOC). Captures system audio via `SCStream` + mic via `AVAudioEngine.inputNode` in a single process; converts mic from hardware format (48kHz 1ch on this Mac) to target (Float32 mono 16kHz) via `AVAudioConverter`; serializes both queues' frame writes through a shared `NSLock`-protected `writeFrame` so framing can never interleave. Stdout protocol: `[1-byte tag 'S' (0x53) | 'M' (0x4D)][4-byte BE u32 payload length][N bytes Float32 LE PCM]`. Per-stream 10s no-callback watchdog detects the TCC silent-failure mode DECISION.md flagged. TCC preflight for both Screen Recording (`CGPreflightScreenCaptureAccess`) and Microphone (`AVCaptureDevice.authorizationStatus(for: .audio)` → request → fail-fast on denied). Lifecycle: stops on stdin EOF (parent process death) or SIGINT.

**Single-binary vs two-procs.** DECISION.md left both on the table; I picked single-binary despite "two procs simpler to reason about." Reason: TCC keys grants on the binary's cdhash. Two binaries means user has to grant twice (once for each cdhash) and maintain two grants. One binary = one cdhash, two grants against the same identity in two different TCC services. Materially better install/permissions UX, and the framing protocol that single-binary needs cost ~10 LOC.

**Smoke-test results (S197 in-tree, ad-hoc-signed).** Compile: clean (`swiftc -O`, exit 0, 88KB binary). Mic stream: 105 callbacks in 12s, ~6.4KB per chunk, RMS ~0.025 during `say` (real signal). Decoder consumed 105 frames with zero short-reads or alignment drift — framing protocol works. System stream: zero callbacks. Watchdog fired at exactly 10s with the predicted diagnostic message. **This is the binary working correctly** — it's the empirical replay of the 14.20.1 spike's silent-failure mode. The SCK code path is byte-identical in shape to voice-preserved's production `audio_capture.swift` (which works in prod). Live SCK validation requires Developer-ID code-signing to stop TCC re-prompting on every rebuild; deferred to release-time per `project_apple_dev_account_deferred.md`. End-to-end SCK confirmation belongs in 14.20.5.

**14.20.3 — doctor TCC checks.** Two new `CheckResult`s in `pipeline/doctor.py`, both gated on `sys.platform == "darwin"` since slip is mac-only. The probe path: TCC.db is SIP-protected on read (DECISION.md §2 — even sqlite3 as owner returns "authorization denied," and `tccutil` only supports `reset`, no `read`). The only supported alternative is to ask the system from inside a binary about *its own* grants. So the Swift helper got a `--probe` flag that runs `CGPreflightScreenCaptureAccess()` + `AVCaptureDevice.authorizationStatus(for: .audio)`, prints `{"screen_recording":"ok|denied","microphone":"ok|denied|restricted|not_determined"}` JSON to stdout, and exits 0 — never prompts. Doctor invokes the helper with `--probe`, parses JSON, renders `CheckResult` with status detail and a fix line pointing at the exact System Settings pane (`System Settings → Privacy & Security → Screen Recording → enable for your terminal app, then quit and relaunch it`).

**Helper locator.** `_audio_helper()` in doctor.py prefers `~/.operator/bin/operator-audio-capture` (production target — install.sh will compile here in 14.20.4) and falls back to `src/_1_800_operator/swift/operator-audio-capture` (dev — what `swiftc` produces in-tree). Returns `None` when neither exists; doctor renders a "audio helper not built — re-run install.sh" failure with the upstream-shared cause flagged on the Microphone row.

**Cosmetic.** `run_doctor()` no longer prints empty `fix:` lines when a failure has no actionable command (the Microphone row depends on the upstream Screen Recording cause and shouldn't duplicate the fix command). Pre-existing pattern; one-line tightening.

**.gitignore.** Added `src/_1_800_operator/swift/operator-audio-capture` so the compiled binary doesn't get tracked. The source `.swift` ships with the package via hatchling's default non-`.py` inclusion (`pyproject.toml:60` documents this).

**Smoke tests passed:**
- `swiftc operator-audio-capture.swift -O -o operator-audio-capture` compiles clean.
- `./operator-audio-capture --probe` prints valid JSON in <100ms with both grants reported as `ok` on this Mac.
- 12s capture run produces 105 mic frames + watchdog-fired system message. Framing decoded by `debug/14_20_audio_spike/decode_frames.py` (untracked spike utility) with zero protocol errors.
- `python -m _1_800_operator doctor` renders both new check rows green (happy path).
- Negative path (binary moved aside): doctor renders failed Screen Recording with actionable fix + Microphone deferred to upstream (no duplicate fix line).

**Exact next step (session 198): Phase 14.20.4 — wire helper into AttachAdapter + MeetingRecord.** Real session-sized work:
1. Add `mlx-whisper`, `numpy`, `soundfile` back to `pyproject.toml` (all dropped post-14.19.7 — they were voice-preserved-only deps).
2. Port a simplified `AudioProcessor` from `voice-preserved:pipeline/audio.py` — keep VAD (`UTTERANCE_SILENCE_RMS=0.02`, `UTTERANCE_SILENCE_THRESHOLD=2`, `UTTERANCE_MAX_DURATION=10`), keep the 0.5s pre-pad in `transcribe()` (whisper drops first word without it), keep mlx-whisper-base path. Drop the TTS echo-guard machinery (`is_speaking`) — slip is chat-only, no TTS.
3. Two `AudioProcessor` instances in `AttachAdapter` — one fed by `[S]` frames (speaker="other"), one fed by `[M]` frames (speaker="user"). Each runs its own utterance loop on its own thread.
4. Spawn the helper as `subprocess.Popen([helper_path], stdin=PIPE, stdout=PIPE, stderr=...)` in `AttachAdapter.join()` after CDP connection. Reader thread parses framed stdout, dispatches PCM to the right `AudioProcessor`. Keep stdin held open for the lifetime of the meeting; closing it triggers the helper's clean shutdown.
5. When an `AudioProcessor` finalizes an utterance, call `MeetingRecord.append_caption(speaker, text, timestamp)` — same JSONL shape `captions_js.py` produces, so `mcp_servers/transcript_server.py` reads slip captions identically to dial.
6. Smoke-test mic-only path end-to-end (skip system-stream live confirmation since SCK is gated on Developer-ID signing); verify slip caption JSONL line shape matches dial.

**install.sh build wiring** rolls into 14.20.4 since both touch the helper-path resolution logic. After `uv tool install`, install.sh resolves the package's swift/ dir via `python -c "import _1_800_operator; print(_1_800_operator.__file__)"`, runs `swiftc <pkgpath>/swift/operator-audio-capture.swift -O -o ~/.operator/bin/operator-audio-capture`, marks executable. macOS-only branch; Linux skips silently (slip is mac-only).

**14.20.5 (live-test)** stays gated on Developer-ID code-signing → release time. With ad-hoc signature, every `swiftc` rebuild produces a new cdhash and re-prompts TCC; can't reliably validate the SCK callback path until the binary has a stable identity.

**Open questions / blockers:**

## Prior Status (preserved)

**Session 196 (May 5, 2026) — Phase 14.19.8 SHIPPED in one commit (`a30537a`). The sterile templated `Run? tool: args\nOK?` permission card is gone. Inner-claude now authors the permission UX in the streaming reply path; the bridge gates writes silently and waits for the user's chat reply. Tiered reads/writes + recent-yes auto-approve + YOLO override layered on top.**

**Implementation summary.** Three production-side changes plus one stale-comment fix.

1. **`src/_1_800_operator/pipeline/providers/claude_cli.py`** — added `_PRE_TOOL_VOICE_RULE` (the load-bearing tool-UX rule) and `_PRE_TOOL_VOICE_RULE_YOLO_OVERRIDE` (appended after the main rule when `OPERATOR_YOLO=1`). The main rule splits into two tiers: READ tier (verbs `get_/list_/search_/find_/read_`, plus built-in `Read/Grep/Glob/LS/WebSearch/ToolSearch`) → declarative narration, no question; WRITE tier (`Write/Edit/Bash/Task/WebFetch` + verbs `create_/update_/delete_/save_/send_/post_/run_`) → one-sentence question ending in `?`, ALWAYS a question (even if user gave an explicit command — declarative would leave nothing on screen for the user to reply to). The rule is voice-agnostic — it explicitly tells the model "do NOT default to 'Want me to...' or 'Pulling...' — those are shape examples, not required phrasings; match whatever voice your `system_prompt` established (caveman, pirate, etc.)." YOLO override flattens WRITE → READ tier (declarative, no question) since the framework's gate is bypassed and a question would mislead the user. Both rules are composed onto `--append-system-prompt` in `_spawn()` at the single injection point, alongside the agent's `system_prompt` and the transcript backstop.

2. **`src/_1_800_operator/pipeline/permission_chat_handler.py`** — `_round_trip` no longer posts a templated card. The model's pre-tool narration (the question) lands in chat via the streaming `on_paragraph` path BEFORE the bridge fires; `_round_trip` just blocks waiting for the user's next chat message. Added the **recent-yes auto-approve** before `_await_reply`: if the user's most recent chat message is `_is_yes()` and within `RECENT_YES_WINDOW_SECONDS = 30`, the gate auto-allows and marks the message id consumed (so chained tool calls within the same turn fall through to the normal await path — one yes, one tool). Reads `_latest_user_msg` and `_approval_msg_ids_used` from the runner.

3. **`src/_1_800_operator/pipeline/chat_runner.py`** — added `_latest_user_msg: tuple[id, text, monotonic_ts] | None` and `_approval_msg_ids_used: set[str]` slots; populated `_latest_user_msg` in the new-message path of the polling loop. `_wire_permissions` now branches on `OPERATOR_YOLO`: gated mode wires `auto_approve` with `ToolSearch`, built-in reads, and MCP read globs (`*__get_*`, `*__list_*`, `*__search_*`, `*__find_*`, `*__read_*`, `*__whoami`); YOLO mode wires `auto_approve = ["*"]` belt-and-suspenders alongside `--dangerously-skip-permissions`.

4. **Stale comment fixed in `claude_cli._spawn`.** The 14.19.2 comment claimed `--dangerously-skip-permissions` bypasses PreToolUse hooks at the CLI level, making the bridge plumbing inert under YOLO. Live-confirmed in S196 it does NOT — the handler still fires under YOLO (line 646 of `/tmp/operator.log` from the live test showed `auto-approve 'ToolSearch'` firing with the flag set). The flag overrides denials but doesn't suppress the hook itself. Comment now says so; `chat_runner._wire_permissions` adds the `*` auto_approve list under YOLO so the handler always returns allow regardless.

**Spike data.** `debug/permission_mcp_spike/cli_probe_09_ask.py` answered the load-bearing unknown for mech 1: when our PreToolUse hook returns `permissionDecision: "ask"` headlessly, claude-CLI doesn't abort or hang — it injects the reason into the model as a `tool_result` `is_error=True` and the model narrates it through the normal reply stream ("The write was blocked with: '...'"). Plumbing-viable but the model's "blocked with:" prefix is system-y and tool can't be resumed in place. `cli_probe_10_pre_tool_voice.py` ran 3 trials (Write / Read / Bash) and got 3/3 reliable pre-tool voice from system-prompt steering. Findings written up at `debug/permission_mcp_spike/SPIKE_14_19_8_PERMISSION_VOICE.md`.

**Live test trajectory.** Four Meet sessions across the implementation:
- **First (gated, with original card):** baseline — confirmed sterile prompt was annoying.
- **Second (gated, mech-1.5 first cut):** caught Failure 2 — model invoked tool with no preceding text after a "yes" reply, bridge silently waited forever for an approval the user already gave. Fix A (recent-yes auto-approve) shipped.
- **Third (gated, tiered reads/writes shipped):** caught the model emitting declarative for an explicit Write command (`"I'll write the marker file as requested."`) — strengthened the WRITE rule with "ALWAYS a question, even when user gave explicit command + reasoning explanation." Worked.
- **Fourth (YOLO):** zero permission prompts. `Create Linear issue → list_teams auto-approved → declarative narration → save_issue auto-approved → "Done — PRO-109"`. The one remaining question was a *real* clarification ("Two teams: Product and Engineering — neither fits a chore — want me to file under one anyway, or skip?") which is correct behavior.

**Test coverage.** 5 new tests in `tests/test_permission_chat_handler.py` lock the recent-yes contract: `test_recent_yes_auto_approves_without_chat_round_trip`, `test_recent_yes_consumed_so_chained_gate_falls_through`, `test_recent_yes_outside_window_does_not_auto_approve`, `test_recent_non_yes_does_not_auto_approve`, plus updates to the existing `test_chat_round_trip_*` tests to reflect that the handler is silent now. 1 new test in `tests/test_claude_cli_provider.py`: `test_yolo_mode_writes_narrate_declaratively` confirms the YOLO override flattens writes to declarative form. **All 21 tests pass.**

**Exact next step (session 197): Phase 14.19.9 — `install.sh` sendoff/welcome refresh.** Today's install script doesn't mention the `--yolo` bypass or the `~/.claude/settings.json` overlay path that power users would set up to auto-allow specific tools. Plan ~45min. **Mid-F regression caught and fixed.** Initial F over-deleted by ripping `_wire_track_a_permissions` AND deleting `permission_chat_handler.py` + `confirmation.py`. The handoff said "claude owns its permissions hierarchy via `~/.claude/settings.json` + the existing PreToolUse hook in `claude_cli.py`" — I read that as "no operator-side bridge needed." Wrong. The user's `~/.claude/settings.json` only allows `Bash(...)` + `Read(...)` rules, nothing for MCP tools (`mcp__transcript__*`, `mcp__linear__*`). With `claude -p` having no tty for an interactive prompt, every transcript and Linear tool call silently denied — model invented an explanation ("the permission prompt got denied"). User caught it on the smoke. **Restored** `permission_chat_handler.py` + `confirmation.py` from HEAD via `git checkout HEAD -- <file>`. Added 25-line `_wire_permissions` to chat_runner with hardcoded empty `auto_approve` / `always_ask` lists (v1 ships ask-on-every-tool; `--yolo` bypasses via `--dangerously-skip-permissions`). Restored `kind="confirmation"` in `_send` so confirmation prompts get audited but invisible to LLM replay. Live-proven across 7+ tool round-trips (ToolSearch + transcript list/search) approved via chat. **Lesson: documented procedure outranks ambiguous prose.** When the handoff describes architecture that doesn't match what the code currently does, default to "what does the code currently do" + verify by reading, not "what the handoff says it should do." This regression cost ~30min of debug + restore.

Locked in `bridges/claude.py:REPLY_PREFIX_SLIP`. The strip-on-read in `attach_adapter.read_chat` keys on `self._reply_prefix` at runtime so the change auto-propagated; only two illustrative docstring comments needed updating.

Then we pivoted to caption work. The user surfaced research about Granola's audio capture architecture (mic via AVFoundation + system audio via ScreenCaptureKit/CoreAudioTaps). With slip Chrome being a separate minimizable window (S192's pivot), the "DOM captions ruin the magic" objection collapses but doesn't disappear — Granola-class clean transcripts via system-level audio capture remain materially better. **Phase 14.20 promoted from Post-MVP to launch-blocker:** new top-level phase `Phase 14.20: Slip caption capture — Swift + ScreenCaptureKit + Whisper`, sequenced after 14.19.6 and before 14.19.10, marked `BLOCKS LAUNCH`. Five sub-steps (~17h budget): spike → Swift helper binary → macOS permission UX → AttachAdapter wiring → live-test.

**14.20.1 spike** (background subagent, `debug/14_20_audio_spike/{spike_capture.swift,STT_COMPARISON.md,DECISION.md}`):
- **STT engine locked**: mlx-whisper-base. Already a dependency on `voice-preserved` branch, measured at 110ms inference for 3s audio on M-series — total e2e budget pencils to ~1.7s, inside the 2s target. whisper.cpp stays as an optional `STT_PROVIDER` knob via the existing provider-neutral seam.
- **Architecture locked**: two parallel pipelines (system + mic), each with its own AudioProcessor/VAD, tagged `[mic]` vs `[system]` at source. Single transcript downstream. Carries forward the 0.7s VAD silence gap from voice-preserved, including the 0.5s pre-pad gotcha that whisper needs to not drop the first word.
- **Two empirical risk confirmations from running the spike binary live:**
  1. **TCC silent-failure mode is real, not theoretical** — `CGPreflightScreenCaptureAccess()` returned `true`, `SCStream.startCapture()` succeeded, zero `didOutputSampleBuffer` callbacks fired during 8s of `say` audio. So Risk #1 (10s no-callback watchdog) is now mandatory for 14.20.2, not nice-to-have.
  2. **Ad-hoc-signed binaries are TCC-attribution-cursed** — every `swiftc` recompile produces a new cdhash, every cdhash is a new TCC subject, every new subject means a re-prompt or silent denial. So Risk #2 (Developer-ID code-signing) is a *day-one* requirement for 14.20.2, not polish. Helper binary must ship pre-signed in the operator package; `swiftc`-on-the-fly is dev-only.

  Note on Risk #1 framing: the original "macOS lies to you about a perfectly-granted permission" framing was stronger than evidence supports. What we actually observed is more accurately "preflight returns a misleading positive when no real grant attaches to the binary's responsible-process attribution chain." Once a Developer-ID-signed helper has been properly granted, frames will likely flow normally. Keep the watchdog as cheap insurance against documented edge cases (Sequoia weekly re-prompt, TCC daemon cache staleness, helper-bundle drift across macOS updates), not as defense against constant deceit.

**14.19.7 mass deletion at 5/8** — chunked surgically into 8 sub-steps so each commit is independently smoke-tested green:

- **Step A** (`0b7ad5a`, -238 LOC, S193): wizard CLI surface from `__main__`.
- **Step B** (`ae04a8e`, -2908 LOC, S193): wizard files (`pipeline/setup.py`, `build_card.py`, `picker.py`, `face.py`, `connectors/terminal.py`, `custom_template.yaml`, `__main__._sync_claude_imports`).
- **Step C** (`e7ccadf`, -1090 LOC, S193): bundled `agents/{claude,codex}/` and `skills/`.
- **Step D** (`b64feab`, +140 / -1,198, S194): `config.py` rewrite + `__main__` cleanup + `build_provider()` collapse — covered above.
- **Step E** (`2703c4c`, -1,154, S194): cascade-delete `pipeline/skills.py`, `pipeline/codex_import.py`, `pipeline/providers/openai.py`, `pipeline/providers/anthropic.py`.

**Exact next step (session 196): Phase 14.19.8 — chat-surfaced `permission_request` flow.** Today's bridge posts a sterile auto-generated prompt (`Run mcp__linear__list_issues (linear)? OK?`). 14.19.8 hands authorship to the LLM so the prompt arrives in the bot's voice ("Want me to dig into the open Linear issues?"). Mechanism: rather than the PreToolUse hook returning allow/deny directly, it returns `ask` with a synthesized chat message authored by the model from the tool name + args. Or: separate the permission prompt from the bot's reply stream — bot proposes the action in its own voice in the reply, the bridge then asks for confirmation against the proposal. Decision deferred to S196 implementation start. After 14.19.8: 14.19.9 (install.sh sendoff/welcome refresh — needs to mention the `--yolo` bypass + the `~/.claude/settings.json` overlay path), 14.19.10 (full 14.19.x ladder live-test on a fresh Mac end-to-end — install.sh → login → doctor → dial → multi-tool turn), 14.19.11 (docs refresh — CLAUDE.md test list already reflects survivors, but the architecture section still references skills/MCP_SERVERS/wizard schema). Then the heavy 14.20.2-5 (Swift helper build + macOS permissions UX + AttachAdapter wiring + live-test) before launch.

**Open questions / blockers:**
- Apple Developer account for 14.20.2 — user explicitly deferred this S194 to release-time (saved as `project_apple_dev_account_deferred.md`). Reframed: it's a release-time blocker, not a 14.20.2-day-one blocker. During 14.20.2 dev, ad-hoc signing works fine (cost: TCC re-prompts every recompile). Surface again before any public release that includes the audio helper.
- TCC permission UX in `doctor` — still pending for 14.20.3.
- `mcp_client.py` is dead in production (no MCPClient instance anywhere — `chat_runner` constructor lost the `mcp_client` arg, all call sites stopped passing one). Module still on disk because `claude_cli.py` imports `read_user_mcp_config` from `claude_code_import.py` for the `disabledMcpjsonServers` settings hook... actually wait, F removed that overlay. Re-audit needed: is `mcp_client.py` itself completely unreferenced now? If so, it should be deleted in a follow-up alongside its remaining `inject_*` helpers in `llm.py` (also dead — no caller). Estimated ~700 LOC of additional cleanup in a future "14.19.7-I" or rolled into 14.19.11 docs refresh.
- The session-188 known issue (operator-spawned MCP subprocesses inherit cwd from the user's invocation dir, NOT a sandbox; could be a problem if a malicious config tries `command: "/bin/sh"` with `args: [...]`). Not a regression, but worth flagging for 14.19.8 review since chat-surfaced permission flow makes the user complicit in tool launches.

## Prior Status (preserved)

**Session 192 (May 5, 2026) — Phase 14.19.1, 14.19.2, 14.19.3 implementation + STRATEGIC PIVOT to separate-profile slip model after discovering Chrome 121+ silently disables `--remote-debugging-port` for the user's logged-in default profile. Slip works end-to-end as a "decide before joining" tool with a dedicated Chrome window. ~20 commits on main, none pushed yet.**

The session started executing the bridge architecture cutover and ran into a wall mid-Phase 14.19.3: the original "claude attaches to your existing Chrome tab" vision is technically impossible on modern Chrome. Chromium issue 40066423 — security mitigation against malware harvesting OAuth tokens via DevTools — silently disables CDP debug port binding when launched against the user's default (logged-in) profile. The flag is accepted into argv, observable in `pgrep`/`ps`, but Chrome refuses to bind the TCP listener. Verified via diagnostic spike on Chrome 147.0.7727.138.

**The pivot (commit `8b7f9d1`):** slip launches a SEPARATE Chrome window with operator's own profile dir at `~/.operator/slip_profile/`. This sidesteps the restriction (Chromium only blocks the default profile). The separate-profile Chrome reliably exposes 9222. User-visible consequence: slip is now "decide BEFORE joining"; if the user is already in a meeting in their main Chrome and decides they want claude, they cannot add claude to that existing tab. They must close their main-Chrome tab and rejoin via slip.

**The user explicitly accepted this constraint for v1** ("no extension. this is fine for v1."). The only architectural path that would re-enable mid-meeting handoff is a Chrome extension (different distribution, different permission model, ~1-2 weeks of work). Reserved as Post-MVP.

**Slip's locked v1 semantics:**
- `operator slip claude <meet-url>` opens a dedicated Chrome window (operator-owned profile)
- First run: user signs into Google in slip Chrome once; profile persists
- claude joins as the user's identity (room sees one participant); replies prefixed with `🤖 ` to distinguish bot vs. user typing
- **Quiet mode**: no intro, no "Hold for Claude…" filler, ALWAYS requires `@claude` trigger (no 1-on-1 bypass) — slip is "speak when spoken to"
- Other Chromes on port 9222 silently SIGTERM'd before slip launches its own
- On Ctrl+C: claude detaches; slip Chrome stays running so the meeting continues

**Functional gaps deliberately deferred to Post-MVP** (documented in roadmap):
1. **No caption capture in slip** — AttachAdapter has zero caption path. Dial/deploy still capture via existing DOM observer. Slip Chrome is visible to user, so DOM captions would show on screen — either accept (with "minimize the window" UX hint) or build the cancelled Swift+Whisper STT pipeline. Pick after some user testing of (a).
2. **First-run sign-in friction** — slip drops user on Google sign-in inside slip Chrome window, no friendly preflight.
3. **Mid-meeting handoff** — architecturally impossible without extension.
4. **Default URL handler** — registering operator as macOS default for meet.google.com would route Meet links to slip automatically, eliminating pre-planning.

**Cancelled mid-session:** the planned 14.19.3c.2-c.6 Swift audio capture + Whisper STT pipeline (~10h scope) became moot once the slip-Chrome-is-a-separate-window pivot landed. With slip Chrome minimizable, captions can be enabled visibly without ruining the user's main browser experience — DOM captions cover the use case at zero implementation cost. Spike artifacts kept as historical record at `debug/resume_spike/`.

**Two new feedback memories saved this session:**
- `feedback_substantiate_design_deviations.md` — when proposing a deviation from existing design, substantiate with concrete reasoning, not vague cleanliness claims. Earned after I proposed a Bridge dataclass with a flag that lived on the wrong axis.
- Audit lesson (encoded inline): when writing connector-adjacent code, read `connectors/session.py` first. Shared infrastructure usually already covers the case (JoinStatus, save_debug, Meet-URL regex). Caught after I wrote AttachAdapter from scratch without consulting battle-tested helpers.

**Exact next step (session 193):** Live-test slip in a REAL meeting with another participant. The latest commit (`3321a1c`, quiet mode + prefix strip) changed slip's behavior meaningfully and only had one earlier live test against the older code. Validate: no intro fires, ambient chat from another participant doesn't trigger claude, `@claude` invocation works, no self-reply cascade, `🤖 ` prefix renders correctly. If green → push 20 commits to origin/main and tag, then proceed to 14.19.4 (`operator login claude`) or directly to 14.19.7 (mass deletion of wizard-era code, half the codebase).

**S192 git state:** ~20 commits on `main`. Nothing pushed to origin or public yet. Local tag `phase-14.18-frozen` from session start (pre-pivot reference). Should add `slip-cdp-v1-foundation` on HEAD before pushing. Untracked: `debug/resume_spike/` (historical), `docs/pre-launch-audit.md` (S187, defer until 14.19.7).

## Prior Status (preserved)

**Session 191 (May 5, 2026) — Strategic pivot session. No code changes. Major roadmap restructure: bridge architecture cutover queued as Phase 14.19, custom-bot work deferred to Post-MVP "Operator Studio", Claude Code Plugin vision locked in Post-MVP as Shape E (terminal replacement for Operator users).**

This was a conversation-and-roadmap session, not an implementation session. Started from S190's just-shipped install path A, pivoted to broader pre-launch product questions, then arrived at a major v0.0.1 scope reduction.

**The core decision:** Cut the entire custom-bot construction surface from v0.0.1. Operator stops being "a meeting-bot platform" (a category nobody currently shops for) and becomes "the way to bring the Claude you already trust into your Google Meet" (a category that maps to a real, immediate desire). The wizard, the agent presets (`pm`/`engineer`/`designer`), the `system_prompt` composition layer, the multi-agent dispatch — all of it asks users to evaluate a bot Operator constructed before they've decided they trust AI presence in meetings at all. That's a backwards trust ladder. The bridge model inverts it.

**The new product surface (Phase 14.19, ~22h, blocks launch):**
- Three commands: **`slip`** (CDP-attach to user's Chrome, Claude responds as user with marker), **`dial`** (fresh Meet with Claude as separate participant, private), **`deploy`** (Claude joins user's existing meeting with real participants). Each rung escalates commitment.
- Two purpose-built setup commands: **`operator login claude`** (Google sign-in for bot account, dial/deploy only — single-purpose, NOT a wizard), **`operator doctor`** (diagnostic checker analogous to `brew doctor`).
- `--yolo` flag on slip/dial/deploy — passes through claude's `--dangerously-skip-permissions`. Default = ask-mode (claude prompts per-tool, Operator surfaces in Meet chat).
- **v0.0.1 = claude only.** Codex + Gemini are explicit fast-follows. The S188 codex parity work re-homes under v0.0.2.
- **Zero user-facing config files.** No `.env`, no `config.yaml`. All hardcoded code constants in `bridges/claude.py`. Persistent state files only (`auth_state.json`, `browser_profile/`, `history/`, `debug/`).
- Reply attribution in slip mode: robot emoji `🤖 ` prefix as leading default; final pick after side-by-side mockup of 3 candidates (brackets / robot / italics).
- Trigger phrase: `@claude` hardcoded.
- READ_TOOLS allowlist deleted — permission policy fully delegated to claude.

**Mass deletions queued (Phase 14.19 step 7):** `setup_wizard.py`, `edit.py`, `agents/{pm,engineer,designer,codex}/`, `OPERATOR_BOT` env routing, agent/llm/mcp_servers/skills/system_prompt config schema, `_sync_claude_imports`, `READ_TOOLS` + auto-approve branch in `chat_runner.py`, `load_dotenv` calls + every `.env` reference, `intro_on_join`, `first_contact_hint`, `tagline`. Conservatively half the codebase.

**Operator Studio (Post-MVP)** captures the deferred wizard work — not as "wizard, but later" but as a fully-realized second product. Trigger criteria locked: 25% of v0.0.1 users on dial/deploy + multiple "can I make my own bot?" asks.

**Claude Code Plugin (Post-MVP)** locked as Shape E — terminal-replacement for Operator users. 8 slash commands (`/operator:slip`/`dial`/`deploy`/`login`/`doctor`/`status`/`tail`/`hangup`) that shell out to locally-installed `operator` binary; backgrounding via `nohup ... &` in SKILL.md, NOT via Operator-side flag. S187 + S190 spikes locked Shapes A–D as non-viable. Trigger: 2–4 weeks of real curl-install signal first. ~5h work post-launch.

**Spike findings (May 2026 plugin model):** Postinstall hooks still missing (Issue #11240 + #9394 both open). Plugin primitives now include `bin/` (executables on PATH while plugin enabled), `monitors/monitors.json` (long-running command stdout piped to Claude as notifications during session), `hooks/hooks.json` (event handlers like PostToolUse). None of these enable bootstrap-installing Operator or driving Chrome/Playwright from inside Claude. Shape E (slash commands + transcript MCP, plugin assumes Operator already installed) is the only viable plugin shape at present.

**`docs/scratchpad.md` created** as running pool for marketing copy, taglines, and verb-logic notes. Locked verbs: `slip → dial → deploy`. Considered and rejected: merge (git collision + no try-feel), channel (too metaphysical), patch (more about connecting than blending), tag (wrestling sub implies tag-out), pair (too software-coded). One-line product description leading candidate: "The Claude you already trust, but in your meeting."

**Exact next step (session 192):** Begin Phase 14.19 implementation. Recommended starting point: step 14.19.1 (create `bridges/claude.py` with hardcoded constants — spawn cmd, trigger phrase, reply prefix, transcript-MCP wiring). This is the foundation everything else replaces references to. Then step 14.19.2 (wire the three commands in `__main__.py` with JIT preflights and `--yolo` flag). Step 14.19.3 (CDP attach for slip mode in `connectors/attach_adapter.py`) is the meaty one — quit-Chrome-relaunch dance + reply-attribution prefix injection. Steps 14.19.7 (mass deletion) and 14.19.8 (permission flow rewrite) come once the new shape is functional.

**Open questions for session 192 start:**
- Reply prefix iteration (step 14.19.6) — the side-by-side mockup needs to happen in a real Meet to eye-check what reads cleanest. User picks; we hardcode. Don't lock the choice from a markdown file.
- The S190 carry-over warnings (`[claude] ⚠ MCP needs attention: ...` for hosted connectors) — likely become moot once `_sync_claude_imports` is deleted in step 14.19.7. Verify when that step lands.
- `docs/pre-launch-audit.md` (untracked, S187-era) — most passes (1–3, 5–8) survive the bridge cutover. Pass 4 (dead code) gets *easier* because we're deleting half the codebase first. Re-run audit *after* Phase 14.19 lands, not before.

**S191 git state:** One commit (`0870966`) on origin/main containing roadmap + scratchpad changes. Nothing pushed to public — this is dev-only planning work, no public-facing changes.
