## Prior Status (preserved)

**Session 190 (May 4, 2026) — Phase 14.8 install path A verified end-to-end on a fresh Mac. Thirteen fix commits across install.sh, wizard, dial, and macOS adapter — all driven by real QA observations, not pre-emptive cleanup.**

The session was structured as: user runs through every user-facing surface on a never-used MacBook, reports observations, I diagnose + fix + push to both `origin/main` (private dev) and `public/main` (1-800-operator/operator). End state: first successful `operator dial claude` on a fresh machine, redirecting from `meet.new` to a real meeting URL via the green-room flow.

Commits landed (origin → public, in order):
- `9cf88f2` / `ef23048` — install.sh: drop `--from "git+..."` for playwright, tweak closing instructions ("Then" → "Or", added `<meet-url>` form). *Reverted later this session — see below.*
- `999ab88` / `2d56e98` — flip curl one-liner from `| sh` to `| bash` everywhere (install.sh preamble, README hero + Option B, pypi-stub, e2e-qa-checklist).
- `20e4d00` / `d038128` — install.sh sendoff redesign: green ✓ + bold "operator successfully installed!" + Docs line + bold-magenta `Next:` line. The Next-line auto-prefixes `source ~/.local/bin/env &&` when `~/.local/bin` wasn't on PATH at script start (snapshotted as `INITIAL_PATH` before step 2 mutates PATH).
- `5978382` / `82bfa7d` — pyyaml as a direct dep. `config.py`, `pipeline/auth.py`, `pipeline/skills.py`, `pipeline/setup.py` all `import yaml` but neither pyproject.toml nor requirements.txt declared it. Worked in dev because pyyaml was getting pulled in transitively from somewhere; fresh `uv tool install` failed with `ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'yaml'`. ruamel.yaml stays for round-trip work.
- `b9d4391` / `a31bdc2` — Phase 14.8 batch 1: wizard step-1 polish (loop the picker not the heading, single-line warning, "then rerun `operator setup`" hint), readiness probe reasons trimmed of diagnostic noise (`exited non-zero` prefixes dropped), claude/codex taglines shortened, 4 bundled skills culled (codebase-walkthrough, design-review-feedback, live-bug-triage, migration-plan), CLAUDE.md stale-roster references cleaned up, `docs/e2e-qa-checklist.md` added, `docs/claude-use-cases.md` renumbered Top-10 → Top-7.
- `38278e4` / `b46297b` — wizard exits on prereq-gate failure instead of re-prompting. Re-prompting after the warning looked like a UI bug because the picker re-rendered below the warning even though the heading printed once. Fix is out-of-band anyway (install/login the CLI then rerun) so re-prompting was the wrong UX. `WizardCancel` grew an optional `silent=True` flag; top-level handler skips its generic "Cancelled." line when silent. Symmetric `operator edit claude` path collapsed to one line for consistency.
- `c923389` / `a31ea2d` — `load_skills` got a `quiet` kwarg. The wizard's MCPs step calls `load_skills` a second time (via `_required_mcps_from_skills`) to compute mcp-required server locks; that second load was re-emitting discovery warnings under the MCPs step heading where they looked misplaced. quiet=True suppresses discovery-level warnings but real parse errors still surface.
- `16307da` / `ebb827a` — install.sh playwright invocation reverted from `--from playwright` back to `--from "git+${REPO_URL}"`. The earlier change caused uv to resolve *latest* PyPI playwright (whatever that is at install time) and download the chromium build matching that version, but operator's pinned dep is `playwright==1.58.0`, so at meeting-launch time playwright 1.58 looked for chromium at a path the latest playwright hadn't written to: `Executable doesn't exist at .../chromium_headless_shell-1208/...`. Resolving via the operator git+url forces uv to use operator's full dep tree (pinned 1.58.0) and the matching chromium. Cosmetic uv warning returns; correct trade. Same commit also adds `→ run \`operator auth <slug>\`` hint to the dial-time MCP-needs-attention warning.
- `e71cc30` / `da90e03` — macOS adapter Chromium args extended with `--use-fake-device-for-media-stream`. Existing `--use-fake-ui-for-media-stream` only bypasses the in-page Meet permission prompt; macOS still gates Chromium's mic access at the OS level, prompting the user. Fake-device flag makes Chromium synthesize fake audio/video, OS never sees a request. Operator is chat-only; no real mic needed.
- `6be2a96` / `38aff6f` — dial preflight: hard-exit if `~/.operator/browser_profile/` is missing. New `chrome_preflight.require_signed_in_or_exit()` — checks the profile dir up front. Without sign-in, the headless Chromium has no Google session and meet.new redirects to a sign-in form the bot can't fill in, hanging 30s before failing with a misleading "did not redirect" timeout. Now exits 2 with a clear pointer to `operator setup`.
- `952af50` / `f2585dd` — `save_debug` call wired into the meet.new redirect-timeout path. Was bailing without saving any debug artifact, so `~/.operator/debug/` stayed empty when this failure mode hit. Now the screenshot + HTML get captured before bailing — the screenshot is the fastest path to root cause for "first dial after fresh install hangs at meet.new" failures.
- `699984b` / `61fe06d` — **the meet.new fix.** On a fresh persistent profile, meet.new sometimes sits on `meet.google.com/new` showing a "Do you want people to see and hear you in the meeting?" interstitial with a "Continue without microphone and camera" button — instead of redirecting straight to a real meeting URL. The adapter already had logic to dismiss that button, but it ran AFTER `wait_for_url(_is_real_meet_room)` succeeded — chicken-and-egg, since the URL was held at `/new` until the button was clicked. Replaced the single wait_for_url with a 30s poll watching for either (a) URL becoming a real meeting room, or (b) the button appearing — clicks it when it does, redirect completes.

**Public-push procedure:** all commits landed via the surgical worktree-push approach — `git fetch public main`, `git worktree add /tmp/operator-public-tmp public/main`, `cp <file>` from local to worktree, `git -C <worktree> commit + push public HEAD:main`, `git worktree remove`. No orphan-snapshot dance. Direct file mirror, surgical diffs, fast iteration. This is the pattern from session 189's mid-session pushes — significantly faster than full re-snapshots.

**Exact next step (session 191).** Two reasonable directions:

1. **Finish Phase 14.8 — remaining install paths + live-meeting test.** Path A is verified; paths B (`curl → less → bash`) and C (`uv tool install git+... + operator setup`) untested. The install_preflight module from S189 should make path C work cleanly, but it hasn't been exercised on a fresh machine. After that, the actual claude top-10 use-case live-test against a real Meet — that's the marathon. Phase 14.8 sub-bullets (d), (e), (f) are still ⬜ in the roadmap.

2. **Phase 16.1 README rewrite.** Per Phase 16.1 spec — hero positioning ("Claude Code in your Google Meet"), agents-gallery framing, demo-GIF placement, MCP compatibility notes, one annotated example config. The S189 README now documents three install paths cleanly but doesn't have the launch-tier polish.

The user closed session 190 with a successful first dial; the obvious "let's verify everything else" path is more 14.8 sub-items. README rewrite (16.1) is the bigger pre-launch lift but doesn't gate on more QA.

**Open carry-overs / known issues:**
- The dial-time `[claude] ⚠ MCP needs attention: ...` warnings still fire on the test Mac for hosted connectors. The hint text now points at `operator auth <slug>`, but it's unclear whether running that actually clears the warning (the warning's source is `claude mcp list`, which reads Claude Code's account state, not operator's mcp-remote bridge state). May be a deeper diagnostic-vs-actionable mismatch worth untangling. Not blocking — those connectors aren't tool-callable until authed but the dial proceeds.

**Session 189 (May 4, 2026) — Phase 15.11 (community + support infra) shipped + uv-only install path made first-class via new `install_preflight` module + repo flipped public + Cloudflare Pages live at `1-800-operator.com/install`.**

Three batches landed this session:

- **Batch 1 — Phase 15.11 community/support infra (commit `d674992`, public snapshot v3 `f694977`).** Issue templates (form-style `bug_report.yml` + `feature_request.yml`, `config.yml` with `blank_issues_enabled: false` + contact links), `SUPPORT.md` routing bugs/questions/security to right channels, README "Help & community" footer. Reproducible label scheme via `scripts/setup_labels.sh` — applied to repo, status + `area/*` labels created, four GitHub default labels removed (`documentation`, `good first issue`, `help wanted`, `invalid`). Discussions enabled via `gh api`; default categories cover Q&A / Show & tell / Ideas / General. Welcome post created as discussion #1 ("Welcome — what would you delegate to a meeting agent?") — pinning was UI-only (no `pinDiscussion` GraphQL mutation), user pinned manually. Smoke-test issue #2 filed via `gh issue create` with bug+needs-triage+area/installer labels — user verified template + labels + notification routing all work.

- **Batch 2 — install_preflight bridge (commit `3923948`, public snapshot v4 `f0ef723`).** New `src/_1_800_operator/pipeline/install_preflight.py` module bridges curl-installer and uv-only install paths so users skipping `curl | sh` get the same provisioning. Three idempotent checks fire at the top of `operator setup` and `operator edit <bot>`: (1) `seed_env_file()` writes `~/.operator/.env` mode 600 with the same commented placeholder content `install.sh` writes (no-op if file exists; never overwrites real keys); (2) `chromium_installed()` globs `PLAYWRIGHT_BROWSERS_PATH` (env-var override) or platform default (macOS `~/Library/Caches/ms-playwright`, Linux `~/.cache/ms-playwright`) for any `chromium-*` build; missing → prompts user, runs `python -m playwright install chromium` on consent (streams output, returns exit code); (3) macOS-only Chrome.app warning — soft now (was previously a hard exit at wizard entry via `require_chrome_or_exit()`; meeting-launch keeps the hard exit at `_run_macos:953`). 5 tests in `tests/test_install_preflight.py` all pass.
  - **Why this exists:** `install.sh` provisions Chromium + `.env` + Chrome.app warning before the user ever runs `operator setup`. Users on the `uv tool install git+...` path (skeptical of `curl | sh`) skipped all of that and would hit opaque Playwright crashes 30 steps into the wizard. This preflight is the bridge — Option C in the README is now self-sufficient.
  - **README rewrite:** new "Install" section with three options. **A** = `curl -fsSL https://1-800-operator.com/install | sh` (hero CTA); **B** = `curl -o install.sh; less install.sh; sh install.sh` (audit-then-run for the polite skeptic); **C** = `uv tool install git+https://github.com/1-800-operator/operator.git` + `operator setup` (no shell script from us — trust only `uv` + the GitHub repo). Pitch line corrected from "Install via pip" to "Install in one command."

- **Batch 3 — Cloudflare Pages live (no commit; dashboard work).** Repo flipped public via `gh repo edit ... --visibility public --accept-visibility-change-consequences`. Verified raw GitHub URLs return 200. Then user drove the Cloudflare Pages dashboard flow with my real-time guidance — first attempt accidentally created a Worker (Cloudflare's unified UI defaults to Workers); user deleted and re-created via the "Continue with GitHub" path (no Pages tab anymore — Workers and Pages are now unified). Build settings: framework=None, build command=empty, build output directory=`/`. Project URL: `operator-f4w.pages.dev`. Custom domain `1-800-operator.com` attached — DNS resolves to Cloudflare edge IPs (104.21.36.112 / 172.67.192.209), `curl -fsSL https://1-800-operator.com/install` returns 200 with `content-type: application/x-sh` and the actual `install.sh` body. The `/install` → `/install.sh` rewrite from `_redirects` works. Hero CTA in the README is now a real, working command.

- **Phase 15.11 fully closed across all 11 sub-steps.** Including the manual-action ones the original spec earmarked for the user: notification routing verified (15.11.8), private triage SLA reminder set (15.11.9), discussion #1 pinned (15.11.7 manual-action), smoke-test verification done (15.11.11). All checkboxes in `docs/roadmap.md` flipped from ⬜ to ✅; phase header changed from "← BLOCKS LAUNCH" to "✅ SHIPPED session 189".

## Prior Status (preserved)

**Session 188 (May 4, 2026) — Phase 14.18 shipped (`3ed5ff2`): transcript tool API beef-up + codex captions parity + 3 pre-existing bug fixes uncovered by autonomous pressure testing.**

- **Part A — claude transcript tools beef-up.** `recall_transcript` replaced by 3 new MCP verbs in `src/_1_800_operator/mcp_servers/transcript_server.py`: `search_captions(query, speaker?, start_minutes_ago?, end_minutes_ago?, context_lines=0, limit=20)` (case-insensitive substring search with optional ±N context, grep-style match prefix `> `), `list_captions(start_minutes_ago?, end_minutes_ago?, last_n?, speaker?, limit=100)` (chronological browse, time-window-around-X via start+end semantics), `list_speakers()` (counts + relative time-since-last-spoke). Server-enforced 12 KB byte ceiling via `_enforce_byte_ceiling` trims oldest first and prepends a truncation hint that steers the model to narrow filters. Marker-file resolution at `~/.operator/.current_meeting` with env-var fallback (claude uses env-var; codex uses marker — both resolve through same `_resolve_record_path`). System-prompt directives in `agents/claude/framework.py:31` and `claude_cli.py:~196` (defense-in-depth backstop, fires on `set_meeting_record_path`) point at the new verbs.

- **Part B — codex captions parity via shell + marker file (NOT MCP).** Direct MCP-handshake spike against `codex mcp-server` 0.128.0 confirmed the inner model does NOT see `-c`-registered child MCPs (it sees only `web`, `functions`, `multi_tool_use`). The transcript subprocess spawns but its tools are never surfaced to the model. So registering the bundled transcript MCP into codex via `-c` flags is dead-end. **The fix that actually shipped:** codex's inner model has shell access via `functions`, and read-class commands (`cat`/`grep`/`tail`/`jq`) are on its safe-allowlist (no escalation). The codex framework prompt at `agents/codex/framework.py` directs the model: "Only when a chat message is specifically about in-meeting dialogue, read the JSONL whose absolute path is in `~/.operator/.current_meeting`" — with example shell pipelines (`grep -i ... | jq -r 'select(.kind=="caption") | "[\(.sender)] \(.text)"'`). Verified end-to-end: codex correctly reads the marker, queries the JSONL, quotes captions verbatim with speaker attribution. The conditional ("only when... about in-meeting dialogue") was tested separately with non-caption queries (math, date, joke) and codex did NOT read the file.

- **Pressure-test matrix — 8/8 every cell.** Autonomous test rig at `debug/14_18_pressure/run_pressure_test.py` drives `operator try <bot>` via stdin pipe across realistic (30 caps, 15 min, 3 speakers) / heavy (1000 caps, 60 min, 5 speakers, 213 KB) / extreme (20K caps, 8 hr, 5 speakers, 4.15 MB) loads. Uses bot's stderr `✓ Replied — Xs` markers (chat_runner.py:683 `ui.ok`) as deterministic turn-end signals. Both claude and codex pass 8/8 across all 3 loads — claude via MCP, codex via shell. Pressure-test outputs preserved in `debug/14_18_pressure/outputs/*.json` for posterity.

- **Three pre-existing bugs uncovered + fixed.** (1) `claude_cli.py:342` referenced `operator.mcp_servers.transcript_server` but package is `_1_800_operator.mcp_servers.transcript_server` — broken since the Phase 14.5 package rename, meaning the bundled transcript MCP has been silently dead in production for ~3 sessions. (2) Transcript MCP tools were missing from `permissions.auto_approve` in `agents/claude/config.yaml` — every transcript call would have hit the user-confirmation prompt. Added `mcp__transcript__{search_captions,list_captions,list_speakers}`. (3) Race condition in `chat_runner._handle_message`'s pre-intro buffer: user messages persisted to meeting record at detection time (line 592) then intro persisted after, leaving JSONL with `user(Q1) → assistant(intro)` order. On Q1 drain, `_tail_messages` returned `messages[-1].role == 'assistant'` and `claude_cli`'s strict-last-must-be-user assertion rejected the call. Fix: defer `record.append` for buffered messages until drain time, after intro lands in the record. See Hard Won Knowledge for fuller writeup.

- **Marker-file lifecycle wiring shipped.** `__main__.py._wire_meeting_record` writes the active meeting path to `~/.operator/.current_meeting` on join (line ~1019); `_shutdown` deletes it on bot exit. Harmless even when codex isn't running (claude doesn't read the marker — uses env var); useful when codex is running (codex's shell pipeline reads it).

- **Asymmetric architecture by design.** Claude bot uses the typed MCP tools (schema-validated args, server-enforced byte ceiling, pre-formatted output with timestamps/speaker labels). Codex bot uses raw shell+JSONL (no schema, model composes pipelines). The asymmetry isn't accidental — it reflects each CLI's strengths: claude_cli has rich MCP plumbing and tool-description dispatch; codex's `mcp-server` mode gates child MCPs from the inner model but exposes shell. Same outcome (caption parity), different mechanism per bot. Documented at `agents/codex/config.yaml` header comment.

- **Carry-overs (still applicable from S182/S187).** Repo-flip + Cloudflare Pages walkthrough still pending (`gh repo edit ... --visibility public --accept-visibility-change-consequences` + dashboard steps + `curl|sh` second-Mac QA). Re-snapshot procedure for any ship-list file change. install.sh end-to-end unverified pending second-Mac QA. PyPI bump from v0.0.1 (post-launch). Tier-2 audit + ~70 appendix nits (post-launch). 5 test files needing in-file `OPERATOR_BOT` (post-launch). Phase 15.11 (community/support infrastructure — issue templates, Discussions, SUPPORT.md) is still uncommitted in `docs/roadmap.md` from a prior session — pre-launch task.

- **Exact next step (session 189).** With Phase 14.18 shipped, the launch-blocker stack is now: (1) Phase 15.11 (community/support infra) still queued in roadmap; (2) repo-flip + Cloudflare Pages walkthrough; (3) `curl|sh` second-Mac QA. Pick whichever the user prioritizes. Phase 14.18 itself is done — both bots have caption parity, all unit tests pass, both pressure-test 8/8, and the three pre-existing bugs are killed.

- **Closed-source pivot split.** Yesterday's full-pivot decision was reversed at session start: user wants the OSS product to ship first, with the closed-source v1 becoming a fast-follow rather than a replacement. Cloned this repo to `~/Desktop/operator-cloud/` carrying full git history through S185 (the seven pivot commits + `experiments/cloud-browser-spike/` + four pivot-era memory files mirrored to `-Users-jojo-Desktop-operator-cloud/memory/`). On this repo, reverted the seven pivot commits (`beff05b..5d6cd06`) via `git revert --no-commit` folded into a single `63d4934`. Result: `docs/agent-context.md`, `docs/handoff.md`, `docs/roadmap.md` are bit-identical to S182 state at `1292593` (modulo the new S187 entries layered on top in this commit). - **Phase 14.17 shipped — claude_cli `--resume` for crash recovery.** Replaced the synthesized-opener crash-recovery path (`pipeline/providers/claude_cli.py:_build_synthesized_opener`) with claude's native `--resume <session-id>` mechanism. Closes the deferred S166 carry-over: the prior recovery path only carried `(user_text, assistant_text)` pairs, so a recovered bot dropped tool calls and tool results and would hedge or hallucinate when asked about prior actions. With `--resume`, the new subprocess rehydrates from claude's local session store (`~/.claude/projects/<encoded-cwd>/<session-id>.jsonl`) with the full message history including tool use + tool results.

  - **Spike** at `debug/resume_spike/probe.py` (gitignored) confirmed `claude -p --resume <id> --input-format stream-json --output-format stream-json --include-partial-messages` composes end-to-end. Cache survives rehydration: stage 2 had `cache_read_input_tokens=30872` vs `cache_creation=314`, so resumed subprocess gets near-full prompt-cache hits.
  - **Implementation:** dropped `--no-session-persistence` from spawn (mutually exclusive with `--resume` per claude's help text); added `_session_id` field captured idempotently in `_validate_init_event`; spawn cmd appends `--resume <session_id>` when set. Deleted `_build_synthesized_opener` (~38 LOC) + `_turn_history` field + every `_turn_history.append` site. Net ~70 LOC removed.
  - **Tests:** new mock-based `test_restart_spawn_includes_resume_flag` pins the cmd shape (`--resume <id>` present, `--no-session-persistence` absent). Renamed live `test_subprocess_restart_with_resume` (was `_with_history_rebuild`) — existing assertion (turn 3 = "11" after subprocess kill) still passes via real `--resume` against live claude 2.1.126; added assertion that `_session_id` survives the restart unchanged. All 8 tests pass.
  - **README** "Privacy & logs" gained a "Resume your meeting in Claude Code" subsection — explains the on-disk session location, frames co-location with regular Claude Code sessions as a feature (user can `claude --resume` from the same dir afterwards to keep working with the same brain in their terminal), surfaces the picker-mixing UX with a "don't grab the wrong session" caveat. Out-of-scope agents (`pm`/`codex`/custom) explicitly noted as not using this path.

- **Phase 14.18 queued as launch-blocker — transcript tool API beef-up + codex captions parity.** User wants both bots at feature parity for launch this week. Investigation surfaced that the existing `recall_transcript` tool API is too thin for real long-meeting use: only `minutes_back` and `last_n`, no keyword filter, no time-window-around-X, no by-speaker, no length cap. So Phase 14.18 is sequenced **tool beef-up FIRST, then extend to codex** — codex inherits the better tool from day one rather than us shipping the thin one twice. Codex 0.128.0 supports `-c key=value` overrides on `mcp-server` (verified live: `codex mcp list -c 'mcp_servers.test_inject.command="..."'` registers the entry), so the S179 finding "mcp-server doesn't accept --mcp-config" is now obsolete. Mechanism for codex parity will be a marker-file approach (`~/.operator/.current_meeting`) — `transcript_server.py` reads the active meeting path from that file on each tool call, so the codex YAML can register the transcript MCP via fully-static `-c` flags with no per-meeting interpolation. Avoids `${VAR}`-substitution-in-args extension, avoids __main__ ordering refactor for meet.new mode, keeps claude's existing path working unchanged.

  - **Exact next step (session 188):** Phase 14.18 Part A — A1 (GitHub-MCP scoping spike for inspiration) → A2 (finalize new tool surface in conversation with user; user has approved renaming `recall_transcript` if a clearer verb emerges) → A3 (implement) → A4 (fixture-based unit tests) → A5 (live-test, claude bot, real Meet). Then Part B — B1 (marker file mechanism) → B2 (transcript_server reads from marker, env fallback for back-compat) → B3 (codex YAML `-c` flags) → B4 (drop captions-disabled disclaimer; `transcript.captions_enabled: true` default for codex) → B5 (live-test, codex, real Meet). Full sequencing + risk callouts in `docs/handoff.md` and in Phase 14.18 entry of `docs/roadmap.md`.

  - **Fixture survey done at end of S187:** real long-meeting JSONLs exist in `~/.operator/history/`. Best candidate `avd-axqi-obq.jsonl` (424 captions, 85 min span). Smaller candidates: `fkr-echg-mfw.jsonl` (98 caps, 63 min), `fsv-qbyd-amd.jsonl` (73 caps, 41 min). **Catch: every real history JSONL is single-speaker (Jojo Shapiro only).** For testing the by-speaker filter we'll need to synthesize a small multi-speaker fixture (~30 captions, 3 speakers, 15 min) at the top of S188 before tool implementation.

  - **Open risks for Phase 14.18:** TOML nested-key override compatibility (`mcp_servers.X.env.KEY=value`) verified for top-level keys but not nested env — ~30s verify before locking the codex YAML. Codex's transcript-MCP child needs to inherit operator's PYTHONPATH so `python -m _1_800_operator.mcp_servers.transcript_server` resolves under codex's spawn — likely default via env trickle-down, but confirm. Tool naming: user has approved renaming `recall_transcript` if a clearer verb emerges in A2 — coordinate with `claude_cli.py:~196` system-prompt directive backstop so the new verb name lands in the prompt nudge too.

## Prior Status (preserved)

**Session 182 (May 3, 2026) — Phase 14.13.1 + 14.5 ship; orphan-snapshot publish flow established; Cloudflare Pages walkthrough handed to user. Two commits on local main this session (`d646008`, `18e028f`). Three orphan snapshots force-pushed to public repo (v0 → v1 → v2). Repo flipped private at end of session as a pause-state.**

- **First-attempt mistake worth recording.** Initial sequence: `gh repo create 1-800-operator/operator --private --description "..."` → `git remote set-url origin git@github.com:1-800-operator/operator.git` → `git push -u origin main` (24 commits ahead at session start). User immediately deleted the repo because the full dev history was exposing files they did not want online (debug artifacts, internal docs, dev spike scripts). Required `gh auth refresh -h github.com -s delete_repo` because the default token scope from `gh auth login` is `repo` not `delete_repo` — useful diagnostic detail for any future history-rewrite or "burn this repo and start over" operation. Pivot decision: **never push raw dev history to the public repo** — push only a curated ship list via orphan branches.

- **Carry-over triage.** Held a structured triage of the 8 carry-overs from session 181 before doing any pushing. User clarified: PyPI bump + Pages attachment + codex R8 caption parity + outbound MCP sync + audit nits + S177 nits + the 5 in-file `OPERATOR_BOT` test files all stay on the post-launch slate; item 8 (~27 historical `operator run` → `operator dial` references in roadmap blockquotes) explicitly removed from the carry-over list per user — preserved as historical record of how the rename landed.

- **Decision: stay on `uv tool install git+URL` for v1 (PyPI deferred to post-MVP).** User asked whether `pip install` was rejected as the install path. Confirmed yes via `docs/agent-context.md` line 815 (Phase 14.5 spec) + line 836 ("**shape B** — `curl ... | sh` bootstraps `uv` and runs `uv tool install git+...`. **PyPI moves to post-MVP.**"). The system-level pieces (`playwright install chromium`, real Chrome on macOS, `~/.operator/.env` seeding) live in `install.sh` regardless of whether the package source is git or PyPI — `pip install` alone was insufficient because it ships none of those. **Implication of this decision for the public repo: it must be public when QA users `curl | sh`**, because anonymous `uv tool install git+https://github.com/...` resolves via anonymous git clone. Cloudflare Pages can serve `install.sh` from a private repo via the GitHub App, but the install flow itself can't.

- **Ship list audit.** User-driven decision on what does + doesn't go to the public repo. **Ships (11 items):** `.gitignore`, `LICENSE`, `README.md`, `SECURITY.md`, `pyproject.toml`, `requirements.txt`, `operator` (bash wrapper), `install.sh` (new this session), `_redirects` (new this session), `src/`, `tests/`. **Does NOT ship:** `.vscode/` (personal editor settings), `CLAUDE.md` (user call — keep dev workflow private for now), `debug/` (spike scripts + DOM/screenshot dumps), `docs/` (entire — both gitignored internal docs AND tracked ones like `claude-use-cases.md`, `mcp-auth-errors.md`, `security.md`, `promo-video-script.md`; user wants nothing from `docs/` shipped this round), `experiments/`, `pypi-stub/` (the v0.0.1 PyPI placeholder package — separate concern, separate package), `scripts/` (dev probes), `test/` (singular — sample workspace, not the test suite). User decision is a value judgment, not a security requirement: README ships as-is and will be rewritten before final launch then re-snapshotted (Phase 16).

- **Orphan-snapshot publish flow (the new dev workflow).** Three force-pushes to the public repo this session, each from a fresh orphan branch:
  - **v0 (`f79e1f6`)** — initial 9-item ship list. `git checkout --orphan public-snapshot-v0` → `git rm -rf --cached .` → `git add` keepers → `git commit -m "Initial public release"` → added new `public` remote (`origin` left at `dufis1/operator`) → `git push -u public public-snapshot-v0:main`. After push, `git checkout -f main` to return to dev branch — `-f` is safe because the unstaged-not-modified files on the orphan are bit-identical to main's tracked content.
  - **v1 (`51acf1e`)** — added `install.sh`. Local commit `d646008` on main. Same orphan procedure with v1 branch + force-push.
  - **v2 (`058b4f5`)** — added `_redirects`. Local commit `18e028f` on main. Same procedure.
  - **Force-push discipline:** orphan branches don't share ancestry with each other or with previous public-repo state, so every snapshot push is a force. `uv tool install git+URL` users get whatever HEAD resolves to at install time — force-push doesn't break their flow.
  - **The handoff documents the procedure** so any future re-snapshot reproduces it byte-for-byte.

- **`install.sh` (Phase 14.5 — `d646008`, snapshot v1 `51acf1e`).** 138 lines, `set -euo pipefail`, idempotent, color-coded output (`bold`/`info`/`warn`/`err` shell helpers). Steps in order: (1) detect macOS or Linux (other platforms exit with clear error), (2) verify Python ≥3.10 via inline `python3 -c` — exits with version mismatch message if older or missing, (3) bootstrap `uv` via `curl -LsSf https://astral.sh/uv/install.sh | sh` if not on PATH; folds `~/.local/bin` and `~/.cargo/bin` into PATH for the rest of the script; bails with "open new shell + retry" if uv still not findable, (4) `uv tool install --force git+https://github.com/1-800-operator/operator.git` (force = idempotent on re-runs), (5) `uv tool run --from "git+..." playwright install chromium` (~170 MB download), (6) seed `~/.operator/.env` with commented placeholders for `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` / `OPENAI_API_KEY` / `GITHUB_TOKEN` (mode 600, only if file doesn't exist — never overwrites existing keys), (7) macOS-only Chrome.app cask nudge with `brew install --cask google-chrome` hint and direct download URL, (8) PATH check for `operator` binary, (9) "next: `operator setup`" hint pointing at https://github.com/1-800-operator/operator. **Fold note:** Phase 14.5.1 (separate roadmap row for the brew-cask offer) was folded into 14.5 itself — the cask nudge is just one block in the same install script, not its own deliverable.

- **`_redirects` (Cloudflare Pages prep — `18e028f`, snapshot v2 `058b4f5`).** Single-line file at repo root: `/install   /install.sh   200`. The `200` status is a **rewrite**, not a redirect — Cloudflare Pages serves `install.sh`'s contents at `/install` URL with no 30x roundtrip. `curl https://1-800-operator.com/install | sh` works without curl needing `-L` to follow redirects. Trailing newline preserved.

- **Cloudflare Pages walkthrough delivered to user (Steps 2 + 3 are dashboard work, user-driven).** Step 1 (add `_redirects` + ship it) shipped as commit `18e028f`. Steps 2 and 3 require Cloudflare dashboard access and are queued for next session: (2) Workers & Pages → Create application → Pages → Connect to Git → authorize Cloudflare on the `1-800-operator` GitHub org → pick `1-800-operator/operator` → production branch `main`, framework preset None, build command empty, build output directory `/`. (3) Pages project → Custom domains → add `1-800-operator.com` → Cloudflare auto-creates DNS (zone already on CF nameservers per session 180) → wait ~1 min for HTTPS cert. Step 4 verification curls (`curl -I https://1-800-operator.com/install`, etc.) Claude can run from the host once the user reports the Pages project is wired up. **Two-shape consideration noted:** Shape A = Pages deploys from operator public repo, output dir = `/`. Other repo files (src/, tests/, README) become accessible at `1-800-operator.com/<path>` — same as github.com but feels weird on the marketing domain. Shape B = separate `1-800-operator/landing` repo with just install.sh duplicated. Recommended A for now; flip to B during Phase 16 README/landing rewrite when a real `index.html` lands.

Ran `gh repo edit 1-800-operator/operator --visibility private --accept-visibility-change-consequences`. **State at session end:** public repo is at `058b4f5` ("v0.1.0-pre: install.sh + Cloudflare _redirects"), 11 ship-list files at root, 0 commits in history aside from the orphan snapshot. - **Wizard polish (`d053a74` + end-of-session bundle).** User flagged five rough edges in the codex flow + one cosmetic carryover on the claude flow + one width bug on the reveal card. All addressed:
  - **Step numbering threaded through every step function.** Every step (`_step3_skills`, `_step2_mcps`, `_step_permissions`, `_step_permissions_codex`, `_step4_system_prompt`, `_step6_api_keys`, `run_signin_step`) now takes a `step_num: int` kwarg; `run()` advances a counter starting at `1` for edit mode and `2` for setup (after `_step1_fighter_select` already burned step 1). Edit mode reads `1..6`, setup mode `1..7`.   - **Codex skills + MCPs are now real acknowledgement steps.** Previously these returned silently for codex agents and got `console.clear()`'d before the user could read them, making the codex flow feel like steps had been skipped (jumping from "1. Choose your base agent" straight to "4. Permissions"). Both steps now render their inheritance content as locked `[✓]` checkbox glyphs in dim styling (mirrors the `[✓]/[ ]` look from `picker.py:114`), then pause on `Press Enter to continue…` so the user actively passes through them.
  - **Codex spinner reworded** from `"reading your codex setup"` to `"loading your Codex skills and MCPs"` to match claude's `"wiring in your Claude skills and MCPs"` shape — the codex flow now has the same loading beat the claude flow does.
  - **Codex add/remove instruction blocks trimmed** to a single dim line each (`"To add or remove MCPs/skills, manage them globally in codex."`). The bullet rows (`add`, `remove`, `codex mcp add` / `codex mcp remove` example commands, "changes take effect on the next operator run codex") are gone — user said "Nothing more."
  - **Removed two stale instructional lines**: (1) `"Codex's internal allowlist filters read-class commands automatically. Pick the approval policy + sandbox for everything else."` from `_step_permissions_codex` (the radio knobs above are self-explanatory); (2) `"Permissions — space to toggle, enter to confirm"` `select_many` title from the claude permissions step (the picker's own footer already says it).
  - **Reveal card width is content-aware.** Added `build_card.width_for_reveal(console, items=...)`: derives natural width from `longest_name + _ITEM_LINE_OVERHEAD` (overhead is now `2 + 12 + 3 + 2 + 1 = 20` cells — body indent + 12-cell label column + the wide `⚡ ` glyph segment + panel borders + 1 cell of right-side breathing room), capped by `console.size.width - 4`, never below `DEFAULT_WIDTH=40`. `WizardState.card()` accepts an optional `width` override; `_reveal()` computes the width from the union of equipped MCPs + skills and passes it. Long names like `claude-ai-google-calendar` (25 chars) now render on one line. **Picker steps still call `width_for(console)` unchanged** — the right-pane card during the picker shouldn't expand because it shares the row with a left column.
  - **The bug that took the most iterations to nail down.** First pass on `width_for_reveal` undercounted the glyph. `⚡` is a wide glyph (cell_len 2), and the body string is `"⚡ name"` (3 cells of prefix), but I'd budgeted only 2. So the first attempt computed `width = 25 + 18 = 43`, the inner pane ended up 41 cells, and `_hang_wrap` saw `avail = 41 - 2 - 12 = 27` < 28, so the long name wrapped anyway. Fix was bumping `_ITEM_LINE_OVERHEAD` from 18 → 20 (2 cells: 1 for the wider glyph, 1 for breathing room).
  - **End-of-session wizard bundle (folded into `d053a74`).** Three small follow-ups the user flagged after the polish landed:
    1. **`(brain)` → `(MCP bridge)` for codex.** User asked whether "codex (brain)" was an OpenAI product name (it isn't — "brain" is operator's internal jargon for the CLI subprocess running as an MCP server). Renamed in `setup.py:689` (the `_step2_mcps` codex branch label). Internal jargon left alone (config.yaml description string, framework prompt's "you ARE the meeting brain", code comments — those are documentation, not user-facing UI).
    2. **Step 6 skip for codex.** User noticed the wizard jumped from `5. System Prompt` → `7. Sign-in` for codex agents. Root cause: `_step6_api_keys` always printed its `6. API keys` header, but `console.clear()` immediately after wiped it before the user could read. Codex has zero `${VAR}` placeholders (`OPENAI_API_KEY: ""` is a literal-empty value to clear ChatGPT-subscription auth, not a `${VAR}` ref), so step 6 was a flash-and-clear no-op. Fix: in `run()` (`setup.py:1610`), pre-compute `missing_keys` and only call `_step6_api_keys` (and consume a step number) when there's a key to prompt for. Sign-in now renders as **step 6** for codex (and any future preset with no API-key prompts), and stays at **step 7** when keys ARE needed.
    3. **Build card removed from in-flight picker steps.** User wanted the build card off the right pane during the MCPs (`_step2_mcps`) and Skills (`_step3_skills`) pickers because terminal resizes mid-step were going to mangle it. Removed the `right_pane=right_pane` arg + the closure that called `state.card(...)` in both steps. Permissions step (`_step_permissions`) was deliberately left alone — its right pane is a plain text summary (auto-approve / always-ask lists), not a build card. Reveal card at the end (`setup.py:1517`) untouched — that's the only build card the user sees now. Also dropped the now-unused `card_w` / `budget` arithmetic in step 3 since the budget no longer needs to share the row with a card pane (sublabels can take the full width minus padding).

Existing skill-load code already enforces this — `_discover_skill_candidates` skips shared library when `state.based_on == "claude"`. All previously-passing tests still green under `OPERATOR_BOT=claude`.

- **14.13.3 (DNS housekeeping, no commit — registrar-side work).** `1-800-operator.com` was on Porkbun nameservers (`{curitiba,fortaleza,maceio,salvador}.ns.porkbun.com`) with parking A records (`44.230.85.241` / `52.33.207.7`) and Porkbun mail-forward MX/SPF. Mirrored Phase 14.6's session-142 playbook on the new domain: added the zone to Cloudflare (Free plan), deleted all 9 imported parking records (2 A + 2 CNAME wildcard/www to `uixie.porkbun.com` + 2 MX `fwd1/fwd2.porkbun.com` + 1 SPF TXT `include:_spf.porkbun.com` + 2 stale `_acme-challenge` TXTs), swapped Porkbun's authoritative NS to `deb.ns.cloudflare.com` + `devin.ns.cloudflare.com`. Propagation <5min. Pages attachment + apex `/install` host deferred to Phase 14.6 proper post-`install.sh` (Phase 14.5 is still pending — one clean GitHub-connected Pages wire-up beats a throwaway upload). - **Side ship (`7796f39`).** Async working-tree updates from this session that weren't part of the prune: codex preset polish (`agents/codex/config.yaml`, `pipeline/codex_import.py`, `pipeline/setup.py`); post-MVP roadmap entry "mid-meeting brain reset" (`@bot reset` chat command to gracefully tear down + respawn the brain MCP subprocess so newly-installed skills/MCPs take effect without re-joining); 90s promo video script at `docs/promo-video-script.md` ("remote tech worker. Aha: meeting-tail post-work avalanche dissolved by Operator doing it all in-meeting").

- **Codex wizard parity (`7796f39` + `69d7dc2`) — design conversation summary.** User asked whether codex has skills + MCPs analogous to Claude Code, and how the wizard should treat them. We discovered `~/.codex/skills/` (with `.system/` carrying codex's built-ins: skill-creator, skill-installer, plugin-creator, openai-docs, imagegen) and `codex mcp add/remove/list` (writes to `~/.codex/config.toml`). **Architectural posture decided:** codex IS the harness for the codex agent (operator just spawns `codex mcp-server` and relays chat). Codex's own MCPs and skills load inside that subprocess from disk. Operator does NOT mirror them into its own state — toggling there would be a *lie* because codex still loads them internally. So the wizard's job is **read-only surfacing for visibility**, not togglable management. **What shipped:** (1) `codex` is now a third step-1 preset in `_step1_fighter_select` alongside `claude` + `custom`, with the same CLI-prereq gate (`codex login status` ChatGPT-only). (2) `discover_codex_mcps()` + `discover_codex_skills()` in `pipeline/codex_import.py` shell out to `codex mcp list --json` and walk `~/.codex/skills/` + `.system/` (last-wins dedup). (3) `_surface_codex_inheritance(state)` runs after `_edit_preset` for codex (mirrors `_auto_import_claude_setup`'s shape); stashes results on state and prints a "Codex CLI inheritance:" banner. (4) `_render_codex_inheritance_footer(state, surface=...)` renders the read-only list + management guidance. (5) For codex agents, `_step3_skills` and `_step2_mcps` short-circuit before the togglable picker — the inheritance panel + guidance is the whole step content. The MCP step shows the brain entry as a fixed `✓ codex (brain) — always enabled` row + the inheritance panel. The skills step skips both the picker AND `_prompt_add_external_path` (codex's loader hard-codes `~/.codex/skills/` — no external_paths analogue, no point asking). **Bundled YAML divergence:** removed `skills:` block from `agents/codex/config.yaml` entirely; comment block explains "INTENTIONALLY ABSENT" reasoning. `permissions.auto_approve` / `permissions.always_ask` were never in the codex config (only `default_approval_policy` + `default_sandbox`); reaffirmed by the wizard's `_step_permissions_codex` which pops them on every save. `_step3_skills` + `_step7_write` pop any stale `skills:` block on each wizard run for codex. **Liability audit:** verified every read of `cfg["skills"]` / `bot_cfg["skills"]` across runtime + wizard. Runtime `config.py:360` uses `_skills = _config.get("skills") or {}` and `config.py:412-414` defaults perms to `[]` — defensive against missing blocks. Wizard's unsafe `state.bot_cfg["skills"]["external_paths"]` access at `setup.py:1088` is gated behind the codex early-return I added at `setup.py:945` so it can't fire. Booted config.py with `OPERATOR_BOT=codex` to confirm clean output (LLM_PROVIDER=codex_mcp, SKILLS_ENABLED=[], PERMISSIONS_AUTO_APPROVE=[], MCP_SERVERS={'codex'}). **Locked the divergence with regression tests (`69d7dc2`):** `tests/test_codex_agent_config.py` gained `test_bundled_codex_yaml_omits_moot_blocks` (asserts no `skills:` / no `auto_approve` / no `always_ask` in bundled YAML) and `test_runtime_defaults_for_omitted_blocks` (asserts SKILLS_ENABLED, PERMISSIONS_AUTO_APPROVE, etc. default to `[]` cleanly). Verified the test bites by injecting a stale `skills:` block and watching it fail with the right error message. **Did NOT add runtime validation that rejects user hand-edits** — would conflict with the `feedback_user_owns_their_config` memory; runtime is defensively coded; bundled-config drift is the only path to a real bug, which the tests catch at PR time.

**Exact next step (session 181): Phase 14.13.1 — repo creation + initial push.** Sequence: `gh repo create 1-800-operator/operator --private --description "Claude Code, in your Google Meet"` → `git remote set-url origin git@github.com:1-800-operator/operator.git` → `git push -u origin main` (16 commits ahead of `origin` at session end) → `git push --tags` → manual sanity check → flip public via `gh repo edit --visibility public`. Then **Phase 14.13.4** — archive `dufis1/operator` with description "moved to github.com/1-800-operator/operator" via `gh repo edit ... && gh repo archive ...`. Inventory of the old repo: 0 stars, 0 forks, 3 closed test-y issues, 4 PRs (2 merged, 2 closed) — fresh push is fine, no transfer needed. Then **Phase 16** (README rewrite, demo GIF, landing site at 1-800-operator.com, launch campaign — needs to mention BOTH the claude and codex agents). Open product question deferred to next session: user briefly questioned the 1-800-operator org-name choice — punted with the trade-off written down (separate-org buys brand separation + future-proofing for collaborators + clean parallel to the domain handle, costs one extra GitHub UI hop).

**Prior status (session 179) — codex agent shipped. v1 scope expanded from claude-only to claude + codex. Spike + 5-phase implementation in one bundled commit (`7642f95`); 6 new test files (39 tests), all green. R3 (auto-disable kills brain) mitigated. R8 (caption parity) deferred to v2 with a documented gap.**

User asked at session start whether it was feasible to add a second meeting brain via OpenAI Codex CLI. We started with a multi-probe spike (`debug/codex_spike/`) that found Codex's native `codex mcp-server` mode round-trips MCP `elicitation/create` for command approval — meaning we could plumb Codex as an MCP server and reach feature parity with the claude track at ~1/4 the LOC of writing a streaming-subprocess provider. Locked design after phase-0 probes simplified the plan further: deleted the auto_approve / always_ask permission lists (Codex's internal safe-allowlist already filters read-class commands), replaced with a two-knob `default_approval_policy` + `default_sandbox` block. Built the agent across 5 phases (elicitation in mcp_client → provider + handler → agent files → preflight + wiring → R3 mitigation), then bundled into a single commit.

- **Phase 0 — spike completion (`debug/codex_spike/`).** Six probes resolved seven blocking unknowns: SDK has clean `elicitation_callback` kwarg at `mcp/client/session.py:118`; tool-name namespace `codex__codex-reply` survives `__` split; `codex login status` writes to STDERR not stdout; every elicitation typed `unknown` (read-class auto-approved internally); compound shells collapse to single `unknown` entry (R6 non-issue); `approved_execpolicy_amendment` payload shape captured + suppression confirmed via end-to-end round-trip (`probe_amendment.log` shows 2 elicitations across 3 prompts, the repeat was suppressed). v1 deferrals: `~/.codex/config.toml` MCP-import sync; codex skills overlay (no `~/.codex/skills/` analogue); caption parity (codex's mcp-server doesn't accept `--mcp-config`).

- **Phase 1 — `pipeline/mcp_client.py` inbound elicitation handling.** Added `MCPClient.set_elicitation_handler(server_name, handler)` (late-bind safe), `_ServerHandle._dispatch_elicitation` async shim that routes inbound `elicitation/create` requests to a synchronous handler on the executor pool, validates handler return shape (`{"decision": ...}`) and falls back to ErrorData(INVALID_REQUEST) on missing/invalid. Also added `MCPClient.last_structured_content(server_name)` accessor for fields the SDK doesn't surface in joined text content (codex's `threadId` lives there). 3 integration tests against real `codex mcp-server`.

- **Phase 2 — `pipeline/providers/codex_mcp.py` + `pipeline/codex_elicitation_handler.py`.** Provider holds `_thread_id` across turns; first call invokes `codex__codex` with `developer-instructions` (codex stores per-thread, never re-sent), subsequent calls invoke `codex__codex-reply` with the stored threadId. Dead-thread fallback: catches `MCPToolError` matching `_DEAD_THREAD_HINTS` ("thread not found", "session not connected", "session disconnected", "unknown threadid"), clears threadId, retries once with fresh `codex` call. Handler is ~half the size of `PermissionChatHandler` because no fnmatch/glob lists — strips `/bin/zsh -lc` wrapper for plain voice, maps replies via new `is_yes_always` helper (added to `pipeline/confirmation.py`) → amendment-form decision; `is_yes` → single-shot approved; else → abort. 17 tests across two files.

- **Phase 3 — `agents/codex/`.** `config.yaml` mirrors claude schema with codex-specific deviations clearly noted in the header: `provider: codex_mcp`, `transcript.captions_enabled: false` (R8 deferral), `permissions.{default_approval_policy: on-request, default_sandbox: read-only}`, `mcp_servers.codex` bundled with `command: codex`, `args: [mcp-server]`, `env: {OPENAI_API_KEY: ""}` (R5 layer-1 — clears at spawn to force ChatGPT subscription auth), `skills.enabled: []`. `framework.py` is codex-flavored with shell-sandbox vocabulary; mentions the "yes always" → remember-this-call UX prominently so users discover it.

- **Phase 4 — preflight + wiring + setup.** `pipeline/codex_import.py:codex_installed_and_logged_in()` mirrors claude's preflight shape — PATH check, version probe (WARN-not-fail on drift past `0.128.x`, R7), `codex login status` parse combining stdout+stderr (codex writes the auth banner to stderr — phase 0 finding), R5 layer-2 reject of API-key auth ("subscription-only"). `__main__.py` adds an `if name == "codex":` branch that hard-fails with a clear stderr message when the preflight returns False. `chat_runner.py` adds `_wire_codex_elicitation()` which registers the handler on the codex MCP server AND late-binds `provider._mcp_client` after `MCPClient.connect_all()`. `setup.py:_step_permissions` branches on `provider == "codex_mcp"` to a new `_step_permissions_codex()` two-radio UI (no `_BUILTIN_TOOLS_CODEX` — phase-0 simplification). `config.py` validates the new `default_approval_policy` / `default_sandbox` enums; loads `CODEX_APPROVAL_POLICY` / `CODEX_SANDBOX` exposed to `build_provider`. 10 tests across two new files.

- **R3 mitigation — brain-MCP exemption.** `MCPClient` auto-disables a server after `RUNTIME_FAILURE_THRESHOLD=3` consecutive failures. For sidekick MCPs (Linear, Sentry) this protects the meeting from a chatty failing server. For the codex brain it would silently kill the agent ("@codex ..." → no response, no error). New `_is_brain_mcp(server_name)` returns True only for `codex` server when `LLM_PROVIDER == "codex_mcp"`; `record_tool_result` checks it at the trip moment and bypasses with a WARNING log. Failures still propagate via `MCPToolError` → `LLMClient.ask` → `chat_runner._narrate_failure` (session 178's machinery), which falls through to the hardcoded apology when the LLM-narrated apology can't be generated (because the brain is the failing thing). 9 new assertions extend the existing runtime-failure test block.

- **End-to-end smoke.** Real `codex mcp-server` spawned via operator's MCPClient; provider sent prompt; codex replied "spike pong"; threadId tracked. Plus 3 integration tests in `test_mcp_client_elicitation.py` driving real subprocess elicitation round-trips: happy path, no-handler-blocks-write, invalid-shape-blocks-write.

- **Tests green at session end:** all 8 affected/new suites pass — `test_chat_hardening`, `test_mcp_client` (28 → 37 with brain-exemption block), `test_mcp_shutdown` (9), `test_mcp_client_elicitation` (3), `test_codex_mcp_provider` (8), `test_codex_elicitation_handler` (9), `test_codex_import` (6), `test_codex_agent_config` (4). Codex commit (`7642f95`) is one bundled atomic commit.

- **Mid-session design pivot worth noting.** Initially planned to ship `permissions.auto_approve` / `always_ask` lists keyed on `parsed_cmd.type`. Phase 0 taxonomy probe showed every elicitation that reaches operator is typed `unknown` — Codex's internal safe-allowlist filters read-class commands (`list_files`, `read_file`, etc.) before they ever round-trip to us. That made per-type matching dead code. Pivoted to the simpler two-knob `default_approval_policy` + `default_sandbox` block. Plan doc was updated mid-stream to reflect this; total LOC dropped from 1,140-1,400 estimate to ~745 + 600 tests = ~1,345 actual.

## Prior status

### Session 178 (May 1, 2026)

**Session 178 — code-quality audit tier-1 sweep complete. Persnickety reviewer-style pass over ~11k LOC of runtime; 12 PR-blockers found (`docs/code-quality-audit-session-178.md`); 9 resolved + 3 deferred in one commit (`500a3bc`). 4 new test files. v1 = claude-on-Meet only, no scope changes (later expanded in session 179).**

Walked the audit doc one finding at a time, pausing at each to recheck framing, weigh cost vs payoff, and make a deliberate ship/defer decision. A few audit claims were rewritten mid-session after deeper code reading proved the original framing wrong (T1.7 in particular — "chat and record disagree" was incorrect; canonical_text was actually dead computation under streaming, fix was a deletion not a swap).

- **T1.1 (`__main__.py`).** `_sync_claude_imports()` ran before `os.environ["OPERATOR_BOT"] = name`. Dormant today but the contract was enforced by comment, not code position. Moved env-var assignment to first line of `_run_bot`'s post-arg-parse block. Verified `pipeline.setup` and `pipeline.claude_code_import` have no top-level `config` imports.

- **T1.2 (collapse `personality` + `ground_rules` to `system_prompt`).** Two separate YAML keys were composed with `\n\n` at runtime — schema split that the wizard's fresh-input path silently collapsed (always wrote to `personality`, forced `ground_rules=""`). Decided to admit it's one concern. Single `system_prompt` field across `config.py` (validator + loader + composition: `FRAMEWORK_SYSTEM_PROMPT + USER_SYSTEM_PROMPT + CLAUDE_MD_BLOCK`), `setup.py:_step4_system_prompt`, four bundled YAMLs (pm/engineer/designer/claude — combined the two blocks), `agents/claude/framework.py` docstring, comments in `chat_runner`/`permission_chat_handler`/`claude_code_import`/`providers/__init__`/`providers/claude_cli`, tests (`test_config_loader`, `test_voice_modes`, `test_legacy_permissions_migration`, `test_setup`), docs (`CLAUDE.md`, `README.md`, `agents/README.md`, `docs/permission-mcp-spike.md`, `docs/test-plan.md`). No legacy-key migration shim — user wiped `~/.operator/agents/` mid-session and reseeded from bundled.

- **T1.4 + T1.5 + T1.12 (unified `_narrate_failure` helper).** Started as "add an `else` arm to `_dispatch_result`." User pushed back on filter-by-exception-class with "why not feed the failure back to the LLM?" That was the right instinct — the original `chat_runner._loop` exception path was silent (just logged + emitted turn-done, sent nothing to chat — every user message could go silent on a 429). New `_narrate_failure(*, context, fallback)` builds a tiny prompt with the failure context, calls `self._llm.ask(prompt, record=False, tools=None, retry_rate_limits=False)`, posts the bare-string return inline, falls through to hardcoded `fallback` on raise/empty. Always emits `turn_done(failed=True)`. Applied at 4 sites: dispatcher else-arm (T1.4), `_handle_load_skill` exception (T1.5), main loop LLM exception (T1.12 main loop), tool-result summary failure (T1.12 — additionally inlines truncated raw tool result into the prompt so the user can get the underlying answer). Threaded `retry_rate_limits=True` kwarg through `LLMProvider.complete`/`complete_streaming` interface (base + 3 implementations: anthropic honors it, openai/claude_cli accept as no-op). 12 tests in `test_narrate_failure.py`.

- **T1.6 (`anthropic.complete_streaming` mid-stream 429).** Original retry loop reset `buffer = ""` per attempt. If a 429 fired mid-stream after `flush_paragraphs(...)` had already posted to chat, the retry re-streamed from the start and the user saw the reply twice. Considered a "continue from here" recovery prompt; rejected because (a) same input bucket → likely 429s again, (b) model often rephrases at the seam, (c) extra wait on top of the existing retry window. Shipped the simple bail: `flushed_any` flag, mid-stream 429 after flush → log + `on_paragraph(apology line)` + `bailed_mid_stream = True` + `break`. Post-finally if `bailed_mid_stream`, return synthetic empty `ProviderResponse` so caller treats the turn as complete (paragraphs already streamed; caller doesn't fire its own narrate fallback on top). Pre-flush 429s still retry as before (safe — buffer reset per attempt is fine when nothing reached the user). Two new tests: mid-stream + pre-flush.

- **T1.7 (deleted dead `canonical_text`).** Audit framing was wrong. Re-read the data flow: chat-side flushes go through `on_paragraph` → `_streaming_callback` → `_send` → meeting record (so chat AND record both get `accumulated`). The function returns `ProviderResponse(text=canonical_text)` but `chat_runner._dispatch_result` skips the resend on `streamed=True`, so canonical was dead. Deleted `canonical_messages` init and the `len(canonical) != len(accumulated)` divergence-warning block. Slimmed assistant-event handler to only dispatch `tool_use` blocks to `progress_callback`. `final_text = "".join(full_text_parts).strip()`. Function is now honest: returns what reached the user.

- **T1.9 (shared `is_yes` helper).** Two divergent yes/no matchers — `permission_chat_handler._is_yes` (track-A claude_cli regex with bare `y`, `okay`, `approved`) vs `chat_runner._handle_confirmation` (track-B word-set without bare `y` or `okay`). Same user-facing "OK?" prompt, different rules per provider. New `pipeline/confirmation.py:is_yes(text) -> bool` exposes the union vocab. `permission_chat_handler` re-exports as `_is_yes = is_yes` (preserves call-site signature); `chat_runner._handle_confirmation` becomes `affirmative = is_yes(text)`. Removed unused `import re` from `permission_chat_handler`. 12 tests (canonical, embedded, phrase override, negations, contractions, word-boundary safety, two delegation tests).

- **T1.10 (Linux participant signal).** Linux's `_process_chat_queue` only handled `send`/`read`. Linux inherited base's `get_participant_count() -> 0`, so `saw_others` never flipped, intro never posted, alone-grace never fired, 1-on-1 never engaged. Mirrored mac's full surface verbatim (Meet's tile DOM is platform-agnostic): public `get_participant_count`/`get_participant_names` methods, `_do_*` helpers using `[data-requested-participant-id]` locator + `page.evaluate` JS, two new arms in `_process_chat_queue`. The drain logic at the bottom already had `participant_count`/`participant_names` cases — was half-done plumbing waiting for the rest. T2.1 still tracks the larger refactor of pulling shared adapter code into a mixin/base; this fix is tactical. 10 tests in `test_linux_adapter_participants.py`.

- **Deferred (3) with documented rationale:**
  - **T1.3** (Linear `limit`-strip duplication, `chat_runner.py:736-738` + `mcp_client.py:366-368`): no user impact today (both flows strip before execute_tool runs); duplication is the only real concern. Low payoff vs T2.5 (server-specific knowledge in neutral abstractions) which would clean the broader pattern.
  - **T1.8** (in-memory vs disk `MeetingRecord.tail()` semantics): `slug=None` mode used only by `operator try` and tests, not production. Test fidelity concern only; would notice the moment we wrote a multi-session in-memory test.
  - **T1.11** (Chrome vs Chromium profile path on macOS): wizard signs in via real Chrome; runtime adapter uses bundled Chromium against same `~/.operator/browser_profile/`. Theoretical risk if Google moves auth cookies to keychain-encrypted slot or Chrome's monthly schema bumps beyond Chromium-for-Testing. Works today. Updated comment in `google_signin.py:197-211` to accurately document the divergence and the deferred-fix conditions. Revisit when a "logged out at runtime" failure surfaces.

- **Mid-session catches.** Two audit findings I had to honestly downgrade after closer reading: (a) T1.4 was framed as "this fires today" — it's actually a dormant safety net for unknown result shapes; downgraded to "structural cleanup converting silent failures into loud ones." (b) T1.7 was framed as "chat and record disagree" — actually canonical_text was unused; the real finding was dead computation. Both fixes still landed, but with corrected framing in the audit doc.

- **Tests.** Full sweep green at session end: `test_chat_hardening` 7/7, `test_911_size_management` 6/6, `test_912_tool_timeout` 4/4, `test_913_tool_history_collapse` 3/3, `test_915_reconnection` 6/6, `test_narrate_failure` 12/12, `test_confirmation` 12/12, `test_linux_adapter_participants` 10/10, `test_anthropic_provider` 13/13 (with 2 new mid-stream-429 cases), `test_claude_cli_provider` 7/7, `test_setup` (all pass), `test_config_loader` 13/13, `test_voice_modes` 8/8, `test_legacy_permissions_migration` 4/4. Branch is 33 commits ahead of `origin/main`.

### Session 177 (May 1, 2026)

**Session 177 — Phase 15.10 pre-launch hardening complete. 12-cluster edge-case audit shipped 12 fixes across 7 commits + 12 regression tests. Launch-blocker (`~/.operator/history/` world-readable) closed. Microsoft Teams probe + Zoom adapter business logic deferred to post-launch; v1 = claude-on-Meet only.**

Walked the full Phase 15.10.2 cluster review end-to-end. Surfaced and shipped fixes for: chat_runner record-append-after-send, `_send_lock` for cross-thread Playwright safety, negation gate in `_handle_confirmation` ("ok no don't" was approving), correction-path heartbeat leak, permission_chat_handler negation gate (same shape, two surfaces stay consistent), dead `HARD_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` in permission_bridge, `claude mcp list` failure-caching (broken CLI costs 10s not 30s), wizard `_step7_write` rolling back on Ctrl+C between renames (`except BaseException`), friendly CONFIG ERROR on YAML parse failure, `_run_bot` propagates platform-runner exit codes, `~/.operator/history/` + JSONL files retroactively tightened to 0o700/0o600 for legacy installs. Clusters 2/5/6/10/12 closed audit-only (no v1-grade (c) findings). 12 commits ahead of session-start; branch is now 32 commits ahead of `origin/main`.

- **Cluster 1 — chat_runner.py (commit `4fac5fd`):** Four edge cases. (a) `_send` appended to meeting record BEFORE `send_chat` returned, leaving phantom assistant messages in the record on send failure → swap order. (b) `_send` called from main poll loop + progress narrator pump thread (track A) + claude-stream tail thread; Playwright sync API is single-threaded by contract → wrap body in `self._send_lock`. (c) `_handle_confirmation` affirmative match counted "ok no don't do that" as approval because "ok" matched anywhere → add negation gate `{no, nope, nah, stop, cancel}` + `don't`/`dont`/`do not` substring. Test caught a real edge case during dev — `re.findall(r"\b\w+\b", lower)` splits "don't" into `{don, t}`, so contractions need substring detection. (d) Correction-path `send_tool_result` exception path bare-returned without `_emit_turn_done(failed=True)` and without telling the user → emit failed-turn + fallback chat line.

- **Cluster 3 — permission bridge (commit `4153466`):** Ported the same negation gate to `permission_chat_handler._is_yes` so track-A confirmation flow agrees with track-B chat_runner on the yes/no contract. Removed dead `HARD_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` constant from `permission_bridge.py` and corrected the docstring — the bridge has no Python-side watchdog; the CLI's hook timeout (600s, set in `claude_cli._setup_permission_bridge`'s settings.json) is what governs.

- **Cluster 4 — claude_code_import.py (commit `5a32e31`):** `_claude_mcp_list_cached` returned None on `OSError` / `TimeoutExpired` without setting `_CLAUDE_MCP_LIST_CACHE`. Boot makes three callers (`discover_hosted_mcps_via_cli`, `discover_mcp_health`, runtime view in config.py); under a broken `claude` CLI, each one re-shelled out and paid another 10s timeout → cache a sentinel `CompletedProcess(returncode=-1)` on the failure path. Existing `if r is None or r.returncode != 0: return []` branches degrade correctly without changes.

- **Cluster 7 — wizard atomic write (commit `7a11ee8`):** `_step7_write`'s inner cleanup caught `Exception` (not `BaseException`), so a Ctrl+C between `os.rename(target, backup)` and `os.rename(tmp, target)` bypassed rollback entirely. Result: intact backup at `agents/<name>.bak-<ts>/`, no live agent dir at `agents/<name>/`. Switching to `except BaseException` makes the existing rollback ("if backup exists and target doesn't, rename backup back") run on KI too.

- **Cluster 8 — config.py YAML error (commit `ad8a0e1`):** `yaml.safe_load(_cfg_path.read_text())` ran without try/except, surfacing a malformed config as a raw `yaml.YAMLError` traceback. Every other shape violation goes through `_validate_config` which emits a friendly "CONFIG ERROR in <path>:" stderr block. Wrap in try/except, emit the same shape, exit 2.

- **Cluster 9 — `_run_bot` exit codes (commit `17b85d3`):** `_run_bot` returned 0 unconditionally regardless of what `_run_macos` / `_run_linux` did, so a meet.new redirect failure exited 0 — CI scripts couldn't tell join failures apart from clean exits. `_run_macos`'s meet.new failure path fell through to a bare `return`. Both now return 0/1 explicitly; `_run_bot` dispatches via `return _run_macos(...) or 0` (legacy callers returning None still surface as 0).

- **Cluster 11 — meeting record perms (commit `855d910`, LAUNCH-BLOCKER CLOSED):** `MeetingRecord.__init__` was creating `~/.operator/history/` and JSONL files without explicit perms, relying on `__main__.main`'s umask 0o077. That works for fresh installs but leaves legacy installs from before the session-172 umask fix with world-readable dirs/files — the explicit launch-blocker carry-over from session 173. Now mirrors the pattern in `google_signin.py` and `macos_adapter.py`: `mkdir(mode=0o700)` + defensive `os.chmod(self.root, 0o700)` (retroactively tightens legacy dirs) + `os.chmod(self.path, 0o600)` once on open (covers both new files and legacy world-readable rejoins). Old meeting JSONLs that aren't reopened stay with whatever perms they had — acceptable, those are dormant.

- **Audit-only clusters (no fix shipped, all bucket-(a/b)):** Cluster 2 (`claude_cli` provider) — already heavily live-validated; tempdir-leak findings are theoretical (mkfifo doesn't fail on macOS tmpfs in practice); docstring inaccuracy on `_on_tool_use` threading model noted but trivial. Cluster 5 (`macos_adapter`) — `_do_send_chat` ID-readback race when another participant chats during the 1s window is real but very low frequency under v1's single-bot scope; deferred. Cluster 6 (`transcript_server` + `meeting_record` race) — POSIX `O_APPEND` writes <PIPE_BUF are atomic; no race. Cluster 10 (`mcp_client`) — entire surface is dead code under v1 (track A skips `MCPClient.connect_all` per `__main__.py:1007`); session-164 API-key-leak path verified inert. Cluster 12 (`guardrails`) — heavily covered by 911/912/913 suites.

- **Roadmap deferral.** Session 177 also deferred Microsoft Teams DOM probe + Zoom adapter business logic to post-launch (per user direction). Zoom DOM inventory in `docs/dom-inventory-zoom.md` stays as a parity checklist; `connectors/zoom_adapter.py` work doesn't happen pre-launch. Teams probe (`docs/dom-inventory-teams.md`) waits until after launch. Phase 14.13.1 (`gh repo create`) skipped per user direction.

**Exact next step (session 178): Phase 14.13.3** — flip install copy / marketing references to `1-800-operator.com`; redo the 14.6 DNS work (Cloudflare nameservers) on the new domain. Install one-liner becomes `curl -sSf https://1-800-operator.com/install \| sh`. Then **Phase 16** (README rewrite, 30s demo GIF, landing page, launch campaign).

**Session 176 (April 30, 2026) — Phase 14.13.2 brainchild → operator rename SHIPPED end-to-end. All carry-overs closed. 7 pre-existing test failures triaged + fixed (one was a real prod bug).**

Walked the full rebrand in four phases across four commits, with a fifth commit fixing every test failure that surfaced. Every user-facing surface is now `operator`; the only remaining `brainchild` references in the tree are two dictionary-sense uses ("AI newsletter brainchilds" in `mvp-bar.md`, "Kubernetes brainchilds" in `mcp-pressure-test.md`) that don't reference our project. Branch is 25 commits ahead of `origin/main` and pushed.

- **Three-name mapping locked in.** Distribution name `1-800-operator` (pyproject `name`, future `pip install` / curl-bash). CLI command + brand `operator` (bash wrapper, env var `OPERATOR_BOT`, data dir `~/.operator/`, log path `/tmp/operator.log`, copy in CLAUDE.md / README / wizard). Python import `_1_800_operator` (dev-internal only — required because `operator` is a Python stdlib module that cannot be shadowed without breaking `import operator` for `itemgetter`/`attrgetter`/etc.). End users never touch the import name; it surfaces only in source code, tracebacks, IDE jump-to-definition, and `/tmp/operator.log` logger names. The user accepted `_1_800_operator` even though it's underscore-heavy because of how rarely they'll see it.

- **Phase B (commit `17b42e1`).** `git mv src/brainchild src/_1_800_operator`, `git mv brainchild operator` (bash wrapper). Pyproject: `name = "1-800-operator"`, `[project.scripts] operator = "_1_800_operator.__main__:main"`, `packages = ["src/_1_800_operator"]`, GitHub URLs `1-800-operator/operator`. Bulk-rename inside `src/_1_800_operator`: `brainchild` → `operator` for paths/log/CLI/copy/env-var, `Brainchild` → `Operator`, `BRAINCHILD_BOT` → `OPERATOR_BOT`, then `from operator. → from _1_800_operator.` for internal imports only. Plus one `importlib.import_module("operator.agents.…")` site that needed manual fix (sed didn't catch it because the import name is built from a format string).

- **Phase C (commit `1948ad2`).** Tests + scripts + debug. Same rename rules, plus the three bundled agent configs (`pm/`, `engineer/`, `designer/config.yaml`) that reference `args=["-m", "operator.agents.engineer.claude_code"]` — these don't go through Python imports so the Phase B perl pass missed them. Any non-claude bot crashed with `UnboundLocalError` before browser spin-up. Hoisted both `import time as _time_init` and `import logging as _logging_init` above the claude block. Dead path in v1 (claude-only) but pm/engineer/designer paths now actually run.

### Session 175 prior status — Zoom DOM inventory probed end-to-end. `docs/dom-inventory-zoom.md` shipped.

Walked the DevTools-console probe-state-list workflow that was queued in the session-174 handoff. User opened a Zoom meeting in their daily Chrome (signed-in operator account), I sent self-contained IIFEs at each lifecycle state, user pasted output back, I logged selectors verbatim into `docs/dom-inventory-zoom.md`. Architecturally-critical states all captured.

- **States covered (all ✅):** 1 (launcher page — "Join from browser" via text-content match; `zoommtg://` deep-link is browser-chrome modal, ignorable under Playwright), 2a (camera + mic permission modals — **two sequential** ReactModal dialogs; "Continue without microphone and camera" is a `<span role="button">`, not a `<button>`), 2b (preview + name input — `#input-for-name` is the only stable hook, no placeholder/aria/name attr; Join enabled via `button.preview-join-button:not(.zm-btn--disabled)`), 4a (in-meeting toolbar — aria-label hooks throughout: `Leave`, `Share`, `React`, `open the chat panel`, etc.), 4b (chat panel — major implementation risk surfaced; chat input is `div.tiptap.ProseMirror[contenteditable]`, NOT a textarea; per-message DOM has `data-userid` + `data-name` on `.chat-item__sender` and a UUID `data-id` on the row for dedup), 4c (More menu — `react-bootstrap` dropdown, `a.dropdown-item[aria-label]`), 4c.1–4c.3 (Captions submenu + first-run language modal + caption rendering DOM), 4d (participants count + roster — count exposed in toolbar button aria-label `"open the participants list pane,[2] particpants"` (sic — Zoom typo), full roster in `#participants-ul` with `[role="application"][aria-label="<Name> (Me|Host),computer audio <state>,video <state>"]`).

- **Deferred non-critical states:** 4e (React menu / raise-hand) and 5 (Leave confirmation modal) — one click + probe each, picks up next session at minimal cost. Punted because chat I/O + participant count + caption rendering are the architecturally-decisive surfaces, all of which are now logged.

- **Architectural-decision data point.** The session-174 handoff flagged "Captions on Zoom/Teams" as the open architectural decision (Option A native scrape vs Option B tab audio + Whisper). **Native scrape (Option A) is viable on Zoom** — the free guest meeting we tested let us enable captions client-side without host-gating, and `.lt-subtitle-wrap` + `.live-transcription-subtitle__item` are stable hooks. Three caveats to design around: (1) speaker attribution is initials-only (`JS` for Jojo Shapiro; we'll cross-reference against the roster to recover full names — feasible since state 4d gives us both); (2) no `aria-live` on the caption container (Zoom accessibility miss; means `MutationObserver` on `.lt-subtitle-wrap`, not screen-reader-style live-region events); (3) the box only renders the **latest utterance** — no scrolling history in the DOM, so we accumulate client-side per mutation. This shifts the v1.5 captions architecture toward Option-A-primary-with-Option-B-fallback; Option B's research spike is not blocking unless Teams probing turns up "captions not available" surfaces frequently.

- **Implementation risks now logged in the inventory** that the Zoom adapter must solve:
  1. **TipTap/ProseMirror chat input** breaks Meet-style `page.fill()`. Adapter needs a per-connector text-input strategy: Meet uses `fill()`, Zoom uses `keyboard.type()` against the focused contenteditable (or paste-via-clipboard).
  2. **Side-panel exclusivity.** Chat and participants share the right-side panel slot; opening one closes the other. Adapter must restore the chat panel after a roster fetch (the "common case" is reading chat for triggers, occasionally reading participants).
  3. **Captions enable is a meeting-wide side effect.** The first-run language modal explicitly says "Captions will appear in this language for everyone" — the bot enabling captions affects every participant. Gate behind explicit per-meeting config; do not enable by default.
  4. **Build-hashed class names** (`g7nkJFrV` on state 1's "Join from browser" button) will rotate on Zoom's next deploy. Lock selectors to text + tag, not class.
  5. **Verbose Zoom aria-labels** (e.g. `"open the participants list pane,[2] particpants"` — sic) — adapter should prefer `aria-label*=` (contains) over exact match. My state-4a regex bug was the canonical example: `^participants$` missed the toolbar Participants button entirely; the wider sweep caught it on the next round.
  6. **Zoom typos appear in production strings** (`particpant`, `particpants`). Selectors must match the typoed form verbatim.

**Exact next step (session 176).** Repeat the same probe-state-list workflow for Microsoft Teams. User opens a Teams meeting URL in Chrome and walks the lifecycle states; Claude sends the same kind of IIFEs; selectors land in `docs/dom-inventory-teams.md`. Optionally pick up Zoom's two deferred states (4e React menu / raise-hand, 5 Leave confirmation) at the start of the Teams session if convenient. After Teams is logged, platform-expansion moves into adapter-implementation territory (`connectors/zoom_adapter.py`, `connectors/teams_adapter.py`).
