**Session 174 (April 29, 2026) — Hold-for-bot intro UX + participant-aware greeting + Meet DOM inventory + Platform Expansion phase scoped (commit `114240c`). Earlier in same session: Phase 14.16.1 `708e413` (overlay-model MCP cfg for claude agent + cwd-aware discovery) and Phase 14.16.2 `8b7ac0d` (CLAUDE.md double-load fix + MCP disable wired through to inner CLI + wizard step 4 simplified).**

Three small UX fixes plus prep for the Zoom + Teams adapter expansion. No live-meeting test ran this session — smoke checks only (imports clean across all touched modules; 7 prompt-assembly cases for `intro()` render correctly with self-name filter; 8/8 `test_llm_client.py` tests pass).

- **Hold-for-bot intro UX** (`pipeline/chat_runner.py`, `pipeline/llm.py`, `config.py:421`). Bot now posts a deterministic `Hold for {AGENT_NAME}...` line as its first chat message after a human appears in the room (gated on `saw_others` for the same reason the LLM intro is — Meet only renders messages received after a participant opens chat, so posting before a human is in the room means nobody sees it). `HOLD_DURATION_SECONDS = 2.0` in the INTERNAL TUNING block enforces a "connecting you now" beat between the hold line and the LLM-generated intro, even when intro generation finishes faster than humans can read; floor only — never delays past the LLM call. Originally shipped at 3.0s, dropped to 2.0s after live testing felt draggy.
- **Participant-aware intro.** Intro generation moved from parallel-kickoff at `run()` start to triggered-on-`saw_others` inside the loop. At trigger time we scrape participant names + count via the connector and pass them into `LLMClient.intro(participant_names=, participant_count=)`. The prompt now renders one of: `1-on-1 with <name>` / `meeting with: <names>` (≤4) / `meeting with N people, including A, B, C` (>4) / count-only fallbacks (`1-on-1 with one other person` / `meeting with N other participants`) / nothing if unknown. Filters bot's own name from scraped list (case-insensitive). Drops the closed greeting-word allowlist (`'Hey'/'Hi'/'Greetings'/'Howdy'/'Hello'`) entirely — it was anchoring the model's choice to plainspeak even when persona screamed otherwise (caveman persona producing "Howdy" instead of "Ugh"). Also drops `"to the meeting"` from the imperative — that word was the strongest plurality cue, forcing "hey all"/"hey team" greetings even in 1-on-1s. The structural shape directive (`<greeting>, I'm <name> — <substance>`) was also removed; user wants to test if the "Hello, Claude" misread surface returns. The `I'm`/`I am` anchor was the load-bearing piece preventing it; the greeting-word list was defensive overkill.
- **Connector `get_participant_names()`** (`connectors/base.py`, `macos_adapter.py`, `linux_adapter.py`). New base method returning `[]`; macOS implementation via `_do_get_participant_names()` runs `page.evaluate()` over `[data-requested-participant-id]` tiles with three fallback strategies per tile: `[data-self-name]` child textContent → tile `aria-label` (filtered to drop "More options"/"Menu" labels) → trimmed `textContent` <60 chars. Returns deduped list; degrades to `[]` on any failure. Linux adapter handles the queue command in the drain path but doesn't implement scraping (Track A is macOS).
- **Meet DOM inventory** (`docs/dom-inventory-meet.md`, new). Canonical list of every browser-side action operator performs on Meet — ~56 actions across 9 lifecycle phases (auth/sign-in, pre-join, lobby/admission, in-meeting setup, chat, admission queue, health, leave/cleanup, cross-cutting fallbacks). All selectors quoted verbatim from the macOS/Linux adapters, captions_js, session, and google_signin modules. Built as the parity checklist for Zoom + Teams adapter work.
- **Platform Expansion phase scoped** (`docs/roadmap.md`, post-MVP section). Replaced the bare three-row stub with a proper phase entry: working assumptions agreed (guest-first join, account-fallback only when bot-detected, four cross-platform rows beyond Meet's set: app-handoff interstitial / mic-mute pre-join / sign-in gate / kicked modal). Captions architectural decision matrix: Option A (native scrape where allowed; degrade gracefully) recommended as v1.5 floor; Option B (in-browser tab audio capture + local Whisper) as parallel research spike for true cross-platform parity (hard part: speaker diarization without it can't answer "what did Bob say"); Option C (Recall.ai) as bail-out; Option D (BlackHole audio loopback) rejected; Option E (hybrid) deferred. Per-platform work blocks estimated at ~30–45h total excluding Option B research.

**Carry-over caveat: chat_runner.py heartbeat code committed as part of this session.** The per-turn heartbeat additions (`_turn_start_ts`, `_turn_tool_count`, `_emit_turn_done`, the `Replied — N.Ns · M tools` line in `ui.ok`) were pre-existing untriaged work hanging in the working tree before this session — they hitched a ride in commit `114240c` because they were interleaved with the runner code I needed to touch for the hold/intro logic. Not my work; not validated this session; predates session 174. If anything looks weird about turn timing or stdout output, that's where to look.

**Exact next step (session 175).** Run the Zoom probe-state-list workflow. User opens a Zoom meeting in their daily Chrome (signed in as the operator account so DOM matches Playwright runtime; falls back to Incognito if any single probe looks weird since extensions inject DOM in daily Chrome that Playwright won't see) and walks through each lifecycle state: landing page → join modal → guest-name screen → in-meeting → leave. At each state Claude provides a self-contained DevTools-console IIFE that enumerates candidate elements (role / aria-label / data-* / text-content) for every action in the Meet inventory, ranks them by likelihood, and returns structured JSON. User pastes the output back; selectors land in `docs/dom-inventory-zoom.md`. **Probe #1 is gated on the user pasting a Zoom meeting URL** — Claude is ready to send the IIFE the moment that lands. Phase 14.13.1 (`gh repo create 1-800-operator/operator --public`) is still the next launch-blocking step after the platform-expansion DOM probes are done.

**Session 173 (April 29, 2026) — Phase 14.16 build/edit split + CLAUDE.md mirror data model. (Earlier in same session: credential hygiene shipped as `9a6d02e`.)**

Three slices, all unit-tested (56+ tests across the touched suites pass), live-validation plan written into `docs/handoff.md` for next session before users hit the new behavior. Two commits: `ebfb056` (memorialize credential hygiene in SECURITY.md + finalize docs/security.md L2 carry-over) and `4cfa334` (Phase 14.16 code + tests + handoff updates).

- **Slice 1 — `build` reset semantics** (`pipeline/setup.py:_maybe_reset_to_bundled` + `_edit_preset` + `_reveal`). `operator build <name>` now detects when user-scope cfg differs from bundled, prompts `Reset <name> to defaults? [y/n] (n)` with off-ramp `For surgical changes, use operator edit <name>`. Accept → backup to `<name>/config.yaml.bak.<YYYYMMDD-HHMMSS>` + reset to bundled + walk wizard. Decline → `WizardCancel` with explanatory message. Wizard's success line surfaces backup path: `Previous config saved at .../config.yaml.bak.<ts> — restore with cp ... if needed.` Per-agent surgical: sibling agents' configs never read or modified. Pristine state (user-scope == bundled byte-for-byte) skips the prompt silently — no point asking when there's nothing to lose. **The byte-comparison shortcut is the key UX move** — it means fresh installs walk the wizard without friction; only customized configs hit the gate.
- **Slice 2 — CLAUDE.md mirror data model** (`config.py:_resolve_claude_md_path` + `_read_claude_md_imports`, `pipeline/setup.py:1048` rewrite). Wizard step 4 retired the "bake content into ground_rules" approach. New shape stores PATHS in `claude_md_imports: [~/.claude/CLAUDE.md, ./CLAUDE.md, ./.claude/CLAUDE.md]`; `config.py` reads each fresh at every boot. `~/...` resolves against current `$HOME`, `./...` against current `cwd`, abs paths used as-is. Missing paths warn-and-skip via stderr (`[<bot>] ⚠ claude_md_imports: skipped missing source 'X' (resolved to Y)`) — common when configs travel across machines or the user launches from a different cwd than originally configured. Default at the wizard prompt flipped to `y` (mirror by default — opinionated; the claude agent's identity is "your Claude Code setup," and CLAUDE.md is part of that). Decline persists empty list (`claude_md_imports: []`) so re-runs don't silently re-mirror — the empty list is the persistence signal that the user *was* asked and *did* decline. **`normalize_path_for_storage` helper added to `claude_code_import.py` is unused in the critical path today** — reserved for a future "add custom CLAUDE.md path" UI; the auto-discovered labels (`~/.claude/CLAUDE.md`, `./CLAUDE.md`, `./.claude/CLAUDE.md`) are already in storage-ready form. **The big architectural shift here is path-vs-content** — content is ephemeral, path is the source of truth. Editing your `CLAUDE.md` takes effect next session without re-running the wizard.
- **Slice 3 — `edit` repurposed** (`__main__.py:_run_edit` + `_run_edit_env_file`, `pipeline/setup.py:run` signature change). `operator edit <bot>` no longer opens YAML in `$EDITOR` — it now invokes the same wizard as `operator build`, but with `target_agent=name` (skips preset gallery, jumps straight to `_edit_preset`) and `reset_allowed=False` (skips reset gate). Title bar reads `Operator edit wizard` vs `Operator build wizard` so users see which mode they're in. `operator edit .env` keeps the legacy `$EDITOR` flow because env-var key/value pairs are the wrong shape for a TUI. `operator edit <missing-bot>` fast-fails with `No agent named X found. Run operator build X to create one.` (rc=1, no wizard runs). Mirrors the claude prereq gate from `_step1_fighter_select` — if Claude Code isn't installed and the target is `claude`, fails with the same red `✗ claude agent requires Claude Code:` block that `build` shows. **The "edit = build minus reset gate" framing is the entire conceptual move** — same UI, same UX, same code paths. ~30 lines of wiring instead of a 500-line new TUI; future wizard improvements automatically apply to both modes.

**Tests: 9 new across 3 files, all 56+ tests in the touched suites pass.**
- `tests/test_setup.py` +5: `test_reset_to_bundled_skips_when_user_scope_missing`, `test_reset_to_bundled_skips_when_user_scope_identical_to_bundled`, `test_reset_to_bundled_writes_backup_and_replaces_when_confirmed` (with decoy `pm` agent verifying per-agent isolation), `test_reset_to_bundled_raises_wizard_cancel_on_decline`, `test_edit_preset_skips_reset_when_reset_allowed_false`, `test_run_target_agent_unknown_returns_1`.
- `tests/test_config_loader.py` +2: `test_claude_md_imports_mounted_into_system_prompt` (multi-source merge with section headers, walk order preserved), `test_claude_md_imports_missing_paths_skipped_silently` (cross-machine resilience).
- `tests/test_claude_code_import.py` +1: `test_normalize_path_for_storage_prefers_home_then_cwd_then_absolute`.

Refactored to a new `discover_claude_md_sources()` helper returning `[(short_label, content)]` tuples; wizard now renders accurate provenance for single OR multi-source. That asymmetry is what motivated the path-vs-content data-model rewrite in slice 2.

**Session 173 (earlier) — `~/.operator/` file-perm hardening pass prompted by the Vercel/Context AI OAuth-token incident.**

- **Framing.** User asked for an OAuth-scope audit after the Vercel/Context AI breach (malware on a dev machine → exfiltrated OAuth bearer tokens with overly broad scopes → Gmail compromise). Important conceptual distinction surfaced: we don't run a real OAuth flow at all — there is no `code → token` exchange and no `scope=` parameter. We keep a Playwright persistent Chrome profile + a `storage_state()` JSON export. So "trim scopes" doesn't apply directly; the analogous mitigation is "harden local artifacts."
- **Audit results.** Two credential stores: `~/.operator/browser_profile/` (full Chrome user-data-dir, `0o700` already) and `~/.operator/auth_state.json` (Playwright JSON, world-readable on default umask). Verified `auth_state.json` is NOT dead weight — macOS uses it as the recovery seed when `detect_page_state == "logged_out"` (Google rotates session cookies; without the JSON the bot dies instead of recovering); Linux uses it as the primary auth source via `new_context(storage_state=...)` since the Linux adapter has both a persistent-context "guest" path and a non-persistent "authenticated" path. Removing the JSON breaks Linux entirely. Fix F (delete the JSON) ruled out.
- **Hardening shipped.** Five-file commit `9a6d02e`:
  - `__main__.py:main()` — `os.umask(0o077)` at process start so any new file under `~/.operator/` is born `0o600` and any new dir `0o700` by default.
  - `pipeline/google_signin.py:_write_artifacts` — explicit `chmod 0o600` on both `auth_state.json` and `google_account.json` after the `context.storage_state()` and `account_file.write_text()` calls (belt + suspenders alongside the umask, in case the wizard is ever invoked from a context that re-sets umask).
  - `connectors/session.py:save_debug` — `mode=0o700` on `DEBUG_DIR` creation, `chmod 0o600` on each saved `.png` and `.html`.
  - `connectors/macos_adapter.py` + `connectors/linux_adapter.py` — `mode=0o700` passed to all `os.makedirs` for `BROWSER_PROFILE_DIR` and the in-line `DEBUG_DIR` creation in `chat_btn_not_found.png` paths. Closes the mkdir → chmod race window where the dir briefly existed with default perms before the chmod landed.
- **No retroactive migration.** Pre-prod, single machine, no other users — the new code only protects new writes; existing files keep their current perms. Out-of-scope per user direction.
- **`~/.operator/history/` flagged but not addressed.** Per-meeting chat JSONL is world-readable; same sensitivity tier as `debug/`. Harden before launch.
- **No new tests.** Hardening is structural — the umask is set once and stamps every subsequent operation; the chmod calls are belt-and-suspenders. Manual smoke test (delete artifacts, re-run wizard, `ls -la` to verify `0o600` / `0o700`) is the standard validation; deferred per the no-prod scope.
- **`docs/security.md` L2 updated** to reflect the new ground-truth (was previously citing only `browser_profile/` `0o700`).
- **Exact next step.** Phase 14.13.1 — `gh repo create 1-800-operator/operator --public` and push current `main`. Open question to settle first: fresh start vs. GitHub repo-transfer flow to preserve history + open PRs + redirects from `shapirojojo/operator`. Pre-existing untriaged code changes remain in the working tree (more than the session 170 handoff listed — `claude_code_import.py`, `setup.py`, `test_claude_code_import.py`, `agent-context.md`, `roadmap.md` joined the carry-over set during sessions 171/172). User to triage before the rename in 14.13.2 so they don't get tangled in a giant rename diff.

### Session 173 carry-overs (running list)

- **(NEW)** `~/.operator/history/` is world-readable (`drwxr-xr-x`). Contains per-meeting chat JSONL (every chat message ever sent through any bot). Same sensitivity tier as the `debug/` dumps now hardened. Mitigation: walk every `Path.mkdir` / `os.makedirs` site that touches `~/.operator/history/` and add `mode=0o700` + `0o600` on the JSONL writes. Also: chmod the existing dir + files retroactively at first boot when we approach prod (one-shot in `_migrate_legacy_user_artifacts`).

Worth a unit test in `tests/test_perm_hardening.py` that monkey-patches `os.umask` and asserts we set `0o077` early in `main()`, plus a wizard-path test that verifies `os.chmod(0o600)` on `auth_state.json` after `_write_artifacts`. **Session 172 (April 28, 2026) — Phase 14.14 live-validation pass + project-scope parity for MCP/skills/CLAUDE.md + Track A pre-flight MCP health surface.** Walked the 7-test handoff plan end-to-end; in the process discovered the user's installed config was *already* in a doubly-broken state from a prior session 171 boot (corrupt `permissions.always_ask` entry + duplicate orphan `mcp_servers` entries from per-entry merge writing before validation caught the corruption). All 6 of the planned tests we exercised passed cleanly; #6 (Track B chat surface) skipped because the v1 product is now narrowed to Track A only.

- **V1 narrows to Track A.** User confirmed mid-session: only the `claude` agent ships in v1; `pm`/`engineer`/`designer` (Track B) are not part of the product surface. Memory saved (`project_v1_track_a_only.md`). This re-frames any Track-B-only fix as lower priority and elevates Track A architectural gaps to launch-blocker status.
- **Project-scope MCP blindness fixed.** `extract_imported_mcps` in `pipeline/claude_code_import.py` only walked `~/.claude.json#mcpServers` (user scope); project-scope entries at `~/.claude.json#projects.<cwd>.mcpServers` were silently dropped. Real-world impact: Sentry MCP missing from the imported set, and `claude mcp add demo --` (which defaults to project scope) never reached operator. New `_collect_mcp_servers_from_cfg(cfg, cwd)` helper merges both scopes (project wins on collision); cwd is injectable for testability. 2 tests.
- **`(HTTP)` annotation in `claude mcp list` regex tolerated.** Same file. Original regex required `URL\s+-\s+status` immediately after the URL, but claude-code prints `URL (HTTP) - status` for HTTP-not-SSE remote MCPs (Sentry being a real-world example). Added `(?:\s+\([A-Z]+\))?` group. 1 test.
- **Skills: project-scope walk added.** `pipeline/skills.py:load_skills` gained an optional `cwd` param (defaults to `Path.cwd()`); walks `<cwd>/.claude/skills/` implicitly so Claude Code's project-scoped skills surface without needing a config edit. Project scope wins on name collision (last-wins after shared library + external paths). 2 tests. Same shape of fix as MCP.
- **CLAUDE.md: project-scope walk added.** `read_user_claude_md(cwd)` now also reads `<cwd>/CLAUDE.md` and `<cwd>/.claude/CLAUDE.md`. Single-source returns bare content (preserves old wizard contract); multi-source includes section headers per source. Wizard-time only — runtime is unaffected because the inner claude subprocess does its own native CLAUDE.md discovery via `cwd=os.getcwd()` from `build_provider`. 2 tests.
- **Track A pre-flight MCP health surface (the v1 launch concern).** New `discover_mcp_health()` parses `claude mcp list` for status (`✓ Connected`, `! Needs authentication`, `✗ Failed to connect`). `_sync_claude_imports` prints one stderr line per unhealthy entry: `[claude] ⚠ MCP needs attention: <name> — <status>`. Without this, Track A users only learn an MCP is broken when its tools silently fail in-meeting — the inner-claude subprocess swallows the startup error. Stderr-only (a1) with raw status (b1) per the surgical scoping decision; chat-surface variant queued as future polish if needed. 2 tests.
- **Doubly-broken file mode found.** Session 171's per-entry merge + atomic write fires BEFORE schema validation. When the user's pre-existing config had a corrupt `permissions.always_ask` (`{'Taskmcp_servers': None}` from a missing newline in an earlier hand-edit), the safeguards wrote a new correct `mcp_servers:` block at top level *before* the validator rejected the still-malformed permissions entry. Net result: file ended up with both original corruption AND a duplicate orphan import block. Logged as a Phase 14.15 deferred follow-up.
- **Test totals.** `tests/test_claude_code_import.py` 32 → 37/37 (added 5 across project-scope MCP, HTTP regex, mcp_health × 2, project CLAUDE.md × 2). `tests/test_skills.py` +2 (project-scope walk + collision). All other tests unchanged.
- **Commit.** `e174eb3` — only Phase 14.15 work; pre-existing carry-overs (`README.md`, `docs/handoff.md`, `docs/live-skill-tests.md`, `chat_runner.py`, `debug/*`, `tests/test_stdout_heartbeat.py`) intentionally untouched per the session 171 handoff note.
- **Exact next step.** Phase 14.13.1 (`gh repo create 1-800-operator/operator --public`) remains the launch step. Optional pre-launch: address the order-of-operations bug (task #5) so the doubly-broken file mode can't recur.

### Session 172 carry-overs (running list)

- **(NEW)** Order-of-operations in session 171's safeguards: per-entry merge + atomic write fires before schema validation. When pre-existing corruption survives the merge (e.g. malformed `permissions.always_ask`), the user ends up with a doubly-broken file (original corruption + new clean block appended). Fix order should be: parse → validate raw → merge → validate post-merge → write. Caught while live-testing on session 172. Not a runtime bug today (validator still exits 2 with a clean message) but the file's state on disk is worse than before the boot.
- **(NEW)** `discover_mcp_health()` shells out to `claude mcp list` a SECOND time after `discover_hosted_mcps_via_cli` already did it on the same boot. Doubles the ~3s shell-out cost (so ~6s per boot for the claude agent). Documented hash-based fast-path on `~/.claude.json#mcpServers` would naturally cover both calls if implemented.
- **(NEW)** CLAUDE.md project-scope walk is wizard-time only — `read_user_claude_md` is called from `_auto_import_claude_setup` to merge into `ground_rules`, but runtime CLAUDE.md is delivered by the inner subprocess's own native discovery. If the wizard ever runs from a directory the user doesn't intend as the runtime working dir, it'll merge the wrong project's rules. Acceptable today (wizard usually runs once per install in the user's home or operator dir) but worth noting if multi-project workflows emerge.
- **(NEW)** Skills cwd-walk picks up whatever `<cwd>/.claude/skills/` exists at boot time. Operator dir doesn't have one today, so this codepath is exercised only by tests. First real user with a project-scope skill will surface any wiring issues.

**Session 171 (April 28, 2026) — Track A captions-on-demand + YAML lifecycle hardening. Demo bug ("what name did I just say" failed even with captions on) root-caused, fixed via a bundled `recall_transcript` MCP server. Same session swept the YAML auto-import / wizard rewrite cycle: atomic writes, schema validation, ruamel round-trip, always-re-import with per-entry merge, MCP-failure chat surfacing, `operator edit` UX fix. All shipped under new Phase 14.14 (8 sub-steps, 33 new tests, 1 live test in Meet).**

- **Captions-on-demand (the headliner).** Live demo broke when user said "Purple" aloud and Claude couldn't tell them what color was said. Diagnosis from log: `pipeline.transcript.caption_finalized` events fired, captions were appended to the meeting record, `_tail_messages` wrapped them as `<spoken>` blocks correctly — but `claude_cli.complete_streaming` only sends `messages[-1]` to its long-lived subprocess and discards the tail. Fix: bundled `transcript` MCP server (FastMCP stdio) registered with Claude Code via `--mcp-config <tempdir>/mcp.json` written per-spawn. Inner-claude calls `recall_transcript(minutes_back?, last_n?)` against the meeting JSONL on demand. Live-tested: spoke "Purple", asked "what color did I just say?", Claude replied "Hey Jojo — purple."
- **YAML safeguards (lifecycle hardening).** User's edit of `~/.operator/agents/claude/config.yaml` lost a newline between `- Task` and `mcp_servers:`, producing structurally-valid YAML where `permissions.always_ask` contained a dict, which then crashed `chat_runner.py:177` with `TypeError: '<' not supported between dict and str`. Discussion led to a focused trim list: ship the safeguards that prevent confusing crashes (atomic write, schema validation, comment preservation, surface MCP failures in chat), draw the line on auto-fixing user mess (path rewriting at import, secret detection — out of scope, user's responsibility, documented). Six items shipped: ruamel round-trip preservation, atomic writes, schema validation with surgical errors, always-re-import with per-entry merge, MCP failure chat-surfacing, `operator edit` UX confirmation.
- **Test coverage added.** `tests/test_transcript_mcp.py` (8), `tests/test_claude_mcp_sync.py` (5), `tests/test_config_validation.py` (10), `tests/test_mcp_failure_chat.py` (5). Plus an ad-hoc handshake test confirming `recall_transcript` is discoverable through real stdio MCP.
- **Pre-existing uncommitted changes carried over.** `src/_1_800_operator/pipeline/chat_runner.py`, `README.md`, `docs/live-skill-tests.md`, `tests/test_stdout_heartbeat.py`. Still NOT from this session — user to triage separately. This session's commit deliberately scopes only to the 14.14 work (MCP server, YAML safeguards, tests, docs, roadmap).
- **Exact next step.** Live-validate the 14.14 changes per the test plan in `docs/handoff.md` (7 in-Meet tests covering captions-on-demand, edit UX, per-entry merge, schema validation, ruamel preservation, MCP-failure chat surfacing, atomic-write hygiene). ### Session 171 carry-overs (running list)

- **(NEW)** Track A MCP startup failures (inside the claude subprocess) are NOT surfaced in chat — only Track B is. Out-of-scope per the trim list, but if a user installs a transcript-server-style bundled MCP that fails to spawn under inner-claude, they'd only learn from inner-claude failing to call the tool. **Session 170 (April 28, 2026) — Naming decision: `operator` → `operator`. Domain `1-800-operator.com` purchased, GitHub org `1-800-operator` created, PyPI placeholder `1-800-operator` v0.0.1 published. New Phase 14.13 (rebrand) added to roadmap, blocking launch.**

- **Naming research.** ~25 candidates evaluated against PyPI / npm / GitHub / USPTO / domains / AI-product mindshare across multiple parallel agent sweeps. Final shortlist was `operator`, `speeddial`, `pageboy`, `participant`. `operator` chosen for utilitarian fit + clean CLI binary; `1-800-operator.com` solves the "every desirable operator.X domain is taken" problem with a recognizable wordmark whose curl one-liner reads like a phone number — matches the switchboard-operator metaphor. Hard limitations accepted: PyPI bare name `operator` is permanently blocked (Python stdlib reservation), `github.com/operator` org is taken (real entity since 2008), SEO permanently downstream of K8s Operator pattern + OpenAI's deprecated Operator product.
- **Domain `1-800-operator.com`** purchased via the user's registrar (Cloudflare/Porkbun TBD). DNS not yet wired for hosting; reuses the Phase 14.6 work pattern (currently configured for `operator.build`).
- **GitHub org `1-800-operator`** created via web flow (org creation is web-only, no `gh` CLI command for it). Repo not yet created — exact next step is `gh repo create 1-800-operator/operator --public` from inside the repo.
- **PyPI placeholder `1-800-operator` v0.0.1** published using the user's PyPI account token (revoked immediately after upload per security best practice — don't share tokens in chat). Stub package source preserved at `pypi-stub/` in the repo for any future republish; the `operator` console script in the wheel prints the curl install instructions and exits 2. Live at <https://pypi.org/project/1-800-operator/0.0.1/>.
- **Phase 14.13 added to roadmap** with five sub-steps (repo create, codebase rename, Phase-16 doc updates, GitHub redirect, CLAUDE.md/agent-context.md/roadmap.md sweep). Slotted *before* 14.12.3/14.12.4/14.12.5 because the rebrand touches the wizard copy and bundled agent configs that those phases edit — easier to do once on the new name.
- **Pre-existing uncommitted changes from prior sessions remain unsynced** — `src/_1_800_operator/__main__.py`, `src/_1_800_operator/pipeline/chat_runner.py`, `README.md`, `docs/live-skill-tests.md`, `tests/test_stdout_heartbeat.py`. These are NOT from session 170; user to triage separately. Session 170's commit only touches `pypi-stub/`, `docs/roadmap.md`, `docs/agent-context.md`, `docs/handoff.md`.
- **Exact next step.** Phase 14.13.1 — `gh repo create 1-800-operator/operator --public`, push current main as the initial commit. Then 14.13.2 (the actual codebase rename, ~3–4h) which is the bulk of the work and the riskiest step.

Bundled claude config gets `ToolSearch` in default `auto_approve` (kills the deferred-tool-loader prompt that fired on every first MCP-tool turn). Wizard adds a Permissions step (single tool-level checklist, claude_cli only at land time). 11 unit tests; README "MCP permissions" section added.

Wizard Permissions step gate dropped — now fires for all bots. 4 new tests covering translation in both directions and chat_runner integration.
- **Voice mode redesign (`325cbdb`) and simplification (`66bb71c`) — both merged to main.** Replaced `permission_verbosity: terse | verbose` with `agent.voice: plain | technical`. First commit shipped per-tool English templating in Python (`_format_plain` per-tool table, `_friendly_mcp_name` MCP-tool translator, `_narrator_plain` category classifier — ~150 lines). Live test exposed two problems: (a) hardcoded English broke persona customization (pirate bot would still see modern conversational English), (b) the long tail of grammar bugs (`"find a organizations"` — wrong article + plural mismatch + `a` vs `an`). User pushed back on the architecture; second commit reverted templating, replaced with two ground_rules directives (self-narrate auto-approved tools, self-preamble destructive tools) so claude speaks in its own persona-faithful voice. Operator emits a sterile, neutral approval challenge as the safety gate; persona lives in prompt territory. Net: -150 lines, persona customization works free, the article/plural bug class is structurally impossible.
- **URL-imperative-field bug fixed.** Terse fallback at `permission_chat_handler.py:113-122` (now expanded to imperative-aware) was collapsing any field over 80 chars to `(89 B)` — the Sentry URL prompt in the morning's run rendered as `url=(89 B)`, defeating the safety check. New `_IMPERATIVE_FIELD_NAMES` set (`url`, `path`, `file_path`, `command`, `query`, `pattern`, `search`, `notebook_path`) shows verbatim regardless of length, with a 1KB sanity cap. Same principle as Bash command staying verbatim. Verified live in the 16:24 run — the entire `naturalLanguageQuery=unresolved production issues from the last 24 hours, sorted by recency` rendered visibly.
- **`confirm_tools` / `read_tools` deferred carry-over:** bundled bot YAML rewrites (deleting per-MCP `read_tools`/`confirm_tools` in favor of inline `permissions:` blocks) intentionally not done. Back-compat translation handles them at runtime; rewrites are mechanical follow-up.

The `operator` shim at `~/.local/bin/operator` is already a symlink to `/Users/jojo/Desktop/operator/operator`, which is a wrapper that activates the venv, sets `PYTHONPATH=src`, and runs `python -m _1_800_operator`. So `operator run claude` from any directory always runs the live repo on the current branch. The `python -m _1_800_operator` workaround I suggested mid-session was unnecessary.

**Session 168 (April 25, 2026) — Phase 14.12.2 live-meeting Sessions 1+2 COMPLETE (8/8 PASS) + 4 UX fixes shipped + PR #5 open. One commit (`0c1bcc9`) on branch `session-168-track-a-ux-polish`, ~3h.**

- **Live-validation pass through Sessions 1+2 of `docs/live-skill-tests.md`.** Session 1 (engineer flow): codebase walkthrough → real `chat_runner.py:283` cite for `_loop`; migration plan (Slack connector) → 6 phases naming real files (`MeetingConnector`, `MeetingRecord`, `agents/<name>/config.yaml`); test generation for `is_valid_email` fixture → 7-case pytest passing; live `--version` CLI edit → `git diff` showed clean 5-line patch, reverted post-test. Session 2 (PM/sprint flow): scope estimate via Linear MCP (fixture issue ENG-167 created via tool); PRD from 90-second caption transcript → 7-section PRD at `/tmp/prd_stealth_mode.md` with real-phrase quotes ("ship a V1 within two weeks", "intro message on join", "captions ingestion when stealth"); release notes for last 10 commits via `gh` (after install) → grouped by Track A / Live validation / Self-loop watchdog / Docs with all 10 SHAs cited; full structured PR review of #5 via `gh pr diff` → real `file:line` cites including the operator-precedence callout at `permission_chat_handler.py:122`.
- **Four UX fixes shipped during the live run** (commit `0c1bcc9`, +233/-11):
  1. **`claude_cli` cwd → `os.getcwd()`.** Default `$HOME` left inner-claude with no project context — bot asked permission for `Bash: ls /Users/jojo` before tracing the codebase. `build_provider()` now passes `cwd=os.getcwd()` mirroring the bare `claude` CLI. Verified on re-run: silent Read/Grep, no `ls $HOME` round-trip.
  2. **Intro pre-warm + participant-count seed.** Intro LLM call ran AFTER `_connector.join()` completed and the `saw_others` gate could wait up to 3s for the next `PARTICIPANT_CHECK_INTERVAL` poll. Moved `_generate_intro` thread to BEFORE the join wait (LLM call needs only a live LLM, not browser state) and added a synchronous `get_participant_count()` seed at the top of `_loop()`. Join → intro-posted: ~8s → ~1–2s.
  3. **Terse confirmation prompts.** New `_format_terse(tool_name, args)` in `permission_chat_handler.py` collapses bulk content fields per tool: `Write <path> (<size>)`, `Edit <path>`, `MultiEdit <path> (N hunks)`, `WebFetch <url> — <prompt>`, `Task: <desc>`, `Read/Grep/Glob/LS/WebSearch` get tight one-liners. **Bash commands stay verbatim** because the user's safety check depends on seeing the literal command. New config knob `agent.permission_verbosity: terse | verbose` (default terse). Both modes regression-tested live.
  4. **Progress narrator for auto-approved tools.** `ClaudeCLIProvider.set_progress_callback(callback)` late-binds a per-`tool_use` callback (called on the pump thread); streaming pump scans `assistant` event content for `tool_use` blocks and fires the callback. `ChatRunner._on_tool_use` only narrates auto-approved tools (always-ask tools post their own prompt — feedback enough); throttled by `min_silence_seconds=4` (skip if user-facing send happened recently) and `throttle_seconds=5` (gap between narrator messages). Posts as `"Working: Read /tmp/foo.py; Grep 'def main' in src/"` reusing `_format_terse`. Config block: `agent.progress_narration: { enabled, min_silence_seconds, throttle_seconds }`.
- **`gh` CLI installed + authed (`gho_***` keyring).** Test 2.4 first run used WebFetch (function-level cites only); after install + `gh auth login`, re-run got line-level `file:line` cites via `gh pr diff 5`. Add `gh` as an explicit prereq in 14.12.5 README rewrite.
- **PR #5 open** at github.com/dufis1/operator/pull/5 — bundles the 4 UX fixes (the head commit) but the PR diffs against `origin/main`, which is 40 commits behind local `main`, so the PR currently contains 41 commits / 109 files / +10.5k lines across sessions 152–168. When ready to land: either push local main first (`git push origin main`) so future PRs diff cleanly, or split by phase. The bot's own structured review caught this and recommended both options.
- **Latent bug surfaced by Claude's PR review** (file as deferred carry-over): `permission_chat_handler.py:122` operator-precedence — `return f"{tool_name}: " + ", ".join(parts) if parts else tool_name` parses as `(...) if parts else tool_name`, so empty-args correctly returns just `tool_name` (no colon) but it's "correct by accident." Wrap the truthy branch in parens to make intent explicit. Small but real.
- **Linear ticket fixture created via MCP** — ENG-167 "Add `operator list-skills` subcommand to print enabled skills for the current bot," in the Engineering team. Used as the fixture for Test 2.1.
- **New log lines** (`ChatRunner: progress narrator wired (...)`, `ChatRunner: seed participant_count=N (saw_others=True)`) — should flow into `debug/model-log.md` whenever that file gets created during 14.12 finalization. File doesn't exist yet (carryover from session 167's deferred list).
- **Working-tree state at session end.** Session-168 changes committed in `0c1bcc9` and pushed to `origin/session-168-track-a-ux-polish`. `docs/handoff.md` updated for next session (gitignored). Untracked debug PNGs/HTMLs from prior sessions still float — same precedent.

**Session 167 (April 25, 2026) — Phase 14.12.2 live-meeting Session 0 COMPLETE end-to-end + 6 fixes shipped. One commit (`6f6d7f3`), ~3h.**

- **Ran Session 0 of `docs/live-skill-tests.md` against a real Meet** with the user driving chat. All 6 safety gates green: subscription-auth assertion, PreToolUse allow round-trip, auto-approve silent path, deny + redirect, mid-meeting subprocess crash recovery, fail-loud on API-key leak. Validated track-A architecture end-to-end before the use-case sessions.
- **Six real bugs found and fixed in the process** — the ROI of running Session 0 first was very high. All fixes in commit `6f6d7f3`:
  1. `__main__.py:_print_startup_banner` crashed `TypeError: sequence item 4: expected str instance, NoneType` on every track-A boot. Root cause: `LLM_MODEL = None` under `claude_cli` provider (model is whatever the user's `claude` CLI is configured for, not pinned in our config). Fix: substitute `f"{config.LLM_PROVIDER} (subscription)"` when `LLM_MODEL` is None.
  2. `macos_adapter.py:587` `pre_join_ready` selector waited the full 15s timeout when the no-URL `meet.new` flow auto-joined the bot already-in-meeting. The selector was {Join now, Ask to join, Turn on/off camera, Sign in} — none of those exist post-join. Fix: added `button[aria-label*="Leave call"]` to the OR list so the wait short-circuits the moment the in-meeting Leave button is visible.
  3. `macos_adapter.py:677` then hunted for "Turn off camera" button (5s timeout) which doesn't exist post-join either. Fix: gated the entire camera-toggle block on `not already_in_meeting`. **Combined effect of bugs 2+3: cold-start `total_join` 25.7s → 4.6s.**
  4. `__main__.py` MCP `KeyError: 'command'` on every boot. Root cause: under track A, `config.py:273` writes `MCP_SERVERS[name] = {"_track_a_toggle_only": True}` (no `command` key) — correct, since the user's `claude` subprocess owns those MCPs via `~/.claude.json`, operator's process must NOT try to connect them. But all 4 MCP touchpoints (`_run_terminal`, `_run_macos` background thread, `_run_linux`, `preflight_mcp_readiness`) called `mcp.connect_all()` regardless. Fix: gated each on `config.LLM_PROVIDER != "claude_cli"`. Side benefit: kills the "Heads-up — claude-ai-X didn't load" banner the bot was sending into chat as its first message under track A.
  5. **Duplicate-message bug** in claude_cli streaming path (`pipeline/llm.py:305` + `pipeline/chat_runner.py:510`). Under track A, `_tools_for_llm()` returns `None` (no MCP, no skills), so `llm.ask` took the no-tools shortcut and returned a raw string. Chat_runner saw `isinstance(result, str)` and called `_send(result)` — but the `on_paragraph` callback had already streamed every paragraph during the turn, so the user got the whole reply twice. Fix: when `on_paragraph` is provided, return `{"type": "text", "content": reply, "streamed": True}` like the with-tools path; removed the now-vestigial `isinstance(result, str)` early-return.
  6. **Paragraph-smoosh bug** in `claude_cli.py` streaming. When claude calls a tool mid-turn, the wire emits two `assistant` events with text deltas at index 0 of each (indices reset between messages). Index-based break detection didn't help. New approach: use the terminal `assistant` event itself as the paragraph boundary — when it fires and buffer has pending text, force-flush it as a paragraph. Also accumulate canonical_text across all sub-messages joined by `\n\n` so the parity check stops failing on every multi-message turn (was warning `streamed accumulator (86 chars) diverged from canonical assistant event (58 chars)` every time).
  7. **Restart-opener framing caused self-denial.** The synthesized opener said "You are picking up a conversation that was already in progress" — model read this as third-party transcript and denied its own real tool actions when asked to recap (e.g. "I incorrectly claimed I wrote /tmp/different.txt — no file was actually written" when the file DID exist). Fix in `_build_synthesized_opener`: reframed as "Continuation of YOUR in-progress chat-meeting conversation. The Assistant lines below are YOUR prior turns... Treat any tool actions you previously claimed as actions you performed and that are already complete. If you need to verify, read the relevant file/state — do not deny your own prior claims without doing so first." Live-tested: bot now correctly recaps three real file ops without hedging.
- **Live-validation methodology that worked:** post the test number, user types the trigger phrase + interacts, says "done," I grep `/tmp/operator.log` for the per-test markers and the file-system effects, post a pass/fail summary, move to the next test. Tight cadence let us find + fix bugs in-flight without abandoning the session.
- **Deferred carry-over.** The synthesized opener still doesn't carry tool calls or tool results — only `(user_text, assistant_text)` pairs in `_turn_history`. Acceptable when prior assistant text is honest (the opener-framing fix gets us most of the way), but would inherit corruption if any assistant text ever lied. Real fix is recording `tool_use` + `tool_result` events on the wire and replaying them in the opener — invasive, worth its own phase. Filed in roadmap status note for Phase 14.12.2.
- **Working-tree state at session end.** Everything committed in `6f6d7f3`. Untracked debug PNGs/HTMLs from prior sessions still float — same precedent.
- **Exact next step.** Session 168 runs **Sessions 1–3 of `docs/live-skill-tests.md`** (engineer flow, PM/sprint flow, live ops). Session 1 needs only the operator repo (~15–20m). Session 2 needs a fixture Linear ticket pre-created (~15m). Session 3 has the heaviest setup — Sentry account + project + DSN + fixture trigger script (~15m prep + 10m test). After live validation lands fully, **14.12.3** (track-B repositioning), **14.12.4** (skills migration to `~/.claude/skills/`), and **14.12.5** (README rewrite) remain before MVP can ship.

**Session 166 (April 26, 2026) — Phase 14.12.2 (track A claude_cli provider) COMPLETE in code. One commit (`28153b9`), ~6h. Live-meeting validation pending in session 167.**

- **Shipped end-to-end the track-A LLM provider.** New `pipeline/providers/claude_cli.py` wraps a per-meeting `claude -p --input-format stream-json --output-format stream-json` subprocess as an `LLMProvider`. Lazy spawn, subscription-auth assertion (`apiKeySource == "none"`) at the first system-init event, paragraph streaming via `--include-partial-messages`, PreToolUse hook + named-pipe IPC bridge, restart-on-death recovery using probe 7's synthesized-opener strategy.
- **Five new probes ran before the implementation** (probes 4–8 in `debug/permission_mcp_spike/`): baseline hello (probe 4 — sanity floor), per-turn vs per-meeting head-to-head (probes 5/6 — per-meeting wins 4× on follow-up turns: 1.3s vs 5.4s), restart-with-history-rebuild (probe 7 — strategy 2 synthesized opener wins on bounded recovery latency), partial-message event shape (probe 8 — locked the `stream_event.event.content_block_delta.delta.text_delta` envelope). Findings written up at `debug/permission_mcp_spike/SPIKE_PER_TURN_VS_PER_MEETING.md`.
- **Architectural redesign mid-session: dropped worktree isolation.** Original spike-report recommendation #3 was per-meeting `--worktree` as second line of defense. Re-derived from track-A's threat model: chat-confirmation hook gates every destructive tool call, so the sandbox's purpose (catching damage between coarse-grained approvals — required under track B's `delegate_to_claude_code` model) doesn't apply. Sub-agent opacity (probe 2b finding) handled by denying the `Task` tool in the always-ask list. Result: track-A claude operates directly on whatever absolute paths the user names, multi-repo workflows in one meeting work naturally, no path-rewriting layer.
- **Companion modules.** `pipeline/permission_bridge.py` (Python rewrite of `perm_bridge.sh` — runs as standalone script with stdlib-only imports, dodging the PYTHONPATH-vs-pip-install dance because operator isn't `pip install -e .`'d in the venv during dev). `pipeline/permission_chat_handler.py` (round-trips PreToolUse decisions through meeting chat — `auto_approve` list runs silently, everything else posts a chat prompt and blocks; `_is_yes` detection mirrors `chat_runner._handle_confirmation`; reads chat directly from connector and claims consumed user-reply IDs in `runner._seen_ids` to prevent the main poll loop from re-feeding them to the LLM).
- **Wiring.** `build_provider()` routes `llm.provider: "claude_cli"`. `config.py` parses new `permissions.{auto_approve, always_ask}` lists (defaults empty so track-B bots are unaffected) and skips full MCP block parse when LLM_PROVIDER is claude_cli (toggle-only). `chat_runner._wire_track_a_permissions()` runs at the top of `run()` — if the provider is `ClaudeCLIProvider`, build the handler from config and `provider.set_permission_handler(handler)` before `_loop()`.
- **agents/claude/config.yaml rewritten 398→95 lines** for track-A schema. `provider: claude_cli`, no `model` / `history_messages`, new `permissions:` block with sensible defaults (Read/Grep/Glob/LS/WebSearch silent; Bash/Write/Edit/MultiEdit/NotebookEdit/WebFetch/Task always-ask), `mcp_servers: {}` placeholder (wizard populates from `~/.claude.json` on first boot), personality + ground_rules rewritten to drop the `delegate_to_claude_code` paragraphs (claude IS the meeting brain, no delegation indirection). User-level `~/.operator/agents/claude/config.yaml` was deleted at end-of-session per user request so the first `operator run claude` reseeds from the new bundle.
- **Per-skill disable not supported in CLI today** per [GH #43928](https://github.com/anthropics/claude-code/issues/43928). Only `--disable-slash-commands` (nuclear) exists. Track-A skills toggle is all-or-none for now; revisit when Anthropic ships per-skill control.
- **Tests.** `tests/test_claude_cli_provider.py` (8 smoke tests, all hit the real `claude` CLI under subscription auth): 3-turn arithmetic conversation, idempotent stop, warmup + complete, streaming paragraph callback (3 flushes, 98% coverage of canonical reply), permission allow path (Write lands), permission deny path (Write blocked, claude relays denial), mid-meeting subprocess restart with history rebuild (kill pid mid-conversation, fresh subprocess, synthesized opener feeds prior transcript, claude correctly answers turn 3 with the rebuilt context), `build_provider` selection. `tests/test_permission_chat_handler.py` (8 unit tests with a fake connector + stub runner): yes-detection variants, prompt formatting + truncation, no-arg formatting, auto-approve silent path, chat round-trip yes/no, own-echo skipping, seen_ids claiming. All 16 pass.
- **docs/live-skill-tests.md rewritten for track A.** Every prior use case (codebase-walkthrough, migration-plan, test-generation, scope-estimate, prd-from-discussion, release-notes, pr-review, live-bug-triage, live coding edit) preserved but reshaped to exercise claude's native tools + inherited MCPs instead of the operator skill bundles + `delegate_to_claude_code`. Pass signals unchanged where the use case is the same. New Session 0 (track-A safety) added with 6 gates: subscription-auth log line, PreToolUse allow round-trip, auto-approve silent (Read), always-ask deny with reason, mid-meeting subprocess crash recovery, fail-loud on intentional API-key leak. Session 0 gates everything that follows — if the architecture isn't round-tripping, no use-case test can succeed.
- **Working-tree state at session end.** Everything committed in `28153b9`. Untracked debug PNGs/HTMLs from sessions 163/164 still float — same precedent as prior sessions.
- **Exact next step.** Session 167 runs `docs/live-skill-tests.md` against a real Meet, starting with Session 0 (track-A safety gates). Pre-flight: confirm `claude auth status --json` shows authenticated, run `operator build` so the bundled track-A claude config seeds into `~/.operator/agents/claude/config.yaml`, verify `claude mcp list` shows the MCPs we'll lean on (Linear, GitHub, Sentry), verify `/tmp/operator.log` is wired. Then Session 0 → Session 1 (engineer flow) → Session 2 (PM/sprint flow) → Session 3 (live-bug triage). After live validation lands, 14.12.3 (track-B repositioning), 14.12.4 (skills migration to ~/.claude/skills/), 14.12.5 (README rewrite) remain before MVP can ship.

**Session 165 (April 26, 2026) — Phase 14.12.1 Permission MCP spike COMPLETE. One commit (`4b0e96d`), ~3.5h.**

- **Three probes ran end-to-end** against `claude -p` under the user's Claude Max subscription (no `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`). All three artifacts in `debug/permission_mcp_spike/` are committed and re-runnable: `cli_probe_01_hook_ipc.py` (happy path), `cli_probe_02b_subagent_bypass.py` (sub-agent visibility under bypass), `cli_probe_03_deny.py` (deny semantics). Plus `perm_bridge.sh` (the IPC bridge prototype) and stream-json captures.
- **Probe 1 — happy path:** PreToolUse hook fires synchronously, named-pipe IPC writes the tool-use details to the parent (this script simulates operator), parent's "allow" decision is honored, file is written. `apiKeySource: "none"` in stream-json's system-init event confirmed actual subscription billing end-to-end. Round-trip latency negligible (<1s for IPC).
- **Probe 2b — sub-agent visibility:** definitively confirmed sub-agent (Task tool) inner tool calls do NOT fire our hook. Top-level `Agent` dispatch DOES fire (full sub-agent prompt visible in our hook payload — gateable). Sub-agent's internal Writes appear in stream-json with `parent_tool_use_id` set — visible for chat progress reporting but not gateable inline. The architectural mitigation is per-session worktree sandbox.
- **Probe 3 — deny path:** clean semantics. Hook returns deny → claude exits 0 with `subtype: "success"`, `permission_denials` array populated, deny-reason text appears verbatim in claude's final result text. No retries, no loops.
- **Two corrections to early research surfaced.** First: `--permission-prompt-tool` does NOT exist on the actual installed CLI (early research agents got this wrong, both citing it as a CLI flag). The real mechanism is PreToolUse hooks via `--settings <file-or-json>`. Second: `--settings <file-or-json>` DOES exist despite the public docs at code.claude.com claiming it doesn't — direct `claude --help` confirms. Generalizable lesson captured in Hard Won Knowledge: when integrating with another tool, verify the API surface against the actual installed binary, not against agent-recalled docs (which can be stale or hallucinated).
- **Agent SDK pathway researched but not probed.** Definitively API-key-only per [GitHub #559](https://github.com/anthropics/claude-agent-sdk-python/issues/559) and confirmed in the Anthropic docs ("Anthropic does not allow third party developers to offer claude.ai login..."). Running a probe would have burned API credits to generate paper-only data on a path structurally incompatible with track A's no-API-key promise. Documented in the spike report from research alone.
- **PreToolUse policy layering locked.** Three layers, no overlap, captured in the handoff: (1) operator's PreToolUse hook itself is internal plumbing — load-bearing, not user-tunable, like the chat-polling loop. (2) Native Claude Code `permissions.allow` / `ask` / `deny` rules in `~/.claude/settings.json` compose naturally — they pre-evaluate before our hook fires, so user's solo-CLI muscle memory transfers cleanly. (3) operator's "what to confirm in chat" knob is exposed in track A config as `permissions.auto_approve` / `always_ask` lists — the meeting-context tunable. Wizard does NOT expose this surface (track A's pitch is zero setup); `operator edit claude` is the power-user path. Custom hook layering not supported in track A — users wanting that belong in track B.
- **Architectural recommendation for 14.12.2** captured in `docs/permission-mcp-spike.md`. Five points: (1) `pipeline/providers/claude_cli.py` implementing `LLMProvider` with one `claude -p` subprocess per LLM turn (or per meeting — spike both during impl, default to simpler). (2) Named-pipe IPC bridge between hook script and operator parent. (3) Per-session worktree sandboxing as second-line defense. (4) **Subscription-auth assertion at startup** — read system-init event's `apiKeySource` and fail loud if not `"none"`. Catches any future env-var leak (the same class as session-164's $5 burn). (5) Defer the `defer` permissionDecision pattern — synchronous IPC works today.
- **Spike findings reduce 14.12.2 estimate from 2–3d to ~1.5–2d.** Concrete sub-tasks in the spike report: IPC bridge script (1–2h), claude_cli.py provider (4–6h), chat_runner integration of permission bridge (2–3h, reuses `_request_confirmation`), worktree-per-session lifecycle (1–2h, mostly removing now-redundant `delegate_to_claude_code` plumbing), subscription-auth assertion (30m), bundled-MCP retirement + dead Chrome preflight (1h), tests (2h).
- **Working-tree state at session end.** Everything committed. Untracked debug PNGs/HTMLs from session 163 still float — same precedent.
- **Exact next step.** Phase 14.12.2 starts. First atomic unit: write `pipeline/providers/claude_cli.py` with `complete()` and `complete_streaming()` mirroring `anthropic.py`'s shape. Get it answering a trivial `"hello"` query under subscription auth before wiring permissions. The IPC bridge + chat-runner integration come after that's green. Estimated session-1-of-14.12.2 = ~4–6h.

**Session 164 — late, post-hardening (April 25, 2026, 11:00 AM-ish PST) — STRATEGIC PIVOT to two-track architecture. No commits yet (planning/roadmapping); next session is the spike.**

- **Trigger.** User re-upped $5 in Anthropic API credits last night, was already out by morning. Console showed Apr 25 spend = **$6.50** across Sonnet 4.5 ($2.87, matches operator outer LLM), Sonnet 4.6 ($2.77), Haiku 4.5 ($0.87). Single API key in console = the same one operator uses in `~/.operator/.env`. The Sonnet 4.6 + Haiku 4.5 was unaccounted by `/tmp/operator.log` reconstruction — gap of $3.64 needed explanation.
- **Diagnosis (definitive).** `~/.operator/debug/claude-stream.jsonl` (which operator writes for every delegate via the session-164 stream-json work) showed the inner `claude -p --worktree` subprocess running with `apiKeySource: ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` + `model: claude-sonnet-4-6`. So every `delegate_to_claude_code` call was billing API rates instead of consuming the user's Claude Max subscription. Leak path: `pipeline/mcp_client.py:593` spawns MCP server processes with `env={**os.environ, **self._srv_config["env"]}`; operator's process loaded `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` via `load_dotenv(~/.operator/.env)`; child inherits it; inner claude CLI's auth-precedence rule prefers env-var over claude.ai login when both are present. A handful of delegates × dozens of inner LLM calls each (Sonnet 4.6 sub-agents + Haiku 4.5 fast paths) = $3+ spend per morning of testing.
- **Why API rates feel so much higher than expected.** Anthropic's Max subscription bills *flat* (~$200/mo for the high tier) and meters by messages-per-5h-window. API bills *per token*. The same task that's effectively free under Max costs $1–3 on API. **Subscription is heavily subsidized; API is the canonical price.** Most users don't intuit this.
- **Refused the surgical fix.** I offered an env-strip patch (`agents/engineer/claude_code.py:_run_claude` builds an env that excludes `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` + `ANTHROPIC_AUTH_TOKEN` before spawning the inner CLI). User explicitly rejected: *"I don't need to stop the bleeding now. I've made up my mind and want to fully pivot to this new direction now regardless of launch."* The pivot is the strategic answer.
- **Two-track architecture decision.** Track A — `operator run claude` is plug-and-play, no setup, no API key. Inner LLM is the user's Claude Code (`claude -p` subprocess, subscription-billed). Permission MCP routes inner-claude tool confirmations through Meet chat. Personality + ground_rules pass through as system-prompt augmentation. **The "claude" name is reserved exclusively for track A — wizard no longer offers it as a choosable preset.** Bundled operator MCPs drop from claude (user's claude.ai-connected MCPs cover the surface and were already imported via Phase 15.9). Bundled skills migrate to `~/.claude/skills/<name>/SKILL.md` so inner-claude picks them up natively. Track B — `operator build` is the custom-agent framework. Existing operator orchestration stays. Wizard pivots to "build a custom bot" only — name yourself, pick a provider (Anthropic API / OpenAI / local model), wire MCPs, set personality. Both paths exist; track A is free for Max subscribers, track B is bring-your-own-keys. The README's "Claude Code in your Google Meet" hero becomes literal for track A; track B is the secondary story.
- **Why D1 over D2 (the architectural sub-decision).** Walked through both shapes. D1 = let inner-claude run its own loop (real Claude Code in a meeting). D2 = use `claude -p --no-mcp-config` as a pure text-completion engine and keep operator's loop. I initially leaned D2 for caution (preserves operator's confirmation flow, MCP routing, READ_TOOLS allowlist, skills system); user pushed back. Honest answer: operator's orchestration was built when there was no Claude Code substrate option, but Claude Code already implements much of what operator's loop does (permission modes, skills system, MCP routing, caching, retry, paragraph flushing). D2 = re-implementing 60% of Claude Code inside operator. D1 = "Claude Code in your Google Meet" matches the README hero pitch literally, inherits Anthropic's Claude Code improvements for free, and turns operator's claude bot into a thin wrapper. The other three bots (pm, engineer, designer) keep operator's full orchestration under track B. **D1 it is.**
- **Launch on hold.** All Phase 14.5 / 14.8 / 16.x work paused until Phase 14.12 ships. Roadmap updated.
- **Working-tree state at session end.** Six earlier commits from this session already committed (1413318 / d0ff5a7 / 20a6d58 / b1b5058 / 5af360c / 1e7e3e1 / b943ba3 docs). Doc updates from this strategic-pivot conversation (roadmap + agent-context + handoff) staged for /end-session to commit.
- **Exact next step.** **Phase 14.12.1 — Permission MCP spike (1 day).** Probe whether `claude -p` exposes a host-resolvable permission callback for non-TTY callers. Two outcomes drive the rest of the design: (a) confirmed → track A as designed; (b) not available → fallback plan (probably bypassPermissions in a sandboxed worktree, scoped narrowly). Output: working probe that demonstrates a chat-confirmable inner tool call, plus a 1-page write-up of the API shape. After spike: 14.12.2 (track A implementation), 14.12.3 (track B repositioning), 14.12.4 (skills migration), 14.12.5 (README + landing rewrite). **Total: ~4–5 days of engineering before launch.**

**Open product questions to resolve during 14.12 (captured here so the next agent doesn't lose them):**
1. Bundled "default voice" for track A — what personality + ground_rules string ships? Probably a small `agents/claude/voice.md` baked into the package.
2. Does customization door open from track A? E.g., `operator voice` subcommand to tweak personality without going to track B.
3. (Pre-launch — no migration UX needed. First run after the pivot just writes the new track-A config; any old dev-machine config gets overwritten without ceremony.)
4. Captions in track A — still flow through operator's adapter, transcript wired into inner-claude prompt via meeting record JSONL (same as today, just `claude -p` substitutes for the Anthropic SDK call).
5. pm/engineer/designer preset retention — keep as wizard-suggested starter templates, or retire in favor of Phase 15.5.2 gallery?
6. Subprocess-spawn-per-LLM-call latency — ~1–2s overhead. Acceptable for meeting cadence (humans take longer to read replies anyway). Post-MVP optimization: warm pool of pre-spawned claude processes.

**Session 164 (April 25, 2026) — Test 1.2 hardening pass: six commits stacked, ~2.5h. Triggered by re-running Test 1.2 (`migration-plan`) clean against the headless build from session 163.**

- **(`1413318`) Confirmation-decline UX fix + TTFT instrumentation.** Live retest exposed two bugs and one diagnostic gap. (a) When the user replies non-yes during a pending tool confirmation, `chat_runner._handle_confirmation` was sending a synthetic tool_result with bland text ("User wants to adjust this call and said: ..."), which the LLM read as a successful tool result and hallucinated *"running, waiting for results"* even though the MCP call had never fired. Reworded with `[TOOL NOT EXECUTED]` prefix + explicit "no output exists" + 2-option directive — model now correctly re-proposes or asks. Tool result still goes through Anthropic's API (every `tool_use` block requires a paired `tool_result` per spec); the framing change is what disambiguates. (b) Added `ttft` and `first_flush` fields to `anthropic.py:complete_streaming` TIMING line — fingerprints Anthropic-side request-queue spikes vs streaming-rate slowdowns vs our paragraph-flush buffering. Paid for itself the same session.

- **(`d0ff5a7`) Stream-json side-log + live worktree progress.** The 5-minute claude-code delegate had been the worst demo moment — chat went silent for minutes with cute placeholder verbs (Embossing… Frolicking…) substituting for real signal. Switched the inner claude CLI from `--output-format json` to `--output-format stream-json --verbose`. `agents/engineer/claude_code.py:_run_claude` now reads stdout line-by-line, appends every event to `~/.operator/debug/claude-stream.jsonl` (truncated per call so the tailer only sees this run's events), and extracts the final `{"type":"result", ...}` event as the return value (same top-level keys as old json mode — drop-in for downstream code). `chat_runner._execute_and_respond` spawns a tailer thread for `claude-code__delegate_to_claude_code` calls; tailer reads new lines via seek-and-resume every 1s and posts one chat message per inner-claude `tool_use`: Read → "Reading X.py...", Edit/MultiEdit → "Editing Y.py...", Write → "Writing Z...", Bash → "Running: <first 60 chars>...", Glob/Grep → "Searching: <pattern>...", WebFetch → "Fetching <url>...", Task → "Spawning sub-agent: ...". TodoWrite + assistant-text events are suppressed (inner planning + final result, both noisy/redundant). Replaces verbs for claude-code only; other tools fall through to the next commit's silence path.

- **(`20a6d58`) Drop verb heartbeat infrastructure.** Once stream-json covers claude-code, the verb pool's only remaining consumers are short-lived MCPs (linear/github queries; usually <1s) where placeholder pings added more noise than signal. Deleted `pipeline/heartbeat_verbs.py`, `TOOL_HEARTBEAT_SECONDS`/`TOOL_HEARTBEAT_MAX_SECONDS` from `config.py`, the import in chat_runner, and the verb-tick branch in `_execute_and_respond` (collapsed to `done_event.wait()`). `tests/test_912_tool_timeout.py` rewrote the two heartbeat-cadence tests to assert silent execution. Net: claude-code calls show real progress; every other tool runs silent and surfaces results when done. If a non-claude-code tool genuinely hangs, MCP per-server timeout fires through the existing error-handler path.

- **(`b1b5058`) Stuck-LLM watchdog with one-shot status ping.** Yesterday's 49.8s Anthropic stall produced ~50s of silent chat. New `LLM_STUCK_THRESHOLD_SECONDS=45` in `config.py`; watchdog Timer in `complete_streaming` posts via `on_paragraph` exactly once if no token has arrived by 45s. Cancelled in try/finally around the retry loop so a failed call never leaves the watchdog ticking and firing stale. Healthy calls (TTFT 1–3s, total 3–15s) never trigger; only fires on real spikes. Threshold deliberately above cache-cold first-call cost (~4s on this prompt size). Retry semantics deferred — handling user "retry" replies mid-stream requires concurrency between the chat reader and the dispatcher (currently chat_runner's poll loop is blocked inside the streaming call); informational ping is the minimum viable for the silence problem.

- **(`5af360c`) Drop trailing newlines in stuck-LLM watchdog message.** Live retest caught a self-reply cascade. Watchdog posted `"...hang tight.\n\n"` (trailing newlines per the streamed-paragraph contract `flush_paragraphs` followed). Meet's chat DOM strips trailing whitespace on render → chat read-back came back as `"...hang tight."`. ChatRunner's text-match own-message dedup is exact equality → mismatch → bot reprocessed its own watchdog as a user prompt → LLM "replied" with the same string → looped 3 times before the user noticed. Surgical fix: drop the `\n\n` (the watchdog is a one-shot notice, not a streamed paragraph that needs separators). Also exposed the underlying brittleness — text-match dedup couldn't handle DOM normalization — which the next commit addressed structurally.

- **(`1e7e3e1`) ID-based own-message dedup + stripped text-match fallback.** The architectural fix for the cascade. Connector contract change: `connectors/base.py:send_chat` now returns the new message's stable ID (or None on read-back timeout). `macos_adapter._do_send_chat` snapshots existing `data-message-id` values pre-send via a brief Playwright `page.evaluate`, runs fill+Enter, then polls every 50ms (up to 1s) for one new ID to appear; returns it through the chat-queue handler. `chat_runner._send` captures the returned ID and adds it to `_seen_ids` — subsequent MutationObserver events with the same ID short-circuit at the existing line-341 ID check, so sender/text comparisons are never reached for own messages on the happy path. Belt-and-suspenders text-match fallback: `_own_messages` now stores `text.strip()`, comparison strips both sides — catches adapters that can't return an ID (linux_adapter still returns None — out of scope) and the race window where the post-send DOM read times out. `tests/test_chat_hardening.py` + `test_912_tool_timeout.py` still green.

- **Roadmap delta.** Added Phase 15.10.5 (`operator worktrees` CLI) — found 11 stale worktrees in `.claude/worktrees/` from prior delegate runs; `git worktree prune` doesn't touch on-disk dirs whose metadata is still valid. Defer to next session before Phase 14.5 install.sh so the launch artifact has a clean disk story.

- **Working-tree state at session end.** Six commits landed clean. docs/{agent-context,handoff,roadmap}.md updated this turn but not committed (the /end-session pattern). Untracked debug PNGs/HTML from session 163 still float — same precedent as before.

- **Exact next step.** Re-run Test 1.2 (`migration-plan`) cleanly with the new dedup + stream-json + watchdog stack live. If it passes, Test 1.3 (`test-generation`) — pre-step is creating `/tmp/test_fixtures/email_validator.py` per `docs/live-skill-tests.md` — then 1.4 (live coding delegation), Sessions 2 and 3, then Phase 15.10.5 (`operator worktrees` CLI). **MVP budget: ~5–7h remaining; launch target Apr 28–30 aspirational, May 1–2 acceptable.** No roadmap rows fully closed this session — work was hardening discovered during live testing, not a phase-tracked deliverable; 15.10.5 was added as a deferred follow-up.

**Session 163 (April 25, 2026) — headless bundled-Chromium pivot during Test 1.2. Two commits: `273b4b1` (headless pivot + 5 probe scripts + production modal-dismiss patch) and `0d6f0e1` (heartbeat fixed-cadence). ~2h.**

- **The trigger.** During Test 1.2 (`migration-plan` skill, paste of "what would it take to migrate this codebase from chat-only to also supporting Slack as a connector? give us a phased plan") the model fired skill, asked clarifying questions, eventually delegated to `claude-code` for read-only repo analysis. Tool ran 5 minutes, returned a 19,055-byte plan. Then chat went silent. Investigation: `chat_runner` started logging `send_chat failed: ` with empty error message every 10 seconds — `queue.Empty` stringifies to ''. Root cause: at 08:26:40 the `MacOSAdapter` browser session died (`Page.wait_for_timeout: Target page, context or browser has been closed`). The user had quit Chrome mid-run — they'd tried to open a new browsing window, dock click did nothing, ⌘N got eaten, gave up and force-quit the app. operator's tab died with it.
- **Why Chrome appeared broken to the user.** `connectors/macos_adapter.py:512` was `launch_persistent_context(executable_path="/Applications/Google Chrome.app/...", headless=False, args=["--use-fake-ui-for-media-stream", "--headless=new", "--mute-audio"])`. The `--headless=new` Chrome flag was a no-op: Playwright's `headless=False` won, so operator ran a *headed* real Chrome. macOS treats `Chrome.app` as a singleton by bundle ID — even with separate `--user-data-dir`, the user's dock click + ⌘N route to whichever Chrome process owns the front window. operator's window owned it, dropped the keystrokes silently, user thought Chrome was hung.
- **Probe sequence (5 self-contained scripts under `debug/`, each takes a Meet URL on argv).** `headless_meet_baseline.py` (Playwright bundled Chromium, no profile, no auth) hit a meet URL → walled with `"You can't join this video call"`. **Same wall non-headless gets** — proved the long-standing `project_meet_bot_detection.md` memory was stale: the gate is unauthed/uninvited, not headless detection. `headless_meet_invited.py` (bundled Chromium + `~/.operator/browser_profile/` + `headless=True`, after user invited `heyoperator2026@gmail.com` from the meeting) → admitted to pre-join lobby cleanly with `Operator` display name + `"Jojo Shapiro is in this call"` participant visibility. `headless_meet_join.py` clicked through `"Continue without microphone and camera"` link → `Join now` → admission → in-meeting screenshot showed full Meet UI rendering (camera tile, bottom bar, chat button). `headless_meet_send.py` opened chat panel via `Chat with everyone` button → filled `textarea[aria-label="Send a message"]` → pressed Enter; message landed in real Chrome's view. `headless_meet_captions.py` reused `connectors/captions_js.CAPTION_OBSERVER_JS` + `enable_captions(page)` against the headless context, exposed `__onCaption` via `expose_function`, captured 13 progressive caption events from the user speaking into their mic ("As. As, and. As and this is. As and this is me speaking out loud again. And this is my last sentence.").
- **Production change for the pivot.** `connectors/macos_adapter.py:512`: dropped `executable_path` (uses Playwright bundled Chromium), flipped `headless=False → True`, removed redundant `--headless=new` Chrome flag (now redundant when Playwright's `headless=True` is in effect). Single shape: `p.chromium.launch_persistent_context(user_data_dir=BROWSER_PROFILE, headless=True, args=["--use-fake-ui-for-media-stream", "--mute-audio"])`. First production run hit `no_join_button`: a different device-permission modal variant ("Do you want people to see you in the meeting?", camera-only, no decline link) was blocking the Join now click. Patched the pre-camera-toggle path in `_attempt_join` to try the existing `Continue without microphone and camera` text-selector first, fall back to a single `page.keyboard.press("Escape")` (closes any modal dialog, no-op on empty pre-join). Live re-run joined cleanly: `total_join=9.2s` (vs ~13s headed), captions `enabled via Shift+C (attempt 1, 0.5s)`, `observer_attached label=scoped_region`, intro posted, real chat exchange + a `linear__list_issues` MCP tool call posted formatted output for 3 Linear issues.
- **Heartbeat fixed-cadence (separate commit, also session-163 work).** Exponential backoff (8 → 16 → 32 → 60s cap from session 157) read as "the bot hung" once gaps got long enough. Steady cadence reads as "still alive." `config.TOOL_HEARTBEAT_SECONDS` 8 → 30 (commented for session 162-and-earlier swap rationale); `TOOL_HEARTBEAT_MAX_SECONDS` retained as `30` for back-compat with the test signature; `chat_runner._execute_and_respond` lost its interval-doubling line (`interval = min(interval * 2, max_interval)`). `tests/test_912_tool_timeout.py`: `test_heartbeat_interval_backs_off → test_heartbeat_interval_is_fixed_cadence`, both expected gaps within ~1s window; fast/slow heartbeat detection switched from `"Still working"` substring to the real `m.endswith("...")` shape that matches session 161's verb pool. `test_config_loader.py`: `assert mod.TOOL_HEARTBEAT_SECONDS == 8 → 30`.
- **Stale memory entry to update next session.** `~/.claude/projects/-Users-jojo-Desktop-operator/memory/project_meet_bot_detection.md` claims Meet blocks headless bots and recommends invite-based demo strategy. The "headless is blocked" claim is now disproved; the "invite-based" half is correct (just for a different reason — auth gating, not headless detection). Rewrite to reflect the actual gate.
- **Session-160 Chrome-runtime preflight is dead weight.** The whole `_check_chrome_runtime_preflight` path that session 160 added was scaffolding for `executable_path="/Applications/Google Chrome.app/..."`. Bundled Chromium ships with Playwright; the preflight has nothing to check. Safe to retire in a follow-up cleanup commit.
