**Previous (session 136, April 20, 2026):** Commit `e5bd0ef` on `main`.

- **Aligned with user on a three-tier logging model before touching code.** **Stdout/stderr** = user-facing narrative (join, participants, tool-confirm, disconnect, goodbye, errors) — a skeptical first-time user is watching this and silence reads as "broken." **`/tmp/operator.log`** = forensic DEBUG trail (every LLM call, every MCP frame, every chat poll, every participant-count change, expected errors without tracebacks, unexpected with tracebacks). **`OPERATOR_DEBUG=1`** = dev firehose (raw MCP JSON-RPC frames, full LLM prompts, Playwright action traces) — reserved for later, not yet wired. Main tradeoff: erring toward quiet stdout loses live-debugging signal, but `/tmp/operator.log` is the safety net, so quiet stdout wins for a launch audience.
- **Scope extras user approved at planning time:** error affordances (append `— see /tmp/operator.log` to failure messages when a detail trail exists), clean shutdown visibility (single final line after teardown actually completes, not before), stderr split (errors to stderr, narrative to stderr, usage prints to stdout — lets you pipe `2>/dev/null`), color (rolled a tiny ANSI helper, no new dep), first-5-seconds heartbeat (banner was already first but Chrome takes 3–8s silently — added "Launching Chrome…" right after). **Deferred post-launch:** log rotation, multi-instance logfile collision (two brainchilds clobber `/tmp/operator.log` — per-slug `/tmp/operator-<slug>.log` is the fix, matches `~/.operator/history/<slug>.jsonl` convention).
- **Implementation, one atomic change per step, tests between each.**
  - **Step 1 — `pipeline/ui.py` (new, 64 lines).** `say/ok/warn/err/chat_in/chat_out` helpers. ANSI colors auto-disabled when `$NO_COLOR` is set (per https://no-color.org) or stderr isn't a TTY. All output to stderr. `err()` appends a dim `— see /tmp/operator.log` suffix unless `hint_log=False`. Smoke-tested in both TTY (colors on) and piped-Bash (colors stripped) contexts.
  - **Step 2 — Logging setup in entry points.** `_run_macos` had a root `StreamHandler(sys.stderr)` with timestamped format — piping every `log.info` from every module (including `ChatRunner`, MCP handshake, TIMING lines) straight to the terminal. That's the main noise source. Removed. Kept the `httpcore/httpx/openai/anthropic` WARN pins. `_run_linux` switched from `basicConfig(level=INFO, stream=stderr)` (default) to the same file-only DEBUG pattern as `_run_macos` and `_run_try`, picking up the same WARN pins. Now all three entry paths behave identically: detail to `/tmp/operator.log` only, stderr stays reserved for `ui.*`.
  - **Step 3 — Narrate key events.** Imported `ui` in `__main__.py` and `chat_runner.py`. Converted user-visible `print()` sites: `print("Fresh meeting: ...")` → `ui.ok(...)`; kill-reason `print(f"⚠️ {reason}")` → `ui.warn(reason)` (kept log.info for the file trail); `print("Goodbye.")` → `ui.ok("Left meeting — goodbye.")`; "Restart with: ..." → `ui.say(...)`; meet.new resolution failure → `ui.err(...)`. In `chat_runner.py`: added `ui.ok("Joined meeting — listening for chat.")` as the join milestone right after the existing `log.info("ChatRunner: joined")`; converted the three auth-failure branches (`session_expired` → `ui.err("Not authenticated — run: python scripts/auth_export.py")`, `already_running` → `ui.warn(...)`, unknown → `ui.err(f"Join failed: {reason}")`); disconnect → `ui.warn("Meeting connection lost — chat loop stopped.")`; alone-leave → `ui.ok("Everyone left — dropping from the meeting.")`. Kept every existing `log.info/warning/error` call for the file trail.
  - **Step 4 — Error prints to stderr.** Linux `MEETING_URL` missing + `DISPLAY` missing prints had the `❌` prefix and stayed on stdout; converted to plain `print(..., file=sys.stderr)` with the `❌` stripped (stderr semantics carry the failure meaning; emoji is redundant). MCP client startup failure in both `_run_macos` and `_run_linux` now `ui.err("MCP startup failed")` alongside the existing `log.error`.
  - **Step 5 — "Launching Chrome…" heartbeat.** Single `ui.say(...)` line right after `_print_startup_banner(...)` in both `_run_macos` and `_run_linux` (Linux variant says "Launching Chromium…"). Chrome spin-up is 3–8s of silence otherwise and a skeptical user reaches for Ctrl+C.
  - **Step 6 — README seed (40 lines).** README was 0 bytes. Wrote a short project blurb + four-command usage block + **Privacy & logs** section flagging what lands in `/tmp/operator.log` (Meet URL as capability token, chat content with sender names, LLM prompt/response metadata, tool call args + results, captions when `transcript.captions_enabled: true`) and `~/.operator/history/<slug>.jsonl` (same sensitivity). Called out that `/tmp` is typically cleared on macOS reboot, not Linux — delete manually if it matters. Pointed to CLAUDE.md / docs/roadmap.md / docs/agent-context.md for more.
- **Verified.** Full 143-test suite green across 12 files (`test_chat_hardening`, `test_911_size_management`, `test_912_tool_timeout`, `test_913_tool_history_collapse`, `test_915_reconnection`, `test_guardrails`, `test_anthropic_provider`, `test_openai_provider`, `test_mcp_client`, `test_mcp_shutdown`, `test_entry_cli`, `test_connectors`). Covered: `ask()` no-tools wiring (system = `config.SYSTEM_PROMPT`, tail = record tail, tools=None); `_tail_messages` shape (agent sender → assistant role, user → `"first: text"`, caption → `[spoken] first: text`, first-contact hint attached once per first name); `ask()` tool_call seeds `_scratch` with the assistant turn and returns a `{"type": "tool_call", ...}` dict; `send_tool_result` appends tool_result to scratch then clears scratch on final text; `ContextOverflowError` returns `{"type": "context_overflow"}` and halves `_max_messages` with floor 2; `intro()` single `provider.complete` call with no history, returns trimmed text, exceptions propagate (ChatRunner handles).
- **C finding — captions don't trigger greeting.** While writing test 2, discovered (and confirmed as correct) that `_tail_messages` has `continue` immediately after appending a caption message — meaning captions never receive the first-contact hint, and they don't mark the speaker as "greeted." Intentional: ambient spoken talk shouldn't be treated as a direct greeting. Bob's first *chat* message is his first direct contact; the hint attaches there. Documented in the test-plan notes.
- **G — Skills loader (Gap-fill, 5 tests).** Appended to existing `tests/test_skills.py`: no frontmatter skipped (warns "missing frontmatter"), unterminated frontmatter skipped (warns "unterminated frontmatter"), non-dict frontmatter (yaml list) skipped (warns "not a mapping"), `allowed-tools` as comma-separated string parses to a list, empty parent folder (subdirs with no `SKILL.md`) warns "no SKILL.md found." 18/18 tests now pass (was 13 visible + 5 silently failing, see next bullet).
- **G incidental fix — test_skills.py OPERATOR_BOT default.** Added `os.environ.setdefault("OPERATOR_BOT", "pm")` at line 7 of `tests/test_skills.py`. Without it, tests 9–13 (LLM/ChatRunner wiring tests that `from pipeline.llm import LLMClient`) were silently dying on `SystemExit(2)` from `config.py` at import time — the runner caught `Exception` but not `SystemExit`, so they reported as `FAIL` once and then the loop continued. Now all pre-existing tests actually execute. Matches the pattern used in every other test file in the repo.
- **F — MCPClient (Gap-fill, 6 tests).** New `tests/test_mcp_client_units.py`. Pure-function and lightweight branches not exercised by the subprocess-level `test_mcp_client.py` and `test_mcp_shutdown.py`: `_classify_startup_failure` (FileNotFoundError → "command not found"; "process exited" pattern → "exited before handshake" with debug hint; `BaseExceptionGroup` unwrapping so anyio task-group errors resolve to the inner cause, never leaking the group type name); `server_for_tool` + `tool_timeout_for` (per-server override wins, unknown tools return `None`, servers without override return `None`); `execute_tool` strips unprompted `limit` arg from Linear calls but preserves it for non-Linear servers; `execute_tool` blocks `get_file_contents` with binary extensions (.png) pre-execution with `MCPToolError`, but proceeds for text paths.
- **F race carve-out deviation — documented in test-plan.** The plan flagged "tool timeout racing with reconnect" and "orphan cleanup during active call" as the Boundary+race cases. Reading `pipeline/mcp_client.py` showed: (a) there is no reconnect path (each `_ServerHandle` runs once per session), so the first case has no target in current code; (b) orphan cleanup is already covered by the existing `test_mcp_shutdown.py`, so the second case has no new work. Documented as a deviation in the test-plan Notes rather than fabricating tests against imaginary code — revisit if reconnect is added post-launch.

**Previous (session 132, April 19, 2026):** Commit `1fdbc4e` on `main`.

- **Design discussion: nailing internal terminology for the three customization levers.** User flagged that system prompt, MCPs, and skills have overlapping properties — where does identity go vs. always-on rules vs. multi-step playbooks? — and asked for terminology that signals "building on top of each other." Iterated through several framings (Character → Tools → Playbooks; Tools → Playbooks → Identity; Tools → Instructions → Identity). User pushed back on "Instructions" after my concern that it's overloaded in LLM-land, landed on **Tools (MCPs) → Playbooks (Skills) → Ground Rules → Personality** as the four-layer frame. User chose to keep yaml keys `mcp_servers` and `skills` as technical parlance (not rename to `tools` / `playbooks`) — wizard labels diverge from yaml keys on purpose.
- **Split `llm.system_prompt` into two top-level yaml blocks.** `personality` (voice, tone, who-the-bot-is) + `ground_rules` (always-true constraints). Composed in `config.py` as `personality\n\nground_rules`, rules-last for LLM end-of-prompt weighting on adherence. Either block can be absent/empty. User locked the uniform split rule: voice/identity → personality, rules → ground_rules — all three bundled bots follow the same logic, only the text differs. Hard cut: no backward-compat shim for `llm.system_prompt`, all three bot configs migrated in the same PR.
- **Three bundled bots fully migrated** (`agents/pm/config.yaml`, `agents/engineer/config.yaml`, `agents/designer/config.yaml`). Reordered yaml to: `agent → llm → transcript → mcp_servers → skills → ground_rules → personality`. Designer's personality preserves the opinion-forward register ("direct, specific, never mealy-mouthed"; "That spacing is cramped — bump it to 16px, the eye needs room to breathe" is the register). Engineer's ground rules kept the full tool-routing block (github__* vs delegate) and delegation-rules block (repo_path handling). Standard rules shared across all three: side-panel reminder, lead-with-answer, 1–3 sentences, bare URLs, ask-when-ambiguous, greet-once, [spoken] captions handling.
- **Wizard expanded 5 → 7 steps with instructional copy on each** (`pipeline/setup.py`). Step 2 "Tools (MCPs)", step 3 "Playbooks (Skills)", step 4 "Ground Rules" (new), step 5 "Personality" (new), step 6 API keys, step 7 atomic write. Steps 4+5 pop `$EDITOR` via new `_edit_prompt_block(state, key=..., label=...)` shared helper plus `_edit_in_editor(seed=..., label=...)`. Editor resolution: `VISUAL` → `EDITOR` → `vi` fallback. Two modes: edit-preset shows a two-path picker (inherit-current-with-cursor vs start-blank); from-scratch always opens blank. User locked the pedagogical order: **ground_rules first, personality second** — opposite of concatenation order, because authoring rules first and voice second is more intuitive, but rules-last in the prompt fights adherence-decay. `_from_scratch()` now explicitly clears personality + ground_rules (blank starting point; doesn't inherit pm's text).

Updated the opening prose to name the six top-level blocks in the new top-to-bottom order. `CLAUDE.md` Configuration section rewritten to match.

**Previous (session 131, April 19, 2026):** Commit `8684a4f` on `main` — self-intro on join shipped (still unvalidated live).

- **Strategic conversation about the skills/tools mental model.** User asked how skills, tools, system prompt, and MCP hints relate — surfaced a real product ambiguity. Mapped the four steering surfaces: tools = capability (yes/no can the bot do X), system prompt = identity & always-on heuristics, MCP hints = server-scoped framing injected when that MCP is in play, skills = playbooks for multi-step procedures with quality bars. Heuristic for "where do I tweak X": capability gap → tool, one-line guardrail → hint or system prompt, multi-step procedure → skill, identity → system prompt. Concluded the abstraction is right; what's missing is *visibility* of it.
- **Walked through how the existing `pipeline/llm.py` already has the right pieces.** `inject_skills()` appends a name+description menu (or full bodies if not progressive); MCP tools pass as full schemas to every `provider.complete` call; `inject_mcp_hints()` appends per-server usage notes; `inject_mcp_status()` notes which servers loaded vs. failed vs. were disabled. So if a user asked "@operator what can you do" today, the model would *technically* have the data but the answer would be improvised — no instruction for the meta-question, granular tool names would either flood or get vaguely summarized, and the "Default to 1–3 sentences" directive fights enumeration.
- **User chose to ship intro-on-join instead of a "what can you do" handler.** Cleaner: every meeting starts with the bot proactively framing what it can do, no user typing required, generic across all bots. Locked spec across 6 turns: field defaults true; sync-vs-async resolved as background gen + deferred message processing (NOT blocked polling); no re-intro on reconnect (don't care about edge case); single toggle covers 1-on-1 and group; length-capped via prompt; dynamic-via-LLM (not static string) so the intro auto-updates as skills/MCPs change; on LLM failure log + skip silently (fake-success masks real problems — if intro fails, next message will fail too and surface it honestly).
- **`config.py:40` — added `INTRO_ON_JOIN = _config["agent"].get("intro_on_join", True)`.** Defaults true so existing bundles inherit the feature without per-bot edits. Three bundled configs (`agents/pm/config.yaml`, `agents/designer/config.yaml`, `agents/engineer/config.yaml`) explicitly set `intro_on_join: true` under their `agent:` block — opt-in is the same one-line flip if a contributor wants it off.
- **`pipeline/llm.py:280` — added `LLMClient.intro() -> str`.** Single `provider.complete` call with no message history (the bot is greeting the room, not reacting to it). System prompt is the live one — already carries skills + MCP hints + status from boot-time injection — so the model knows what it can actually do this session. Hard-coded prompt: 2 sentences, "I can…" framing, 2–3 concrete use cases as inline list, focus on outcomes not mechanisms, never name tools/MCPs/skills (too technical for a meeting greeting), no greeting filler ("Hi everyone!"), no offers/questions back, plain text (no markdown). Returns the trimmed response. No try/except — caller is responsible.
- **`pipeline/chat_runner.py` — wired the intro flow with thread-safety in mind.** Added `_intro_ready: threading.Event`, `_intro_text: str`, `_intro_posted: bool` (starts True if `INTRO_ON_JOIN=False`), `_pre_intro_buffer: list[dict]` to `__init__`. After join completes (line ~107), if `INTRO_ON_JOIN` is true, spawns a daemon thread `_generate_intro()` that calls `self._llm.intro()`, stores result in `_intro_text` (empty string on exception, with log), and sets `_intro_ready`. Main `_loop()` checks at the top of each iteration: if intro is ready and not yet posted, calls `_send(self._intro_text)` from the main thread (so `connector.send_chat` stays single-threaded — no risk of off-thread Playwright calls), marks posted, then drains `_pre_intro_buffer` in order. Per-message processing: persist to record always (unchanged), check pending tool confirmation (unchanged), then if `not _intro_posted` buffer the message (text + one_on_one snapshot) and `continue` instead of dispatching. Otherwise fall through to new helper `_dispatch_user_message(text, one_on_one)` — extracted from the existing trigger-check + handle_message block so live and drained messages share one routing path.
- **`docs/test-plan.md` updated.** Added an entry to the Notes and decisions section that names the three components whose inventories must include intro-on-join coverage when their session comes up: A (config-loader default + presence read), C (LLMClient.intro behavior — single call, no history, exception propagation), E (ChatRunner gating + buffering + drain + INTRO_ON_JOIN=False short-circuit). Boundary depth is the right level — intro is greenfield code, no prior tests, no concurrency surface beyond the one event/buffer pair.
- **Not yet live-tested.** `operator try pm` is the cheapest sanity check (TerminalConnector skips the join wait so intro fires within ~2s of boot). Real Meet test via `operator pm`. User opted to test independently rather than walk a pre-written flow list — also relevant: earlier in the session, user proposed and then dropped a "pressure-test main user flows → punch list → fix → then test" plan in favor of doing those flow walks themselves.

**Next action:** **Live-smoke the intro on a real Meet** (`operator pm <url>` — verify intro fires, lands cleanly, shape feels right; check log for `LLM intro generated` line; check `~/.operator/history/<slug>.jsonl` to confirm the intro is the first non-meta line and tagged `kind: chat`). Then **start walking `docs/test-plan.md`, Component B (MeetingRecord) first** — small, zero current coverage, every other component reads from it. Follow per-session protocol: read `pipeline/meeting_record.py`, produce bulleted behavior inventory at Boundary + race depth (target 5–8 cases), user picks which to write, write one at a time. Pre-existing test failure still pending: `test_912::test_timeout_sends_failure_message` (likely two-line MagicMock fixture fix). After a few component test sessions, Phase 13.2 log cleanup → 15.6 security → 14 → 15 → 16. Budget: ~14h vs April 19 launch.

**Previous (session 127, April 18, 2026):** Commit `2a7de34` on `main`.

- **Live-smoked Phase 15.5.7 via `operator try engineer`** against fresh `/tmp/test-delegate` + `/tmp/test-delegate-2` scratch repos (created at session start with `git init` + one initial commit each). Walked the 8-step handoff plan from session 126: (1) startup banner + 2 delegate tools discovered ✅, (2) Engineer asked "which repo?" on first delegation instead of guessing ✅, (3) supplied `/tmp/test-delegate` → tool fired with footer `[workdir: /private/tmp/test-delegate/.claude/worktrees/vivid-mapping-hoare]` ✅, (4) verified file lived in sandbox (`scratch/hello_op.py` with `print('hello from operator')`) and NOT in user's working tree ✅, (5) `--resume` reused the same workdir on follow-up "prove it" prompt ✅, (6) multi-repo isolation initially failed in a non-obvious way — see chat_runner fix below — then worked cleanly on re-run, (7) `land_worktree_changes` returned in 0.1s and correctly staged `scratch/hello_op.py` as a new file in `/tmp/test-delegate`'s working tree ✅. Filesystem confirms three independent sandboxes coexisting (vivid-mapping-hoare + sorted-shimmying-shore in repo 1, dynamic-inventing-owl in repo 2). Per-repo session map (`_SESSIONS`) is doing its job under the live harness, not just the Python smoke from session 126.
- **Diagnosed and fixed an unrelated chat_runner.py bug surfaced by the smoke.** Initial multi-repo run failed: user prompt "now in /tmp/test-delegate-2, list the top-level files" → Engineer answered "README.md and a .git directory" without ever calling delegate. Repo 2 actually contained `f.txt` only — Engineer hallucinated the answer with content bled from repo 1's README.md. Log analysis showed no `tool_call` was emitted between the user's prompt and the wrong answer; the model produced text that looked exactly like the harness's confirmation prompt ("I'd like to run delegate_to_claude_code via delegate with: ..., OK?"), the user replied "ok", and then the model just hallucinated a result. Same pattern was causing double-confirmation prompts on every successful tool call (user had to type "ok" twice — once to the model's parroted prompt, once to the harness's real one). Root cause: `pipeline/chat_runner.py:_request_confirmation` writes its prompt via `self._send(msg)`, which persists to the meeting record as `kind="chat"`. `pipeline/llm.py:_tail_messages` replays everything tagged `chat` or `caption` back to the model on the next turn. The model saw "I'd like to run X. OK?" repeating in its assistant-side history and learned to imitate it. Fix in three small edits: (a) `_send` gained `kind: str = "chat"` keyword arg, (b) `_request_confirmation` calls `self._send(msg, kind="confirmation")`, (c) inbound message persistence in `_loop` tags the user's reply with `kind="confirmation"` whenever `_pending_tool_call` is set. Confirmations stay in the JSONL audit trail (auditable via `cat ~/.operator/history/<slug>.jsonl`) but the LLM never sees them. `tests/test_chat_hardening.py` still 7/7 green.
- **Re-ran the smoke after the fix.** Clean: single confirmation prompt per call (no parroted duplicate), repo-2 listing returned the actual `f.txt` ground truth, repo-1 recall question answered correctly from chat memory. Step 6c of the smoke ("and in the first repo, what file did you create?") didn't actually exercise the resume path — the model answered from chat history without calling delegate — but the answer was correct and resume was already verified in session 126's Python smoke and step 5 of today's run, so coverage is fine.
- **Two non-blocking notes for later.** (a) One smoke turn produced a mangled chat output `[ox at /private/tmp/test-delegate/...` — looks like a Meet-chat or terminal-connector rendering quirk where the leading bytes of a streamed message dropped; not related to today's fix, worth investigating during 13.2 log cleanup. (b) `.claude/worktrees/` in Operator's own repo still has ~10 stale entries from 15.5.6 sessions — unchanged, still worth a manual prune before launch.

**Next action:** **Phase 13 — log cleanup (~2h) + 13.1 gap check (~30m).** 13.1 was flagged as "actually incomplete" by the user at session 124 start but the specific gap was never captured. Open the 13 work by asking the user what's missing under 13.1 before touching 13.2. Budget: ~19h vs April 19 launch.

**Previous (session 126, April 18, 2026):** Commit `23bf258` on `main`.

- **Session kicked off with a live `operator try engineer` run** that exposed three coupled regressions in the delegate path. User typed "write a python script scratch/hello_op.py that prints 'hello from operator' and confirm it runs" → Engineer delegated, reported "confirmed working" → user said "prove it" → Engineer delegated a second task that silently re-created the file (different wording: "Show the contents of scratch/hello_op.py and run it" first, then pivoted mid-turn to "Create a Python script at scratch/hello_op.py"). Post-hoc filesystem check: no `scratch/` in `/Users/jojo/Desktop/operator/`, but three new entries under `.claude/worktrees/` from the run (one per delegate call), two of which had their own copy of `scratch/hello_op.py` and one of which had nothing (the "show contents" call that couldn't find the file from the prior sandbox and drove the LLM's silent pivot). Root cause: `claude -p ... --worktree` creates a brand-new worktree every invocation; no session continuity + no land flow + hard-pinned to Operator's own cwd.
- **Rewrite landed in one PR.** `agents/engineer/delegate_to_claude_code.py` now has two tools. `delegate_to_claude_code(task, repo_path)` where `repo_path` is a required absolute path to a local git repo. Module-level `_SESSIONS: dict[repo_canon, {session_id, worktree_path, base_sha}]`. First call per repo: `cwd=repo_path`, add `--worktree`, snapshot `_list_worktrees(repo_path)` before, parse `session_id` + new entry after, store with `base_sha = git rev-parse HEAD` at call time. Subsequent calls same repo: `cwd=worktree_path`, add `--resume <session_id>`, **do NOT** add `--worktree`. Fallback on "No conversation found" error (stdout, not stderr — `claude --resume` exits 0 with plain text, so we treat non-JSON stdout as an error and fall back to a fresh worktree). New tool `land_worktree_changes(repo_path)`: `git -C <worktree> add -A` (untracked files), `git diff --cached <base_sha>`, `git -C <repo> apply --index -` (with non-indexed retry if the staging fails). Tool result footer on every delegate carries `[workdir: ...]` + `[repo: ...]` lines so Engineer can surface the sandbox path.
- **System prompt + hints updated.** Added to `agents/engineer/config.yaml` `llm.system_prompt`: "delegate_to_claude_code requires repo_path… ask the user on first delegation in a chat… reuse the same repo_path for follow-ups… mention the workdir from the tool footer… offer to land changes with land_worktree_changes after success." Delegate server `hints` block expanded with the same guidance plus "land_worktree_changes only works after a delegate_to_claude_code call for the same repo_path this chat."
- **`agents/engineer/README.md` gained a "How delegation works" section** explaining sandbox vs working tree, the repo-naming requirement on first delegation, per-repo continuity, switching repos mid-chat, the land flow, and limitations (one repo per call, no clone-on-demand, inherits shell auth).
- **Verified in isolation before committing.** Ran `claude -p "..." --worktree --output-format json` in `/tmp/delegate_verify/` → captured session_id and worktree path; ran `claude -p "..." --resume <id>` from the worktree cwd → same session returned, prior file visible. Confirmed that running `--resume` from the parent repo cwd (not the worktree) errors with "No conversation found" — this is the reason cwd must be the worktree path on resume. Then smoke-tested the rewritten MCP via `python -c` importing `delegate_to_claude_code` directly: three fresh `/tmp/` repos (delegate_e2e, repo_a, repo_b) with `git init` + one initial commit each. Sequence: create file in repo_a (new session) → read file back in repo_a (resume) → create file in repo_b (new session, independent) → read back in repo_a (resumes original session, remembers alpha.txt, does not leak beta.txt). All three green. Land flow initially returned "No changes to land" because Claude Code left new files untracked — added `git add -A` before `git diff --cached` and land correctly stages+applies into the parent repo's working tree.
- **Not live-smoked via `operator try engineer` yet.** User asked to save that for session 127 via the handoff doc. Plan is in `docs/handoff.md`.

**Next action:** Live-smoke Phase 15.5.7 via `operator try engineer` per the handoff plan. Then Phase 13 — log cleanup (~2h) + 13.1 gap check (~30m). Budget: ~19h vs April 19 launch.

**Previous (session 125, April 18, 2026):** Commit `9040340` on `main`.

- **`connectors/terminal.py` (new, ~50 lines) — stdin/stdout `MeetingConnector`.** Implements the six-method seam (`join`, `send_chat`, `read_chat`, `get_participant_count`, `is_connected`, `leave`) without a browser. Stdin read on a daemon thread pushes lines into a `queue.Queue`; `read_chat()` drains it and surfaces messages as `{"id": "term-N", "sender": "you", "text": ...}`. `send_chat` prints `[<bot>] <reply>` with cyan ANSI so it stands out from echoed input. `get_participant_count` is pinned to 2 (see Hard Won Knowledge) so `ChatRunner` auto-enters 1-on-1 mode and skips the `@operator` trigger. `join()` returns `None` — `ChatRunner` treats that as "already joined" and skips the browser-join block entirely.
- **`__main__.py` — added `try` subcommand.** New `_run_try(name)` mirrors the macos path minus Playwright: builds `TerminalConnector`, runs MCP setup synchronously (no browser to overlap), spins a fresh `MeetingRecord(slug=f"terminal-{int(time.time())}")`, calls `runner.run(meeting_url=None)`. `_print_usage()` gained a `operator try <name>       Terminal test-drive (no Meet)` line; dispatch now routes `first == "try"` before the bot-name dispatch. `pipeline/setup.py:RESERVED_NAMES` updated to `{"setup", "list", "try"}` so no one can create `agents/try/`.
- **`agents/README.md`** — quickstart gained a new step 2: `operator try engineer` in-terminal before the Meet join.
- **`/quit` routes through SIGINT.** First draft of `TerminalConnector` flipped `_connected=False` on `/quit`, which `ChatRunner` detected as an unexpected disconnect and printed "Meeting connection lost" noise. Rewired to `os.kill(os.getpid(), signal.SIGINT)` — uses the existing Ctrl-C handler so shutdown is clean. Same path for stdin EOF.
- **Delegate permission-mode is now configurable.** `agents/engineer/delegate_to_claude_code.py` reads `DELEGATE_PERMISSION_MODE` env var (default `bypassPermissions`) and passes it through as `claude -p ... --permission-mode <mode>`. `agents/engineer/config.yaml` adds an `env:` block on the `delegate` server so users can flip to `acceptEdits` (file edits yes, Bash no) for a tighter sandbox. Root cause: `claude -p` with no TTY defaults to "ask" mode which auto-denies every Write/Edit/Bash — all `delegate_to_claude_code` calls from the harness were failing silently. See Hard Won Knowledge for the full diagnosis.
- **Engineer's system prompt got a tool-routing paragraph.** Harness surfaced that Engineer was calling `github__get_file_contents(owner='dufis1', repo='pipeline', ...)` to answer questions about *local* files in the Operator working directory — 404ing against GitHub because those paths aren't remote repos. Added an explicit paragraph: `github__*` tools are for inspecting remote repos (user names owner/repo explicitly); any local file operation must delegate to Claude Code. "When in doubt between the two, prefer delegate."
- **Tool-failure UX replaced hardcoded copy with LLM-authored explanations.** Old path printed `"Sorry, that tool call failed. Check the logs for details."` on every tool timeout/exception — user called it "aggravating." New `ChatRunner._handle_tool_failure(tc, signpost, fallback)` feeds the real exception + dispositional instructions back through `LLMClient.send_tool_result` so the LLM authors a one-sentence contextual explanation (references the specific cause — 404, auth, network, missing arg — and suggests a next step). Hardcoded fallback remains only if the LLM *also* errors. Signposts follow the `feedback_llm_steering_via_tool_results` memory pattern: fact + disposition, don't script exact user-facing wording.
- **Latency visibility added.** Both `pipeline/providers/openai.py` and `pipeline/providers/anthropic.py` now log a `TIMING llm_call=Xs TOKENS in=... cache_read=... cache_create=... out=... cache_hit=N%` line on every `complete()` call. `pipeline/chat_runner.py._execute_and_respond` logs `TIMING tool_exec=Xs name=<tool> result_bytes=N` around each MCP tool call. This lets `grep TIMING /tmp/operator.log` break end-to-end latency into first-LLM / tool-exec / second-LLM legs. First look at numbers during the harness session: cache hit rates were 95–98% (not the bottleneck); tool latency dominates (delegate runs 30–120s).
- **13.1 flagged "actually incomplete"** at session 124 start but the specific gap wasn't captured before scope shifted. Still unclear what's missing. Raise with user when 13 starts.

**Next action:** **Phase 13 — log cleanup (~2h) + 13.1 gap check (~30m).** Budget: ~22h vs April 19 launch.

**Previous (session 123, April 18, 2026):** Commit `60cadef`. Two workstreams, one commit.

- **Build card — rainbow only at reveal + wrap fixes.** User flagged that the session-122 rainbow frame showed up on every step which diluted the reveal-as-gift beat. Added `rainbow: bool = False` to `build_card.render()` (and `WizardState.card()`). Steps 2 & 3 pass `rainbow=False` (default) → plain white `rich.panel.Panel`. Reveal passes `rainbow=True` → existing per-character ANSI frame. Two real bugs in the existing card renderer surfaced in the same session:
  1. **Tagline crashing the face.** `_compose_body` was zipping portrait lines with a raw `meta_lines = [name, tagline]`. A long tagline would overflow the 38-cell inner width and wrap unpredictably *across* the face rows (Rich's wrap splits mid-row). Fix: wrap the tagline into the right-hand meta column (width = `_INNER - 2 - portrait_w - 3`) via `_wrap_cells` *before* zipping with the portrait, so extra tagline lines extend vertically under the name without touching the face grid.
  2. **Long MCP / skill rows truncating + leading indent getting stripped on wrap.** Original rainbow path hard-truncated to `_INNER` chars with `while cell_len(truncated) > _INNER: truncated = truncated[:-1]`; Panel mode let Rich reflow which stripped the `"  "` left indent on continuation rows. Fix: `_compose_body` now emits pre-wrapped, pre-padded rows using a new `_hang_wrap(prefix, body, width, inner)` helper — power-ups / skills rows get `"  power-ups:  "` style hanging indent on continuation lines so wrapped items align under the first item, and every row is padded to exactly `_INNER` cells before return. `_rainbow_wrap` no longer wraps (assumes pre-padded input). Panel created with `Text(..., no_wrap=True, overflow="crop")` so Rich doesn't re-flow and re-strip. Net effect: a tagline like "finds everything and summarizes long sources for you in real time" plus `power-ups: github linear notion slack` plus `skills: security-review begin-session end-session` all render cleanly with the face grid intact and full left-padding preserved on every row.

- **Phase 13.1 — killed `USER_DISPLAY_NAME` completely.** Dead field, vestigial from voice era. Removed from `config.py:36` (constant gone), `pipeline/setup.py:248` (defensive `cfg["agent"].pop(...)` no longer reachable because baselines no longer carry the key), `agents/{pm,designer,engineer}/config.yaml` (3 files), `agents/{pm,designer,engineer}/README.md` (dropped the `# 2. Update your display name` setup-snippet step), `CLAUDE.md:89` (field list), `docs/plan.md:32` (wizard-prompts description), and `tests/15_5_{1,2,2b}_testing.md` (3 prep sections; renumbered remaining steps to stay sequential). Runtime `git grep` clean. Two references left in `docs/agent-context.md` + `docs/roadmap.md` are session-log narratives explaining *why* the key was removed — not runtime references, so they stay for audit trail.

- **Pre-strip restore.** `agents/pm/config.yaml` + `agents/engineer/config.yaml` entered the session dirty in working copy — both showed the `yaml.safe_dump` comment-stripped shape from prior wizard smoke-tests, and engineer had `linear: enabled: true` / `delegate: enabled: false` flipped from a test run. Restored both via `git checkout --` at step 1 of the cleanup so the diff landing in `60cadef` was purely the `user_display_name` surgical strip, not bundled with the wizard-round-trip artifacts. Both files now back in canonical form.

- **Config reference added to `agents/README.md`.** New top-level section between Folder layout and Available agents. Six markdown tables — one per top-level block (`agent`, `llm`, `connector`, `skills`, `transcript`, `mcp_servers`) — each documenting Field / Type / Default / What it does. Source of truth for the schema. Replaces the plan of shipping inline YAML comments (which would have been wiped by the `yaml.safe_dump` round-trip anyway). Also dropped the stale "copy the root `config.yaml` as a starting point" sentence from the existing `### config.yaml` subsection — there's been no root `config.yaml` since the session 105 refactor.

Material concerns assessed: preset configs ship with explanatory inline comments that get stripped on wizard edit-in-place; user-added comments get wiped silently; structural grouping disappears. Zero data loss, purely ergonomic. Proper fix is `ruamel.yaml` round-trip, ~1–2h plus a new dep. Not a launch blocker — user is the only writer today. Revisit when inviting external contributors.

**Previous (session 122, April 18, 2026):** Two small polish passes on the wizard, both driven by user feedback. Commit `037ef87`.

- **Custom-mode prompts trimmed (5 → 2).** `_from_scratch` now asks only for `name` and `tagline`. `display_name` auto-equals `name` (user asked "can they be the same thing?" — yes). `trigger_phrase` auto-derives as `@<name>`. `user_display_name` prompt dropped entirely: grepped the codebase and found that `USER_DISPLAY_NAME` is loaded in `config.py:36` but never referenced anywhere else — it's a dead config key, almost certainly vestigial from the voice era when we needed to filter the user's own captions out. Wizard now pops the key from the cloned pm baseline so new bundles don't carry it forward either.
- **Tagline label simplified.** Was `tagline (one line, under ~60 chars) ():` — removed the hint parenthetical, and Rich's Prompt was also rendering an empty `()` because `default=""` shows as an empty default in parens. Passed `show_default=False` to kill that. Now reads just `tagline:`.
- **Rainbow-framed build card.** User supplied five raw ANSI codes (`\e[0;31;40m` red, `\e[0;32;40m` green, `\e[0;33;40m` yellow, `\e[0;34;40m` blue, `\e[0;35;40m` magenta — all on black bg) and asked if the card frame could rainbow with those. Wrote a standalone demo (`/tmp/rainbow_card_demo.py`) with two variants (per-character cycling vs. per-side solid bands) before implementing — user picked per-character. Replaced `rich.panel.Panel(border_style="bright_magenta")` in `pipeline/build_card.py` with hand-composed frame: `itertools.cycle(_COLORS)` walks every border glyph (`╭`, each `─`, title chars, `╮`, each `│`, `╰`, `╯`) and wraps each in its own ANSI color + reset. Body padding uses `rich.cells.cell_len` for cell-accurate alignment around the 2-wide `⚡` glyph (naive `len()` would have misaligned the power-ups row). Final result goes through `Text.from_ansi` so Rich re-parses the ANSI into segments when it renders.
- **Everything else demoted to plain white.** User's followup: "ensure all text has white font color. Only colored thing should be the build card." Stripped color from `⚡` (was yellow) and `★` (was cyan) in the card body; from the picker cursor glyph (`bold cyan` → `bold` in `picker.py:_render_rows`); from the wizard banner (`bold magenta` → `bold`), reveal header, and the success/error/cancel lines (dropped `[red]`/`[green]`/`[yellow]` markup). Kept `[bold]` and `[dim]` — they're weight/intensity modifiers, not colors. Fighter-select preview panel border stays `dim` (still white, just dimmer).
- **Tests.** 15/15 setup + 3/3 chat-hardening green. No test file changes needed — tests don't assert on colors, and the rainbow card still returns a Rich renderable that `state.card() is not None` passes cleanly.

**Same-session YAML comment-loss aftermath.** Session-start `git status` showed `agents/designer/config.yaml` dirty — the comment-stripped form from session 121's smoke-test. Restored via `git checkout --` before committing so only the wizard code changes landed. This is the same `yaml.safe_dump` bug logged under Hard Won Knowledge; still unfixed, `ruamel.yaml` replacement still the proper path.

**Previous (session 121, April 17, 2026):** User smoke-tested the session-120 wizard and dictated a series of UX tweaks. No architectural changes — all polish.

- **Step headers / titles.** "1. Fighter select" → "1. Choose your base agent" (and emptied the picker title to kill the duplicate). "Equip your MCPs" and "Equip bundled skills" picker titles removed — the console-printed step header carries the weight. "3. Skills" → "3. Add-ons (Skills)" with a new `Your <name> agent comes with the following:` subtitle.
- **Step 3 restructured twice.** First pass: merged the 3a text-input block into a single picker with a `+ Add my own skills` sentinel row at the bottom. User flagged the UX mismatch — "if I toggle the row, an input field should appear" doesn't work inside a Rich `Live` region. Second pass: dropped the sentinel, added a plain `Confirm.ask("Add your own skills?", default=False)` after the bundled-skills picker. Cleaner mental model. Also removed the auto-found `~/.claude/skills/` default path; floated an "only auto-find for the engineer preset" variant as a future enhancement (not wired yet).
- **Sublabel cut-off fix.** User reported skill descriptions truncating at exactly 60 chars ("Draft a structured PRD from meeting discussion — use when th"). Two causes: (a) `_skill_subtitle` applied a hard `desc[:60]` slice — dropped entirely (uncapped); (b) the picker rendered sublabels *inline after the label*, and the 40-col build-card right column squeezed the left column narrow enough that Rich truncated dim inline text. Fixed by restructuring `picker.py:_render_rows` to render sublabels on their own indented line under each label (6-col indent under checkbox rows, 2-col under cursor-only rows). Fix also helps step 1 and step 2 readability.
- **MCP sublabels gone.** Step 2 picker now shows MCP names only — `_mcp_subtitle` deleted, sublabel omitted. User asked to drop the "Always set includeArchived=false unless..." hint-tagline entirely.
- **Build card visuals.** `border_style` flipped `cyan` → `bright_magenta` (user wanted brighter/more saturated). Fixed `width=40` for uniform sizing. "based on X" meta line removed from the card body (dropped `based_on` kwarg from `build_card.render` and `WizardState.card` — the one caller).
- **Step 1 portrait centered.** User asked for the preview-pane bot face to be centered rather than left-aligned. Extended `Choice.preview` to accept `str | RenderableType` (previously `str | None`). `_custom_preview` and `_preset_preview` now return a `Group(Align.center(...), Text(""), Align.center(...), ...)`. Picker's fallback preview branch wraps bare strings in `Text()` and passes renderables through unchanged.
- **Screen clears between steps.** `console.clear()` fires between steps 1→2, 2→3, 3→4, and before the write+reveal block. Previous step + card disappear entirely so the user isn't looking at a cluttered scrollback.
- **Confirm → reveal beat.** Removed the `Confirm.ask("Write bundle to agents/<name>/?")` gate. Replaced with `console.input("Press Enter to reveal your bot ✨🎁")` — same role (final Enter-to-proceed), but framed as a dramatic beat instead of a "are you sure" prompt. Remaining "Blank line to finish." hint in the user-skill-path loop was also trimmed (user found it noisy).
- **Banner color.** "Operator setup wizard" title `[bold cyan]` → `[bold magenta]`.

All 15/15 setup tests + chat-hardening suite still green. Tests didn't need restructuring — the changes are layout/wording tweaks that don't touch helper signatures, and the picker tests still drive via injected `key_source` without caring about title text or sublabel layout.

User's pm/designer/engineer configs showed up in `git status` with all the helpful header comments gone even though they hadn't changed any wizard inputs. **Previous (session 120, April 17, 2026):** User walked through the session-119 wizard, said the comma-separated number-list UX felt janky and asked for an arrow-key gallery for step 1 with a portrait preview pane on the right (so users can browse fighters and see their faces) and a "build your character" panel that grows as they pick power-ups. Did a careful design pass before any code (~5 rounds of Q&A) — landed on: arrow-key picker for all three picker steps, persistent live build card on the right (Flavor B with portrait + name + tagline + based_on + power-ups + skills rows), placeholder portrait = `?? / ??` face matching the real face shape, real portrait revealed in step 5 only ("the gift"), edit-in-place shows the existing portrait from the start, no clutter (disabled MCPs hidden in card), unified `★` glyph for skills regardless of source, arrows + enter + space + `q`/`esc` only (no vim keys), reveal lands *after* the bundle is written so the portrait shown matches what's on disk.

Implementation in three building blocks plus a test pass:

- **`pipeline/picker.py`** (new, ~190 lines) — `Choice` dataclass + `select_one(title, choices, *, right_pane=None, initial=0, console=None, key_source=None)` and `select_many(title, choices, *, initial_checked=None, right_pane=None, ...)`. Both use `rich.live.Live` to redraw one region in place and `readchar.readkey()` for cross-platform key reads. Right-pane behavior: an explicit `right_pane: Callable[[cursor, checked], Renderable]` wins (used by build-card closures), else falls back to per-choice `Choice.preview` (used by step 1's gallery), else no right pane is drawn. `key_source: Iterable[str]` makes the picker deterministically testable without a TTY. `PickerCancelled` is raised on `q`/`Q`/ESC/Ctrl+C. ENTER handles both `\n` and `\r`.
- **`pipeline/build_card.py`** (new, ~75 lines) — `PLACEHOLDER_PORTRAIT` constant (the `▄▄▄▄▄▄ / █ ?? █ / █ ?? █ / ▀▀▀▀▀▀` face) + `render(*, name, tagline, based_on, portrait, power_ups, skills, title="Your build")` returns a Rich Panel. Top half is a `Table.grid` with portrait on the left and `name / tagline / based on X` on the right; bottom half is `power-ups: ⚡ X   ⚡ Y` and `skills: ★ A   ★ B` lines (empty rows show `—`). Cyan border, `Your build` as the default title; reveal step overrides title to `Meet <name>`.
- **`pipeline/setup.py`** rewritten around a `WizardState` dataclass (mode/name/display_name/tagline/based_on/portrait/bot_cfg/user_sources/bundled_skill_dirs). Methods: `equipped_mcps()`, `equipped_skills()` (concatenates user-source-resolved names + bundled-dir names), `card(mcps=, skills=, title=)`. Step 1 (`_step1_fighter_select`) builds choices = `Custom` + each existing bot, each with a per-choice `preview` string; calls `select_one`. Step 2 (`_step2_mcps`) builds Choices from MCP servers, passes `right_pane = lambda c, ch: state.card(mcps=names_where(ch))`. Step 3 (`_step3_skills`) keeps the user-paths text-input loop (no card during text input — agreed with user) then runs the bundled-skills picker with `right_pane = lambda c, ch: state.card(skills=user_skill_names + bundled_now)`. Step 4 (`_step4_api_keys`) unchanged (text input, no card). Step 5 (`_step5_write`) refactored to take a `WizardState`. New `_reveal(state)` reads the just-minted `agents/<name>/portrait.txt` via `face.load_or_render`, mutates `state.portrait`, and prints `✨ bot reveal 🎁` + the final card under `Meet <name>`. Removed `_render_toggle_list` and `_parse_number_list` (obsolete with the picker).
- **`tests/test_setup.py`** — dropped the number-list test, added: `WizardState.equipped_mcps`/`equipped_skills`/`card` (smoke), `_resolve_user_skill_names` for all three input shapes (md / SKILL.md folder / parent-walk), `_reveal` portrait swap (asserts `state.portrait` changes from placeholder to a face containing real `█` glyphs), and three picker tests with injected `key_source` (`select_one` ↑↓↓↵ → returns choice 2; `select_many` SPACE↓SPACE↵ → returns `[True, True, False]`; `select_one` `q` → raises `PickerCancelled`). 15/15 green. `tests/test_chat_hardening.py` still green.

**Two design pivots mid-session:**

1. **Right pane should be persistent across steps, not "card prints below after each step."** Original Flavor B sketch had the card flushed to scrollback between steps; user pushed back: "for consistency we should have this gallery vibe for each step." Refactored picker primitive to accept a `right_pane: Callable[(cursor, checked), Renderable]` argument so steps 2/3 could close over global wizard state and re-render the build card on every keystroke without mutating state during render.
2. **One `?` was too small for the placeholder face.** First draft was a single centered `?` with a blank line above; user said "the question mark is small for the custom bot face. If there's no way to get one big one then please fill the entire face with question marks." Switched to `?? / ??` matching the real face's eyes/mouth pattern density.

**Throwaway: `_picker_demo.py`** at repo root is an interactive smoke-test the user ran twice during development. Delete when convenient.

**Previous (session 119, April 17, 2026):** Merged `rename-roster-to-agents` into `main` at session start (fast-forward, 3 commits). Then built the wizard end-to-end per `docs/plan.md`.

- **`pipeline/setup.py`** — five steps: (1) fighter-select with two modes — from-scratch clones pm baseline, prompts for name/display/trigger/tagline/user-display, loops on invalid/colliding names, reserves `setup`/`list` and any existing agent dir; preset inherits the name and operates in edit-in-place mode. (2) Power-ups — numbered-list toggle rendering each MCP block's `enabled` flag as `[ ]` or `[✓]`; comma-separated numbers flip. (3) Skills — user-added paths (folder with SKILL.md, parent of such folders, or single `.md` file wrapped in a stem-named folder as SKILL.md) plus bundled skills from the base bot as the same toggle (all-checked default). All selected skills are **copied** into `agents/<name>/skills/` — no external references. (4) API keys — scans enabled MCP blocks for `${VAR}` refs, prompts for any missing from `.env`, appends (never overwrites). (5) Atomic write via `tempfile.mkdtemp` inside `agents/` + `os.rename`. Edit-in-place **seeds the tempdir from the existing bundle** before overwriting owned files, fully re-authors `skills/`, overwrites `config.yaml` + `portrait.txt`, and only writes a README stub when absent — preserves `.env.example`, `delegate_to_claude_code.py`, hand-written READMEs. `.bak-<timestamp>` swap on edit-in-place is the abort-recovery path (deleted on success). Custom YAML str representer keeps multi-line hints as `|` block literals.
- **`__main__.py`** — `_run_setup` now dispatches to `pipeline.setup.run`. `operator setup` runs the wizard.
- **`requirements.txt`** — `rich` added.
- **`tests/test_setup.py`** — 10 cases all green: name validation + reserved names, MCP `enabled` flip round-trip through yaml dump/load, three skill-copy shapes (folder / single-file wrap / parent walk), atomic-write rollback on build failure, edit-in-place preservation of unknown files + wipe of stale skills, from-scratch bundle creation, `.env` append safety (never overwrites existing keys), number-list parser edge cases.
- **Smoke-tested both modes** end-to-end via scripted stdin. From-scratch wrote a clean `agents/smoketest/` bundle; `OPERATOR_BOT=smoketest python -c "import config"` loaded cleanly (`MCP_SERVERS: []`, `SKILLS_PATHS: ['agents/smoketest/skills']`). Edit-in-place on designer diffed only `config.yaml` (comments stripped — known tradeoff) and preserved every sibling file; restored via git.

**Two bugs caught in the smoke cycle, both fixed inline:**

1. **Rich markup swallowed `[x]`.** The checked-state marker for the bundled-skills toggle list rendered as a blank: Rich's markup parser treats `[x]` as a (non-existent) style tag and strips it. `[ ]` (with a space) is not valid markup so it printed literally — exposing the asymmetry only when some items were default-checked. Fix: switched to `[✓]` (non-ASCII content inside brackets is not parsed as a style).
2. **Edit-in-place wiped unknown files.** First implementation did `os.rename(tempdir, target)` as the swap, wholesale-replacing the bundle. Designer's `.env.example` and hand-written README got nuked. Fix: at the start of `_step5_write` in edit mode, `shutil.copytree(target, tmp, dirs_exist_ok=True)` seeds the tempdir with the existing bundle; then `skills/` is wiped and re-authored (so deselections drop skill folders), owned files are overwritten, and the README stub is only written if the seed didn't already carry one. Tests updated to assert preservation + stale-skill wipe + no-backup-on-success.

**Known tradeoff:** YAML comments in `config.yaml` are lost through the wizard's dump/load cycle (no ruamel dep). Values are semantically preserved. Worth revisiting if users complain; for now ruamel would be overkill.

- **Smoke-test `operator engineer <url>` + `operator designer <url>`** under positional CLI — still deferred (six sessions now). ~15m.
- **Demo GIF** in `agents/*/README.md` still placeholder.
- **YAML comment loss on edit-in-place** — acceptable for now; may warrant ruamel.yaml later.

**Previous (session 117, April 16, 2026):** Started by investigating a "tool calls feel less performant on `operator pm` vs `operator pm <url>`" report from the user. Diagnosed as a correctness bug, not a perf one: same URL = same slug = same JSONL → `MeetingRecord.tail(n)` returned accumulated entries from every prior run, including the agent's own prior assistant replies. Over multiple runs the LLM started echoing those prior replies instead of calling tools fresh. Worst case observed: "mojo jojo" → bot reply "Created https://linear.app/mojo-jojo/issue/MOJ-11/fold-my-laundry" with **zero tool calls logged** — the model pattern-matched on MOJ-N URLs it had seen in history and hallucinated one. Fix: write a `{"kind": "session_start", "timestamp": ...}` boundary marker on every `MeetingRecord.__init__`; `tail()` now scopes to entries after the most recent marker. Raw JSONL preserves full audit (two `session_start` lines visible after reopen). `tests/test_chat_hardening.py` updated: `test_meeting_record_tail_roundtrip` now asserts that reopening the same slug yields empty tail until new appends, and that meta lives in the raw file (not in `tail()` output).

Then moved to Phase 15.5.4. User pointed at a reference mock (`temp.md` — now untracked/scratch) that reframed the work: not 16×20 half-block pixel art with ANSI 256-color as originally specced, but a stylized 4-line glyph face inside a small `█ ▄ ▀` box frame, monochrome. Much simpler and more legible. Implemented in one pass, pausing twice for user review (tagline draft → "punchier please" → second pass approved; banner placement → "where's the banner" → moved from post-MCP to pre-MCP boot splash).

- **`pipeline/face.py`** — deterministic glyph-face generator. 25 eye glyphs × 20 mouth glyphs = 500 combos. `_seeded_index()` uses `hashlib.sha256(f"{name}:{salt}".encode()).digest()` — explicitly NOT Python's `hash()` (which is process-randomized via PYTHONHASHSEED). Hand-curated `OVERRIDES` dict for the MVP bots matches a fighter-select reference mock: engineer `▲▲/══`, pm `⊙⊙/‿‿`, designer `◠◠/▽▽`. `render(name, plain=False)` returns the 4-line face. `load_or_render(name, portrait_path)` prefers a committed file, falls back to a fresh render. `write_if_missing(name, path)` is the first-run hook — idempotent, writes only if the file doesn't exist.
- **`agent.tagline` config field** — each roster bot now has a one-line capability reminder. Engineer: "spins up Claude Code worktrees while you meet". PM: "turns decisions into Linear tickets before you forget them". Designer: "opens your Figma and pulls no punches". Wired into `config.py` as `AGENT_TAGLINE`. `_bot_tagline()` in `__main__.py` prefers `config.yaml`'s `agent.tagline` over the README-first-line fallback used by pre-tagline bots.
- **`roster/*/portrait.txt` committed** for the three MVP bots. Generator output was good enough to commit as-is (the "hand-curation" from the spec collapsed to "generate, eyeball, commit" since the overrides already lock the look).
- **Startup banner** in `__main__.py` via `_print_startup_banner(skills, plain=False)` — prints face on left + name/tagline/loadout on right across 4 lines to stderr. Loadout: `linear · github · 4 skills · claude-sonnet-4-5` (MCP server names from config, skill count, model). First-run hook fires inside the banner helper: if no `portrait.txt` for this bot, `face.write_if_missing()` mints one and logs the path. **Banner placement was a live-verification finding** — initial attempt put it after MCP connects so it could show ✓/✗ per server; that printed it ~40 lines into scrollback, user said "Where's the banner?" Rewrote to fire as a boot splash before MCP + browser start, dropping the ✓/✗ (existing per-server connect logs already surface status). Now it's the first non-trivial thing on screen when you run `operator <name>`.
- **`--plain` flag** — ASCII-only fallback for screen readers / hostile terminals. Box becomes `+----+`, eyes/mouths use a smaller pool of ASCII glyphs (`oo`, `**`, `--`, `==`, etc.), separator in loadout swaps `·` → `|`. Plain-mode first-run writes are skipped so the ASCII fallback doesn't get persisted as the canonical portrait.
- **`tests/test_face.py`** — 9 cases: determinism, cross-process stability (guards against a regression to `hash()`), overrides, render shape, plain mode, library size (≥400 combos), file preference, fallback, first-run write idempotency.
- **Live-verified** — `operator pm` boot splash renders as expected: `▄▄▄▄▄▄ PM` / `█ ⊙⊙ █ turns decisions into Linear tickets before you forget them` / `█ ‿‿ █ linear · github · 4 skills · claude-sonnet-4-5` / `▀▀▀▀▀▀`. Fires at t=0 before any log output. Full admission + Linear tool-call flow exercised clean.

**Previous (session 116, April 16, 2026):** Smoke-tested `operator pm` and discovered a flaky 5–15s shutdown hang on the tool-call path. Root-caused via stack dumps to a Playwright greenlet wedge on a dead CDP socket, landed two fixes, live-verified.

- **Smoke test found flaky teardown.** Three-trial matrix: A (quiet Ctrl+C after admission), B ("hey" → reply → Ctrl+C), C (Linear tool call → reply → Ctrl+C). A and B always clean (~1s). C wedged ~5–15s and the safety net caught the Playwright Node driver as an orphan. Not consistently reproducible — ~1 in 3 tool-call shutdowns.
- **Stack dump + instrumented `leave()` identified the wedge.** Added a `_browser_thread.join(timeout=5)` + `sys._current_frames()` stack dump to `connectors/macos_adapter.py:leave()`. Stack showed the greenlet parked in `sync_playwright/_context_manager.py:56 greenlet_main` → `run_until_complete(connection.run_as_sync())` → asyncio `base_events._run_once` → `selectors.KqueueSelector.select` → `kqueue.control(None, max_ev, timeout)`. `timeout=None` means "wait forever for I/O." The Node driver's CDP socket was dead (Chrome self-exits in `--headless=new` a moment after the Leave click) but the greenlet was waiting for CDP responses that never arrived.
- **First attempt (didn't fully fix):** removed the explicit `browser.close()` from `_browser_session`'s finally block. Rationale: `browser.close()` on a persistent context was the most obvious place for the hang. That helped the clean path but the same wedge signature reproduced inside `sync_playwright.__exit__` → `playwright.stop()` on the tool-call path — so the hang isn't unique to `browser.close()`, the whole context-manager exit can hit it.
- **Fix 1 — kill the Playwright driver directly.** New `_kill_playwright_drivers()` helper in `macos_adapter.py`: `pgrep -P <self_pid>` + `ps -o command=` to find children whose cmdline matches `playwright` + `run-driver`, SIGKILL them. `leave()` now does `_browser_thread.join(timeout=2)` → if still alive, call `_kill_playwright_drivers()` → re-join 2s. SIGKILLing the Node driver closes its socket, which unblocks the greenlet's `kqueue.select(None)`, the greenlet's event loop exits, and the context-manager unwinds cleanly. Shrinks the worst-case shutdown from 5–15s + outer safety-net (~7s total) down to ~3s deterministic, with no orphan.
- **Fix 2 — stop ChatRunner promptly on SIGINT.** The secondary symptom was a stray `ChatRunner: participant count changed 2 → 0` log appearing *after* `left meeting`. Root cause: the ChatRunner loop runs on the main thread, SIGINT runs the shutdown handler synchronously on the main thread (setting `_stop_event`, then blocking 6s inside `connector.leave()`), then returns control to the loop — which continues one more iteration's body before the top-of-while check. Added `if self._stop_event.is_set(): break` guards in `pipeline/chat_runner.py:_loop` after the blocking `read_chat()` and `get_participant_count()` calls, so the loop bails before logging/processing anything if stop was set while those were in flight.
- **Live-verified.** Three clean `operator pm` runs (quiet + two chat turns) — ~1s shutdown, no safety-net line, no stray logs. Then a tool-call run (`create an issue in linear to fold my laundry` → MOJ-11) deliberately hit the wedge: log reads `waiting for browser to close...` → `clicked Leave call` → `force-killed stuck Playwright driver pid=84330` → `left meeting` 4ms later. Total Ctrl+C → shutdown = 3.1s. No `Safety net: killing` line (inline SIGKILL beat the outer safety net). No stray `participant count changed` after `left meeting` (stop_event guard held). Fix working end-to-end on the exact scenario that was flaky.

**Previous (session 115, April 16, 2026):** Closed out Phase 15.5.3 by landing reliable auto-admit. Two iterations.

- **Iter 1 — added post-action verification + diagnostics.** Replaced the original "fire and log success unconditionally" admission block with: log the pill's actual `inner_text()`, log `admit_btn count=N visible=B`, save `debug/post_admit_pill_persisted.{png,html}` when the action runs but pill stays put, suppress the keyboard-fallback "admitted" log unless the pill disappears. Live test revealed the real issue: admission *did* succeed (participant count went 1→2 right after tray click), but Meet leaves the "Admit 1 guest" pill widget sticky in the DOM — visible to the human, visible to Playwright. So a "wait for pill gone" verifier loops forever.
- **Iter 2 — verification via participant-count delta + cooldown.** Swapped pill-disappearance check for `_do_get_participant_count(page)` polling for up to 3s post-click; success = count went up. Added a `(pill_text, participant_count)` cooldown so the same stale pill silently skips re-attempts until something actually changes. New diagnostic snapshot `debug/post_admit_success.{png,html}` saved on verified admission. Logs now read: `admit pill detected text='Admit 1 guest' count=1` → `admit_btn count=1 visible=True` → `admitted via tray click (verified — participant count 1 → 2)` then silence. Bonus: graceful shutdown also clean this run (Leave call clicked, browser closed in <1s, no 10s timeout).

**What just happened (session 114, April 16, 2026):** Live-validated Phase 15.5.3 in pieces, fixed three issues, added auto-admit plumbing (not yet confirmed).

- **Issue 1 fixed — "browser never opened":** On `operator pm` (no URL), `meet.new` was auto-joining us as the creator (we were already in the meeting). The pre-join flow raced for "Join now" / "Ask to join" / "Sign in" buttons and all three waits timed out → adapter treated it as `join_fail` and tore down. Fix: detect already-in state via `Leave call` button visibility *before* the pre-join race, skip camera toggle + join-button race, set `clicked_label = "already_in"`. Applied to both macOS and Linux adapters.
- **Issue 2 fixed — wrong meeting URL captured:** `wait_for_url(lambda u: ...)` was accepting Google's interstitial `https://meet.google.com/new?authuser=0&hs=178` as the "real" meeting URL because the old ends-with check didn't strip query strings. Bot then redirected to a real room (`ofz-btin-pcd`) and the human got handed the interstitial URL by `webbrowser.open`, which spun up a *different* fresh meeting under the user's account → bot and user in separate rooms. Fix: added `_is_real_meet_room(url)` using `urlparse().path` + regex `^/[a-z]{3,}-[a-z]{3,}-[a-z]{3,}/?

, passed as the predicate to `wait_for_url`.
- **Issue 3 fixed — no visible browser for the human:** Bot runs headless by design (`--headless=new` Chrome flag, invisible). That's correct. The missing piece was opening a *separate* visible tab for the human to join the same Meet. Fix: `__main__.py` now calls `webbrowser.open(meeting_url)` after the URL resolves (meet.new path only).
- **Host/knock problem — auto-admit plumbing added (not yet live-confirmed):** When the bot creates the meeting, the bot is host; the human knocks and needs to be admitted. Implemented auto-admit inside the adapter's in-meeting hold loop: every 2s, find the "Admit N guest(s)" pill via `get_by_text(regex)`, `.hover()` to trigger Playwright's real CDP mouse move (the pill is a *hover-tray widget*, not a button — synthetic `dispatchEvent` won't open the tray), then click the tray's `role=button name="Admit"`. Keyboard fallback: `pill.focus()` → `ArrowDown` → `Enter` (the pill's aria description says "Press Down Arrow to open the hover tray and Escape to close" — it's keyboard-activatable). Saves `debug/admit_diagnostic.{png,html}` on first hover-fire for future inspection. **Live test failed to admit** on last attempt; out of context before retry.
- **Doc scrub:** `./operator` → `operator` across 11 files (CLAUDE.md, roster READMEs, tests/15_5_*_testing.md, tests/11_*_testing.md, config.py error string) — the bash wrapper is symlinked into `~/.local/bin/` so bare `operator <name>` works from any directory.

**Open items:**
- **Auto-admit live-confirmation** — run `operator pm`, knock from another account, confirm admission fires. If it doesn't, inspect `debug/admit_diagnostic.{png,html}`.
- **15.5.4 (face system) + 15.5.5 (wizard)** still outstanding in Phase 15.5 scope.
- **Demo GIF** in `roster/*/README.md` still a placeholder — user has deprioritized.

**Next action:** Live-retest auto-admit. Then proceed to Phase 15.5.4 — face system + profile banner.

**What just happened (session 112, April 16, 2026):** Walked `tests/15_5_2b_testing.md` T1–T7 against fresh Meet `cyv-utza-jxp`. The "soft" catalog restriction on Figma's official MCP turned out to be hard. Fell back to GLips mid-session, re-ran, all tests passed, then promoted GLips to bundle default with full doc update.

- **OAuth catalog gate is hard.** Official Figma MCP via `npx -y mcp-remote https://mcp.figma.com/mcp` failed at T1 with `HTTP 403: Invalid OAuth error response ... Raw body: Forbidden` raised from `mcp-remote`'s `registerClient` (dynamic client registration). Figma's `/register` endpoint rejects arbitrary clients — only those in Figma's MCP Catalog succeed. Operator is not (yet) in the catalog. Browser OAuth consent never opened because we didn't make it past `registerClient`. Pipeline correctly logged `MCP: 0/1 servers loaded (figma ✗)` and kept running.
- **Fell back to GLips** (`figma-developer-mcp`, PAT-authenticated). Env-mapped `${FIGMA_TOKEN}` → `FIGMA_API_KEY` for the child. Relaunched with `--force` (first-run left a stale session lock), bot joined, `MCP: 1/1 servers loaded (figma ✓)` with 2 tools (`get_figma_data`, `download_figma_images`).
- **All T1–T7 passed on the GLips path** (T4 marked N/A — GLips is read-only; verified by reading GLips' `src/mcp/index.ts`, which registers exactly two tools both with `readOnlyHint: true`, regardless of the PAT's write capability).
  - **T3 anti-hallucination guard live-demonstrated.** First test URL (`bTJlOWqmnmqVRmc2e4GGYd`, "Product carousel.") came back as a single RECTANGLE with an image fill — 592 chars, not a multi-card frame. Verified against Figma's REST API directly: the entire file contains just that one rectangle. Designer correctly read the thin payload and pushed back ("That's just a single image rectangle — no cards or spacing to review. Is this the right node?") instead of fabricating card critique. Iterated on a second URL (Plant-shop-curved-carousel from Community, node 1:2) which returned a 12KB payload; Designer produced a specific, grounded critique: "5 cards × 386×512px, 40px gap too tight, increase to 64–80px, plant-image breathing room, thumb-swipe targets."

Per test plan this is the explicit fail signal. But the persona *can* do the conversational register: on redirect ("that was long, brief thoughts?") Designer replied with the canonical 1-sentence shape ("Bump the gap to 72px and make the plant names heavier — right now everything blurs together."). Trigger-sensitivity gap, not a capability gap. User chose to ship as-is and log the tuning note.

Decided NOT to adopt as default: (a) plugin + bridge is more moving parts than the GLips npx-only default, (b) addressability regression — it operates only on the file currently open in the plugin, losing the "paste any Figma URL in chat" UX that's core to the hero moment. **Previous context (session 107, April 15, 2026):** Phase 12 validated (OpenAI provider spot-check, ~1h vs ~3h estimated — gap covered by thorough 11.x testing). Then planning for Phase 15.5:

- **`agents/` renamed to `roster/`** — "agents" felt gimmicky/overused. Explored ~30 naming options. `roster` won: lives natively in both the gaming metaphor (fighting game character select) and the meeting/team metaphor ("here's the roster"). Fits the "choose your fighter → add power-ups → go" onboarding model.
- **Three roster members (was two):** expanded from engineer + PM to engineer + PM + designer, framed as a "pre-built execution team."
  - **`roster/engineer/`** (was `claude-code`, then `coder`) — GitHub MCP + bundled `delegate_to_claude_code` mini MCP server (~50 lines Python, runs `claude -p "<task>" --worktree`, returns result). Security is Claude Code's problem (own permission model + worktree isolation). Loads user's `~/.claude/skills/`. Prerequisite: `claude` CLI installed. Power-up path: shell MCP (with security warning).
  - **`roster/pm/`** (was `standup-pm`) — Linear MCP (the "one killer MCP"), GitHub for access. Captions enabled by default. PRD-from-discussion skill. Structured standup summary. Power-up path: Notion, Slack, Brave Search.
  - **`roster/designer/`** (new) — Figma MCP (`figma-developer-mcp`, official, production-ready, read-only: pull frames/nodes, export images, get/post comments). Creative persona with personality. Minimal scope — just the idea that we ship with comprehensive value. Power-up path: Canva MCP when mature.
- **Key design decision: no shell MCP for engineer.** GitHub MCP covers code reading. Read-only shell is redundant (GitHub `get_file_contents` + `search_code` already do this). Full shell has real prompt-injection risk (arbitrary code execution as user). Instead, `delegate_to_claude_code` gives the "it can actually code" capability without the security surface — Claude Code has its own battle-tested sandbox.

**Previous context (session 105, April 15, 2026):** Tiny Phase 11.7 fix + architectural discussion.

- **`config.py:79`** — changed `OPENAI_API_KEY = os.environ["OPENAI_API_KEY"]` to `.get(..., "")`. `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` was already using `.get()`.
- **`pipeline/providers/__init__.py` `build_provider()`** — added symmetric guard in the openai branch (`if not config.OPENAI_API_KEY: raise RuntimeError(...)`) matching the existing anthropic pattern. Each provider's key is now required only if that provider is configured.
- **Verified both paths:** `OPENAI_API_KEY= python -c "import config"` imports cleanly; building with `llm.provider: anthropic` + empty OPENAI_API_KEY works; forcing `llm.provider: openai` with empty key raises the expected clear RuntimeError. Unblocks Anthropic-only BYOK users and `--check-mcp` without a provider key.
- Committed as `d756962`.

**Architectural threads discussed (no code, deferred to post-MVP):**
- **Bash/code execution for Operator.** Options ranked: bash-MCP > skill-as-CLI-recipe > built-in. Bash-MCP gives per-tool confirm gating + audit trail (`READ_TOOLS`-style); skill-as-CLI-recipe is faster to author but every invocation looks like "bash ran" from `chat_runner.py`'s perspective. Noteworthy bash-MCP servers: `tumf/mcp-shell-server`, `blazickjp/shell-mcp-server`. Low adoption of bash-MCPs in general is because *sandboxing* (Docker/container per tool call) is the hard part, not the server.
- **Phase 15.5.1 is a roster entry WITH Claude Code delegation (revised session 107).** Originally (session 105) this was a gallery-only entry with no subprocess integration. Session 107 added a bundled `delegate_to_claude_code` mini MCP server (~50 lines Python) that runs `claude -p "<task>" --worktree` as a subprocess. This is NOT the heavy sub-agent architecture discussed in session 105 — it's a single tool call that shells out to the CLI. Security is Claude Code's responsibility (own permission model + worktree isolation). The engineer roster member both *resembles* Claude Code in shape (skills, engineering persona) and *delegates to* Claude Code for actual execution.
- **Modular sub-agent spawning (Codex / Claude Code / scrapers).** Recommended shape: model sub-agents as MCP tools exposing `spawn`, `status`, `result`, `cancel`. Default execution = async-detached. Deliver artifacts *around* Operator (sub-agent writes directly to Linear / GitHub PR / Slack), not *through* it (avoid blowing Operator's context window). Three design axes: transport (MCP-per-agent vs dispatcher vs subprocess), execution model (sync / async-blocking / async-detached), result channel (through Operator / around Operator). All post-MVP.
- **CLI-as-skill vs MCP.** CLI skills are great for breadth + fast authoring (SKILL.md + `--help`), but you lose structured tool-call logging, confirm gating, and `READ_TOOLS` allowlist. Recommendation: support both post-MVP; MCP stays for write-side tools where audit/confirm matters.
- **Claude API + shell vs Claude Code.** Same raw capability; difference is the curated loop (tool-call handling, context management, confirm UX, session state, hooks, subagents, skills, slash commands, IDE integration). Operator already has its own loop in `chat_runner.py` + `llm.py` — we are a Claude-Code-shaped thing, specialized for meetings.

**Next action:** Tackle **Phase 15.5.1** (`roster/engineer/`, ~2h — config.yaml + delegate_to_claude_code mini MCP server + README + skills + .env.example). After that: 15.5.2 (PM) → 15.5.2b (designer) → 15.5.3 (wizard) → 15.5.4 (meet.new) → 13 → 15.6 → 14 → 15 → 16. Phase 15.5.0 (rename) complete. MVP target still April 19, 2026.

**Previous context (session 104, April 14, 2026):** Walked `docs/11_4_testing.md` T1–T9 end-to-end against two fresh Meets (progressive mode → non-progressive mode → broken-config mode).

- **T1** startup banner + menu injection ✓ — `SKILLS: 2/2 loaded` and `LLM injected skills (menu): hello, tone` both present.
- **T2** `@operator use the hello skill` produced `tool_call name=load_skill`, `SKILLS turn=1 load_skill called: 'hello'`, `send_tool_result tool=load_skill result_len=81`, and reply `skill-token-7h2x acknowledged` — body reached the model, no confirmation prompt.
- **T3** `/tone how was the sprint demo` produced `SKILLS turn=2 slash-invoke: tone`, zero `load_skill` tool_calls, single `LLM ask` for the turn, reply started with `Arrr!` — `extra_system` threading works.
- **T4** `/nope what's up` produced `SKILLS turn=3 unknown slash token: /nope` at DEBUG, normal reply, no counter bump.
- **T5 (critical)** three chit-chat turns (`what's 2 plus 2`, `thanks`, `tell me a joke`) produced **zero** `load_skill` tool_calls. Menu wording is correctly non-tempting — no prompt tightening needed.
- **T6** model's first instinct on `call load_skill with name="ghost"` was to reason from the menu and reply directly without calling the tool — actually ideal UX. A second, more forceful prompt (`force-call load_skill for the skill named "ghost"`) did trigger the tool, producing the literal `Error: no skill named 'ghost'. Available skills: hello, tone.` string. Error path works when forced.
- **T7** flipped `progressive_disclosure: false` and restarted. Startup logged `LLM injected skills (full-body): hello, tone`. First chat turn (`use the hello skill`) got the `skill-token-7h2x acknowledged` reply with **zero** tool_calls. `tools=72` vs `tools=73` in progressive mode confirmed `load_skill` correctly gated out.
- **T8** added `/tmp/does-not-exist` to paths and `/tmp/op-skills/broken/SKILL.md` without frontmatter. Startup logged both WARNs (missing path, missing frontmatter) and `SKILLS: 2/3 loaded (hello ✓, tone ✓)`. Operator came up healthy.
- **T9** `SKILLS session summary: turns=1 load_skill_calls=1 by_name={'tone': 1}` emitted on Ctrl+C. Slash invocations correctly increment the counter.

Cleanup done: `rm -rf /tmp/op-skills` and `config.yaml skills.paths` reverted to `[]`.
