**Previous context (session 103, April 14, 2026):** Implemented Phase 11.4 in one pass.

- **New `pipeline/skills.py`:** `Skill` dataclass + `load_skills(paths)`. Each config entry resolves to either a single skill folder (contains `SKILL.md`) or a parent dir scanned one level deep for `*/SKILL.md` — deeper nesting is ignored by design. Frontmatter parsed with `pyyaml`; malformed YAML, missing `name`/`description`, or unreadable files WARN + skip, never crash. `allowed-tools` parsed from either list or comma-string; anything outside the supported set (`load_skill` only for now) WARNs but the skill still loads (model may decline). Duplicate names across paths resolve last-wins + WARN. Startup banner matches the MCP shape: `SKILLS: N/M loaded (<name> ✓, ...)`.
- **`LLMClient.inject_skills(skills, progressive)`:** in progressive mode, system prompt gets a name+description menu plus instructions that restrict `load_skill` calls to requests that *clearly* match a description (prompt-tightening knob if the model over-calls). In non-progressive mode, full bodies are inlined. Also added an `extra_system` one-shot kwarg to `ask()` so slash-invocation can thread the skill body through without duplicating the user turn or mutating the persistent system prompt.
- **`ChatRunner` — three wiring additions.** (1) Accepts `skills` + `skills_progressive` kwargs and builds a name-indexed lookup. (2) `_tools_for_llm()` centralizes the MCP tools list and appends a synthetic `load_skill` function tool when progressive mode is on and at least one skill is loaded — replaced all three `self._mcp.get_openai_tools()` call-sites. (3) `_dispatch_result` short-circuits `load_skill` tool calls to a local handler (`_handle_load_skill`) that resolves the body and feeds it back via `send_tool_result` — auto-executed, no confirmation prompt. Slash-invocation (`/<name>` after the trigger strip) bypasses the round-trip entirely by passing the body via `extra_system` on a single `ask()` call. Unknown `/slash` is a pass-through (DEBUG log, no counter bump, no error).
- **SKILLS logging:** per-turn `SKILLS turn=N slash-invoke: <name>`, `SKILLS turn=N load_skill called: '<name>' (available: ...)`, `SKILLS turn=N unknown slash token: /<name>`, plus a session summary `SKILLS session summary: turns=N load_skill_calls=M by_name={...}` emitted from `stop()`. Per-turn visibility is the user's monitor for "is the model over-calling load_skill on chit-chat" — the open-item flag from session 102.
- **`config.yaml`/`config.py`:** `skills:` block with `progressive_disclosure: true` (default) and `paths: []`. Both flags surface as `SKILLS_PATHS` / `SKILLS_PROGRESSIVE_DISCLOSURE`.
- **`__main__.py`:** loader called up-front in both macOS and Linux paths, `inject_skills` lands *before* `inject_mcp_hints/status` so the final system-prompt ordering is base → skills → MCP hints → MCP status (most-dynamic last, future prompt-caching-friendly). `ChatRunner` gets `skills=` + `skills_progressive=` kwargs on both platforms.
- **`tests/test_skills.py` — 13 cases, all passing:** loader happy path, parent-dir scan, missing path (WARN + no crash), malformed YAML (skip + WARN), missing name/description (skip + WARN), duplicate last-wins + WARN, deep nesting ignored, `allowed-tools` WARN on unsupported entries, LLM menu-mode doesn't leak bodies, LLM full-body mode inlines them, `load_skill` tool gated on `progressive AND skills_loaded`, call-rate sanity (6 unrelated messages → 0 load_skill calls locally), slash-invocation increments counters + threads body into `extra_system`. Full existing suite (chat_hardening, 911/912/913, guardrails) still green.
- **Live-test plan at `docs/11_4_testing.md`:** 9 tests. T1 startup banner, T2 `load_skill` tool end-to-end (uses `skill-token-7h2x` sentinel string to prove body reached model), T3 slash fast path skipped the round-trip (verify zero `load_skill` tool_calls for that turn), T4 unknown slash pass-through, T5 over-eagerness regression (three unrelated messages → zero `load_skill` calls — this is the real behavioral test, since locally we can only check counter increments), T6 unknown skill name graceful error, T7 non-progressive full-body mode, T8 broken config degrades gracefully, T9 session summary on Ctrl+C.

**Design decisions made this session worth remembering:**
- **`extra_system` for slash invocation > pre-populating scratch.** The plan said "synthetic load_skill tool result pre-populated before the ask." Attempting that in `_scratch` would have conflicted with `ask()` clearing scratch at the start of every user turn. And prepending the body to the user message text would have both (a) required the meeting record to carry the expanded version or risk the LLM seeing two user turns, and (b) polluted the record on disk. A one-shot `extra_system` kwarg on `ask()` is invisible to the record, non-persistent on `_system_prompt`, and passes through to the provider as a normal system suffix. Cleanest fit for the constraint.
- **Unified `_tools_for_llm()` instead of ad-hoc list concatenation.** Three call-sites were doing `self._mcp.get_openai_tools() if self._mcp else None`. Moving that into one method that also knows whether to append `load_skill` means any future synthetic tool slots in without hunting for call-sites. Also lets the `load_skill` schema use an `enum` of loaded skill names to prevent the model from inventing one.
- **Auto-execute `load_skill` with no confirmation.** It's local, read-only, and purely a context-pull. Routing it through `_needs_confirmation` would have been the consistent path but would add friction for zero gain. The check in `_dispatch_result` lives at the top of the `tool_call` branch so it's hard to miss.
- **Log per-turn + session summary, not just summary.** The user's stated concern is "is the model calling load_skill too eagerly?" Per-turn logs let a human grep for occurrences in real time; the summary is the quick post-mortem. Without per-turn lines, a 20-turn meeting that ends with `load_skill_calls=3` doesn't tell you *which* turns fired.

**Known limitations remaining:**
- **Prompt-tightening is the real control if the model over-calls load_skill.** Code-side tests only verify our local counters don't fire on chit-chat; whether the LLM itself resists calling `load_skill` on "what's 2+2" is a behavioral property of the menu wording in `LLMClient.inject_skills`. T5 in the live-test plan is the only real check. If it fails, tighten the wording; do not add code gates.
- **`skills.local.yaml` personal overrides not yet implemented.** Deferred per session 102 — add post-MVP if users ask.
- **No hot reload.** SKILL.md changes require an Operator restart. Meeting-scoped sessions are short enough that this is fine.
- **Calendar-mode captions still need `ChatRunner.run_polling()`.** Carried from session 101.

**What just happened (session 101, April 14, 2026):** Walked the full captions live-test plan against `https://meet.google.com/fqx-xndc-odd` with a second human participant. Found and fixed three issues, then re-walked the critical subset (T1/T2/T6/T9) clean.

- **Issue #3 (CRITICAL — caused T6 to fail with 400 `messages: at least one message is required`).** `__main__.py` constructs `LLMClient` at line 201 *before* the captions path creates `meeting_record` at line 217, and only `ChatRunner` was ever wired to the new record (`chat_runner.py:66-72` only calls `llm.set_record(...)` when ChatRunner has to construct the record itself). With captions enabled, the LLM was holding its default empty in-memory `MeetingRecord` while everything else wrote to the on-disk one — `_tail_messages` returned `[]` and Anthropic rejected the call. **Fix:** added `llm.set_record(meeting_record)` immediately after `meeting_record = MeetingRecord(...)` in `__main__.py:218`. One line. Diagnosis was the longest part — the two startup log lines `MeetingRecord opened in-memory (no slug)` and `MeetingRecord opened …<slug>.jsonl` were the smoking gun once we knew to look.
- **Issue #1 (same-speaker dedupe).** Google Meet keeps the prior caption text visible in the same speaker's region, so each finalize re-emits everything Meet hasn't scrolled off yet. Without dedupe, a same-speaker continuation persists as "prior + new" instead of just "new." First attempt used strict `text.lower().startswith(prior.lower())` and that failed live because Meet auto-corrects casing/punctuation on prior text between finalizes (e.g. `"here,"` → `"Here."`). **Fix:** ported the `_normalize_for_match` token-prefix idea from `voice-preserved/pipeline/captions.py` into a new `_strip_prior_prefix(text, prior)` helper that compares words via `\w+` regex (case + punct insensitive) and cuts the original text at the end-position of the last matched token. Per-speaker dict so A's prior never affects B. Validated live across 5 finalize boundaries in a single Deepak monologue — every row contained only the new portion.
- **Issue #2 (cosmetic).** `caption_finalized` log line was truncating text at 80 chars (`text[:80]`), which made the log look out-of-sync with the JSONL. **Fix:** removed the slice. Pure cosmetic, no behavior change.

Added `tests/test_transcript_dedupe.py` — 7 cases (exact-prefix, case+punct drift, no-prefix passthrough, identical-text returns empty, empty-prior passthrough, end-to-end same-speaker dedupe via TranscriptFinalizer, per-speaker isolation). Full regression suite (11 test files) green.

**Design decisions made this session worth remembering:**
- **Look at voice-preserved before reinventing.** The voice branch's `pipeline/captions.py` already had a battle-tested fuzzy text-comparison helper for exactly the same Meet-rewrites-its-own-text problem (echo-suspect detection). Strict `startswith` failed live within minutes; the normalized token-prefix approach worked first try. When chat-mode caption code hits an edge case, voice mode probably hit it first.
- **Wire the LLM to the record at the construction site, not in ChatRunner.** ChatRunner's "if I created the record then I'll wire the LLM" pattern was a partial fix — it only covered the no-captions path. The real invariant is "whoever creates the record must tell the LLM about it." Adding the wiring directly under `meeting_record = MeetingRecord(...)` in `__main__.py` makes that invariant local and obvious. ChatRunner's branch can stay (it covers the case where ChatRunner is invoked without a pre-created record), but the captions path now has its own explicit wire.
- **Walking tests one at a time with the user is high-leverage.** The user typing "done" between tests + me grepping the log + reporting pass/fail/findings caught all three bugs in one ~30-minute session. T6 in particular only failed because we tested in order — by T7 we had a retroactive cross-check that proved the LLM behavior was correct and only the wiring was broken.

**Known limitations remaining:**
- **Calendar-mode captions still need `ChatRunner.run_polling()`.** `__main__.py:304` references `runner.run_polling(meeting_queue)` and `runner._in_meeting`, but neither exists on the chat-only `ChatRunner` — voice-era leftovers from before the decoupling. The late-bind fix (session 100) unblocked the *bridge* layer but the runner needs to be restored or replaced before captions actually flow through calendar mode. Out of scope for direct-URL caption use.
- **Dedupe doesn't handle Meet's roll-off perfectly.** If Meet rolls the caption pane such that prior is no longer at the start (only its tail overlaps the new text's head), `_strip_prior_prefix` returns text unchanged → some duplicate words emit. Would require a longest-overlap search instead of strict prefix; deferred unless real testing surfaces it.
- **No automated regression test for observer drift if Meet's caption DOM changes.** Same as session 99/100. T1 catches the acute case; a DOM-fixture replay would be better. Parked for Phase 12.

**What just happened (session 100, April 14, 2026):** Implemented the late-bind caption fix. `MacOSAdapter` now exposes `window.__onCaption` and injects the post-admission caption observer whenever `config.CAPTIONS_ENABLED` is true, regardless of whether `set_caption_callback` has been called yet — the Python-side bridge stub (`_on_caption_from_js`) drops captions silently when no callback is registered. `set_caption_callback(fn)` is now safe to call before OR after `join()`, and accepts `None` to unregister. Updated `__main__.py` to drop the misleading "calendar mode skipped" warning — the bridge will now be live, but per-meeting wiring still has to happen when a URL arrives via the calendar queue (and `ChatRunner.run_polling()` is missing from chat-only main; the `__main__.py:304` reference is a voice-era leftover that will need to be restored or replaced before calendar captions actually flow end-to-end). Added `tests/test_caption_late_bind.py` — 7 unit tests covering: drop-with-no-callback, register/receive, late-bind after first caption, swap routes to new sink, `None` unregisters, callback exception swallowed without breaking the bridge, `filter_caption` short-circuit. Full chat-only suite (9 files) still green. Committed as `1915473`.

**Design decisions made this session worth remembering:**
- **Late-bind over restructure.** Moving caption wiring into `ChatRunner.run()` would have dragged the connector lifecycle inward. Instead, expose the bridge once at browser startup and let the Python callback be swapped at any time. Smaller blast radius, parity-preserving for the direct-URL path, and naturally handles the calendar mode "browser up before URL arrives" sequencing.
- **Bridge stub is the gate, not the JS side.** The JS observer keeps firing `window.__onCaption(...)` whenever Meet renders a caption. The Python `_on_caption_from_js` is the cheap drop point when no callback is registered — keeps the JS observer free of gating logic and means swapping callbacks is just a Python attribute write.

**What just happened (session 99, April 14, 2026):** Ported the Google Meet caption pipeline from `voice-preserved` into main, parity-first on the battle-tested pieces. New `connectors/captions_js.py` holds the `CAPTION_OBSERVER_JS` verbatim (scoped MutationObserver on the Captions region, speaker-badge extraction, dedup, RAF batching) plus `enable_captions`, `captions_are_on`, and `filter_caption` helpers (icon-ligature + system-phrase rejection). `MacOSAdapter` gained `set_caption_callback(fn)`, a JS→Python bridge (`_on_caption_from_js`), `page.expose_function("__onCaption", …)` registered pre-navigation, and a post-join step that calls `enable_captions(page)` + injects the observer — all guarded on "callback was set," so chat-only runs don't pay for any of it. New `pipeline/transcript.py` owns finalization: `TranscriptFinalizer` buffers the latest (speaker, text, timestamp) and flushes on speaker-change OR silence-gap ≥ `CAPTION_SILENCE_SECONDS` (default 0.7s, configurable), appending finalized utterances to `MeetingRecord` as `kind: caption`. Only finalized text hits disk — no caption deltas. `config.yaml` gained a `transcript:` block with `captions_enabled: false` (privacy opt-in by default — captions pull in every participant's speech, bigger consent surface than chat-only). `config.py` exposes `CAPTIONS_ENABLED` + `CAPTION_SILENCE_SECONDS`. `__main__.py` (direct-URL macOS path) creates the `MeetingRecord` + `TranscriptFinalizer` *before* `connector.join()` so the callback is registered before `page.goto()`; the same record is threaded into `ChatRunner` via `meeting_record=` kwarg. `LLMClient._tail_messages` now includes `kind: caption` entries as `[spoken] <FirstName>: <text>` user-role messages, so tail naturally interleaves chat + captions by timestamp. System prompt updated with a one-line explanation that `[spoken]` lines are ambient context, not prompts to respond. Unit-tested the finalizer (speaker-change + silence-gap both flush; in-flight flushed on stop) and the interleaving (chat + caption rows in timestamp order with correct `kind` tags). All existing regression tests green (chat_hardening, 911_size_management, guardrails, mcp_client, anthropic_provider). Live test plan written at `docs/11_3_b_testing.md` — 9 essential-only tests from observer-attach through shutdown-flush.

**Design decisions made this session worth remembering:**
- **Port the observer JS verbatim; ignore the voice-loop 600-line tail.** Parity-first feedback is about preserving battle-tested code. The value in `voice-preserved/captions_adapter.py` is the `CAPTION_OBSERVER_JS` constant (lines 52-240) — scoped region selector, speaker badge logic, icon/system filtering, RAF batching. The rest was voice-coupling (wake detection, TTS echo guards, abort events, blocking `capture_next_wake_utterance()`) and a whole duplicate `MeetingConnector` subclass. Skipping that was correct; porting it would have been dead weight.
- **Unified single-stream transcript, tagged by `kind`.** Considered chat vs captions as separate streams and rejected: through the user lens ("what did Sarah just say about the deadline?", "summarize what we agreed"), the timeline reads naturally when speech and typed chat interleave in order. The LLM can distinguish via the `kind` tag + `[spoken]` prefix. Separate streams would be implementation hygiene at the cost of user-facing coherence.
- **Finalized utterances only on disk.** Deltas (streaming caption updates ~3/sec) stay in memory in the finalizer buffer; only the finalized utterance hits the JSONL. Keeps disk noise down, keeps `tail(n)` readable, matches the "one line per message" shape chat already uses.
- **Captions default off.** Chat is opt-in by nature (people type intending to address the bot). Captions ingest every participant's speech for the whole meeting. That's a meaningfully different consent surface, so the flag defaults `false`.
- **Wire captions in `__main__`, not `ChatRunner`.** `expose_function` must precede `page.goto()`. ChatRunner currently creates the `MeetingRecord` inside `run()`, which runs *after* `connector.join()`. Easier to create the record + finalizer in `__main__` (direct-URL path) and thread the record into `ChatRunner` via the existing `meeting_record=` kwarg than to refactor the lifecycle. Calendar-mode captions will need a separate pass (URL not known at startup).

**Known limitations to revisit post-live-test:**
- Calendar-polling mode skips captions (logged as a warning). When captions are enabled + no URL given at startup, `TranscriptFinalizer` creation is deferred — and never happens — because the URL arrives via the meeting queue inside `ChatRunner.run_polling`. Fix is straightforward: move the caption wiring down into `ChatRunner.run()` where the URL is known, but that means making `set_caption_callback` tolerant of being called post-`page.expose_function` registration (likely requires either re-exposing or always exposing when the connector supports captions). Not blocking MVP if the user's primary demo path is direct-URL.
- No automated regression test for observer drift if Meet's caption DOM changes. Live test T1 catches the acute case (observer didn't attach → no caption log lines → no JSONL entries). A stronger guard would be a DOM fixture saved from a real Meet caption region and replayed against the observer JS in a headless browser — worth adding in Phase 12 regression tooling if captions prove important to users.
- The in-flight drift on macOS DOM polling flagged in session 98 (bare `ok` confirmations occasionally dropped) may or may not intersect with caption-element observers. T1/T2 are the first signal check — if captions arrive cleanly through speech bursts, the polling-drop is isolated.

**What happened before that (session 97, April 14, 2026):** Positioning session. No code shipped (one new folder + README scaffolding). Competitive research surfaced [joinly](https://github.com/joinly-ai/joinly) as a near-peer: multi-platform (Meet/Zoom/Teams), BYOLLM (OpenAI/Anthropic/Ollama), MCP-shaped, voice + chat, MIT licensed, hosted cloud option, shipped 6+ months ago. Joinly's framing is platform/middleware-shaped ("expose meetings to agents") — their Reddit posts got meager response, plausibly because the pitch is abstract and they shipped the full surface at once.

Response: pick two implicit differentiators rather than feature-match. (1) **"Claude Code in your Google Meet"** as the launch hero framing — Phase 11.5 (skill import) is already on the roadmap and gives Operator a concrete, filmable hook that joinly can't easily copy without adopting Anthropic's skill format. Skills are provider-neutral (markdown + YAML frontmatter), so the framing works with OpenAI too; the "Claude Code" name is the marketing wrapper, not a fork. (2) **Opinionated quickstart** — "choose your fighter → add power-ups → go," delivered via an `agents/` gallery (ready-to-run folders committed to main, contributed via PRs) + a minimal `operator setup` wizard + README reading as Steps 1/2/3. Forks were considered as the community-proof primitive and explicitly rejected: galleries unify, forks fragment (Ollama library, LangChain templates, n8n templates, ComfyUI workflows, Vercel templates as reference patterns).

- **New folder: `agents/README.md`** — defines the gallery format (one folder per agent, each self-contained with `config.yaml` + optional `skills/` + `README.md` + `.env.example`), contribution rules (one job per agent; must run on a fresh clone; demo GIF of the artifact; no secrets), and usage instructions. `claude-code` listed as the canonical entry; slot left for a second chat-native agent (user will pick near launch from: standup / triage / incident-commander / interview-notes / research).
- **`docs/mvp-bar.md` updated** — positioning line adds the "AI power user's meeting bot / Claude Code skills natively / any markdown skill file with any model" framing. Three-part differentiation rewritten: #1 "Action, not access" now names joinly's category explicitly; #2 leads with Claude Code skill import as the sharpest implicit differentiator; #3 renamed to "Opinionated quickstart, not a framework" with the agents gallery + wizard as the delivery mechanism. Added a "3-step setup is obvious in under 30 seconds" entry to What Must Work. Added explicit non-goals for voice parity and Zoom/Teams parity with joinly — don't feature-match, fight on positioning. Added a full **Launch Strategy** section: hero framings by channel (Claude Code angle for r/ClaudeAI; standup bot for r/ExperiencedDevs; role-specific for niches), visual hooks (artifact-appearing-mid-sentence is the Pika-equivalent surprise moment; drag-drop-skills-folder as secondary), distribution levers ranked (direct SF outreach > newsletter/influencer mentions à la Pika > seeded `agents/` PRs > specific-JTBD Reddit posts; never generic "open source X" posts), and `agents/` as distribution primitive.
- **`docs/roadmap.md` updated** — new Phase 15.5 (Opinionated Quickstart) inserted between 15 and 16 with three steps: 15.5.1 `claude-code` starter agent (~1.5h), 15.5.2 minimal `operator setup` wizard (~2h), 15.5.3 second chat-native agent (~1h). Phase 16.1 README now explicitly requires 3-step structure and agents-gallery entry point. Phase 16.2 demo spec now calls out the mid-sentence-artifact visual hook. New Phase 16.3 Launch campaign prep (~3h) — draft three hero-framing posts, seeded PR plan, direct-outreach shortlist, newsletter mention targets. Post-MVP "Setup wizard" entry rephrased to clarify the minimal version ships in 15.5; full wizard (voice, MCP OAuth, polished UX) is post-MVP. New post-MVP "Agents gallery expansion" entry for ongoing recipe curation. MVP hour total bumped from ~40h to ~53.5h — right at the ceiling; 15.5.3 and 16.3 can slip post-launch if needed.

**Design decisions made this session worth remembering:**
- **Gallery pattern over forks.** Forks fragment git history and don't make the parent repo look alive. A `roster/` folder with PR contributions keeps everyone on main, makes contributors visible in the commit log, and turns every seeded-persona build into a permanent artifact pinned in the repo. This is the primitive; forks are not.
- **"Claude Code in your Google Meet" is framing, not product.** The product stays Operator; the campaign is CCiYM. Defaulting the skills path to `~/.claude/skills/` is a convenience for Claude Code users, not a lock-in — any markdown skill file works with any model.
- **CLI (end-user commands) vs. SDK (library for other devs).** Joinly's MCP server is effectively an SDK play. Operator's defensive lane is CLI-for-end-users — `operator setup`, future `operator skill add`, `operator doctor`, `operator check-mcp`. Don't race on SDK breadth.
- **Joinly is ahead on surface, not ready on positioning.** Don't chase voice, Zoom, or Teams pre-launch. Win on specificity and seeded community signal instead.

**What happened before that (session 91, April 13, 2026):** Strategic pause before resuming Phase 11. User raised a concern that Operator's orchestration may be too opinionated for an OSS project. Did a three-step alignment exercise: (1) defined the ethos via structured Q&A, landing on core (non-overridable: agentic LLM loop, zero telemetry, no user data on our infra) vs default (overridable: wake phrase, system prompt, tools/skills/MCP, participation degree, STT/TTS/LLM, conversation store, response style, logging dest) vs shape commitments (provider-neutral internal shapes; swappable seams for LLM/tool-protocol/conversation-store/chat-surface; headless core + chat API + reference CLI client target; skill manifest + install consent + sensitive-tier confirmation; layered YAML→env→CLI→per-skill config). (3) Ran the audit read-only; findings in `docs/oss-audit-report.md`. Five criticals: **(a)** chat mode hard-requires a Google Meet URL (`__main__.py:346-350`); **(b)** `OPENAI_API_KEY` is a required import-time env var even when `provider: anthropic` (`config.py:96`), breaking BYOK; **(c)** `READ_TOOLS` is a hardcoded Linear+GitHub allowlist in `chat_runner.py:19-38` — permissioning is a closed Python set; **(d)** no skill manifest / install consent / sensitivity tiers anywhere; **(e)** no headless-core/chat-API/reference-client separation (the named target). Nine majors include OpenAI-shaped tool schemas still leaking into the provider boundary (`_openai_tools_to_anthropic` translates the wrong direction), `MCPTool` as the de-facto neutral tool type (ethos explicitly flagged this), no `ConversationStore` seam, Linear/GitHub quirks leaking into neutral code, framework-injected prompt fragments not user-owned, and hardcoded `/tmp/operator.log`. Six minors in polish territory. Zero-telemetry commitment confirmed intact. Committed as `docs: session 91 — OSS ethos alignment + layer-by-layer audit` (b7fdecb). User will decide which findings to tackle and in what order before resuming 11.3/11.4.

**What happened before that (session 90, April 12, 2026):** Shipped step 11.2 — Anthropic API backend. Went with a provider-neutral conversation shape (Option A) after user rejected a translator-shim approach that would have made Anthropic responses mimic OpenAI's object model ("I don't want our code to be more conducive/oriented toward one provider over another"). Partly redid session 89's work: replaced OpenAI-shaped response objects returned by `OpenAIProvider.complete()` with neutral `ProviderResponse(text, tool_calls: list[ToolCall], stop_reason)` dataclasses in `pipeline/providers/base.py`. History format is now neutral too: `{role: "user"|"assistant"|"tool_result", ...}` with `tool_calls: [ToolCall]` on assistant turns. `OpenAIProvider` and `AnthropicProvider` each translate neutral↔native at the boundary. `AnthropicProvider` (new file) wraps `anthropic.Anthropic`, translates tool schemas (OpenAI's `{function: {parameters}}` → Anthropic's `{name, input_schema}`), stop_reasons (`end_turn`/`stop_sequence`→`end`, `tool_use`→`tool_use`, `max_tokens`→`length`), assistant turns with tool_use blocks, and tool_result as user-role content blocks. Maps "prompt is too long" → `ContextOverflowError`. `build_provider()` factory in `pipeline/providers/__init__.py` reads `config.LLM_PROVIDER` and returns the right provider; raises if `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` is missing. All 4 call sites (`__main__.py` ×2, `pipeline/runner.py`, `cloud/docker/entrypoint.py`) now use `LLMClient(build_provider())`. Three surgical follow-ups after live testing exposed issues: (1) **parallel tool_use disabled** via `tool_choice={"type":"auto","disable_parallel_tool_use":True}` — Claude Sonnet 4.5 emits multiple tool_use blocks by default and our pipeline feeds one tool_result at a time; mirrors OpenAI's `parallel_tool_calls=False`. Logged as post-MVP item in roadmap. (2) **Prompt caching** on system + all tool schemas via `cache_control: {"type": "ephemeral"}` — unblocked 30k ITPM rate limit that killed follow-up turns when 72 tool schemas were resent every call. (3) **429 diagnostic** — `anthropic.RateLimitError` now logs a clear message with the ITPM cap, reset time, and tier-upgrade path. Also: `chat_system_prompt` in config.yaml now says "Render links as bare URLs, not markdown" (Claude was emitting giant `[label](url)` that flooded the chat panel). `anthropic` logger silenced to WARNING in both `__main__.py` and docker entrypoint (SDK dumps full request JSON at DEBUG — 20k+ tokens of tool schema per call). Unit tests: 11/11 pass in `tests/test_anthropic_provider.py` (new), plus existing test_911/test_913/test_guardrails updated to use neutral shape. Live-validated end-to-end in a chat-mode Meet with `provider: anthropic`, `model: claude-sonnet-4-5` across 4 user turns including a 4-tool fan-out ("can you check?" → 2× list_pull_requests + 2× list_commits across 2 repos) — no 429, concise replies, clean stdout. User will commit session 90's work.

**What happened before that (session 89, April 12, 2026):** Shipped step 11.1 — abstract LLM provider interface. Pure behavior-identical refactor: extracted the OpenAI API transport out of `LLMClient` into a new `pipeline/providers/` package. `pipeline/providers/base.py` defines `LLMProvider` (abstract `complete`/`complete_stream`/`warmup`) and `ContextOverflowError` (provider-agnostic signal replacing OpenAI's `BadRequestError(code=context_length_exceeded)`). `pipeline/providers/openai.py` has `OpenAIProvider` wrapping `openai.OpenAI`; it translates the context-overflow `BadRequestError` into `ContextOverflowError` at the boundary. `LLMClient.__init__` now takes a provider instead of a raw openai client; all history/trim/collapse/system-prompt/MCP-injection logic stays put. Response shape unchanged — provider returns the OpenAI-shaped message object (with `.content`, `.tool_calls`, `.to_dict()`), so `LLMClient`'s parsing of tool_call vs. text reply is untouched. **What happened before that (session 88, April 12, 2026):** Shipped step 10.6 — runtime failure backoff for MCP tool calls. `MCPClient` gained `_consecutive_errors: dict[str, int]`, `disabled_servers: dict[str, str]`, `record_tool_result(server, success) -> tripped_bool` (hardcoded `RUNTIME_FAILURE_THRESHOLD = 3`), and `server_for_tool(tool_name)` helper. `execute_tool` short-circuits any call whose server is in `disabled_servers` with the steering string: *"Server 'X' has been disabled for this session after repeated failures. This tool is unavailable. Do not retry; tell the user."* — the wording matters because that MCPToolError text becomes the tool-result the LLM sees back. `get_openai_tools` filters out tools whose server is disabled so the LLM stops attempting them. `LLMClient.inject_mcp_status` now takes a third `disabled_runtime` bucket and is idempotent: it tracks the last-injected text and replaces it on re-call, so a mid-session re-inject doesn't stack. Recording is centralized in `chat_runner._record_mcp_outcome(tool_name, success)` — called from the success path, the MCPToolError path, AND the timeout path (timeouts are enforced in chat_runner and never return through `execute_tool`, so they must be recorded here). On trip, chat_runner sends one announcement (*"The X server seems to be having issues — skipping it for the rest of this session."*) and re-injects MCP status with the merged `failed_to_load | disabled_runtime` state. Unit-tested in `tests/test_mcp_client.py` (new Test 6 covers below-threshold, reset-on-success, trip at N, no-re-trip, tool filtering, and short-circuit steering text). Live-validated in a chat-mode Meet using `debug/flaky_mcp_server.py` (exposes a single always-failing `check_weather` tool): three weather questions produced `failure 1/3 → 2/3 → disabled`, single chat announcement fired, `tools=73 → 72`, fourth weather question produced the steering reply without a tool call, Linear/GitHub unaffected. Committed as `feat: step 10.6 — runtime failure backoff for MCP tool calls` (2b3343a). Session 86's voice-path alone-exit was confirmed live-working by user.

Non-blocking — failures warn but don't abort. Shipped step 10.3 — user-defined MCP server scaffolding, with live end-to-end validation. Also closed two stale open concerns (session-82 correction re-propose flow confirmed validated during 10.2 live test; Linear-vs-GitHub routing bias addressed by a new chat system-prompt line clarifying "repo" = GitHub). Wired in both `__main__.py` chat paths alongside existing `inject_mcp_hints` / `inject_github_user`; (4) `python __main__.py --check-mcp` loads config, starts every configured server, prints `✓ name (N tools)` / `✗ name <reason>`, exits 0 if all loaded else 1. Validation: patched `config.yaml` with a `weather` server pointing at a nonexistent binary, joined a live Meet in chat mode — LLM declined generic "what's the weather" gracefully, answered "which servers failed to load?" with "The weather server failed to load. Please check /tmp/operator.log for details.", and Linear tool calls worked normally. `config.yaml` reverted after test. Committed as `feat: step 10.3 — user-defined MCP server scaffolding`.

**What happened before that (session 86, April 12, 2026):** Tangent session — meeting-exit logic. User asked what conditions cause Operator to self-terminate and identified a missing MVP case: if Operator has seen other participants and they all leave, Operator should drop. Audit confirmed only one auto-leave heuristic existed (past end-time + user display name absent, in CaptionsAdapter); chat path had no self-termination at all. Implemented alone-exit auto-leave: (1) new `agent.alone_exit_grace_seconds` config (60s default); (2) ChatRunner tracks `saw_others` + `alone_since` in its polling loop — after count>1 observed, drop to count==1 starts grace timer; on timeout, logs, prints user-facing message, calls `connector.leave()`, returns; (3) CaptionsAdapter gets parity logic alongside the existing end-time check, sharing the 30s `last_presence_check` throttle, pulled out of the end-time conditional so both can run independently. Pre-join/waiting-room false positives ruled out three ways: both loops only run post-admission, `[data-requested-participant-id]` is a meeting-only DOM, and the `saw_others` latch can't flip until count>1. Tested live in chat mode: saw 0→2 flip, 2→1 start timer, 60s later clean auto-leave with Leave-call click + browser close + MCP shutdown. Voice path untested per user direction. Committed as `feat: auto-leave when Operator is alone after others were present (session 86)`.

**What happened before that (session 81, April 12, 2026):**

Session 81: Reliability fix outside the phase plan — camera-toggle failure on macOS pre-join. User reported camera stayed ON in a live session; logs showed the existing "could not confirm off state" warning fired, but code only logged and proceeded. Diagnosis: the click at `macos_adapter.py:528` returned success (5s `wait_for` passed), but the 3s post-click `data-is-muted="true"` wait timed out. Debug HTML confirmed the button existed with `data-is-muted="false"` — click didn't toggle state. Two root-cause candidates indistinguishable from existing logs: hydration race (button in DOM but listener not wired) vs. overlay intercept. Restructured the pre-join flow: (1) removed camera selectors from the step-2 DOM-ready wait (they race with join buttons at different times); (2) added a dedicated camera step after state gates that waits for the button with `data-is-muted` attribute present (hydration signal); (3) added `_probe_camera_button()` diagnostic logged pre-click and on failure — captures `hydrated`, `data_is_muted`, rect, `elementFromPoint` result, `intercepted` flag; (4) on confirmation failure, falls back to `⌘+E` keyboard shortcut (bypasses both overlay and hydration by going through Meet's global hotkey handler); (5) if both fail, sets `self._camera_on_at_join = True` for downstream visibility. `macos_adapter.py` only — Linux/Docker/Captions adapters untouched per surgical-change preference. Not validated live yet.

**Also this session (session 82, April 12, 2026):** Live pressure-tested BYOMCP guard rails and confirmation handler. Guard rails validated: `.mp3` pre-execution block fired correctly. Three LLM behavior issues surfaced: (1) LLM adds `state='unstarted'` to `list_issues` despite "all open" — root cause was our hint listing state types without marking them optional, and the Linear MCP schema offering the field with no default guidance. Fixed: made hint conditional ("When the user specifies a state...") and added "omitting it returns all states." Multi-state filtering (e.g. "incomplete" = unstarted + started) is an MCP limitation — single `state` param only. (2) LLM guessed `repo='our'` literally instead of asking which repo. Fixed: added system prompt directive "ask the user to clarify rather than guessing" for ambiguous required params. (3) Confirmation rejection said "OK, cancelled" and dropped the interaction — LLM never re-proposed. Fixed: correction handler now passes `tools=` to `send_tool_result` (so LLM can re-issue tool calls) and dispatches the response (text → chat, tool_call → re-confirmation). Also discovered the correction response was being swallowed by `_collapse_tool_exchange` — the LLM generated a clarifying question but it was never sent to chat because the return value was discarded. (4) "read logo.png from the repo" routed to `linear__list_projects` — conversation context bias from prior Linear-heavy usage primed the model away from GitHub tools. No code fix; system prompt clarify-don't-guess directive may help.

**Audit walk-through complete (session 92, April 13, 2026):** All 10 layers of `docs/oss-audit-report.md` parsed collaboratively with user and actioned in `roadmap.md`. Every layer was stripped from the report and replaced with a pointer note explaining where its findings landed. Key outcomes:

- **Promoted pre-MVP to Phase 11:** 11.6 conversation history persistence (L6-a, ~1.5h — JSONL on disk, not the full `ConversationStore` protocol); 11.7 provider API keys optional at import (L1-c, ~15m — real BYOK-Anthropic crash fix).
- **Fast-follow bucket (pre-MVP if time permits, ~10h 45m total):** configurable log destination + level + redaction (absorbs L1-b + L9-b + L10-b); `ChatSource` seam + stdin source (absorbs L1-a + L2 + L3-c, bumped to ~6h to include pushing Meet-specific concerns into `MeetAdapter` and promoting `leave_when_alone` to a config toggle); per-server quirk config (L3-b + L9-a partial — `strip_args`, `identity_tool`, overridable `prompts.identity_guidance`); open provider registry (L4-b — dict + `register_provider`); framework-owned strings as config templates (L3-d + L9-a partial — absorbs `inject_mcp_status` as a global `prompts.mcp_server_unavailable` template).
- **Post-MVP firm:** Skill manifest + neutral `ToolSchema` + install consent (~10-14h, bundles L3-a + L4-a + L5-a + L5-b).
- **Dropped entirely:** L6-b (retention-policy abstraction — current dial + auto-collapse already matches intended design); L7 (daemon/API split — reviewed against hosted-bot vision, containerizing the monolith is the right path, daemon/API is YAGNI); L8-a (CLI flag overrides — field norm for config-heavy long-lived tools like kubectl/terraform/docker-compose is YAML-first).
- **New Post-MVP phase added: Hosted Operator** (~30-35h) — containerize the monolith, per-meeting ephemeral containers, invite-receiver (email or Calendar webhook), orchestrator, hosted Google auth, multi-tenant config isolation, observability. North star vision: Shopify-style inviteable bot.
- **Compliance affirmed:** L10-a — repo-wide grep verified zero outbound network activity beyond configured LLM provider, configured TTS, and opted-in MCP servers. Zero-telemetry commitment holds.

**Framing reframes that happened during the walk-through (worth remembering):** (a) The product IS a meeting bot — needing a meeting URL isn't a violation; the violation was `ChatRunner` being welded to the Meet connector. (b) The ethos doc's "layered YAML → env → CLI → per-skill" was one-size-fits-all; meeting bots aren't CLI tools, and YAML-first with no CLI flags is the correct shape for config-heavy long-lived agents. (c) Daemon/API/client separation is for tools where state outlives client sessions or multiple clients hit one instance simultaneously — neither applies to Operator. (d) The skill-manifest/install-consent commitment is a mature-product concern, not a day-0 demo concern, and deferring it is honest.

Remaining pre-MVP steps in order: **11.3** (meeting transcript as context, ~2h), **11.4** (skill file loading, ~2h), **11.5** (import Claude Code skills, ~2h), **11.6** (conversation history persistence, ~1.5h), **11.7** (provider keys optional at import, ~15m). Phase 11 total: ~13.75h. After 11, Phase 12 (validation, ~3h), Phase 13 (polish), Phase 14 (docs), Phase 15 (setup), Phase 16 (demo). Ship target remains April 19, 2026 (Sunday). Fast-follow audit-fix items are opportunistic grabs if time opens up — 30m + 45m quick wins first if you get an idle hour, `ChatSource` seam (~6h) only if clearly ahead of schedule.

Phase 17 is post-MVP — do not start before April 19.

**Setup wizard deferred (session 75):** Setup wizard (original Phase 15) is post-MVP. README must document MCP OAuth setup manually — `mcp-remote` caches tokens locally after initial browser-based auth, so it's a one-time step. Without guidance, the first meeting launch would trigger an OAuth popup mid-join.

**Top open issue (voice, deferred):** Premature finalization at 0.7s silence threshold cuts off mid-sentence prompts. See `docs/latency.md` for pipeline measurements and six reduction ideas. Will be addressed in Phase 11 (voice steps 11.5–11.8).

**Architecture note (session 47):** CaptionsAdapter and MacOSAdapter have duplicated browser session logic (~150 lines each). User considered refactoring into a shared base but decided against it — chat is shipping first, so keeping them separate avoids unnecessary abstraction. Revisit when both paths need parallel maintenance.

**Architecture note (session 51):** MCP integration uses a dedicated asyncio event loop thread to bridge the async MCP SDK into our sync codebase. Each MCP server runs as a long-lived `_ServerHandle` async task — required because `stdio_client` uses anyio task groups that must stay in one task. Tool names are namespaced as `server__tool` (e.g., `linear__create_issue`) to avoid collisions across servers. Confirmation flow: LLM returns tool_call → Operator asks user in chat → user confirms → tool executes → result fed back to LLM → summary sent. `LLMClient.ask(tools=None)` returns a plain string (voice path unchanged); `ask(tools=[...])` returns a structured dict.

**Architecture note (session 54):** Chat message detection now uses a two-layer approach: MutationObserver in the browser for instant detection, with 0.5s Python polling as a fallback drain cadence. The observer seeds `__brainchildSeenIds` with existing messages on install to avoid replaying history. Participant count uses `[data-requested-participant-id]` which reliably tracks actual in-call participants (not invited-but-absent). The count is 2× `rosterCount` due to UI duplicate elements, so we use `requestedParticipants` instead.

---

## Hard-Won Knowledge (read before touching relevant code)

- **Slip's CDP-reuse path needs liveness, not just identity — a Chrome with zero contexts is a zombie that fails `connect_over_cdp`** (session 205). User's `operator slip claude <url>` failed with terminal `Slip couldn't attach to its Chrome window`; log showed the smoking gun: `AttachAdapter: CDP at http://localhost:9222 is slip Chrome — reusing` immediately followed by `connect_over_cdp failed: Protocol error (Browser.setDownloadBehavior): Browser context management is not supported`. Sequence: previous slip session detached cleanly (slip leaves Chrome running by design so the user can keep the meeting going), user later closed the last slip window, and on macOS that does NOT quit Chrome — the process stays alive in the menu bar with **zero browser contexts**. CDP socket still listens on 9222; `_cdp_endpoint_alive()` says yes; `_cdp_belongs_to_slip()` says yes (the `--user-data-dir=$HOME/.operator/slip_profile` flag is still in argv); reuse path takes it; Playwright's `connect_over_cdp` calls `Browser.setDownloadBehavior` to set up downloads, gets back "Browser context management is not supported" because there's nothing to manage. Misleading error message — `--retry on the next run` would deterministically hit the same dead Chrome and fail identically. Fix in `attach_adapter.py`: track whether the reuse path was taken with a local `took_reuse_path` bool; if `connect_over_cdp` raises and the reuse path was taken, evict the zombie Chrome via the existing `_evict_other_chrome_on_cdp_port()`, settle 0.5s, relaunch via `_launch_slip_chrome`, and retry connect once. On the freshly-launched path, never retry — a connect failure there is a real problem (port held by something un-killable, OS issue) that should surface, not be papered over. **Generalizable**: when reusing a long-lived process via a remote-control protocol, identity verification (the right process) is necessary but not sufficient — you also need liveness verification (the protocol surface is in a usable state). For CDP/Playwright specifically, `connect_over_cdp` itself is the cheapest liveness probe; let it fail and recover, rather than adding a separate pre-flight that's bound to drift from Playwright's actual expectations. The `_cdp_belongs_to_slip()` function name is now slightly misleading (it confirms identity, not viability) — kept as-is because renaming would churn callers without changing behavior. Same shape applies to **C1 in the endurance audit catalog**: the `is_connected()` flag on `macos_adapter` only reflects an internal bool, not real page health — long meetings post-sleep/blip will need the same try-and-recover pattern keyed on actual Playwright errors.

- **Lex sort on version-suffixed directory names breaks at digit boundaries** (session 203). `oauth_cache.mcp_remote_cache_dir()` was using `sorted(d for d in base.glob("mcp-remote-*") if d.is_dir())[-1]` to pick the "latest" cache dir, with a docstring claiming the result was the latest version a user had installed. Real failure shape: as strings, `mcp-remote-0.1.10 < mcp-remote-0.1.9` (digit-by-digit compare; `1 < 9` at position 13). A user with both an older `0.1.4`-era cache and the current `mcp-remote@0.1.38` cache installed would have `0.1.4` selected by `[-1]`. Downstream blast radius: `oauth_cache_exists` reports True off the stale dir's tokens.json, the active mcp-remote (0.1.38) reads from its own dir, finds nothing, hangs at OAuth popup at meeting join. The fix is mtime-based pick (`max(candidates, key=lambda d: d.stat().st_mtime)`) — the currently-installed mcp-remote writes to its own dir at runtime, so its mtime is freshest. Robust to any version naming (semver, prerelease tags, dotted N-part). **Generalizable**: any code that compares user-facing semantic versions as strings is wrong unless every version field is zero-padded to a fixed width — which third-party tools never are. When the intent is "latest installed" or "currently active," prefer mtime over either lex sort or hand-rolled tuple-of-int parsing. The latter is also fragile to non-numeric suffixes (`-rc1`, `+build.5`).

- **Phantom-feature scaffolding outlives its trigger and leaves hidden tests that pass vacuously** (session 203). The Tier 3 audit kept finding the same shape: `install_preflight.run_install_preflight()`, `readiness.preflight_mcp_readiness()`, `readiness.report_mcp_readiness()`, `claude_code_import.read_user_mcp_config()`, the `agents/{claude,codex}/` empty preset directories, the now-deleted `google_signin.run_signin_step()` — all wizard/preflight/preset machinery that didn't get wired into the post-pivot runtime, with **substantial** test coverage of the unreachable code path. `tests/test_bundled_mcps_bootable_static.py` (242 LOC) globbed `agents/*/config.yaml` (zero hits) and asserted against an empty list — three test functions passed vacuously, looking like real coverage. `tests/test_15745_preflight.py` exercises `preflight_mcp_readiness` extensively but the function has no src/ caller. **Lesson**: when grepping for callers of a function turns up only test files, two questions follow: (1) is there a runtime entry point that *should* exist (per docstring or spec) but is missing? (2) does the test actually exercise meaningful inputs, or does it pass vacuously against an empty/never-matched fixture? `glob` patterns and `if X: ...` filters that always evaluate empty are the smoking gun. The S203 sweep uncovered five such orphans in one tier; mass-deletion phases leave them behind systematically (and S202's "passive-consumers" entry above is the sister pattern from defensive code).

- **`os.pipe()` partial-failure leaks fds — the second pipe call must defend the first** (session 203). `_disclaimed_spawn.py:spawn_disclaimed` had two consecutive `os.pipe()` calls before any try/finally. If the second call hit the per-process fd limit and raised `OSError`, the first pipe's fds were never closed — leaks two fds per failure. Real failure rate is low (only fires near the fd ceiling) but the bug is real: the existing `finally` block referenced `stdout_w` and `stdout_r`, which would NameError if the second pipe never created them. Fix: wrap the second `os.pipe()` in a try/except that closes the first pipe on failure and re-raises. **Generalizable**: any sequence of resource allocations before a try/finally needs partial-failure cleanup between them, OR all the allocations need to move *into* the try block with the finally block defended against `NameError` via flag tracking. The cleanest pattern is to allocate one resource then immediately enter a `try`/`finally` for it; nest the next allocation inside that try. The S203 fix used the lighter "wrap second-call only" pattern since the rest of the function already had its own try/finally.

- **Mass-deletion phases leave behind passive consumers that look like live code** (session 202). Auditing Tier 2 cells turned up the same pattern over and over: Phase 14.19.7 deleted big chunks of infrastructure (the wizard, OpenAI/Anthropic providers, OPERATOR_BOT routing, `mcp_client.py`, codex agent, per-bot YAMLs) — and *every* deletion left a trail of passive consumers that were always-defensive code: `getattr(config, "DISABLED_MCP_SERVERS", None) or {}` in `permission_chat_handler.py` always resolved to `{}` and the guard never fired; `logging.getLogger("openai").setLevel(WARNING)` in `__main__.py` × 3 sites had no logger to silence; `_format_confirmation` and friends in `permission_chat_handler.py` had `voice = getattr(config, "VOICE", "plain")` reading a deleted config field, so the code path was unreachable; `_disabled_mcp_for_cli_tool` walked a server-naming map that was always empty. None showed up in tests because their job was always to defend against absence, and absence was now permanent. **Lesson**: after any large-scope deletion phase, the next audit pass should hunt for `getattr(config, "X", default)` patterns + `try: ... except DeletedException` patterns + `if some_condition_that_used_to_be_true` patterns — they're the orphan footprint of the deletion. A grep for the *deleted* names against the surviving code surface is faster than auditing surviving callers one-by-one. The S202 cells purged ~−380 LOC of this footprint across 6 commits in one session; there's almost certainly more in Tier 3.

- **PID-reuse races on macOS make stale `.pid` files dangerous to act on** (session 201). When auditing `connectors/session.py:_chrome_kill_and_clear`, realized the `--force` path reads a saved PID from `.operator.pid`, then SIGTERMs that PID directly. Fine when the PID is current — but if a previous operator run crashed without cleaning up, the PID file sticks around. macOS recycles PIDs aggressively (default range cycles in ~99,999), so by the time a user runs `--force` later that day, the PID may now belong to a totally unrelated process: their browser, IDE, terminal session. Operator would silently SIGTERM/SIGKILL it. The fix that landed in commit `d992052`: shell out to `ps -p PID -o comm=` before signalling, and skip the kill if the comm string doesn't contain "python" or "operator". macOS-specific because Linux operator is headless / no persistent profile so the path doesn't fire there. Generalizable rule for any code path that signals a PID read from a stored file: **never trust a stored PID unconditionally — verify it still refers to your own process before signalling.** `ps -p PID -o comm=` is the cheapest available check; `psutil.Process(pid).create_time()` matched against the recorded start time is the more robust one when you have psutil. Live-fetched PIDs from `lsof -t -iTCP:<port>` are safer than stored ones (the live source is fresh by definition), which is why `_evict_other_chrome_on_cdp_port` in `attach_adapter.py` doesn't need this guard.

- **`shutil.rmtree(..., ignore_errors=True)` is documented to never raise — don't wrap it in try/except** (session 201). Found two `try: shutil.rmtree(..., ignore_errors=True) except Exception: pass` blocks in `claude_cli._teardown_permission_bridge` during the audit. The kwarg's contract per the stdlib docs: `If ignore_errors is true, errors resulting from failed removals will be ignored`. Outer try/except is double-defense that does nothing — the rmtree call cannot escape the function with an exception. Generalizable: when reviewing defensive code, check whether the inner call can actually raise the exception you're catching. Stdlib calls with `ignore_errors=`/`errors=`/`onerror=` arguments often handle their own failure surface internally; wrapping them in try/except is dead code that obscures the real exception sites elsewhere.

- **Early-return guards in cleanup methods can skip cleanup of independent state** (session 201). `claude_cli._teardown_permission_bridge` had an `if self._perm_tempdir is None: return` at the top, intended to make the function idempotent when no bridge was ever created. But the function also cleaned up `self._mcp_only_tempdir` (a separate tempdir created when captions are wired but no permission_handler is set), and that cleanup was AFTER the early return — so a leak occurred whenever a ClaudeCLIProvider had captions but no permission handler. Today's wiring always sets a handler so the path didn't fire in production, but it's a real latent leak. Fix: move the independent-state cleanup BEFORE the early return. Generalizable: when adding new state attributes whose lifecycle differs from existing state, audit any existing cleanup methods to verify the new state's cleanup runs even when the existing-state early-returns trigger. The pattern is "early return for primary state guard, but always clean up auxiliary state first."

- **`ContextOverflowError` is never raised in the live codebase — don't add overflow-handling code without verifying the trigger** (session 199). During the `claude_cli.py` audit cell I traced a phantom failure mode for an hour before realizing the exception that was supposed to fire it doesn't have a single `raise` site anywhere in the codebase. `ContextOverflowError` is defined in `pipeline/providers/base.py`, was caught in `llm.py:ask`, and was triggering a `_max_messages` halving ratchet — all completely unreachable, because the only provider we have (`claude_cli`) doesn't raise it. Inner-claude (the subprocess) manages its own context internally via Claude Code's auto-compaction, so overflow at our layer can't happen the way it could when we talked to OpenAI/Anthropic SDKs directly. **Lesson:** when reviewing a defensive code path that "handles" something, grep for the actual `raise` site BEFORE designing fixes around the failure mode. Cleanup landed in commit `b0d0d65`. The exception class itself stays in `base.py` for now (other audit cells can decide its fate).

- **`claude_cli.complete()` ignores all but `messages[-1]` — full message-list construction is wasted work** (session 199). Discovered while auditing `llm.py`: every call to `_provider.complete(messages=[...])` builds a list with system prompt + tail history + new user turn, but the claude_cli provider walks straight to `messages[-1]` and writes only that content over the subprocess's stdin (line ~756). Inner-claude maintains its own session state via `--resume` and stream-json envelopes; we don't replay history each call the way you would with a stateless API. **The whole `_tail_messages` + `_build_messages` machinery in `llm.py` is therefore vestigial** in the current architecture — built for direct OpenAI/Anthropic providers, kept after the pivot because the sender-prefix construction on the LAST message has to live somewhere. Filed as a deferred follow-up rather than fixed in S199 because the prefix logic genuinely needs a home; cleanest path is to move it into `chat_runner` (which has the sender at hand from the message read) and drop the rest. **Lesson:** in a wrapped-CLI provider where the wrapped tool maintains its own session state, the LLMProvider interface's `messages=` contract becomes a single-message contract. Don't trust the parameter name's implied semantics — read what the implementation actually consumes.

- **Default `gh auth` token is missing the `delete_repo` scope** (session 182). User asked to delete a repo we'd just created via `gh repo delete 1-800-operator/operator --yes`; got `HTTP 403: Must have admin rights to Repository. (https://api.github.com/repos/...)` — followed by `This API operation needs the "delete_repo" scope. To request it, run: gh auth refresh -h github.com -s delete_repo`. The default scopes from a vanilla `gh auth login` are `gist, read:org, repo, workflow` — `delete_repo` is opt-in. This is a **safety feature**, not a bug: GitHub gates repo deletion behind an explicit scope upgrade so a stolen `repo`-scoped token can't nuke your org. The refresh flow is interactive (one-time-code device flow) and adds the scope to the same token. After the refresh `gh repo delete` works immediately, no logout/login needed. Generalizable: when a `gh` API call returns "needs the X scope" + a refresh hint, **trust the hint** — don't blindly retry, don't re-login, don't open the web UI. The exact `gh auth refresh -h github.com -s <scope>` line is the canonical fix for any scope-elevation moment, including `repo:invite`, `admin:org`, `gist`, etc.

- **Force-pushing orphan branches over public-repo `main` is the safe shape for "repo always shows release-state, not dev history"** (session 182). User wanted the public repo to start at the released version, not at commit-477 of internal development — but reserved the right to keep iterating after launch. The shape that works: keep full dev history on local `main` (and on a private mirror if you want it on a remote at all); curate a ship list; for each release, build a brand-new orphan branch with one commit containing only the curated tree; force-push that orphan to public-repo `main`. Each push replaces the previous orphan entirely (different ancestry → no merge possible → force is required, not optional). `uv tool install git+URL` users get whatever HEAD resolves to at install time, so force-push doesn't break their flow. Three subtleties: (1) **switching back to dev `main` after the orphan dance** needs `git checkout -f main` because the dropped-from-orphan files exist as untracked in the working tree and `git checkout main` refuses to overwrite them — `-f` is correct here because the untracked content is bit-identical to main's tracked content (we only `git rm --cached`'d, never modified). (2) **`git diff --cached --name-only` on an orphan after `rm --cached + add` shows REMOVALS, not additions** — it's diffing the index against HEAD (which has all 16 tracked items from the parent), so what shows up is the dropped 7. To inspect what's *staged*, use `git ls-files --cached`. (3) **`git checkout -B` is not orphan** — `-B` creates a branch from the current HEAD with full history, which is the opposite of what you want. Always `git checkout --orphan <branch>` for this pattern. Generalizable: any "show me the polished cover of the album, not the studio outtakes" public-repo flow needs orphan + force-push + ship-list audit, not history-rewrite tools (filter-repo, BFG) which only work after the bad content has already been pushed.

- **Wide-glyph cell width matters when sizing terminal panels from content** (session 181). The reveal card's first content-aware-width pass undercounted by 2 cells and `claude-ai-google-calendar` (25 chars) wrapped anyway. Root cause: I'd written `_ITEM_LINE_OVERHEAD = 2 + 12 + 2 + 2 = 18` (indent + label + glyph segment + borders), assuming `"⚡ "` was 2 cells (1 char glyph + 1 space). It's actually 3 cells — `⚡` is a wide glyph at `cell_len("⚡") == 2`. The math: `_hang_wrap` computes `avail = inner - cell_len(indent) - cell_len(prefix)`, where the prefix is the label-column string `"MCPs:       "` (12 cells, an alias for `hang = " " * len(label)` on continuation rows). The body string passed to `_hang_wrap` from `_render_list` is `f"{glyph} {name}"` = `"⚡ claude-ai-google-calendar"`, which is `2 + 1 + 25 = 28` cells. With width 43 and the broken overhead, `avail = 41 - 2 - 12 = 27 < 28` → wraps. Fix was bumping the overhead to `2 + 12 + 3 + 2 + 1 = 20` (the `+1` is right-side breathing room so the longest item doesn't kiss the border). Generalizable: any time you're computing a panel/line width from content where the content includes a non-ASCII glyph (✓, ★, ⚡, emoji, box-drawing), use `rich.cells.cell_len` rather than `len()`, and budget the *whole* prefix segment (glyph + separator) as a single measured unit. Don't trust visual char counts when wide glyphs are in the mix.

- **Silence between "joined" and "left" is worse than noise — surface terminal failures, hide recovered ones, never echo message bodies** (session 169). First user-visible run had stdout going dark for the entire meeting: banner → `Joined meeting — listening for chat.` → minutes of nothing → `Left meeting — goodbye.` Three consequences: (a) user can't tell if the bot is healthy-but-idle vs stuck vs quietly broken; (b) MCP server failures only appeared in `/tmp/operator.log` so users hit auth errors live in chat with no upstream warning; (c) tool-execution latency and counts vanished from the operator's view, masking regressions. Fix is two-tier: (1) terse always-on heartbeats — single MCP roll-up line `▸ MCP: linear ✓ · sentry ✗ (run \`operator auth sentry\`)`, listening line that includes the trigger phrase + room state, per-turn closer `✓ Replied — 3.2s · 4 tools` (and `✗ Turn N failed — …` on the early-return paths), browser disconnect / stuck-LLM kill escalated from `ui.warn` to `ui.err` because they ARE terminal; (2) per the user's standing rule for OSS, recovered/transient errors stay in `/tmp/operator.log` only — no stdout, no counter. **Hard constraint: heartbeat is metadata only — no message bodies, sender names, or tool arguments**, because args (paths, URLs, Bash commands) all derive from chat content and would leak into the terminal of any future run with sensitive payloads. Tool *names* are fine; tool *inputs* are not. The per-turn closer drains a `_turn_start_ts` flag so it's idempotent across confirmation re-entries and the various early-return failure branches in `_handle_message` / `_execute_and_respond` / `_handle_tool_failure` — all of which had to be wired explicitly because each is a turn-end that bypasses the normal `_dispatch_result` text branches. Generalizable to any long-running CLI: pick a small set of state transitions worth narrating (start/stop, per-unit-of-work close, terminal failures with remediation), route them through one helper that respects `NO_COLOR` + non-tty stderr, and resist the urge to narrate intermediate progress — that belongs in the log file, not on the user's screen.

- **claude in stream-json input mode emits `system/init` only after the first user envelope arrives, not at startup** (session 166). First implementation of `ClaudeCLIProvider._spawn()` was waiting for the system-init event before returning — and timing out at 30s every spawn. Subprocess was alive and healthy; just silent until fed a message. Confirmed empirically: `(claude -p --input-format stream-json --output-format stream-json --verbose < /dev/null)` produces zero stdout for 8s, then exits cleanly when stdin closes. The "ready signal" you'd expect at process boot doesn't exist in this mode. Fix: drop the spawn-time wait entirely, hold a `_init_validated` flag, and run the apiKeySource subscription-auth assertion when the system-init *does* arrive (during the first `_send_and_collect()` call). General lesson: when wrapping an undocumented subprocess protocol, don't assume boot signals exist — write a 5-line probe that pipes `</dev/null` and watches what comes out before deciding the readiness state machine.

- **Bridge scripts invoked by claude shouldn't import the parent package — run them as standalone scripts** (session 166). Initial `pipeline/permission_bridge.py` was wired into claude's settings.json hook as `python -m _1_800_operator.pipeline.permission_bridge <pipes>`. Worked when the test ran via `OPERATOR_BOT=claude python tests/...` because the test script does `sys.path.insert(0, ".../src")`. Failed when claude actually invoked the hook from its own subprocess shell — `ModuleNotFoundError: operator`. Root cause: operator is NOT `pip install -e .`'d in the dev venv; the wrapper script (`~/.local/bin/operator`) sets `PYTHONPATH=$REPO/src` for the main entry point, but that env var doesn't propagate cleanly to a child process that claude spawns. Fix: invoke the bridge by its absolute file path (`python /path/to/permission_bridge.py <pipes>`) rather than `-m`. The bridge's stdlib-only import discipline (json/os/sys/pathlib only) is what makes this safe — it has zero dependence on the parent package's import graph. Generalizable: any helper script that will be invoked from a subprocess context outside the parent's process tree should be (a) absolute-path-invoked, and (b) stdlib-only at the import level. Keep a comment in the helper explicitly stating the constraint so future maintainers don't add a `from operator.foo import bar` and break the wiring.

- **Adapter DOM-wait timeouts hide regressions when the entry path changes — surface them via path-coverage, not just timeout duration** (session 167). Live-validation cold-start `total_join` jumped 9s → 25.7s the moment we tested the no-URL `meet.new` flow under track A. DOM didn't change. Code path through `connectors/macos_adapter.py` did — `meet.new` auto-creates a meeting and lands the bot **already in-meeting**, past the pre-join screen. Two waits at lines 587 and 677 hunted for elements that exist only on the pre-join screen: `pre_join_ready` waited the full 15s for {Join now, Ask to join, Turn off camera, Sign in} (none of which exist post-join), then `camera_toggle` waited another 5s for "Turn off camera." The `already_in_meeting` short-circuit at line 643 was added later but only gated the join-button race — never the two waits before it. Lesson: any `wait_for_selector` with a long timeout needs to either (a) include selectors covering every legitimate landing state in the OR list, or (b) be gated on a state-detect that runs FIRST. Fix here was (a) for `pre_join_ready` (added `Leave call` aria-label) + (b) for `camera_toggle` (gated on `already_in_meeting`). Tell-tale in logs: `pre_join_ready=15.0s` immediately followed by `MacOSAdapter: no pre-join element detected — proceeding anyway` AND `MacOSAdapter: already in meeting — skipping pre-join flow`. When the adapter logs both "didn't find" AND "already in," the wait was misallocated for that code path.

- **Streamed paragraphs in claude-cli need an `assistant`-event paragraph break, not an index-based one — sub-messages reset content_block indices** (session 167). The track-A claude_cli provider streams paragraphs via `flush_paragraphs()` which splits on `\n{2,}`. When claude calls a tool mid-turn (text → tool_use → text after tool result), the wire emits each text span as its own assistant message — content-block indices reset between messages (both texts come at index 0 of their respective messages). First fix attempt tracked `last_text_index` and inserted `\n\n` when index changed; that didn't fire because indices were always 0 → 0. The right signal is the terminal `assistant` event itself (one fires per sub-message). When that event arrives and the streaming buffer has pending text, force-flush it as a paragraph and append `\n\n` to the accumulator. Diagnostic tell: `WARNING ClaudeCLI: streamed accumulator (X chars) diverged from canonical assistant event (Y chars)` where X > Y by exactly the length of the prior sub-message text — means canonical_text was overwriting on each `assistant` event instead of accumulating. Same fix that adds the paragraph break also accumulates canonical_text into a list joined by `\n\n` at end-of-turn. Lesson: when a streaming protocol's event hierarchy has multiple boundary types (delta indices, message terminations, turn results), pick the one that semantically matches your output unit (paragraphs ≈ sub-messages, not delta blocks).

- **Wrap a CLI that uses `cwd` — mirror it, don't pin to `$HOME` for "predictability"** (session 168). `ClaudeCLIProvider.__init__` defaulted `cwd=$HOME` with the rationale "stable, predictable resolution of relative paths." That choice meant inner-claude had no project context: when the user asked "walk us through how the chat polling loop works in this codebase," the bot's first action was to ask permission for `Bash: ls /Users/jojo` to find a repo to walk into. Surfaced live during Test 1.1 — the confirmation prompt itself was the diagnostic. The bare `claude` CLI mirrors the user's invocation cwd; operator was deviating from that contract for no benefit. Fix at `build_provider()`: pass `cwd=os.getcwd()` explicitly. The provider's `cwd` kwarg default still points at `$HOME` for any caller that doesn't want this behavior, but the app-level builder owns it. Generalizable: when wrapping a tool whose UX depends on cwd (compilers, CLIs, REPLs), inherit the parent process's cwd unless you have a specific reason to override — overriding to `$HOME` "for stability" sounds neutral but invisibly strips context the inner tool needs to be useful.

- **Intro latency was ordering, not the LLM call — parallelize independent slow paths and pre-seed gates from prior knowledge** (session 168). Bot intro took ~8s to land after `joined`, breakdown: ~3s subprocess spawn (intro thread started AFTER `_join` returned, so spawn ran serially), ~6.5s for the LLM call itself, then up to 3s waiting for the `saw_others` gate to flip on the next `PARTICIPANT_CHECK_INTERVAL = 3s` poll cycle (the participant-count check ran AFTER `read_chat()` in the loop body, so the first iteration could lag a couple seconds even when the user was already in the room). Two fixes, both small: (a) move the `_generate_intro` thread launch to BEFORE the `_connector.join()` wait — the intro LLM call needs only a live LLM, not browser state, so it parallelizes naturally with the 5–10s browser launch; (b) call `self._connector.get_participant_count()` synchronously at the top of `_loop()` before the polling loop starts, seeding `saw_others=True` immediately if the room is non-empty. Combined effect: intro lands in ~1–2s instead of ~8s. Generalizable: when a multi-stage startup feels slow, stop assuming each stage's wall-clock time is the right thing to optimize — first audit the *order* and look for stages that don't have a real data dependency on prior stages. The cheapest latency win is parallelism, not faster code. Same shape: gate variables that get refreshed on a timer can usually be seeded from a one-shot pre-loop check, eliminating up-to-one-period of dead wait without changing the timer's steady-state behavior.

- **When confirmation prompts dump bulk content, the safety check inverts — users skim past the wall and approve without reading** (session 168). The original `_format_confirmation` rendered every tool argument verbatim with head…tail truncation only above 200 chars. A `Write` for a 30-line test file produced a 30-line chat prompt; a `MultiEdit` with 3 hunks dumped all the old/new strings. Users live-tested the system reported "I just say yes because reading is exhausting" — the prompt's job (giving the user enough to decide) inverted into noise. Fix: per-tool `_format_terse()` that collapses bulk content fields into size hints (`Write /tmp/foo.py (1.2 KB)`, `MultiEdit src/x.py (3 hunks)`) but keeps imperative fields verbatim. **The non-obvious carve-out: Bash commands are NEVER summarized**, even in terse mode — the user's safety decision genuinely depends on seeing the literal command (`rm -rf /` vs `rm /tmp/foo`). So "terse" doesn't mean "summarize all params"; it means "hide bulk content (the body), keep the imperative (the verb)." Adding a verbose mode for power-users is cheap (`agent.permission_verbosity: terse | verbose`) and worth doing — but terse should be the default. Generalizable to any human-in-the-loop confirmation UX: distinguish *what's being done* (must be visible verbatim) from *the payload* (collapse to a size hint by default).

- **Identity framing in restart-after-death openers — "you are picking up" makes the model deny its own real actions** (session 167). The synthesized opener for restart-on-death originally said *"You are picking up a conversation that was already in progress. Here is the transcript so far..."* The model read this as third-party transcript and started SECOND-GUESSING prior assistant claims. Concrete failure: after restart, asked to recap, the model said *"I incorrectly claimed I wrote it to /tmp/different.txt — no file was actually written"* — except the file DID exist on disk. The model was hedging because (a) the framing positioned prior text as someone-else's report, and (b) the restart context provides no tool-result events to verify the action actually happened. Fix is purely prompt-engineering: reframe as *"Continuation of YOUR in-progress chat-meeting conversation. The Assistant lines below are YOUR prior turns — not a third-party transcript. Treat any tool actions you previously claimed as actions you performed and that are already complete. If you need to verify, read the relevant file/state — do not deny your own prior claims without doing so first."* Live-tested: bot now correctly recaps three real file ops without hedging. Lesson: when synthesizing context for an LLM after a state-bearing process death, identity continuity matters as much as content fidelity. The deeper fix (recording tool_use + tool_result events on the wire and replaying them in the opener) is invasive and deferred — but absent that, identity framing alone gets you most of the way for honest prior text.

- **Real Chrome is a hard runtime dep on macOS — preflight before any wizard or bot launch, not deep inside Playwright** (session 160). Both the wizard sign-in step (`pipeline/google_signin.py`) and the macOS adapter (`connectors/macos_adapter.py`) hard-code `executable_path="/Applications/Google Chrome.app/..."` because Chrome profiles aren't compatible across binaries (Chrome-for-Testing vs real Chrome — session 159). When the binary is missing, Playwright surfaces an opaque `Failed to launch chromium because executable doesn't exist` from inside the launch call — the wizard banner has already printed, the user has answered prompts, and the failure looks like a mid-flow crash rather than a missing dep. Fix: `pipeline/chrome_preflight.py` exports `chrome_installed()` + `require_chrome_or_exit()`, called at the top of `__main__._run_setup` and `__main__._run_macos` (and as defense-in-depth at the launch sites in case future code paths bypass `__main__`). Linux skipped (linux adapter uses bundled chromium); `try` skipped (terminal connector, no browser). Why we did NOT bundle Chrome with the package: 600 MB binary inflates a KB Python wheel three orders of magnitude; Chrome ToS prohibits redistribution (Chromium is licit but loses Google sign-in compatibility); Google's auto-updater would fight or stale our copy; users will not trust `curl ... | sh` to drop a 600 MB browser into `/Applications`. Right home for the install nudge is `install.sh` itself (Phase 14.5.1) — `brew install --cask google-chrome` is Google-blessed and matches the `gh`/`hugo`/`volta` pattern of deferring system deps to the platform package manager.

- **macOS Chrome.app is a singleton by bundle ID; bot's `--user-data-dir` profile doesn't isolate it from the user's daily Chrome** (session 163). For most of the project's life `connectors/macos_adapter.py` launched the user's installed `/Applications/Google Chrome.app` with `executable_path=...` + `--user-data-dir=~/.operator/browser_profile/` + `--headless=new`. Two stacked bugs lived in that line for months without surfacing because the user wasn't a daily Chrome user. (1) `--headless=new` was a no-op — Playwright's `headless=False` flag took precedence, so operator ran a *headed* real Chrome despite the Chrome flag asking otherwise. (2) macOS routes dock activation, ⌘N, ⌘Tab by app *bundle ID*, not process. Two Chrome processes with separate `--user-data-dir`s still share `com.google.Chrome` — when the user clicks the dock or presses ⌘N, macOS sends the activation to whichever Chrome process owns the front window. operator's window owned the front, dropped the keystrokes silently, user thought their Chrome was hung, force-quit the app — which killed the bot's tab too. Worse compounding: `chat_runner._send` doesn't notice when the browser thread dies. It just keeps enqueuing `send_chat` requests; `result_q.get(timeout=10)` raises `queue.Empty` (which stringifies to `''`); log line reads `send_chat failed: ` with nothing after the colon. Distinctive log fingerprint to recognize next time: that exact empty-tail error line repeating every 10s — means the browser thread is dead, not that any single send failed. Fix has two parts. (a) Architectural: drop `executable_path` + `channel="chrome"`, use Playwright's bundled Chromium, set `headless=True`. Bundled Chromium has its own bundle ID — fully separate from the user's Chrome, no activation collision possible. The original "we need real Chrome for Google sign-in" assumption (session 14.10) survives because the persistent profile carries the auth state regardless of which binary opens it; we validated `~/.operator/browser_profile/` works under bundled Chromium without re-auth.
