## Phase 11.4 — Skill Loading (design notes)

**History (session 102).** Originally split as 11.4 (generic flat-`.md`) + 11.5 (Claude Code interop on top). Collapsed into a single phase: adopting `SKILL.md` shape + progressive disclosure + `allowed-tools` filtering up front is simpler than shipping twice. `skills.local.yaml` deferred to post-MVP.

Pitch: **"Claude Code in Google Meet."** Users bring their existing Claude Code skills into Operator instead of recreating them.

**Source of truth.** Claude Code skills live at `~/.claude/skills/<name>/SKILL.md` (user-level) and `.claude/skills/<name>/SKILL.md` (project-level). Each skill is a folder with a `SKILL.md` — YAML frontmatter (`name`, `description`, optional `allowed-tools`) plus a markdown body. Format is designed for progressive disclosure: only `name + description` loads up front; the full body is pulled in when the model decides the skill is relevant.

**Load model: reference, not copy.** `config.yaml` stores paths (`~/.claude/skills/<name>` or absolute paths), not file contents. On startup, Operator reads `SKILL.md` live from the user's machine. Rationale: each user's `~/.claude/skills/` is already their curated, personal set — forcing a copy into the repo would be double-bookkeeping, and the open-source story is "each user makes Operator theirs." Downside acknowledged: paths only exist on that user's machine, so a teammate who clones the repo will hit missing skills. Mitigation: log + skip, don't crash.

**Implementation shape.**
- `config.yaml` gains a `skills:` list. Entries are paths (absolute or `~`-expanded). An entry may be either a single skill folder (contains `SKILL.md`) or a parent directory (scanned one level deep for `*/SKILL.md`). Parent-dir scanning is what makes `~/.claude/skills/` a single-line config entry.
- On startup, resolve each path, parse `SKILL.md` frontmatter with `pyyaml` (already a dep).
- **Progressive disclosure.** Inject only `name + description` of each skill into the system prompt as an available-skills list. Register a synthetic `load_skill(name: str)` tool alongside MCP tools. When the model calls it, Operator returns the full body of the named skill as the tool result. Model then re-plans with the body in context. Matches Claude Code's loading behavior; keeps token cost flat as users accumulate skills.
- Missing path → WARN log + skip. Do not crash startup.
- Malformed `SKILL.md` (bad YAML, missing `name` / `description`) → WARN log + skip.
- Duplicate skill names across paths → last one wins, WARN on collision.
- Startup log line: `SKILLS: N/M loaded (<name> ✓, <name> ✓, <name> ✗ missing)`. Mirrors the MCP startup banner pattern from session 87.
- **Deferred to post-MVP:** optional gitignored `skills.local.yaml` for personal overrides — teams share a baseline `config.yaml` and layer personal skills on top. Not MVP-critical.
- System prompt ordering: base prompt → skills block → MCP hints → MCP status (most dynamic last, so skills share a stable prefix for prompt caching).

**Tool-surface filtering.** Most interesting Claude Code skills assume tools Operator doesn't have in a meeting context. Split by `allowed-tools`:
- **Pure-instruction skills** (no `allowed-tools`, or only MCP-backed tools): ship as-is. Tone guides, commit-message style, decision frameworks, interview rubrics.
- **MCP-backed skills** (Linear, Gmail, Calendar): work once the corresponding MCP server is configured.
- **Tool-heavy skills** (`Bash`, `Edit`, `Write`, `Read`): known to misfire. Five common ones that break: `/commit`-style git skills, the `pdf` skill, the office-suite skill (`docx`/`xlsx`/`pptx`), PR-review skills (`/review-pr`, `simplify`), refactor/debug-test-failure skills. Common thread: **anything that assumes a filesystem, a shell, or the Read/Edit/Write triad** breaks in a Meet context.
- On import, check `allowed-tools`; if it references tools Operator can't honor, log a WARN with the specific unsupported tools. Still load the skill (the model may decline to invoke it in the meeting context) but the user knows why it might misfire.

**Out of scope for 11.4.** Skill *execution* beyond injecting body text — i.e., we are not implementing `Bash`/`Edit`/`Write`/`Read` to make tool-heavy skills actually work. Pitch is honest: "bring your instruction skills." Also out of scope: hot-reload when a `SKILL.md` changes on disk mid-meeting — load at startup only (restart required for changes).

---

## Phase 15.5 — Opinionated Quickstart (design notes)

Pitch: **"Choose your fighter → add power-ups → go."** The agents gallery is the gallery layer; the wizard turns it into a 3-step setup. Implicit differentiator vs. joinly's framework-shaped positioning.

**Why a gallery, not forks.** Forks fragment git history and don't make the parent repo look alive. A `roster/` folder with PR contributions keeps everyone on main, makes contributors visible in the commit log, and turns every seeded-persona build into a permanent artifact. This is the primitive; forks were rejected explicitly. Reference patterns: Ollama model library, LangChain templates, n8n templates, ComfyUI workflows, Vercel templates, Hugging Face Spaces.

**Folder format (already locked in `roster/README.md`).** Each roster member is a self-contained folder with a runnable `config.yaml`, optional `skills/` directory, a short `README.md` (what / who / needs / setup / demo), and `.env.example`. The roster member must run on a fresh clone after the user fills in keys — no hidden dependencies.

### 15.5.1 — `claude-code` starter agent

Canonical example. Demonstrates the format and is the launch hero. **Depends on Phase 11.5 (Claude Code skill import) being complete** — without skill import, this agent has nothing distinct to show.

- `roster/engineer/config.yaml` — complete Operator config; either OpenAI or Anthropic as default (decide near build time, lean Anthropic since the framing is "Claude Code"); `mcp_servers` includes Linear + GitHub; `skills:` points at `~/.claude/skills/` by default, with a comment explaining how to swap to a custom path.
- `roster/engineer/README.md` — "What it does: brings your existing `~/.claude/skills/` into Google Meet so the agent files Linear tickets, looks up GitHub PRs, and follows your team conventions during a live call." Setup: copy `config.yaml`, fill `.env`, run. Demo: short GIF of an artifact appearing in chat mid-sentence.
- `roster/engineer/skills/` — leave empty by default. The whole point is the user's own skills get loaded from `~/.claude/skills/`. Optionally bundle one demo skill that's safe to ship (e.g. `file-linear-ticket.md`) so the agent has at least one skill even if the user has none locally.
- `.env.example` — `OPENAI_API_KEY` or `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, `LINEAR_API_KEY`, `GITHUB_TOKEN`.

### 15.5.3 — Runtime architecture (roster as source of truth)

**The architectural shift** (session 113): today, `python __main__.py <url>` reads an ambient `config.yaml` at repo root — "whatever was last copied there." Replaced by explicit per-run bot selection. Every run names the bot.

- Positional CLI in `__main__.py`:
  - `operator <name> <url>` — run that bot in that meeting. Load `roster/<name>/config.yaml` directly.
  - `operator <name>` (no URL) — auto-open `meet.new`, capture slug, join as that bot. (Absorbs old 15.5.4's `meet.new` deliverable.)
  - `operator setup` — launches the wizard (see 15.5.5).
  - `operator list` — prints available roster members + one-line pitches.
  - `operator` (bare) — prints usage + roster list.
- Dispatch rule: if first arg matches a `roster/*` folder, treat as bot-name; if it's a known subcommand (`setup` / `list`), dispatch there; else error with helpful usage.
- Delete root `config.yaml`. Config loading reads `roster/<name>/config.yaml` at runtime.
- `.env` stays at repo root, shared across all bots (keys like `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` are environment-scoped, not bot-scoped).
- Ship `./operator` bash wrapper in repo root: `#!/usr/bin/env bash` + `cd "$(dirname "$0")"` + `source venv/bin/activate` + `exec python __main__.py "$@"`. Provisional launcher until product name is locked and curl installer ships post-launch.
- **Breaking change:** every doc, test, and reference to `python __main__.py <url>` migrates to `operator <name> <url>`. Pre-launch, so the cost is grep + update, not deprecation.

### 15.5.4 — Face system + profile banner

Each bot has a unique pixel-art face that prints on every run. Faces are the bot's identity and the "you're playing as X" moment when a meeting starts.

- **Deterministic face generator.** Half-block Unicode (`▀ ▄ █`) + ANSI 256-color. 16×20 pixels — fits 3-across in a standard terminal, readable. Seed = hash(bot name), so the same name always produces the same face. Parts library: eyes, mouth, brow, hair/hat, accessory, palette.
- **Shipping portraits.** Run the generator for `engineer` / `pm` / `designer`, hand-curate until good, commit as `roster/<name>/portrait.txt`.
- **First-run write hook.** Any `operator <name>` run that finds no `portrait.txt` in the roster folder generates one and writes it. This is the "gift" for contributors: they add `roster/translator/` with a config and README, run `operator translator` once, and a face file materializes for them to commit with their PR.
- **Startup banner.** Every `operator <name>` run prints a block before joining:
  ```
  ╔════════════════════════════╗
  ║   <face>      ENGINEER     ║
  ║               looks up GH  ║
  ║               MCPs: GitHub ║
  ║               Skills: 4    ║
  ║               Model: ...   ║
  ╚════════════════════════════╝
  ```
  Reads from the active config — pulls agent name, one-line tagline (from README h1 or a config field), MCP names, skill count, model.
- **`--plain` fallback.** Prints ASCII-only banner for screen readers / hostile terminals / CI logs.
- Dep: `rich` for color/boxes/layout (new dep — already battle-tested, 1-package install).

### 15.5.5 — `operator setup` wizard (creation flow)

**Key reframe** (session 113): wizard is no longer "activate a bundle by copying config to root." It's a *creation* tool — builds a new `roster/<name>/` folder so the user ends up with their own bot they run explicitly.

- `operator setup` — four steps:
  1. **Choose a template (or start blank).** Fighter-select grid UI — colored boxes, pre-shipped faces visible, numbered prompt. "Start blank" produces a minimal config stub.
  2. **Power-ups — awareness + toggle.** Show the template's bundled MCPs and skills as a checklist (including commented-out power-up entries in the template config). User toggles what ends up in the new bot. Narrow scope: only touches what the template declares. Out of scope: arbitrary MCP discovery, paste-a-URL flow, `~/.claude/skills` path editor (all post-launch).
  3. **Keys.** Prompt for any env vars the new bot needs that aren't already in `.env`. `getpass` for secrets (no echo, never print existing values). Merge into `.env`, preserving unrelated keys. Atomic write.
  4. **Finalize.** Atomic-write the new `roster/<new-name>/` folder: `config.yaml` (built from template + toggles), `README.md` stub, `.env.example`. Generate face via 15.5.4's generator, write `portrait.txt`. Print: `Your bot is ready. Run: operator <new-name> <meet-url>`.
- Re-run-safe: name-collision check against existing roster folders.
- Intent of step 2: pure FYI — user should *know* what their bot can do (so they know to ask it to file a Linear ticket), not be forced into configuration work. Checkbox ergonomics, not a forms-based MCP configurator.
- **Depends on 15.5.3** (for `setup` dispatch surface) and **15.5.4** (for face generator + pre-baked shipping portraits rendered in step 1's grid).
- ~250 lines of Python + `rich`. Out of scope: voice, MCP OAuth flows, model selection UI beyond what the template dictates. Those land in the post-MVP full wizard.

### Launch interplay

The gallery doubles as launch ammunition (see `docs/mvp-bar.md` Launch Strategy). Each seeded persona contributes one `roster/<name>/` PR, then posts about that build. Real users browsing the repo see contributor activity on `main` — social proof as code. Ship 3 roster members at launch (engineer + PM + designer), target 5 within week 1 via seeded PRs.

---

## Phase 15.7 — MCP Hardening + Team Completion (design notes)

*Session 147 approval — six sub-phases sequenced between Phase 14.8 clean-mac smoke and Phase 15.1 Linux. Full roadmap entry at `docs/roadmap.md` Phase 15.7.*

### Motivation
- Three shipped agents + three shipped skills (prd-from-discussion, standup-summary, design-review-feedback) ≠ a **team**. The skills don't yet tell a complete arc from meeting → artifact. Engineer ships with zero bundled skills; Designer only covers aesthetic review.
- Adding 5 new MCPs onto a codebase that only handles missing-creds via `/tmp/operator.log` warnings is a liability — every new MCP multiplies the surface for "enabled-but-unauthed" mid-meeting silence. Hardening must land before breadth.
- Target persona (remote teams with AI in meetings, not just solo founders) — the win is a self-evident "cool, I didn't realize it could do that" moment during `operator setup` skill picker + a corresponding moment in the meeting itself.

### The arc we're closing
`prd-from-discussion` (PM, shipped) → `design-handoff-spec` (Designer, new) → `scope-estimate` (Engineer, new) → delegate_to_claude_code → `pr-review` (Engineer, new) → `live-bug-triage` (Engineer, new, Sentry-backed) → `release-notes` (Engineer, new) → `standup-summary` (PM, shipped) → `schedule-followup` (PM, new, Calendar-backed). That's every relay-runner in a feature's life getting a meeting-native moment.

### Hardening — the four phases A–D land in this order because each compounds
- **15.7.1 (A) error classification** ✅ (session 148, `6beff98`) — `_resolve_env_vars` returns `(resolved, missing_vars)`; `_classify_startup_failure` returns structured `{kind, fix, raw, [vars]}` with `missing_creds` taking precedence over any noisier crash; rename `failed_servers` → `startup_failures`, `disabled_servers` → `runtime_failures`, both now `dict[str, dict]`. `record_tool_result` accepts `error_text` and upgrades tripped servers to `kind="auth_failed"` when any sub-threshold failure matched `_AUTH_ERROR_PATTERNS` (empirical: GitHub "Bad credentials", Figma "Forbidden", plus documented Slack/Sentry/Salesforce/Google patterns). Empirical capture script lives at `tests/probe_auth_errors.py`; results archived in `docs/mcp-auth-errors.md`.
- **15.7.2 (B) proactive banner** ✅ (session 148, `43dae3f`) — `ChatRunner._post_mcp_failure_banner` in `run()` posts one compact line after `ui.ok("Joined meeting…")`, BEFORE the async intro thread so it lands deterministically even if intro generation errors. `_FAILURE_KIND_LABELS` dispatches per `kind`; multi-failure joins with "; " + "Ask for details." Silent when `startup_failures` is empty.
- **15.7.3 (C) OAuth decoupling** ✅ (session 148, `ed63026`) — new `auth: env \| oauth` field + `auth_url` on MCP blocks; `_oauth_cache_exists(auth_url)` checks `~/.mcp-auth/mcp-remote-*/<md5(auth_url)>_tokens.json` (lex-latest version dir). `connect_all` runs the pre-check before spawning auth:oauth servers — missing → skip + `kind="oauth_needed"`. New `operator auth <mcp>` CLI subcommand foreground-spawns the configured command+args with stdin piped + stdout/stderr inherited, polls for tokens.json, SIGTERMs on success. Bundled Linear configs on all 3 agents declare `auth: oauth` + `auth_url: https://mcp.linear.app/mcp` (user-owned `~/.operator/agents/` intentionally NOT modified — session 147 insulation promise). **Zero OAuth hangs at meeting join.** Known limitation: mcp-remote version upgrades create fresh cache dirs (users re-auth on bump); accepted for MVP.
- **15.7.4 (D) wizard credentials status screen + claude-code prereq check** (next, ~2h) — users enable freely, then see a per-MCP `✓/⚠/✗` checklist at the end of the MCP step with remediation URLs. Non-blocking. OAuth MCPs get an optional inline "authorize Linear now? y/n" that invokes the same code path as `operator auth <mcp>`. **Session 148 addition**: when user toggles `claude-code` on, probe `shutil.which("git")` + `shutil.which("claude")` + claude-is-authed check; skip if user says "later"; fails non-blockingly with the install-docs URL. Git-init is NOT a pre-req for enablement (per-call concern, MCP takes `repo_path` at invocation). Uses 15.7.1's `missing_vars` + 15.7.3's `_oauth_cache_exists`.
- **15.7.4.5 (E) runtime MCP pre-flight** (session 148 split-out, ~45m) — same `_report_mcp_readiness(mcp_servers)` helper runs in `_run_bot()` BEFORE browser spin-up. Missing OAuth → interactive "Run auth now? (y/N)" that invokes `operator auth <mcp>` inline, waits for token cache, continues. Missing env vars → "Continue without slack? (Y/n)". **Catches hand-edit-config case** (user enables OAuth MCP by editing yaml outside wizard — 15.7.3 banner catches it mid-meeting today but obtrusively). Wizard + runtime share the same helper; belt-and-suspenders. `--no-preflight` escape hatch for CI/scripted launches.

### New MCPs (15.7.5) and per-agent default enablement
**Rule (session 147):** an MCP is `enabled: true` on an agent **iff a bundled skill on that agent requires it.** Everything else is scaffolded but `enabled: false` — users surface them via the wizard. Prevents "enabled but silently unauthed" noise at meeting join.

Final matrix:
- **PM** → Linear ✓ (standup-summary optional use, ambient filing from spoken commitments) + Calendar ✓ (schedule-followup). GitHub dropped — no PM skill calls it.
- **Designer** → Figma ✓ (design-review-feedback + design-handoff-spec). Linear dropped — no Designer skill calls it.
- **Engineer** → GitHub ✓ (pr-review + release-notes) + Sentry ✓ (live-bug-triage) + claude-code ✓ (live-bug-triage delegate).
- **Slack, Salesforce, Playwright** → scaffolded in all three configs but `enabled: false` everywhere — no bundled skill paired. Users who want `post-recap-to-slack`, `deal-brief`, or `design-qa` flip them on in the wizard.
- Every new block declares `auth: env` + `credentials_url: "https://..."` — feeds 15.7.4's status screen.

**Behavior change on fresh installs:** PM and Designer lose a previously-enabled MCP each. `~/.operator/agents/` is user-owned per 14.3, so existing installs are insulated; only new installs (or `rm -rf ~/.operator/agents/` reseeds) see the narrower defaults. Acceptable for MVP — users who customized the defaults aren't surprised, and fresh installs have a quieter out-of-box experience.

### Skills (15.7.6)
Six new `SKILL.md` files, each following the existing `prd-from-discussion` / `design-review-feedback` pattern (frontmatter + `## Shape` + `## Rules` sections). `live-bug-triage` is the most complex — it chains Sentry MCP + Claude Code delegate. Others are single-MCP or pure-reasoning (`scope-estimate` writes no code, makes no tool calls).

### Estimation and launch impact
- **Total ~9–11h.** Session 148 shipped 15.7.1 + 15.7.2 + 15.7.3 in ~5h (three commits). Remaining: 15.7.4 ~2h (was 1.5h; claude-code prereq check added scope), 15.7.4.5 ~45m (new session-148 split-out), 15.7.5 2–3h, 15.7.6 2–3h. **Remaining envelope: ~6–8h.**
- MVP budget: 17.5h → 28–30h. Launch slips ~2 days from Apr 25–26 to Apr 28–30 aspirational.
- Deliberate bet: shipping a hardened MCP path + complete team-arc is worth 2 calendar days. Skill showcase during `operator setup` is the moment a user decides whether this product reads their mind.

### Open design questions (carry into execution)
1. **Non-mcp-remote OAuth paths** — the cache-check scheme in 15.7.3 is specific to `mcp-remote`'s directory layout (`~/.mcp-auth/mcp-remote-<version>/<md5(url)>_tokens.json`). If any future MCP ships its own OAuth flow outside `mcp-remote`, the readiness check needs a per-server convention (e.g., a callable `is_authorized()` hook declared in config). For v1 the five new MCPs are all API-key-based so this defers — Linear is still the only `mcp-remote` OAuth MCP in the roster.
2. **Salesforce + Playwright as "power-ups without bundled skills"** — intentional per session 147. Salesforce's likely v1.1 skill is `deal-brief` (pre-call account prep for PM); Playwright's likely v1.1 skill is `design-qa` (Designer; screenshot deployed URL + diff vs Figma frame). Neither blocks MVP — ship the MCP scaffolding now so users can wire them up + write their own skills, and the wizard surfaces them as discoverable options.

---

## Open Questions

1. **Wake phrase customization (voice)** — allow users to set their own wake phrase? Test Whisper reliability on custom phrases first. Chat wake phrase is already configurable via `chat_wake_phrase` in config.yaml.
2. **Linux distro coverage** — Ubuntu/Debian tier-1; PipeWire (Fedora, Ubuntu 22.04+) needs validation.

## Hard Won Knowledge

- **A test asserting an "implementation detail" can lock in unintended behavior AND silently rely on the very fallback path you're trying to delete.** (Session 200, cell 5, meeting_record.py audit.) `MeetingRecord.append()` was unconditionally appending every entry to both the JSONL file AND a `_memory` list — but `tail()` only ever reads `_memory` in the slugless test mode (path is None). When path is set, `tail()` reads from disk. So the in-memory mirror was carrying shadow state that was never read in production. Looked like clean dead code to delete. **But:** `test_append_writes_file_and_memory` asserted `rec._memory[-1] == entry` even when path was set — locking in the dual-state behavior as if it were intentional. Deleted the dual state, updated that test, ran the suite — `test_transcript_dedupe.py` then failed. Tracing it: those tests created a `MeetingRecord` inside a `tempfile.TemporaryDirectory()`, did some appends, then read `rec.tail(10)` **outside** the `with` block. The temp dir was gone by then, so `tail()` checked `self.path.exists()`, got False, and silently fell back to `return list(self._memory[-n:])`. The tests were "passing" by exercising the orphan-fallback path I had just made impossible. Two layers of test brittleness papering over each other. **Lesson:** when a piece of code looks like obvious dead duplication but is "tested into the contract," check whether the test is asserting *intentional* behavior or just *current* behavior. Run `grep -rn _memory` (or whatever the dual-state thing is called) in tests/ — if multiple tests touch it, they may all be coupled to the same incidental fallback. And: when a test reads from a resource AFTER the resource's lifecycle scope has exited (`with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory()`), that's a code smell — the test only passes because of some silent fallback the code under test exposes. Move the assertion inside the lifecycle scope as a matter of hygiene; if the test then fails, the fallback was load-bearing and you've found a real finding.

- **ScreenCaptureKit silently fails when launched from plain Python — voice-preserved's load-bearing trick was wrapping the orchestrator in a `.app` bundle.** (Session 198.) Spent ~4 hours debugging why SCStream callbacks never fired from `operator slip claude` (CLI Python) when the same Swift helper, same TCC entry, ran fine from `voice-preserved`'s era. Eventually re-grepped voice-preserved's `docs/agent-context.md` and found the explicit line: **"ScreenCaptureKit requires `.app` bundle on macOS — silently fails from plain Python script."** Voice-preserved had `app.py` running as `/Applications/Operator.app` via `rumps`, and the Swift helper was spawned by THAT process. The .app gave the parent Python a stable TCC identity; the helper inherited a sane responsibility chain. We're spawning from `python` invoked from a CLI inside Cursor's terminal — entire stack is plain CLI processes that SCStream silently rejects regardless of grants. **Lesson:** when a working reference predecessor exists, search its docs for hard-won knowledge BEFORE re-debugging from scratch — the failure mode you're hitting is often documented as a solved problem. Specifically for SCStream: the launching Python process must live inside a `.app` bundle OR the helper itself must be signed as a `.app` bundle (Developer-ID + hardened runtime + entitlements is the productized version). Plain CLI Python = SCStream's audio path silently denies.

- **`responsibility_spawnattrs_setdisclaim` is real, works, but unlocks fresh TCC dialogs for every protected resource the spawned binary touches.** (Session 198.) When the launching IDE has a stale or weird TCC chain (Cursor's ToDesktop wrapper has bundle ID `com.todesktop.230313mzl4w4u92` and a responsibility chain that satisfies `CGPreflightScreenCaptureAccess()` but not SCStream's deeper gate), the helper inherits that broken state and audio callbacks silently never fire. The private API `responsibility_spawnattrs_setdisclaim(&attrs, 1)` from `<spawn.h>` makes the spawned child its own responsible process — TCC then keys against the child's own code-sig identifier instead of the launcher's chain. Live-confirmed it works: from Cursor's terminal post-disclaim, mic + whisper + caption fired end-to-end. **Subtle gotcha:** disclaim makes the binary its OWN responsible process for ALL TCC checks, not just Screen Recording. So on first run after disclaim, the user gets separate dialogs for every resource the binary touches. Our helper lives in `~/Desktop/operator/...`, so the FIRST dialog was Files & Folders (Desktop access) — completely unexpected, blocked the helper at 128KB RSS waiting for the user to click Allow. Only after that did Screen Recording + Mic dialogs fire. **Lesson:** when using `responsibility_spawnattrs_setdisclaim`, document explicitly that the user will see N dialogs on first run where N includes any TCC-protected file location the binary lives in. And consider building the helper to a TCC-neutral location like `/usr/local/bin/` or `~/.operator/bin/` instead of under `~/Desktop/` to avoid the Files & Folders prompt. Implementation lives in `pipeline/_disclaimed_spawn.py` (ctypes wrapper for `posix_spawn` + `posix_spawnattr_setflags` + `responsibility_spawnattrs_setdisclaim`); `subprocess.Popen` doesn't expose the disclaim attr so we can't use it.

- **SCStream fires audio callbacks at the configured rate even during silence — counting them AFTER `guard n > 0 else { return }` means the watchdog never sees them.** (Session 198.) The 14.20.2 helper had a watchdog: "if `systemStats.callbacks == 0` at 10s, FATAL exit 4." Quiet system meant SCK fired `didOutputSampleBuffer` callbacks at the audio rate but with empty / no data buffer attached. Our handler had `guard n > 0 else { return }` BEFORE `systemStats.callbacks += 1`, so empty-buffer callbacks were silently dropped before counting. Counter never advanced → watchdog FATAL'd → entire helper torn down (also killing mic which was working). What made it tricky: voice-preserved's audio_capture.swift counter was at the very top, before any guard, so they never hit this. Also, in our intermittent-failure debugging, we sometimes saw "helper survived 12s" runs — because under SOME conditions SCK fires non-empty callbacks even during near-silence (room tone, fan noise — any RMS above zero produces non-empty buffers). This made the bug look like an intermittent TCC problem when it was actually a logic bug in our code path. **Lesson:** when wrapping a callback-driven API in a watchdog, the watchdog should count CALLBACK INVOCATIONS, not "callbacks-with-useful-data." SCK's contract is "fires at rate X regardless of audio content"; your code is the one filtering empty buffers, so don't double-account. The fix is one line: `systemStats.callbacks += 1` at the very top of the function, before any guards. Generalizable: any time you have `guard X else { return }; counter += 1`, ask whether the counter should track "calls that arrived" or "calls with useful work." For watchdogs detecting "is the upstream still firing?", it's always "calls that arrived."

- **Cursor's ToDesktop wrapper has TCC behavior that satisfies preflight but not SCStream's deeper gate.** (Session 198.) `CGPreflightScreenCaptureAccess()` returns `true` for processes spawned from Cursor's terminal — TCC's responsibility-chain attribution puts Cursor as the responsible process, Cursor has SR granted, preflight reports OK. But SCStream itself does an additional gate check (apparently against the binary itself, or a stricter chain check) that silently denies. No error from `startCapture`'s completion handler, no `didStopWithError` async signal — just zero audio callbacks for the lifetime of the stream. Same Mac, same binary, same TCC entries, but launched from Terminal.app: SCStream works fine. The behavior is specific to ToDesktop's Electron-wrapped responsibility chain. Bundle ID `com.todesktop.230313mzl4w4u92` is the smoking gun in `log stream --predicate 'subsystem == "com.apple.TCC"'` output. **Lesson:** when an IDE/terminal app is built on a wrapper framework (ToDesktop, Electron, Tauri, ...), don't trust its TCC chain to behave like a system-supplied terminal. Verify SCK-gated paths from a baseline app like Terminal.app before assuming the issue is your code. Workaround: `responsibility_spawnattrs_setdisclaim` makes the spawned binary its own responsible process, bypassing the launcher's chain. Productized fix: distribute the helper as a Developer-ID-signed `.app` so its own TCC identity is authoritative regardless of who launched it.

- **TCC keys grants on the binary's cdhash, not its path — ad-hoc-signed binaries are TCC-cursed.** (Session 197.) Smoke-testing 14.20.2's Swift helper reproduced the exact silent-failure mode the 14.20.1 spike predicted: `CGPreflightScreenCaptureAccess()` returns true, `SCStream.startCapture()` completes with no error, and zero `didOutputSampleBuffer` callbacks ever fire. Doctor's `--probe` reports both grants as `ok` because TCC.db genuinely does have an entry — but the entry's cdhash matches an *earlier* build of the binary. Every `swiftc` rebuild produces a new cdhash, so the in-process daemon check sees "this exact binary identity isn't on the allowlist" and routes around the callback delivery silently. What made it tricky: every layer of feedback says success (preflight ok, startCapture ok, doctor green), and the only signal is "callbacks never arrive" which a naive caller would interpret as "system is just quiet right now." The 10s no-callback watchdog is the load-bearing diagnostic — without it, the helper would idle indefinitely with the user wondering why slip can't hear anything. **Lesson:** when integrating with macOS TCC, design a watchdog around "did at least one callback fire after startCapture" rather than trusting preflight + startCapture-success. And accept that ad-hoc signatures (anything `swiftc` produces locally) are not viable past dev — Developer-ID code-signing is a day-one production requirement, not polish, because TCC's entire trust model is keyed on cdhash stability.

- **TCC.db is SIP-protected on read; the only supported probe path is to ask from inside a binary about its own grants.** (Session 197, Phase 14.20.3.) When wiring `operator doctor` checks for Screen Recording + Microphone, the obvious approach was `sqlite3 ~/Library/Application\ Support/com.apple.TCC/TCC.db "SELECT ..."` — DECISION.md called out that even as the file's owner, sqlite returns "authorization denied" because TCC.db is shielded by System Integrity Protection. Granting Full Disk Access to Terminal works around it but defeats the purpose (we're trying to make a check that just runs without scary prompts). `tccutil` looked like the obvious alternative — but as of macOS 13+ it only supports `reset`, never `read`. The supported path that actually works: a binary the user has already attributed to themselves can call `CGPreflightScreenCaptureAccess()` and `AVCaptureDevice.authorizationStatus(for: .audio)` to ask the system about its *own* grants. So 14.20.3 added a `--probe` flag to the Swift helper that runs both API calls, prints structured JSON, and exits — doctor invokes it as a subprocess and parses the output. **Lesson:** when querying macOS privacy state, never reach for the database directly; route the query through a binary that has standing to ask about itself. The same principle applies to other SIP-protected stores (Keychain, Authorization).

- **`claude --dangerously-skip-permissions` does NOT skip PreToolUse hooks.** (Session 196.) An older comment in `claude_cli._spawn` (added 14.19.2) said the flag bypasses hooks at the CLI level, making operator's bridge plumbing inert under YOLO. Live test in S196 disproved it: with `--dangerously-skip-permissions` set, our `PermissionChatHandler` still fired (`/tmp/operator.log` line 646 logged `auto-approve 'ToolSearch'`). The flag appears to override deny *decisions* but doesn't suppress hook invocation itself — so a chat-side handler that returns deny will be ignored, but a handler that round-trips through chat (await_reply blocking on a user message) will still hang. **Lesson:** when integrating an upstream CLI flag, don't trust documentation comments older than ~3 months — claude-CLI ships fast and behavior changes. Run a live test that actually checks whether your hook fires under the flag before assuming you can skip the bridge wiring. We now belt-and-suspenders this with `auto_approve=["*"]` in `chat_runner._wire_permissions` under `OPERATOR_YOLO=1` — even if the flag's behavior changes again, our handler returns allow on every tool.

- **Mech 2 (LLM authors permission prompt + bridge waits silently) has a cross-turn correlation gap.** (Session 196, Phase 14.19.8 spike.) The naive design — bot asks "Want me to do X?", user says "yes", model invokes tool, bridge waits for next chat reply — fails when "yes" is the input that triggered the very turn invoking the tool. The user's "yes" gets consumed as the turn's user_text by chat_runner's main loop; by the time the bridge fires, the user has moved on and won't say yes a second time. The bridge sits silent waiting forever. **Fix:** add a recent-yes auto-approve to the handler — peek at the most recent user chat message; if it's `_is_yes()` and within a short window (30s), treat it as the approval for THIS gate and mark it consumed (set membership keyed on msg id) so chained tool calls within the same turn fall through to the normal await path. Without "consumed" tracking, a single yes would auto-approve every chained tool, eroding the safety contract. **Lesson:** when a permission protocol's contract is "user reply → unblock," the protocol has an implicit assumption that the reply hasn't already been consumed by something else in the system. In a streaming chat-LLM loop where the user's reply IS also the next turn's input, that assumption breaks. Need explicit "did this approval already get used elsewhere?" bookkeeping shared between the chat loop and the gate.

- **Strong rule wording can ovet-correct a model's normal behavior — needs reasoning, not just imperatives.** (Session 196.) After tiering the rule into READ/WRITE, the model began emitting declarative narration for Write tools when the user's prior message was an imperative ("Use the Write tool to create the file..."). The model reasoned: "user explicitly commanded this, asking again is redundant." Architecturally correct from a conversational standpoint but operationally broken — the bridge gate had nothing visible to reply to, hangs. The fix wasn't "shout louder"; it was adding a *reasoning* clause to the rule: "ALWAYS a question — even when the user's prior message was an explicit command. Why: the framework's permission gate blocks the write until the user replies in meeting chat, and a declarative narration leaves the user with nothing visible to reply to (the operation hangs until they realize)." Models often listen better to "X happens because Y" framings than to imperatives stacked on imperatives. **Lesson:** when a steering rule fights with a model's default reasonable behavior, add the consequence/reason. The model is trying to be helpful; explain the system constraint that makes its helpfulness counterproductive in this specific case.

- **Documented "no operator-side bridge" can mean "operator-side bridge with no overrides" — verify what the code does before deleting anything load-bearing.** (Session 195.) The 14.19.7-F handoff said "claude owns its own permissions hierarchy via `~/.claude/settings.json` + the existing `PreToolUse` hook in `claude_cli.py`." I read this as "no chat-side gate needed" and deleted `permission_chat_handler.py` + `_wire_track_a_permissions` accordingly. The smoke tests passed (Chrome opened, chat panel rendered, intro fired). The regression only surfaced when the user actually asked for a transcript / Linear query — then every MCP tool call silently denied because (a) `~/.claude/settings.json` only allowed `Bash(...)` + `Read(...)` rules, nothing for MCP tools, and (b) `claude -p` has no tty for an interactive prompt, so the default permission flow has nowhere to display. The model invented an explanation ("the permission prompt got denied") because tool failures arrived as opaque "tool error" with no visible UI signal. The cost: ~30min to diagnose + restore the bridge from git via `git checkout HEAD -- permission_chat_handler.py confirmation.py` + add back a 25-line `_wire_permissions` to chat_runner. **Lesson:** when a handoff says "X owns Y" and that contradicts what the code currently does, default to "verify what the code currently does" + ask whether the deletion changes user-facing behavior. The PreToolUse hook in `claude_cli.py` is plumbing — it only fires when an operator-supplied `permission_handler` is set. Without one, the bridge plumbing is dormant and inner-claude falls back to its CLI defaults, which under `-p` mode silently fail. Smoke tests that only exercise "did the meeting join" can't catch this; you need a tool-using turn to surface it.

- **`git checkout -f main` after the orphan-snapshot dance silently drops uncommitted working-tree changes — hit twice now.** (Sessions 189 + 195.) The orphan-snapshot publish flow (session 182's `public-snapshot-vN` procedure) needs `git checkout -f main` at the end because untracked-but-bit-identical files exist in the working tree from `git rm --cached`, and bare `git checkout main` refuses to overwrite them. The `-f` overrides that guard — but it ALSO overwrites any genuinely *modified* tracked files in the working tree, dropping the changes silently. **S189 lost the `docs/roadmap.md` Claude Code Plugin section. S195 lost pre-existing `docs/handoff.md` modifications carried in from before this session.** Reflog only tracks commits, so both are unrecoverable from git. **Lesson:** before running the orphan-snapshot dance, audit `git status` for any *modified tracked files* (not just untracked). If anything is modified, either commit/stash first or accept the loss. Procedure for next time: `git stash push -u --keep-index` before `git checkout --orphan`, `git stash pop` after `git checkout -f main`. Or codify in a single-purpose script that does the stash dance.

- **Cloudflare Pages and Workers were unified into one product surface — there's no longer a separate "Pages" tab in the dashboard.** (Session 189.) The roadmap's S182 instructions said to "create a Pages project via Workers & Pages → Pages tab," but Cloudflare merged the surfaces in late 2025. New flow: Workers & Pages → "Create application" → click "Continue with GitHub" (Git-connected path is what Pages used to be). If you accidentally pick "Start with Hello World!" or "Select a template," you get a Worker (which serves dynamic compute, not static files — every path 404s if there's no JS code). Telltale signs of an accidental Worker: tabs read "Bindings | Observability" and there's an "Edit code" button (Pages has "Custom domains | Functions" instead). Build settings page for the Git path is the real Pages config: framework=None, build command=empty, build output dir=`/`. **Lesson:** when documented procedures reference vendor UI tabs or labels, expect them to drift on a 6-month timescale. Encode the *outcome* (e.g. "static-site Pages project, Git-connected") so a future reader can recognize when they've ended up in the wrong product even if the labels have changed.

- **`codex mcp-server` 0.128.0 does NOT expose `-c`-registered child MCPs to its inner model.** (Session 188.) When operator drives codex via the MCP protocol (`codex(prompt=...)` tool call), the inner model handling the prompt sees only `web`, `functions`, `multi_tool_use` — never `mcp__<server>__<tool>` even though the child MCP subprocess gets correctly spawned. The same `-c mcp_servers.X.command="..."` flags work fine in `codex exec` mode (interactive CLI), so the limitation is mode-specific. What made it tricky: registration looks like it works (codex spawns the child process; no error from any layer), but the tools just never surface in `tools/list` to the model. Verified by a direct MCP-handshake spike that asked codex to list its tools — codex itself reported "I don't see any transcript-related tools." Workaround that shipped: codex's inner model has shell access via `functions`, and read-class commands auto-approve, so codex reads the meeting JSONL via `cat`/`grep`/`jq` directed by a system-prompt path hint to `~/.operator/.current_meeting`. Lesson: when integrating with another tool that has multiple invocation modes (interactive CLI vs MCP server), don't assume tool-exposure semantics carry over. Verify both modes against the actual binary.

- **`claude_cli` strict-last-must-be-user assertion + race with `intro_on_join` produces a silent Q1 failure.** (Session 188.) `claude_cli.complete_streaming` asserts `messages[-1].role == 'user'` because it sends only the latest user text to a long-lived subprocess that holds prior history internally. ChatRunner's `_handle_message` was persisting user messages to the meeting record at *detection* time (chat_runner.py:592), but the intro_on_join flow generates the bot's intro asynchronously and persists it *after*. If a user message arrived during intro generation, the JSONL ended up with `user(Q1) → assistant(intro)` in that order. When Q1 drained from the pre-intro buffer, `_tail_messages` returned them in JSONL order, leaving Q1's call with `messages[-1].role == 'assistant'` and triggering the assertion. ChatRunner emitted `Turn 1 failed` (not `✓ Replied`) and the apology-on-failure narration ran. What made it tricky: the bug only manifested when (a) the user sent a message during the intro-generation window AND (b) the LLM provider had a strict assertion about message ordering. Most live testing has the user wait politely for the intro before typing, so this race never showed up. The autonomous test harness, by contrast, pipes Q1 to stdin within milliseconds of `chat ready`, hitting the race deterministically. The fix at chat_runner.py:582-606 buffers pre-intro messages in memory and defers the `record.append` until drain time — JSONL order now matches processing order. Lesson: when persistence order can diverge from processing order (async work alongside synchronous polling), persistence-at-processing-time is more correct than persistence-at-detection-time, because anything reading the persisted log will assume processing order.

- **`pyproject.toml` rename leaves stale module paths in `--mcp-config` JSON dumps.** (Session 188.) The Phase 14.5 package rename `operator → _1_800_operator` swept the codebase via grep/sed, but `claude_cli.py:342` had `args=["-m", "operator.mcp_servers.transcript_server"]` inside a `json.dumps` call — a string literal that the rename pass silently missed. The bundled transcript MCP failed to spawn under claude with `ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'operator.mcp_servers'` at every meeting since the rename — claude would just say "I don't have access to spoken audio" because the tool was never reachable. What made it tricky: nothing in the codebase tried to *import* the broken string; it only became a problem when claude tried to spawn the child subprocess via `--mcp-config`, and the failure surfaced inside claude's own subprocess (not operator's logs). User-facing behavior was a soft "I can't see captions" reply, indistinguishable from "captions are disabled." Lesson: package renames need a literal-string sweep too, not just the import-path sweep. Module names appearing inside `json.dumps`, `subprocess` argv lists, `getattr` lookups, or shell-cmd strings won't be caught by an `import` grep.


**Session 187 — Three entries:**

1. **`claude -p --no-session-persistence` and `claude -p --resume <id>` are mutually exclusive — and claude's own `--help` is the only place this is documented.** When wiring Phase 14.17, I expected to just add a `--resume` arg to `_restart_after_death` and call it done. The spike script worked first try, then I noticed claude_cli.py was passing `--no-session-persistence` on every spawn (added in S166 to keep the session store clean). Re-reading the help text: `--no-session-persistence: Disable session persistence - sessions will not be saved to disk and cannot be resumed`. Without persistence, there's no on-disk session file for `--resume` to rehydrate from. So Phase 14.17 was structurally bigger than I scoped: had to drop `--no-session-persistence` from the steady-state spawn (not just the recovery spawn), accept that meeting sessions now persist to `~/.claude/projects/` like regular Claude Code work, and document the implications in the README. **Lesson:** when integrating a new CLI flag, search the existing spawn cmd for any flags that explicitly disable the feature you're trying to enable — and read the help text fully before architecting. Don't assume the disable-flag is documented separately from the feature flag; CLI authors often note the conflict only on the disable side.

2. **`${VAR}` substitution in operator's MCP server config applies only to `env`, not `args`.** This was load-bearing for the Phase 14.18 architecture decision. We could have extended `${VAR}` resolution to args (a small change in `config.py`) and threaded `OPERATOR_MEETING_RECORD_PATH` through `-c` flags at codex spawn — elegant, reuses tested machinery. But it forced a downstream constraint: the env var must be set BEFORE MCPClient spawns codex, which in meet.new mode (URL not yet resolved) requires reordering `mcp_thread.start()` to run after `_wire_meeting_record`. The simpler answer turned out to be the marker-file approach: `transcript_server.py` reads the active meeting path from `~/.operator/.current_meeting` on each tool call, so the codex YAML can register the transcript MCP via fully-static `-c` flags with no per-meeting interpolation. **Lesson:** when an architecture decision starts requiring "we also need to extend X primitive AND reorder Y AND coordinate with Z timing," that's a signal to look for an alternative that needs none of those. The marker-file mechanism trades a small bit of shared filesystem state (already a pattern in operator: `browser_profile/`, `auth_state.json`, history dir) for zero new substitution rules and zero ordering hazards.

3. **Codex 0.128.0 supports `-c key=value` overrides on `mcp-server` — the S179 finding is now obsolete.** When sequencing Phase 14.18 my first instinct was "S179 said codex's `mcp-server` mode doesn't accept `--mcp-config` so we can't inherit operator's bundled transcript MCP." That was true at the time but six months out of date. Verified live: `codex mcp list -c 'mcp_servers.test_inject.command="/bin/echo"'` registers the injected entry visibly in the MCP listing. Same `-c` flag works on `codex mcp-server`. **Lesson:** when a deferred risk references an upstream limitation, ALWAYS run the help command and a quick verification before scoping work around the workaround. Upstream tools move fast (codex jumped multiple versions between S179 and S187). Treat sessions-old "this doesn't work" findings as falsifiable, not as facts.

**Session 181 — Two entries:**

1. **`console.clear()` immediately after a step's print can hide the step from the user.** The codex flow looked like it skipped step 6 (sign-in jumped from `5. System Prompt` straight to `7. Sign-in`). I almost added a `Press Enter` to make step 6 visible. The actual cause: `_step6_api_keys` always printed the `6. API keys` header — even when there was nothing to prompt for — and then `run()` ran `console.clear()` immediately after, wiping the step before the user could read. Codex has zero `${VAR}` env refs, so step 6 was a flash-and-clear no-op. The right fix isn't "pause longer," it's "don't burn a step number on a no-op." Pre-compute `missing_keys` in `run()` and only call `_step6_api_keys` (and increment `n`) when there's actually a key to prompt for. **Lesson:** when a wizard step appears skipped, don't reach for a pause — check whether the step is doing real work for *this* config. A noop step that flashes a header isn't friendly progress UX, it's misleading; either gate it on actual work, or remove it. Same shape applies anywhere step numbering is dynamic + screens auto-clear between steps.

2. **A "rename" is not the same as "rename + alias."** Renaming `operator run` → `operator dial` looks like a one-line dispatch arm change (`if first == "run"` → `if first == "dial"`). But the codebase had ~25 user-facing strings (Usage:, "Restart with:", re-run nudges, error hints, README templates, YAML comments, code comments) all reading `operator run`, plus 4 tests asserting on those strings, plus 4 active step-by-step doc files with stale commands. The right shape for a rename in a pre-1.0 CLI is: (a) make the dispatch arm accept *both* the new and old form (`if first in ("dial", "run")`), so muscle memory + external links don't break; (b) advertise only the new form in `--help`/Usage; (c) flip every user-facing string to the new form so the canonical UX teaches the new name; (d) update test argv strings AND assertion substrings (the latter is the easy miss); (e) add a regression test that pins the alias path so a future contributor can't drop it accidentally; (f) update active step-by-step docs but leave session-by-session historical narrative alone (rewriting "in session 151 we shipped `operator run claude`" distorts the record). **Lesson:** before doing a CLI verb rename, grep the entire repo for the old string and bucket the hits into 5 categories: dispatch logic (1 site, must change), user-facing strings (many sites, must change), tests (must change AND assert against new substrings), active how-to docs (should change), historical narrative (don't touch). Skipping any of (b)/(d)/(e) leaves a trap for the next contributor.

**Session 178 — Three more entries:**

1. **Audit findings need a second look against actual code, not against the audit's own framing.** Two T1.* findings I shipped had wrong framings on first read. T1.4 was framed as "this fires today" — but tracing the four `_dispatch_result` arms showed they cover every shape `LLMClient` currently returns; the else-arm is a dormant safety net, not a live bug. T1.7 was framed as "chat and record disagree" — but tracing the on_paragraph → `_send` → record-append path showed both chat *and* record receive `accumulated`; the audit's claim about canonical reaching the record was wrong; the actual finding was that `canonical_text` was unused dead computation. Both fixes still landed, but with corrected scope (downgrade T1.4's urgency framing; T1.7's fix was a deletion, not a swap). **Lesson:** treat the audit doc as a hypothesis. Before shipping a fix, re-read the actual code paths the finding implicates and verify the user-impact claim is reproducible. The audit author (even if it's me a few hours earlier) often pattern-matches the finding to a known shape and gets the framing wrong.

2. **A failure-recovery LLM call is safe IFF you can guarantee the response shape AND skip the rate-limit retry.** When building `_narrate_failure`, the user pushed back on filter-by-exception-class with "why not just feed the failure to the LLM?" The original concern ("LLM call also rate-limited → recursion") only holds if (a) the response shape can re-enter the failing dispatcher, AND (b) the fallback call retries on 429 like the original did. Both are addressable: pass `tools=None` to guarantee a bare-string return (can't be `tool_call` or other dict shape, so dispatcher can't loop on it); add a `retry_rate_limits=False` kwarg threaded through `LLMProvider.complete`/`complete_streaming` so the fallback fails fast on persistent 429 instead of making the user wait through a second retry window. **Lesson:** "LLM-narrated apology" is the right UX when the original call failed, but it requires two design decisions explicit in the API surface: a way to constrain the response shape so the fallback can't itself trigger the failure path, and a way to override retry policies so latency on the failure path stays bounded. If the LLM client's `ask()` method doesn't expose these as kwargs, add them — don't try to invoke the call with a "please don't retry" prompt instruction (the model can't enforce that).

3. **`bailed_mid_stream` flags + synthetic `ProviderResponse` keep callers honest after early exits.** T1.6 bails out of `complete_streaming` when a 429 fires after paragraphs have already flushed. The bail can't `raise` (caller would fire its own narrate fallback on top of the apology line we just posted). Can't `return None` (caller's `if response.tool_calls`/`response.text` access would AttributeError). Solution: `flushed_any = True` triggers the bail; `bailed_mid_stream = True` flags the post-finally branch; return `ProviderResponse(text="", tool_calls=[], stop_reason="end")` — the empty-text-streamed-already shape that caller already handles via the `streamed=True` branch in `_dispatch_result`. **Lesson:** when a function has an early-exit path triggered mid-iteration (mid-stream, mid-loop, mid-transaction), don't try to raise or return-None — synthesize the same shape the happy path returns, with empty/sentinel values, so the caller's existing branches handle the early-exit state without needing new awareness. The `streamed=True` flag was already doing the work of "user already saw the content"; the bail just had to produce a shape that respected it.

**Session 177 — Four more entries:**

1. **`re.findall(r"\b\w+\b", lower)` splits "don't" into `{don, t}`.** Cluster 1 added a negation gate to `_handle_confirmation` so "ok no don't" wouldn't auto-approve a tool call. The first iteration tested fine for "ok no" / "approve nah cancel" / etc. but the regression test caught `"yes don't"` slipping through as approval. Cause: `\w` is `[A-Za-z0-9_]`, so the apostrophe is a word boundary; `re.findall(r"\b\w+\b", "yes don't")` returns `["yes", "don", "t"]`. Neither `"don"` nor `"t"` matched the negation set. The fix was to keep the word-set check for plain tokens (`no, nope, nah, stop, cancel`) but use substring detection for contractions (`"don't" in lower`, `"dont" in lower`, `"do not" in lower`). **Lesson:** word-boundary tokenization is wrong for matching contractions or hyphenated phrases. When the negation vocabulary spans both single tokens and apostrophe-bearing forms, mix substring checks alongside the tokenizer — don't try to extend the regex to keep them whole. Same gotcha applies to "won't", "can't", "ain't", any `'s` possessive, etc.

2. **`except Exception` doesn't catch `KeyboardInterrupt`.** Cluster 7 found that `_step7_write`'s rollback (`shutil.rmtree(tmp); rename(backup, target)`) ran inside an `except Exception:` block. A Ctrl+C between `os.rename(target, backup)` and `os.rename(tmp, target)` raised `KeyboardInterrupt` — a `BaseException`, not `Exception` — bypassing the rollback entirely. User ends up with `agents/<name>.bak-<ts>/` intact but no live `agents/<name>/` dir. Fix was a one-word change: `except BaseException:`. The `raise` re-raises so `KeyboardInterrupt` still propagates to the outer `(KeyboardInterrupt, PickerCancelled, WizardCancel)` handler which prints "Cancelled". **Lesson:** any try/except that's specifically a *transactional rollback* (this-must-complete-or-undo) needs `except BaseException:`. The default `Exception` catch is for "expected failures"; transactions need to also catch user-cancel. Only safe to do this when nothing inside the try raises legitimate `SystemExit` / `KeyboardInterrupt` semantics that the caller relies on.

3. **Cache the failure too, not just the success.** Cluster 4 found `_claude_mcp_list_cached` returned `None` on `OSError` / `TimeoutExpired` *without* setting `_CLAUDE_MCP_LIST_CACHE`. Boot makes three callers (`discover_hosted_mcps_via_cli`, `discover_mcp_health`, runtime view in `config.py`); under a broken `claude` CLI each one re-shelled out and paid another 10s timeout. 30s of dead time at boot vs 10s with sentinel caching. The fix: cache a sentinel `subprocess.CompletedProcess(returncode=-1, stdout="", stderr="")` on the failure path. Existing `if r is None or r.returncode != 0: return []` branches degrade correctly to empty results without changes. **Lesson:** when you're caching the result of an expensive call, the failure case is part of the result. "Process is broken" is information that costs the same to discover as "process is healthy" and should be cached at the same priority. Sentinel-as-failure (a real object with a recognizable shape) beats `None` because callers don't have to special-case None vs success — same code path, just yields zero results.

4. **`mkdir(mode=0o700)` is a no-op when the dir already exists.** Cluster 11 closed the `~/.operator/history/` world-readable launch-blocker. Initial pattern was just `mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True, mode=0o700)` and call it done. But `mode=` only applies to dirs the call *creates* — for an existing dir (legacy install from before session-172's umask fix), the perms aren't touched. The fix needs THREE parts: (a) `mkdir(mode=0o700)` for fresh installs, (b) defensive `os.chmod(self.root, 0o700)` to retroactively tighten existing dirs, (c) `os.chmod(self.path, 0o600)` once on open per file (covers both new files where umask already produced 0o600 and legacy world-readable rejoins). Same pattern in `google_signin._write_artifacts` and `macos_adapter._browser_session` — it's the standard shape. **Lesson:** "harden creation" and "retroactively harden existing" are two different operations and you usually need both. `mkdir(mode=)` does the first; explicit `chmod` does the second. The same applies to files — `O_CREAT` mode is set-on-create only; chmod once on open if you need to repair pre-existing files.

---

**Session 176 — Three more entries:**

1. **A bash-only `import` inside an `if branch:` is invisible to most testing.** `__main__.py` had `import time as _time_init` nested inside `if name == "claude":` and then referenced `_time_init.monotonic()` unconditionally a few lines later (preflight TIMING block). Any non-claude bot crashed with `UnboundLocalError` before browser spin-up. The bug shipped in commit `4faed53` (session 174) and survived multiple sessions because v1 is claude-only — the dead path was never exercised in dev. Surfaced only when running `OPERATOR_BOT=pm python tests/test_entry_cli.py::test_run_bot_*` against the production code path. **Lesson:** when a TIMING / logging / observability snippet wants imports, hoist them to the top of the function or module. Conditional imports inside one branch + unconditional use after = a crash that hides whenever the branch happens to fire. If the imports are heavy, lazy-import on first use, but always-import on every code path that needs them. (Also: when a feature is gated to one bot, write at least one fast smoke test for the *other* bots' equivalent paths so dead-path crashes get caught at the test layer, not at the user's first run.)

2. **`mv ~/.brainchild ~/.operator` does NOT do what you want when `~/.operator` already exists.** Did the rename phase out-of-band assuming `~/.operator` was empty. It wasn't — there was a stale `~/.operator/history/` directory from a much earlier rename attempt. macOS `mv source target` semantics: if `target` is a directory and exists, `source` becomes a *child* of `target` (i.e., `mv ~/.brainchild ~/.operator` → `~/.operator/.brainchild/`). All the live data ended up nested. Recovery was straightforward (`rm -rf ~/.operator/history; mv ~/.operator/.brainchild/* ~/.operator/.brainchild/.env ~/.operator/; rmdir ~/.operator/.brainchild`) but it was a confusing five seconds. **Lesson:** before `mv source target` for a renamed directory, check `target` doesn't exist (`[ ! -e ~/.operator ]`). Or use `rsync -a source/ target/ && rm -rf source` which has explicit "merge into" semantics. Or just delete the empty target first if you're sure it's empty. The asymmetric behavior between "target doesn't exist" (rename) and "target exists" (move-into) is a footgun whenever the target's existence is uncertain.

3. **Python stdlib module names cannot be your distribution's import name — but the distribution name and CLI command can still be whatever you want.** Renaming our package to `operator` failed at first import: `from operator import config` resolved to Python's stdlib `operator` module. The CLI command `operator` and the user-facing data dir `~/.operator/` were fine, but the import name had to differ. Three-way split: distribution `1-800-operator` (PyPI / pyproject `name`), CLI command `operator` (`[project.scripts]` entry), Python import `_1_800_operator` (`packages = ["src/_1_800_operator"]`, valid Python identifier with leading underscore + numerics + underscores-for-hyphens). End users only see the first two; the import name surfaces only in source/tracebacks. Distribution names allow hyphens and leading digits (`1-800-operator` is legal); import names require valid Python identifiers (cannot start with digit, no hyphens). **Lesson:** when picking a project name, check Python's stdlib module list early (`python -c "import <candidate>"` — if it works, you'll shadow it). If the user-facing brand collides with stdlib, decouple distribution name + CLI command from the import name. The cost is one extra design decision; the savings are not having `import operator` (the stdlib) silently mean `import operator` (your package) for half your code. Bonus: end users never type the import name into anything when they install via `pip install <distname>` and run `<command>` — so the import name is a purely dev-internal aesthetic choice.

**Session 175 — Two more entries:**

1. **Pasting JS regex literals into Chrome DevTools is a coin flip — use `new RegExp(string)` instead.** The Zoom DOM probe IIFE first failed twice with cryptic errors before I figured out the cause. Round 1: `Uncaught SyntaxError: Invalid or unexpected token` at the closing `})()` of a multi-line arrow-function IIFE — the actual culprit was earlier in the file (a backtick template literal `` `${a.name}="${a.value}"` ``) that the DevTools paste handler had mangled. Round 2: same script rewritten with no template literals, no spreads — got `Uncaught SyntaxError: Invalid regular expression: missing /` even though every regex literal was syntactically valid (`/open\s*zoom|launch\s*zoom/i`, etc.). Round 3 finally worked: replace every regex literal with `new RegExp('open\\s*zoom|launch\\s*zoom', 'i')` (note: double-backslash inside the string for `\s`). Theory: DevTools' "Allow pasting" warning + Chrome's recent paste-protection logic occasionally re-encodes whitespace or quote characters in pasted scripts, and regex literals are uniquely fragile to that — a single mangled space inside a regex turns into a syntax error several lines down. Backtick template literals share the same fragility. **Lesson:** when authoring DevTools-console probes that users will paste, write paste-safe JavaScript: ASCII only, no template literals, no regex literals — use `new RegExp(string)` and string concatenation. The cost is a couple of extra lines; the savings are not having to debug paste-mangling at every error message.

2. **Vendor aria-labels are verbose, sentence-shaped, and often contain typos — match by `*=` (contains), not `=` (exact).** Initial Zoom in-meeting probe missed the Participants button entirely. The matcher used `^(participants|people|attendees|manage\s*participants)$` against `aria-label`. Zoom's actual label: `"open the participants list pane,[2] particpants"` (sic — typoed `particpants`, comma-separated, embeds the count in `[N]` brackets). The wider `_anyVisibleAriaLabeled` net caught it on the next probe. Same shape applies to Zoom's Chat button (`"open the chat panel"`, lowercase, action-phrased — flips to `"close the chat panel"` when open) and several others. **Lesson when scraping vendor DOM:** assume aria-labels are a) full English sentences not single keywords, b) reflective of toggle state ("open the X" / "close the X"), c) typoed (Zoom's `particpants` and `particpant` appear verbatim in production strings — must match the typoed form). Default to `[aria-label*="<keyword>" i]` (case-insensitive contains). Reserve exact match only for cases where you've confirmed a stable, terse label.

**Session 173 — Three more entries:**

1. **"OAuth scope" doesn't apply to a Playwright session.** The Vercel/Context AI breach was about OAuth bearer tokens (issued via `code → token` flow) with overly broad scopes, stored server-side. The instinct after such a breach is "audit our scopes" — but we have no scopes to audit because we never ran an OAuth flow. We launch real Chrome via `launch_persistent_context` and keep the user signed into Google. The persisted artifact is browser session cookies, not a scoped token, so the analogous mitigation is "harden local artifacts" not "trim scopes." Conflating the two leads to wrong threat-modeling and wasted hardening work. **Lesson:** before applying any incident's lesson to your codebase, name the exact mechanism in *your* code first. If the mechanism is different, the mitigation is different too.

2. **`auth_state.json` is load-bearing on Linux, not just a recovery seed.** It's tempting to look at `browser_profile/` (a full Chrome user-data-dir, has all the cookies) and conclude `auth_state.json` is redundant — and the file's docstring even calls it "the recovery seed." But the Linux adapter has TWO launch modes: a `launch_persistent_context` "guest" mode (no auth) and a `launch + new_context(storage_state=auth_state_file)` "authenticated" mode. Linux uses the JSON as the *primary* auth source; `browser_profile/` isn't loaded in the authenticated path at all. macOS does treat the JSON as a recovery fallback (re-injected via `inject_cookies` when `detect_page_state == "logged_out"`), and that fallback is real — Google rotates cookies aggressively and without it the bot dies instead of recovering. Removing the JSON breaks Linux entirely and degrades macOS recovery. **Lesson:** when one credential artifact "looks redundant," walk every reader of it — adapter file paths included — before removing.

3. **`mkdir` then `chmod` has a race window; pass `mode=` instead.** Existing code did `os.makedirs(path, exist_ok=True)` followed by `os.chmod(path, 0o700)`. Between those calls the dir exists with default umask perms (often `0o755`). On a single-user laptop this is theoretical, on a shared/CI host another UID can `ls` it during that window. The fix is `os.makedirs(path, exist_ok=True, mode=0o700)` — atomic-private creation, no window. Same for files: `os.open(path, O_WRONLY|O_CREAT, 0o600)` instead of write-then-chmod. The cheapest belt-and-suspenders is `os.umask(0o077)` once at process start so any incidental write is born owner-only by default. **Lesson:** any time you're locking down perms after the fact, ask whether you can lock them down at creation instead — the difference matters on shared hosts and the syntactic cost is one keyword arg.

**Session 169 — Three more entries:**

1. **English templating in Python is a tarpit when the LLM is right there.** Yesterday's voice-modes commit hardcoded ~150 lines of per-tool English phrases (`_format_plain` dictionary, MCP verb table, narrator categories). Live test surfaced both an immediate bug (`"find a organizations"` — wrong article + plural mismatch) and a structural one (a pirate-mode user would still see modern conversational English because the templating preempts persona). The fix wasn't to extend the templating with `_article_for(noun)` — that would just add another bug class. The fix was to delete the templating entirely and let the LLM speak in its persona via two ground_rules directives (self-narrate auto-approved tools, self-preamble destructive ones). Operator emits a sterile, neutral approval challenge as the safety gate; the bot's voice flows from `personality` + `ground_rules`. Net: -150 lines, no grammar bugs possible, persona customization works free. **Lesson:** when you find yourself building a phrase dictionary inside a project that already has an LLM in the loop, stop. The dictionary will always lose to the LLM on flexibility, and it will always have a long tail of edge cases the LLM doesn't have.

2. **Imperative fields must always render verbatim, even if they're long.** The Sentry triage prompt rendered as `Run? mcp__sentry__get_sentry_resource: url=(89 B)\nOK?` — the URL was hidden as a size hint because the unknown-tool fallback collapsed any field over 80 chars. That defeats the entire point of the safety prompt: the user can't approve what they can't see. Bash commands had a special case ("never summarize") but no other tool did. Generalized: define an `_IMPERATIVE_FIELD_NAMES` set (`url`, `path`, `file_path`, `command`, `query`, `pattern`, `search`, `notebook_path`) — any value under one of these keys renders verbatim regardless of length, with a 1KB sanity cap. **Lesson:** "compactness" is a payload concern, not an imperative concern. Hide the *what's-being-written*; never hide the *what's-about-to-happen*.

3. **MCP discovery is a snapshot, not a live mirror.** The user's installed `~/.operator/agents/claude/config.yaml` had a `mcp_servers:` block listing 4 servers — Calendar, Gmail, Drive, Linear. They added Sentry to `~/.claude.json` later via `claude mcp add`. When they tested, the operator bot said *"No Sentry MCP server is configured on my side"* — because operator's MCP list was frozen from the first-boot import (`_claude_import_done: true` blocks re-import). The fix was operational: wipe `~/.operator/agents/`, re-run `operator`, fresh import picks up the new server. **Lesson:** any "import once, then trust the user's config" pattern needs a corresponding "re-sync" command (or a TTL) — otherwise users who upgrade the source of truth get confusing silent failures. Filed as a follow-up: operator should refresh the MCP list on `operator edit <bot>` or expose a `operator sync claude` subcommand. **Resolved Phase 14.14.3 (session 171):** `_bootstrap_claude_imports` (one-shot) replaced with `_sync_claude_imports` that runs on every boot — re-reads `~/.claude.json` + `claude mcp list`, merges per-server (`command`/`args`/`env`/`auth`/`auth_url`/`description` source-driven, `enabled`/`hints`/`read_tools`/`confirm_tools` user-preserved), drops servers missing in source. Cost: ~3s `claude mcp list` shell-out every boot.

*Append-only log of bugs that were hard to diagnose. Each entry: what the bug was, what made it tricky, how it was fixed.*

- **`claude_cli.complete_streaming` only sends `messages[-1]` to its subprocess — dropping every prior message in the list, including caption `<spoken>` blocks.** (Session 171.) Live demo: user said "Purple" aloud, asked "what color did I just say?" in chat, Claude confidently replied *"No color has been spoken — I only see your typed messages, no voice transcript."* All the intermediate plumbing looked fine: `pipeline.transcript.caption_finalized` events fired, captions were appended to the meeting JSONL, `llm._tail_messages` correctly wrapped them as `<spoken>` blocks, the LLM ask line in the log even reported `messages=37`. The bug was at the transport boundary: `claude_cli` is a long-lived subprocess and assumes its conversation state lives inside the subprocess — so on each turn it only sends the *new* user message (`messages[-1]`) and lets the subprocess remember everything else. Captions never reach the subprocess (they're appended to the JSONL, not sent through the subprocess), so the subprocess has zero awareness of any spoken content. What made it tricky: the inner steps were all individually correct, and the misleading log line `messages=37 prompt_chars=37` showed both a populated message list AND a tiny prompt — easy to read as "37 messages with 37 chars total" instead of "37 messages assembled but only 37 chars actually transmitted." Fix: bundled `transcript` MCP server registered with Claude Code via `--mcp-config`. Inner-claude now calls `recall_transcript(minutes_back?, last_n?)` against the meeting JSONL on demand. Captions stay out of the prompt entirely (cleaner than the original plan to inject them ambiently). Lesson: when an LLM consistently denies seeing data the rest of the system clearly captured, suspect the *transport* between the data store and the LLM, not the data store or the LLM. Each layer's logs only confirm its own job.

- **A missing newline in user-edited YAML produced a structurally-valid `dict` where a `list` was expected — TypeError surfaced eight layers down at runtime.** (Session 171.) User added `mcp__transcript__recall_transcript` to `permissions.auto_approve` via `operator edit claude`, saved cleanly, and on next boot got `TypeError: '<' not supported between instances of 'dict' and 'str'` from `chat_runner.py:177` (`sorted(handler._always_ask)`). The actual error: a missing newline turned `- Task` and `mcp_servers:` into `- Taskmcp_servers:`, which YAML happily parsed as a list-item-whose-value-is-a-dict (`{Taskmcp_servers: ...}`). `permissions.always_ask` ended up containing one dict among several strings, and `sorted()` choked when comparing dict to str. What made it tricky: the file LOOKED reasonable when the user opened `operator edit claude` again — the malformed entry was a single missing newline that wasn't visually obvious in the rewritten YAML. The TypeError stack pointed at `sorted()` ten layers from the source of truth (the bad config line). Fix layers: schema validation in `config.py` now runs after `yaml.safe_load` and surfaces *"`permissions.always_ask[6]` must be a string, got dict"* with a `operator edit claude` next-step hint, all violations batched into one stderr block. Lesson: any time a user-editable file passes through a permissive parser (YAML, JSON-with-comments, TOML), validate the *shape* of the parsed structure at load time before letting it leak into runtime code. The user can fix one clear error at the source; they can't fix a TypeError ten layers down.

- **`operator edit` propagated vim's nonzero exit code to the shell prompt even on successful saves.** (Session 171.) `_run_edit` returned `subprocess.call(cmd)` directly. Vim sometimes exits nonzero for benign reasons (swapfile noise, terminal weirdness) even after `:wq` saved cleanly. The user saw a red X in their prompt, asked me whether their work was lost — exactly the failure mode the system should prevent (had to read the file off disk to confirm the save landed). Fix: `_run_edit` now prints `Saved <path>` on close and returns 0 if the file still exists, 1 only if the file is gone. Lesson: for interactive editor commands, the editor's exit code is a poor signal — it reflects editor-internal noise, not the success of the user's task. The real signal is whether the file landed on disk. Print a positive confirmation; don't propagate uninformative exit codes.

- **`yaml.safe_dump` silently eats comments, blank lines, and hand-formatting.** (Session 121.) The setup wizard's edit-in-place mode runs `yaml.safe_load(existing_cfg)` → user edits → `yaml.safe_dump(cfg)` → writes back. Comments, section dividers, inline explanatory notes, and custom quoting all vanish. Surfaced when the user smoke-tested the wizard on `agents/{pm,designer,engineer}/config.yaml` — `git status` showed huge diffs even on presets that didn't change any wizard inputs, just because `yaml.safe_dump` round-trips drop everything the parser doesn't care about. What made it tricky: the wizard behaves correctly (values round-trip intact) so no test would catch it; you only see the damage in `git diff`. Mitigation for now: restored configs via `git checkout --`. Proper fix (deferred): swap to `ruamel.yaml` with `YAML(typ='rt')` — round-trip loader preserves comments and formatting. Or, only rewrite the specific fields the wizard touches (`enabled` flags, `skills.paths`) via a targeted string/diff approach. Not blocking; worth addressing before inviting external contributors who'll keep editing their configs by hand.
- **Rich markup parser swallows `[x]` in printed text.** (Session 119.) First draft of the power-ups toggle rendered checked items as `[x]` and unchecked as `[ ]`. `[ ]` printed literally (invalid markup), but `[x]` vanished entirely — Rich interpreted it as a (non-existent) style tag and stripped it. Took a minute to spot because the asymmetry only appeared when some items were default-checked. Fix: switched to `[✓]` (non-ASCII bracketed content isn't parsed as a style tag). Generalizable lesson: any `[letter]` or `[word]` in Rich-printed strings is at risk of being treated as markup — either escape with `\[` or use unicode glyphs.
- **Rich `Live` can't host `Prompt.ask`/`input()` mid-render.** (Session 121.) First attempt at step 3's "add your own skills" UX tried to pop a text input when a sentinel row was toggled mid-picker. Doesn't work — the `Live` region owns the terminal until exited, and input prompts don't compose with it. Fix: either exit the Live first (picker confirms → then prompt), or render a "queued action" hint and act on it after the picker closes. Final design landed on the former — `Confirm.ask` after the picker closes, path-input loop if confirmed.
- **Right-pane column squeezes inline sublabels past terminal-width truncation.** (Session 121.) Picker rows rendered `label <spaces> sublabel` on one line in a `Table.grid` left column; a 40-col build card in the right column left only ~32 cols for the left, and Rich silently truncated the dim sublabel text with no ellipsis. Looked like a 60-char cap bug at first because the skill subtitle *also* had a `desc[:60]` truncation in the code, which was a red herring — removing the slice didn't fix the visible cut-off. Fix: move sublabels to their own indented line under the label. No more horizontal-width race.
- **Rich `Panel.border_style` is a single value — no per-char frame colors.** (Session 122.) User asked for a rainbow frame on the build card. `Panel` accepts one `border_style` and applies it uniformly; there's no hook to vary color per character. Fix: drop `Panel` entirely and hand-compose the frame. Build top/bottom/side chars as raw strings, wrap each character with a fresh ANSI color + reset, join into a single string, and feed to `rich.text.Text.from_ansi` so Rich re-parses the sequences into styled segments at render time. Worth knowing because the obvious "style the Panel border" path is a dead end for any gradient/rainbow/per-char frame effect.
- **`len()` lies about cell width for wide glyphs (⚡, emoji).** (Session 122.) When hand-composing the rainbow card, naive `len(line)` padding misaligned the power-ups row because `⚡` is 2 terminal cells wide, not 1. Fix: `from rich.cells import cell_len` (or use `wcwidth`) for cell-accurate padding.
